      "You seem to have caught on fast," I said lightly. I smiled faintly as I reached up and removed my helmet.
      Clarity inhaled sharply as her eyes went first to the fangs peaking over my lower lip and then to my blood-red irises. Corinna's mother let out a faint gasp and took a step backward. I sighed, and my smile faded. I wasn't going to pretend that I wasn't a vampire. Only with honesty could there be trust.
      "It's okay, really," Corinna said. "She won't hurt us."
      "How do you know that?" Clarity demanded. Even though her voice was cold, there was a slight tremor in it now.
      "As Corinna said-I won't hurt any of you," I added, still all too aware of the eyes on me. "You can choose to believe it or not." With that, I set my helmet on the ground and turned to leave the clearing.
      "Talon," Corinna called after me. "Where are you going?"
      I looked back over my shoulder. "I'm going to go prepare a few things for our journey. I can tell your family members are anxious. They'll feel more at ease if you stay with them." As I walked into the shadows of the mossy trees, I could feel their eyes on my back.
      I reached my log and knelt down to rummage through the stash of clothes and weapons. While I could cross the entire forest at record speed, walking through the forest would take at least a few hours for a human. Eventually I dumped everything onto the ground and set aside certain clothing items to bring back to Corinna and her family. When I was satisfied with my selection, I turned to the weapons-knives, daggers, and a couple of swords. I reached for the daggers and examined their blades.
      Swords wouldn't do-especially not on the road. First, I doubted anyone in Corinna's family knew how to properly wield one. Well, that wasn't entirely true-Corinna's brother once fought in the war, but he couldn't do much in his current state. Second, I knew we were already going to be an eye-catching party. Corinna and her family were going to look out of place wherever they went in the western kingdom.
      I picked out a few daggers and dropped them on top of the pile of clothes. After setting aside a sword for myself, I absently reached up to brush my hair over my shoulder, but suddenly remembered that I had sliced it off. Instead, I scooped up the pile of clothes and weapons, then returned to the clearing.
      "Clarity, we need to work with her," Cameren was saying, and I paused to listen behind the trees. "If the vampire really was the monster you think she is, we'd all already be dead by now."
      "Some risks are risks that we have to take," Corinna's mother added tiredly.
      "What use are we to Chloe-Jane if we're all dead?" Clarity countered. "Have you ever thought about that?"
      "Clarity," Corinna said firmly. "No one's going to die."
      "What use are we to Chloe-Jane if we remained in the village?" Corinna's mother asked softly. "Chloe-Jane is your sister, but she is also my daughter. We will get her back."
      "You all said the same thing about Father," Clarity muttered under her breath. "You all said to wait-that if we waited long enough, he'd come back to us."
      When they finally fell silent, I took a step forward from the tree line. Corinna hurried over to me and eyed the pile of clothes in my arms. "Are these for us?"
      I set the pile down on the ground. "Divide these up with your family. Also"-I took Corinna's hand and pressed the hilt of one of the daggers into her palm-"this is for you."
      Corinna just stared down at the weapon in her hands. "A dagger?"
      "Let's just hope you don't have to use it."
      Corinna stared down at the blade as if it were some foreign object. She turned it over in her hands. "Is this really necessary?"
      I gave her a knowing look. "You never know. I understand that you'd probably not want to use it if you can help it, though. Threatening someone with the dagger might be enough to scare them away."
      Corinna pocketed the blade with shaky hands. "Right. I'll keep that in mind."
      I sat down on the forest floor while Corinna went to distribute the clothes among her family. When she was done, she turned and walked back over to me.
      I blinked as she took a seat in front of me and carefully arranged her skirts around her legs. "Why are you helping me?" she asked. "Helping me get my family members out of the village was already more than I could ever hope for. And now you're even willing to go to the capital city with us to find my sister."
      I dropped my gaze. "Have you heard of Karmen, the queen of the vampires?"
      Corinna shook her head as she waited for me to go on.
      I could feel the eyes of Corinna's family members on me. "Let's go collect wood for a fire. Come, we can talk on the way."
      Corinna rose to her feet and followed me deeper into the forest. "Karmen. You were talking about the queen of the vampires."
      "She's the one who turned me into a monster," I said darkly. "I spent at least half a century trying to track her down, but I haven't been able to find her. No one knows her whereabouts or what she looks like. Even at the time when she turned me, her face was still hidden in the shadows of her cloak. All anybody knows for sure is that she's female."
      "So," Corinna said slowly as she put the pieces together, "you think that Karmen is in the capital city?"
      I nodded and began collecting tinder from the forest floor. "Just a few days ago, I found the body of a dead vampire in this very forest. It was Karmen's work."
      Corinna shook her head in disbelief. "She's killing vampires? Why?"
      "It is strange," I agreed. "At least she doesn't seem to be killing humans anymore. She hasn't for a while now. Maybe she got bored of killing them and set her sights on her fellow vampires instead."
      "What are you going to do when you do find her?"
      My hand stilled over the twig I was reaching for. "I would like to get justice for all those innocents she's killed . . . but I don't know. Even though I do have some knowledge of wielding blades, I don't think I could win against her. The queen is known to be quite skilled with weapons herself." There was a long pause, and I picked up a few more twigs before straightening. "We should head back to your family. You should get some sleep. It's a long way to the capital city."
      "You should get some sleep too."
      I let out a dry laugh. "I appreciate your concern, but I don't sleep."
      "Vampires don't sleep?"
      I sighed. "Technically I'm dead. Dead bodies can't sleep-they don't have beating hearts."
      Corinna frowned slightly as we walked. She angled her head to the side as if trying to find which part of me indicated that I was dead. "You look very much alive to me."
      "You should get some sleep," I said again as I averted my gaze.
      "I'll stay up with you," she replied quickly. "I don't think I'd be able to fall asleep even if I wanted to."
      The two of us returned to Corinna's family, and we set down our piles of sticks. It didn't take long to get a fire going, and I felt the curse within me recoil from the flames. I ignored the internal clawing sensation as I inched away from the fire.
      After making sure her family members were seated as comfortably as they could be around the fire, Corinna shuffled back over to me. "Will you tell me more about the queen of the vampires? Now I'm curious to learn more."
      I found a rare smile tugging at the corners of my lips. "What do you want to know about Karmen?"
      "What does she do as queen of the vampires?" Corinna inquired quietly. "Has she always been the queen? Wait-does that make her the first vampire?"
      "If I'm being honest, I'm not exactly sure what she even does as queen. But I know for a fact that 'queen' is a title she bestowed on herself after she killed the first progenitor some five hundred years ago. With the first progenitor dead, that makes Karmen the most powerful vampire around. Occasionally a vampire will figure out where the queen is and try to kill her. But those who do cross her are either never seen again or turn up dead years later."
      "So, if you're already aware of the fate of those who challenge Karmen," Corinna said slowly, "why are you really looking for her?"
      "Closure, perhaps."
      "Closure?"
      I raised my head to the leafy canopy, which blotted out the stars beyond. "I've lived for far too many years, but I could never bring myself to end my existence. If I find Karmen, I'm sure she'll do the job for me. She was the one who gave me immortality. It only makes sense for her to take it back." When Corinna didn't respond, I decided to change the topic. "Is there anything else you'd like to know?"
      "If you don't mind me asking, how long has it been since you were turned into a vampire?"
      "Almost a hundred years now. Anything else?"
      "Is 'Talon' your real name?"
      "No." I let out a humorless laugh. "It's been a lifetime since anyone has called me by my real name. It's pitiful, really. After using so many fake ones over the years, I can't tell which one of them is my own. I'm sure it will come to me eventually if I give it enough thought."
      "Please tell me when you do remember. I would really like to know."
      "If we're still traveling together at that time, I'll make sure to let you know."
      A silence fell between the two of us. Then Corinna rose to her feet. "I think I'm going to try to get some sleep after all. It is a long way to the capital city. Goodnight, Talon."
      I watched Corinna shuffle back to the other side of the fire, where her family members were still wide awake. Even though she had mentioned sleep, Corinna spent another hour or so talking quietly with her family to fill them in on everything that had happened and reassuring them that things were going to work out.
       
~
       
      I led the way through the forest with Corinna and her family following closely behind. My hair had grown out again; I'd need to chop it off again before we reached the main road. After a few hours of walking, the trees began to thin out. We had reached the other side of the forest.
      "There is a town just a few miles north of here," I explained as I turned around to address my company. "The main road is just up ahead as well. Even though it's something that I would normally avoid, the main road is our fastest and most direct path to the capital city."
      Corinna let go of her mother's arm to walk over to me. "It's daytime right now. Are you sure you're going to be alright?"
      "The sun is completely blocked by the storm clouds." I gestured toward the gray sky beyond the trees. "I should be fine, but I'll put a cloak on just in case. We'll see how far we can get down the main road before the storm starts."
      We were able to make it through the first town down the road and had just entered the second town moments before the sky opened up in a roaring downpour, which turned the ground's remaining snow into a muddy slush. The walking had proven difficult for Corinna's brother, and I could tell that the journey was already beginning to take a toll on him. His wounds had never healed in the first place, and it was clear that they were starting to flare up. We needed to find someplace to rest, fast.
      "This way"-I gestured toward a cobblestone building at the end of the street-"we can wait out the storm there." I had to raise my voice so I could be heard over the howling of the winds.
      When we reached it, I pulled open the door, and the five of us quickly hurried inside. The sound of lively chatter greeted us as we entered the tavern. Wooden tables and chairs crowded the entire room, most of which were already occupied by other travelers and merchants who didn't feel like braving the storm.
      "It might be worth checking out a room," I noted quietly. "I don't know how long the storm will last."
      Corinna's family members nodded and followed me to the door at the other side of the tavern. I made to open the door, but Corinna put a hand on my arm and I paused. "How do you check into a room?" Corinna asked quietly.
      "There should be someone behind a desk. We just ask for a room and then give them the amount of coin they ask for in exchange for one night."
      Corinna held out her hand expectantly. "I'll do it."
      I stared blankly at her open palm for a moment before reaching into my cloak and handing her my small coin pouch.
      Corinna pushed open the door and stepped over the threshold. After motioning for the rest of her family to stay outside, I followed Corinna into the room. The door swung shut behind us and Corinna marched up to the desk. The man sitting at the table scowled as he looked down his nose at her.
      Corinna bowed when she stopped in front of the man. "My master asked me to book a room. How much for one night?"
      The man pointed at me with his thumb. "Is that your master?"
      Corinna nodded. Her head was still bowed. "Yessir."
      The man eyed me up and down. "At least he looks like he has the money. Twenty-five silver coins."
      Corinna fumbled in the leather bag and quickly pulled out the money.
      The man took the coins without a second glance at her. "Room two-ten. Here's the key."
      "Thank you, sir." Corinna bowed before turning and hurrying back to me.
      I gave Corinna a quizzical look as we stepped back into the tavern where her family was waiting.
      Even though my face was hidden, Corinna smiled wryly as she understood my silent question. "I thought that it didn't make sense for you to do the talking. That probably would have blown your cover, no? I don't know much about money, but I know enough to rent a room. What now?"
      I began to make my way toward the stairs at the corner of the tavern. "Let's head up to the room. We can rest there. We can bring up some food and drink as well."
      "That sounds great," Corinna's mother-Meyrah, as she had introduced herself-said. "Cameren can finally get some rest from his injuries."
      When we reached the room, I opened the door for Corinna and the others. The room was fairly small. If anything, it was the size of the house Corinna and her family had been living in. There was a small circular window on the back wall and a bed for one person in the corner.
      Clarity silently helped Meyrah lift Cameren onto the bed before rolling up the cuffs of her brother's trousers to examine the gashes on his legs. She had refused to talk to me for our entire journey so far. But that was fine.
      After taking off my helmet, I shook out my hair and found that it had grown out enough to brush my collarbones. I unfastened my chest plate as well and set the armor down against the wall.
      "I'll go get some food," I announced to no one in particular.
      "I'll come with you," Corinna said as she stepped forward. She had been watching Clarity tend to her brother, but it seemed like Clarity wasn't in need of any assistance.
      As we made our way down the hallway, I suddenly froze.
      "Talon?" Corinna asked quietly as I narrowed my eyes.
      I placed a hand on the hilt of my sword as I scanned the empty hall. I knew this presence. One, two, I counted. Vampires. Two of them.
      "Stay behind me," I cautioned as I took a step forward.
      Footsteps sounded on the creaking stairs. I drew my blade and held it out in front of me as they appeared.
      A male vampire reached the landing first, and his sword was pointed directly at me. His brown hair was pulled back in a loose ponytail, and he was dressed in the outfit of a traveler. A female vampire in a simple dress stood a few feet behind him. She had wavy ginger hair that tumbled all the way to her hips. Neither of them looked any older than their late teens or early twenties, but I knew that they were likely already decades old like myself.
      We just stared each other down in silence for what felt like an eternity until the male blinked, and a look of surprise flashed across his blood-red eyes. "Talon?" he said in disbelief. "Is that you?"
      I could tell that Corinna was just as confused as I was as she looked back and forth between me and the other vampires.
      I angled my head to the side as I continued to point my sword at the vampires across the hall. "How do you know my name?"
      "You don't remember us?" the female vampire asked. She looked slightly put out. "We also attended that conference about Karmen fifty-something years back!"
      The male vampire sheathed his sword and raised his hands. "We're not looking for a fight."
      I still refused to lower my blade. "What are you doing, then?"
      The male held my gaze. "We're looking for the queen of the vampires-we're looking for Karmen."

Chapter Five
       
Karmen? I mouthed as I peeked around Talon's shoulder.
      The female vampire's eyes were bright as she held up her hands as well. "How about we go downstairs together and have a nice friendly chat?"
      Talon turned to look at me. What do you want to do? her eyes read.
      I dipped my head in a small nod. I wasn't getting any malicious intent from the two figures across the hall.
      Talon sheathed her sword, and we walked over to the other vampires. "You two know my name, but I don't know yours."
      "My name is Lynden," the male vampire introduced himself. "And this is Phina."
      "Are those your real names?" Talon asked lightly.
      Both Lynden and Phina blinked.
      "No!" Phina's ginger hair flew as she shook her head energetically. "My name's Josephina, you see, but you can call me Phina."
      Lynden let out an exasperated sigh when Talon turned to him with raised brows. "Lynden is my real name."
      "What about you?" Phina looked at me expectantly.
      I tried my best to muster a smile. "My name's Corinna. It's nice to meet you."
      "She's a friend of mine," Talon said when they looked at her for further explanation. "We have similar destinations in mind so we're traveling together for the time being. We're heading to the capital city."
      "The capital city!" Phina exclaimed excitedly as she tugged at Lynden's sleeve. "We're going there too!"
      I found myself smiling as my initial apprehension faded. The ginger-haired vampire gave off a very similar energy to Chloe-Jane.
      Lynden turned on his heel to head back down the stairs. "Let's go downstairs and talk."
      We found a small table in the corner of the room, and Phina, Talon, and I sat down on the wooden benches.
      "Talon"-Lynden clasped his hands together in front of him after taking a seat next to Phina-"are you still looking for the queen?"
      "No one's heard from you for years," Phina piped up. "We thought she got you."
      "I decided to give up my search," Talon said simply. "But then I recently found the body of a dead vampire in the forest I had confined myself to."
      Phina and Lynden exchanged a glance at that, then Phina leaned forward. The splattering of freckles across her nose was stark against her skin. "We also found the body of a dead vampire-multiple bodies, actually."
      "Each of them had been beheaded in the same way," Lynden said grimly. "We suspected Karmen immediately."
      "What are you going to do when you find Karmen?" I asked. I refused to shrink back as all three vampires turned to look at me.
      "Phina and I were both turned by Karmen." Lynden's tone was flat. "We want to thank her for everything that she's done for us-and then end her so that no one else has to suffer at her hands."
      Talon gave him a sideways look. "That's not going to be an easy task."
      Lynden dropped his gaze, and a sadness flickered behind his eyes. "Even if we die in the process, it will be worth it."
      Talon crossed her arms over her chest as she leaned back in her seat. "Well, you're in luck. It just so happens that I have the same goal as you. But if I were to invite you to travel with us, how would that benefit me and my party?"
      "I've seen the queen's face," Phina said softly. "She can't hide from me."
      Talon blinked in surprise.
      "Both Phina and I once worked for the queen," Lynden explained. His eyes were still downcast. "But only Phina got close enough to Karmen to see her properly."
      "What does the queen of the vampires look like?" I cut in, knowing that Talon was probably wondering the exact same thing.
      "Pale with long brown hair," Phina recalled. "Elegant. Cold. There isn't anything particularly special about her appearance, though. She could go anywhere and blend in without anyone looking twice at her."
      "And that's what makes her terrifying," Lynden concluded heavily. "Karmen hasn't been this active in a long time. We thought she had gone into hiding, but with all the vampires that have been turning up dead in these more recent years, she's clearly up to something."
      "So you can identify Karmen for me"-Talon inclined her head in Phina's direction-"but what can you do for the rest of my group?"
      Lynden lifted his gaze. "We can help protect them."
      "You'd do that?" I looked from Lynden to Phina. "You'd help protect my family?"
      Talon let out a sigh. "I guess it won't hurt to travel together until we reach the capital." Then she eyed the two new vampires suspiciously. "What are you two doing here anyway?"
      "We're looking for someone," Lynden said as if he was somewhat annoyed by the idea. "Have you heard of him? He's known as Storm the Dragonhearted."
      Talon and I exchanged a glance. "I've never heard of him," I said.
      Talon shook her head. "Me neither."
      "Storm is the only known human to have single-handedly killed a vampire," Lynden explained. "He's also rumored to have been taught by a dragon deep inside the mountains. But no one really believes that part."
      "A dragon?" My head snapped up to look at Lynden. "But I thought the dragons went extinct centuries ago."
      "There are still a few," Phina piped up. "In hiding, of course."
      "When we do decide to try to hunt Karmen down," Lynden continued, "someone like Storm will be good to have on our side. After all, a human will come across as less suspicious. And"-Lynden admitted-"Phina and I have never been to the capital city before. We'll need a guide of some sort if we don't want to get picked off by Karmen immediately. According to Phina, Storm's been everywhere at least once."
      "How do you know that this Storm will even agree to work with the two of you?" Talon asked quizzically. "Vampires and humans aren't exactly known for working together."
      "But what if they could?" I said, and everyone turned to look at me again. "I'm working with the three of you right now, aren't I?"
      "You couldn't possibly understand," Lynden said coldly. "When you've been alive as long as us vampires have, you too will be mortified by human nature. Why would we want to work with humans?"
      I held Lynden's gaze and tried my best not to flinch from his icy stare. "I think I might be able to understand. Humans have their flaws. They're influenced by greed and corrupted by power. My family and I were stolen from our homeland. Sometimes the overseers were no better than monsters. Yes, humans can be cruel. None of us are perfect, but not all of us have forgotten morality."
      "Don't you want to get revenge on those who harmed you and your family?" Lynden asked quietly.
      I sighed. "I do. But at the end of the day, my family comes first. I can't spend my life consumed by anger and driven by revenge when I have them to protect."
      There was a long silence before Lynden finally looked away. "Karmen offered us immortality, and we blindly accepted the curse. Now we're all living with the consequences."
      "We can't let the same thing happen to anyone else." Phina's voice was tinged with sadness.
      Talon angled her head to the side. "Let's say Storm does decide to join you-then what? Are you really willing to have him go up against Karmen herself? Are you going to take responsibility for his death too?"
      "Death?" Lynden and Phina exchanged a glance. The former didn't seem very concerned, and the latter appeared as if such a possibility hadn't even crossed her mind.
      "You can't just rope innocent people into your plan," I said, frowning.
      "And what about you?" Lynden challenged. "Why are you going to the capital city anyway?"
      I slumped in my seat. "I just want to save my sister. She's barely fourteen years old and was taken there with a bunch of other girls." Suddenly, my blood went cold. The medicine girl had probably been taken to the capital as well. I hadn't even gotten a chance to see her for a final time.
      Lynden fell silent for a long moment, and his expression was unreadable. "Let us help you, then."
      "I'm sorry?" I blinked, perplexed by the vampire's sudden shift in attitude.
      Phina leaned over. "He had a younger sister once," she said quietly. "A long time ago."
      I opened my mouth to say something, but then a familiar figure approached our table. Her hands were crossed over her chest as she stared down at us coldly. "I was wondering what had been taking you two so long." Clarity frowned distastefully. "I see that you found some new friends." She took a step backward, and a single blink was the only amount of surprise she allowed herself to show. "Vampires."
      I looked up at my sister. "They're going to help us."
      "Help us?" Clarity let out a dry laugh. "Help us find Chloe-Jane? Why would any of these vampires help us?"
      Phina shot to her feet. "We can help!"
      "Corinna"-Clarity turned to me-"let's leave these vampires. I don't trust them."
      I took a deep breath. "We won't last a day on our own, Clarity. They can help us. In fact, they're offering to help."
      "Maybe I'll go off and find Chloe on my own!"
      I opened my mouth to respond, but Talon placed a hand on my arm. "We can discuss this more later," she said quietly as she scanned the tavern with narrowed eyes. I followed Talon's gaze to find that a few heads had turned in our direction. Their eyes were watching my sister. If Clarity realized that she was making a scene, she didn't seem to care.
      "I don't trust you either," Clarity said icily. "I hope I've made that clear, Talon." She dragged out the vampire's name as if the syllables were poisonous.
      Talon's eyes flashed. "Don't trust me, then. But if you go, would you really feel safe leaving your sister in our hands?"
      Clarity looked down at me, and her fiery eyes traveled to the hand Talon was still resting on my arm. Scowling, she turned and marched back the way she had come.
      Talon sighed as she stood up from the table. "We should probably go back too."
      I nodded and rose to my feet as well.
      "Wait." Lynden stopped us. "When are you planning to leave?"
      Talon glanced at him over her shoulder. "Once the storm subsides. Do you know when it's supposed to stop?"
      "Storms like this shouldn't last more than a couple of hours," Lynden informed us with a slight frown. "It will be best to leave at nightfall."
      "We'll wait for you, then." Talon turned and began to walk away. I hurried after her.
      "If we're going to be traveling with Lynden and Phina," I said breathlessly, "we'll need better disguises, don't you think?"
      Talon paused at the back of the crowded room where plates of hot food were being served. "You're right-we really are an interesting-looking party as it is." Talon passed me a couple of plates, and I carefully took them from her.
      As we made our way back up the stairs and along the hallway, an idea suddenly came to me. "We could dress as a group of traveling merchants! Or wait-a troupe!"
      Talon turned to me with bright eyes. "Brilliant! I'll go out and buy us what we need."
      When we reached the room, I knocked three times on the door. There was the sound of feet shuffling, then the door swung open to reveal Clarity.
      I tried my best to put on a smile. "We've brought food."
      Clarity just silently took the plates from me and stepped aside to let Talon and me in. I walked into the room, but Talon remained where she was by the door. When I turned to the vampire, she just smiled faintly. "I'm going to get us the supplies we need," she told me. "I'll be back before dark."
      I nodded. Both Mother and Cameren were fast asleep, but even in sleep, Cameren's expression was pained. We had run out of the medicine for his wounds, and neither Mother, Clarity, nor I knew anything about medicine.
      "Here," Talon said suddenly as she pulled out her coin pouch. "This is for you."
      I just stared blankly at the vampire as she held out the pouch. "I couldn't-"
      Talon glided over and gently pressed the pouch into my hands. "Please, just take it."
      "I-how are you going to get the supplies we need, then?"
      "I'll trade these." Talon gestured to her overseer outfit. "And I'm sure the sword will fetch a high price. There are always wanderers coming in and out of small villages like these-wanderers and adventurers are always looking for a good weapon like this. I'll look for medicine for Cameren, too, while I'm out-I better hurry."
      I lifted a hand in farewell as Talon disappeared down the hall. I quietly closed the door to the room behind me and took a seat on the floor across from Clarity. My stomach gave a loud rumble, and I reached for one of the plates of food. I hadn't even realized how hungry I was until now.
      "Are you sure about this, Corinna?" Clarity asked quietly.
      "I don't know." I sighed before stuffing a piece of bread into my mouth. "Our objective right now is to get Chloe-Jane back. After we do that, it's up to us whether we want to stick with the vampires or not. Even if the vampires have ulterior motives," I said quickly before Clarity could open her mouth, "they will take us to our destination. We've never been outside our village before, let alone the capital city."
      "Let's say we do get Chloe-Jane back." Clarity watched me grab another slice of bread from the plate. "Then what do we do? Where do we go?"
      I raised my head to watch the raging storm outside the small window. "We either could go far away and never look back, or we could stay and try to help."
      "Help? Help who? How do we help?"
      I folded my arms over my chest as I turned back to Clarity. "Help the people who live in this kingdom. Help the people who are trapped in this kingdom. We managed to escape our village with Talon's help. Maybe we can help others the same way she helped us."
      "Talon is a vampire, Corinna. A vampire. She's immortal-invulnerable. She can do whatever she wants without facing any consequences. We're not like that-one wrong move and it's over."
      "I know you're cautious. And rightly so," I said, holding my sister's gaze, "but focusing on right now first, I'm willing to take this risk if it means that we'll be reunited with Chloe. The four of us are together-you, me, Mother, and Cameren. But Chloe? She's alone right now and on her way to the capital city. I wish there was a way we could let her know that we're coming."
      Clarity's eyes softened ever so slightly. "I know. When it comes to the people we love, there is no risk too great to take."
      "Exactly."
      Clarity moved to draw the curtains over the window. "You should get some rest. We've been walking all day."
      I nodded before curling up on the floor next to the bed. If I was being honest, I was afraid that if I were to fall asleep, I'd awake to find myself back in the village. Even though it had always been a fantasy of mine, I had never thought that I would be able to escape from the village, let alone with my family. I just wished our circumstances had been better.
       
~
       
      "Corinna."
      I blinked at the sound of my name. Blinking again, I found Mother standing in front of me.
      "It's time to go."
      "Already?" I was suddenly wide awake. After jumping to my feet, I hurried over to the small window and looked out at the night sky beyond. Just how long had I been sleeping? I turned back to the bed. "Where's Clarity? Where's Cameren? Did Talon find medicine for him?" I asked hopefully.
      Mother shook her head tiredly. "After you fell asleep, I actually met up with Talon and accompanied her to the different shops in the town. All we were able to find were disinfectants. They seemed to help a little bit, but the healer we bought them from warned that Cameren is going to need proper treatment, or else in the next few months, he might find himself unable to walk."
      I just stared at Mother. She had really gone with Talon to the shops? Even though she was weary of the vampire, she had set that fact aside to help Cameren. And Cameren . . . would he really be unable to walk if we couldn't find proper treatment?
      "With the disinfectants, Cameren doesn't seem to be in as much pain as before," Mother reassured me with a soft smile. "Also, the other vampires-Lynden and Phina-the two of them helped him out. They know about basic medicine. They said that with them around, they'd make sure he can walk until we find a proper healer at the capital city."
      "They did?" I was surprised by the new information, but a feeling of relief had washed over me and was slowly calming my anxieties.
      The door opened, and Talon stepped into the room. "Corinna. I was just talking with Phina and Lynden outside."
      I did a double take as I took in her new outfit. Talon was dressed in the long and flowy outfit of a dancer, with her now waist-length hair pulled back into a braid. The outfit was complete with an elegant scarf over her head and silver bracelets jingling at her slender wrists and ankles.
      "Corinna!" Phina peeked around the open door. "We've got a costume for you too!" The ginger-haired vampire was also dressed in a dancer's outfit-the design was the same as Talon's, except the color was a sunny yellow instead of orchid purple.
      Talon grinned as she twirled for me, and her long silk-like skirts flowed around her legs. "The troupe idea was brilliant!" Not only did she have the grace of a dancer, but she also embodied it perfectly.
      I clapped my hands enthusiastically as Talon finished with an elegant curtsey. "Here"-Phina hurried over to me and handed me a dancer outfit as well-"I hope you don't mind being orange."
      "Not at all. Are we all going to be dancers?"
      "Lynden and your mother are dressed as musicians," Phina informed me brightly. "And your brother is going to be the troupe leader!"
      I looked more closely at my mother and found that she was indeed wearing the dress of a traveling musician.
      "We'll let you change." Talon ushered Phina out of the room, and the door swung shut behind them.
      "Where are Clarity and Cameren?" I asked Mother for a second time as I swapped my dress for the dancer's outfit.
      Mother came over to help adjust my headscarf over my hair. "They're finishing up their dinner in the tavern downstairs."
      I nodded my head. Then I frowned as I shifted my weight from foot to foot. My gauzy skirts flowed like water, and the bracelets jingled softly. "Do you think we'll be warm enough in these?" My midriff was almost completely exposed and the light fabric of the outfit wouldn't do much to block out the cold.
      Mother frowned as well. "You'll have a cloak. But if you get cold, I can try and find something warm for you. And if I can't find anything, I can go ask the vampires."
      "If it's only for a night or two, it should be alright," I said with more confidence than I felt. "Chole-Jane would have loved these dancer outfits."
      Mother smiled sadly. "I know. But I'm sure we'll get a chance to tell her about them very soon."
      Suddenly, there was a knock on the door. Before I could walk over to check who was outside, the door swung open and Clarity strode into the room. She was dressed in a forest-green dancer outfit, and her curly hair was pulled away from her face. I had never seen my sister in anything other than her ragged dresses. "Clarity," I started with wide eyes. "You look-"
      "We're leaving," Clarity said shortly. Her dark eyes were steely behind her veil. "We all look ridiculous."
      I ran over to grab my sister's arm before she could leave. "Is everything alright?"
      "I want to know what the vampires are going to want in return," Clarity said under her breath. "They helped Cameren, but for what? These creatures are not like us, Corinna. Do you really think they'll give their services freely?"
      "Clarity, a little trust won't hurt anyone."
      "I can assure you that it can. But I'm not the one who's going to get hurt"-Clarity held my gaze-"it will be you."
      I folded my arms over my chest, and my bracelets clinked softly with the movement. "I'm willing to take that risk if it means that we can be reunited with Chloe. I'm keeping this family together no matter what it takes."
      Even though we were nearly the same height, Clarity still managed to look down her nose at me. "I once was optimistic like you. But where did optimism get me?" Clarity gestured to the long scar running across her abdomen. The wound was visible through the gauzy fabric of her outfit, and I bit my lip as she continued, "As your older sister, it's my job to make sure you don't have to fight for your life the same way I had to for mine."
      I dropped my gaze from Clarity's wound. "I know."
      When we finally left the room, Talon, Phina, Lynden, and Cameren were waiting outside. The four of them turned to look at us as we joined them in the hallway.
      "Let's just hope that we won't actually have to do any dancing," Clarity muttered under her breath.
      I let out a weak laugh. Even so, I was inclined to agree. The only kind of dance I knew was the one where the younger children would jump up and down without any real sense of direction. And while it was plenty of fun, something told me that it wouldn't work here.
      "Here." Lynden handed cloaks to Mother, Clarity, and me. "It's going to be cold."
      "At least we have shoes," I remarked to no one in particular as I fastened the cloak over my shoulders.
      Talon drew the hood of her own cloak before striding toward the stairs. "Follow me."
      When we exited the tavern, I quickened my pace to catch up with her. "We won't really have to dance, will we?"
      A faint smile tugged at Talon's lips. "I don't think so. This was actually a great idea, though-no one is going to report a group of dancers."
      "You were the one who decided to pick the dancer's costumes-now that was a brilliant idea."
      Talon just giggled. At first, I stared at the vampire, but then I found myself laughing too. We walked through the bustling streets of the town as the lanterns next to the path illuminated our way in a warm glow of gold and orange.
      "Hey, pretty girl," a slurred male voice called from the doorway of a small shop further down the path. "I see your dancer outfit. Are you gonna dance for me tonight?"
      My spine prickled unpleasantly. "He isn't talking to us, is he?" I asked Talon under my breath.
      Talon's expression melted into a frown. "Just ignore him."
      We continued down the path and refused to give the drunk man a second glance. As Clarity and Phina passed by the man behind us, he called out again to them, and my spine prickled for a second time.
      "When you were sleeping earlier, Lynden and Phina went out to ask around about Storm," Talon informed me as we made our way farther through the town. "Apparently he just passed through here, and if we hurry we'll be able to catch up with him in the next town. Also, even though I've never heard of him myself, it turns out that this Storm is quite famous."
      "Famous?"
      Talon tapped her chin thoughtfully. "He's a legend among adventures-everyone around here knows his name."
      "If he really is such a legend, wouldn't having him with us attract even more attention?"
      "According to Lynden and Phina, Storm's name is the only thing people really know about the boy himself. While everyone's heard of his adventures, no one can say for sure what he looks like other than that he's a sixteen-year-old with black hair and a sword."
      We walked all night, and when we first reached our destination, Phin asked around about Storm and found out that he had just left hours before we arrived. And so now we were on our way to the next town.
      We reached the town an hour before sunrise; the overcast sky was still dark. As we made our way through the deserted streets, Talon silently gestured in the direction of a large tavern sitting on the corner of the block. Light poured out of the windows, and the faint sound of chatter reached our ears.
      "That would be the place to ask about Storm's whereabouts," Lynden observed as he followed our gaze to the building.
      "What are we waiting for, then?" Phina's anklets jingled as she eagerly rocked back and forth on the balls of her feet. "Let's go!"
      I pushed open the door to the tavern and warmth instantly washed over me. The seven of us squeezed into the tavern to find a large crowd gathered around something or someone in the back of the room.
      Clarity immediately took Mother by the arm and led her to the side of the tavern where hot meals were being served. It seemed like she was eager to get away from the vampires. After watching the two of them for a long moment, I turned back to the crowd. I stood on my tiptoes, but I was too short to see over all the heads. "Excuse me"-I tapped the shoulder of one of the onlookers-"what's going on here?"
      The man turned and eyed me up and down. When he finally decided that I was worth talking to, he leaned over to explain loudly over the buzz of the crowd, "You don't know? Why, that's Storm the Dragonhearted!"
      I turned to Talon with wide eyes. The vampire nodded; she had heard it too.
      I tried and failed to squeeze past the crowd. "There's just too many people here-we'll never be able to talk to Storm at this rate."
      "I have an idea," Talon said suddenly. "Leave it to me." Talon just flashed me a smile in response to my bewildered expression. A moment later, she gracefully leaped up onto an empty table in the opposite corner of the room. As I looked on, Talon began to dance. She was an orchid swaying in the wind as she tapped her feet and twirled her wrists. Her bracelets and anklets chimed as she danced to a rhythm of her own creation.
      It didn't take long for the crowd to migrate to Talon's corner of the room, and soon the sound of clapping and cheering filled the tavern as she twirled faster and faster. She was a whirl of purple silk, and her inky black hair had come loose from its braid.
      "Corinna"-Phina tugged at my sleeve-"Talon created an opportunity. Let's go talk to Storm." I followed Lynden and Phina to the back of the tavern where a teenage boy at least a year younger than myself was trying in vain to get his crowd back. He had raven-black hair and a sword at his side just as Talon had said.
      "Hey!" The dark-haired boy called peevishly at the crowd of people watching Talon dance. "I didn't finish telling you about how I single-handedly stopped the bandits and-"
      Lynden cut him off. "Are you Storm?"
      The dark-haired boy puffed out his chest. "Of course I'm Storm." Then he blinked, and his eyes narrowed as his gaze traveled from Lynden to Phina and then back again. "Vampires!" Storm's hand was on the hilt of his sword in an instant.
      But before he could draw the blade, Phina's hand was suddenly on top of Storm's. "I wouldn't do that," Phina said brightly. "We're not here to hurt you."
      Storm frowned as he looked at Phina. He opened his mouth as if to say something but then quickly closed it again as he rapidly shook his head.
      "We would like your assistance," Lynden implored, even though something about his tone suggested he'd rather not have to deal with the dark-haired boy. "We've heard about you and your accomplishments."
      "I'm flattered," Storm said stiffly. "But why would I help you?" He was still trying to draw his blade, but Phina's hand was preventing him from doing so.
      I stepped forward. "Isn't helping people what heroes like yourself do?"
      "Well, of course." Storm looked over at me. "You're a human."
      "Yes, I am."
      "What are you doing with these vampires?" Then his eyes widened, and he pointed a knowing finger at me as if he had just figured it out. "I know! These vampires have taken you captive, and you need me to help-"
      "No." I shook my head in exasperation. "It just so happens that we're working together."
      Storm furrowed his brow. "Working together?"
      Cameren took a step forward to join in our conversation. He offered Storm a friendly smile. "Please, we need your help. My youngest sister was taken to the capital city and we need to get her back. You're a legend. If anyone can help us, it's Storm the Dragonhearted."
      "Of course I can help," Storm said enthusiastically. "I am a legend!"
      Out of the corner of my eye, I saw Clarity and Mother exchange a look as they watched us.
      "Hey." Phina placed her hands on her hips. "We came to you because you are the best person for the job!"
      Storm folded his arms over his chest as he finally gave up on his sword. "I'm not talking to you, vampire."
      Phina just turned her chin to the air and crossed her arms as well.
      "Will you really help us?" I asked uncertainly.
      Storm nodded. "Helping people is my calling. And if there's one thing I'm good at, it's using a sword. Besides, I'd be going against my teachings if I didn't help those who need my assistance."
      "Teachings?" Cameren asked curiously. "Who taught you?"
      "My uncle," Storm said proudly. "He's the one who taught me everything I know."
      "Impressive," a voice said from behind me, and I turned to find Talon standing at my side.

Chapter Six
       
"Another vampire!" Storm reached for his sword, but he dropped his hand at the look Phina gave him.
      Corinna lowered her voice as she took a step closer to Storm. "Look, these vampires are on a mission to kill Karmen, the queen of the vampires."
      Kill the queen of the vampires? Storm mouthed in shock.
      "Have you heard of Queen Karmen?" Corinna asked quickly.
      Storm paled. "Of course I've heard of Queen Karmen. And I've heard enough about her to know that she isn't someone I should ever cross. I know that's a fight I won't be able to walk away from alive. I have no reason to cross her, nor do I want to."
      "Will you at least help us get our sister back?" Cameren asked.
      "That I can do." Then Storm frowned again. "You aren't really a troupe, are you?"
      I shook my head. "No, it's just that we're already a very suspicious-looking group. Disguises are our best option if we don't want to draw negative attention."
      "You're on your way to the capital city," Storm said.
      "That's correct." I took a step forward. Storm flinched at my approach but didn't move back.
      "Seeing that you haven't killed me already"-Storm's gaze traveled from me to Lynden to Phina-"I have a place we can stay while we prepare for our trip to the capital."
      "Really?" Corinna's eyes lit up. "Where's that?"
      "At my uncle's," Storm said matter-of-factly. "I'm actually on my way home right now, and if you really want me to help out, you'll have to follow me up the mountain first. My uncle is expecting me. When I take you to him, he can determine whether you vampires are trustworthy or not."
      "You'll really take us to your uncle?" Phina asked excitedly.
      I watched Lynden and Phina out of the corner of my eye; there was something about them that I couldn't put my finger on. Even though Corinna seemed to be comfortable around them, I didn't trust them. They had both admitted that they had worked for Karmen in the past, and I couldn't help wondering if they were hiding something. Even though Phina's energy and cheerfulness seemed to be embedded in her personality, she still seemed far too eager to meet Storm's uncle.
      Then it hit me. Maybe it wasn't Storm they had been so desperate to meet. Maybe it was his uncle all along. And that led to another question entirely.
      "Storm," I said lightly. "How old is your uncle?"
      Storm's head snapped over to me. "Why do you want to know?"
      "Is he immortal?" If Storm's uncle was really immortal, it only made sense that Phina and Lynden would want to ask him about Karmen.
      Storm stiffened. "He is."
      "I see." A small smile played around the corners of my lips; my suspicions were confirmed.
      Corinna turned to me in confusion, but I just shook my head. I'd tell her about my thoughts once we separated from Lynden and Phina.
      Storm ran an agitated hand through his dark hair. "When do you want to leave? It's nearly morning, and I assume you vampires won't be able to travel during the day."
      "We'll be fine if the sky is as overcast as it was yesterday," Lynden said flatly.
      Storm held up his hands in defense. "Fine." Then he turned to Corinna. "I don't think you'll want to wear that dancer outfit. My uncle lives in the mountains where the temperatures are below freezing in the winter. Besides, we won't be using the main road, so no one will stop us on the way."
      Corinna looked at me again.
      "I'll buy new outfits for the journey," I reassured her.
      Corinna turned back to Storm, and her eyes sparkled with determination. "We should leave as soon as possible-I need to get my sister back before anything happens to her."
      Storm nodded.
      "I'll go buy some clothes," I announced. "The shops and vendors are probably opening up soon."
      "I'll come with you," Corinna said quickly.
      I blinked. "You don't want to stay in the tavern? It's warmer here than it is outside."
      "I've never been out of my village before. I want to look around and explore as much as possible."
      I found myself smiling. "Alright." Then I turned to address Storm and the others. "We'll meet you back here in an hour or so."
      As we made our way out the door, Corinna glanced back at where Clarity and Meyrah were now eating together at one of the many tables. Meyrah looked up from her plate and offered Corinna a warm smile. Clarity, on the other hand, ignored her sister.
      As we made our way down the roughly paved streets, Corinna observed our surroundings. "It's a lot quieter than I expected." The fluttering of her vibrant orange veils in the light wind were a stark contrast to the gray and brown of the buildings.
      "It's early right now," I explained as I glanced around. "It will probably get a lot busier in the afternoon. You've got to be careful, though," I continued as we made our way down another block. "There are always people on the lookout for young women who might fetch a high price."
      "Even here under the eyes of the knights from the capital?"
      I nodded. "The old king kept turning a blind eye to the issue. I doubt the new king will be any better."
      Suddenly, I sensed another human presence lurking in the dark space between two houses. I placed a warning hand on Corinna's shoulder and we stopped walking.
      "Who's there?" I called. My eyes narrowed.
      "Oh ho," a rough male voice said in amusement. "Looks like I've been noticed." A masked man emerged from the shadows, and his footsteps echoed loudly. The man held a long coil of rope in one hand and an unusual knife in the other.
      The masked man eyed me up and down. His gaze lingered unpleasantly on my exposed stomach and then traveled even lower. I stepped in front of Corinna before the man could scrutinize her as well.
      "Entertainers," the man purred. "Looks like I got lucky today."
      I just glared at him silently. There was a quiet rustling from behind me as Corinna reached shakily for the dagger she had stashed behind her skirts.
      "You, little missy"-the man wagged a finger at me- "you can probably fetch a very high price. I bet even the king himself would pay to get his hands on a beauty like yourself. And you"-he looked over my shoulder at Corinna-"I bet if I sold you to one of the farms nearby, they would be quite happy to gain another worker. There's been lots of talk about runaway slaves lately." The man casually took a step forward. "I wonder if you might be one of them."
      The scent of Corinna's fear shoved its way up my nose as the man continued to advance.
      The man chuckled. "That's right-running will just make things more difficult for all of us. Now, be a good girl and . . ." the man trailed off as he noticed the dagger glinting in Corinna's shaking hand. "Give me that!"
      The man lunged forward. In one swift movement, I pushed Corinna back, and in another, I kicked the man firmly in the chest.
      The man flew backward and crashed into the cobblestone wall of a house with a thud. But despite just being thrown against a wall, within moments he was back on his feet, coughing. Bellowing in rage, he raised his knife as he broke into a full-out run.
      I countered him with ease. I ducked under his blade before grabbing his arm and throwing him with all my inhuman strength. The man crashed into the wall again and slid to the ground. This time he did not rise again.
      "Is-is he dead?" Corinna whispered.
      I walked over to examine the man's body. I nudged him with my foot, and he let out a pained groan. "He's fine."
      "Are you okay?" Corinna hurried over to my side, still eyeing the man apprehensively.
      I gave her a reassuring smile as I nodded.
      Corinna let out a shaky breath. Then she stared down at the dagger she was still clutching tightly in her trembling hand. "Talon"-she bit her lip-"I was scared. I was really scared. Not because I thought that you couldn't beat that man in a fight, but because of the fact that I'm holding a weapon, and I don't even know how to use it. I don't know how to defend myself. If you weren't here, I would have definitely been apprehended and taken to who knows where." Corinna lifted her eyes to meet mine. "Could you teach me how to defend myself?"
      "Okay."
      "Okay?" Corinna blinked. "Just like that?"
      I smiled as I bent down to pick up the knife the man had dropped at my feet. This sort of blade would fetch a hefty price. "I don't see why not."
      Corinna's eyes lit up as she broke out into a smile. "Thank you!"
      "What's going on out here?" a woman's voice asked. A middle-aged couple had come out of their house, and it seemed like it was too much to hope that no one would notice the ruckus I'd made.
      I quickly snatched the dagger from Corinna's hand and hid it with the knife I had just picked up behind my skirts. I dropped to my knees and pressed a hand to my face as if I were crying. Corinna quickly followed my lead. She sniffled as she dropped down next to me in a jangle of bracelets and orange silk.
      I heard the woman let out a gasp as she noticed the body.
      "Good heavens," the husband exclaimed.
      "What happened here?" the woman asked faintly.
      "Sir, ma'am," I said between sobs, "we were just walking down the street, minding our own business when that man tried to attack us."
      "Are you two girls alright?" the woman hurried over to us in concern. "What happened to the man?"
      "Someone saved us," I sniffled. "I couldn't see their face, but they knocked the man out and then disappeared." Corinna nodded along, wide-eyed.
      The woman inhaled sharply. "Could it have been Storm the Dragonhearted? I heard that he just arrived in town. I didn't really think that teenager would actually have the skill, but maybe I'm wrong."
      "Look, dear." The husband pointed to the coil of rope still in the masked man's hand. "This man was planning something bad. These girls are lucky to have been saved from whatever he was planning to do with them."
      "You girls should hurry along," the woman insisted worriedly. "We'll turn this man over to the local guards."
      I bowed my head, still wiping fake tears from my eyes. "Thank you, ma'am. We'll be on our way."
      I climbed to my feet and we hurried down the street. Corinna let out a breath when we finally came to a stop. "That was a close one."
      "On a different note"-I looked up at the building we had halted in front of-"we've arrived." A bell jingled as I gently pushed the door open.
      "Welcome," a woman called from behind the counter at the back of the spacious room. "What can I do for you ladies today?"
      "Eight sets of traveling wear"-I counted on my fingers-"and seven cloaks."
      "Sure thing," the woman said with a nod as she scribbled down my request with a feathered quill. "I'll need a name to go with the order."
      "Falon," I said lightly.
      The woman set her quill down. "Alright, Miss Falon. Please wait here-I'll be right back." The door swung shut behind her with a soft click, and I was left alone with Corinna in the front of the store.
      Corinna arched a quizzical brow. "Miss Falon?"
      I laughed. "The name Falon sounds less intimidating, don't you think?"
      The two of us walked around the small shop and examined the various mannequins and their outfits. Corinna leaned forward to run a light finger over the rich fabric of one of the dresses. She frowned slightly. "I know what these are made out of."
      "It's practically everywhere now," I said grimly.
      Corinna fell silent, deep in thought.
      The door at the back of the room opened a few minutes later, and the woman stepped out with a pile of clothes in her arms. "Altogether this is fifty silver pieces."
      After I traded the masked-man's knife for our gear, Corinna and I left the shop.
      "That was brilliant!" Corinna grinned once the doors had swung shut behind us. "Did you take that man's knife because you knew you could trade it for the clothes?"
      I nodded, and a wry smile played on my lips. "We can thank the masked man for paying today."
      Corinna laughed again, and her eyes sparkled behind her veils. "Brilliant!"
       
~
       
      I dropped the pile of clothes on the table our companions were huddled around.
      "Which outfit is mine?" Clarity asked stiffly. "I want to change out of this as soon as possible."
      "They're all pretty much the same," Corinna said tiredly. "Just pick one."
      Clarity picked up one of the outfits before standing up from the table and marching to the back room to change out of her dancer outfit.
      "Are we just about ready to go?" Storm spoke up from where he was sitting uncomfortably between Cameren and Phina. He was leaning as far away from the ginger-haired vampire as he could.
      "Change first, and then we'll meet outside," Lynden said flatly.
      "I need to change too?" Storm asked defiantly.
      "I think it would be better for all of us to be wearing the same thing," Phina pointed out. "If you're the only one who stands out, it will look like you've got quite a lot of followers or personal guards-"
      "Fine, fine."
      Ten minutes later, all of us were standing outside the tavern. We were all dressed in dark-colored travel outfits with cloaks fastened over our shoulders. Then we followed Storm down the snow-covered road.
      Once we were out of town, Storm turned to look over his shoulder. "Just for your information, my uncle hasn't had visitors in ages, and I'm not sure how he'll react."
      Lynden's expression was icy. "That's fine. If he wants to fight, I'll be more than happy to take him on."
      "No one's going to be fighting-" Phina peeped, but Storm cut her off.
      "What makes you think that you could even beat my uncle in a fight?"
      "Your uncle might be immortal," Lynden said coolly, "but he'll definitely be outnumbered. In case you've forgotten, Phina, Talon, and I are also immortal."
      "Who said I was going to help you?" I asked. "I have neither the obligation nor desire to pick a fight."
      Lynden's head snapped to me, but he fell silent all the same.
      Phina wrung her hands together, and the vibrant ginger color of her hair shone starkly against her dull gray cloak. "I don't think fighting is a good idea. Talking things out is a much better way to settle a dispute, no?"
      At least one out of the two vampires seemed to think sensibly.
      "My uncle is very reasonable," Storm said quickly, following up on Phina's statement. "If you really don't want to see my uncle, just stay upstairs while I talk to him myself."
      "And what if he does want to pick a fight?" Clarity spoke up.
      "He won't." Storm's frown deepened. "Look, do you want my help or not?"
      "Don't listen to them," Cameren reassured Storm. "Lead the way. We're right behind you."
      Storm turned back to the road. "Anyway, it's at least a two-day's walk to get to my uncle's place. He lives at the top of a mountain after all."
      "That's certainly an interesting place to live," Cameren remarked. "I guess it's a great place to be if you don't want anyone bothering you."
      "The mountains are great," Storm said enthusiastically. He had warmed up considerably more to Corinna's family than to the vampires. "Even though it's cold most of the year, the view is amazing."
      As we continued further away from the town, the cobblestone road eventually turned into a dirt trail. We had been walking for hours, and the sky was getting progressively darker. Getting caught in the middle of a blizzard wouldn't be ideal, especially for Cameren. Lynden and Phina had temporarily saved his injuries from infection, but he was still in desperate need of treatment.
      My inky hair whipped around in the wind as we trekked through the snow. I couldn't feel the cold, but my human companions certainly could. Corinna had wrapped her cloak tightly around herself and pulled her hood over her bushy hair. Clarity had done the same, and her expression was a permanent grimace. I watched Corinna's mother shiver and pull her cloak tighter around her dangerously thin body.
      "Ma'am." I slowed my pace to walk side by side with Meyrah. My voice was quiet. "Please take my cloak."
      Meyrah looked at me wearily. "I-I couldn't."
      I unfastened my cloak and held it out for Corinna's mother to take. "You need it more than I do. The cold doesn't bother me."
      Phina hurried over to a very surprised Cameren. "You can have my cloak!" she said as she dropped it into his arms. Then she snatched Lynden's cloak and danced it over to Clarity.
      "Are you going to be alright?" I asked quietly as Corinna walked over to me.
      Corinna smiled weakly. "I'm used to the cold."
      After a while, Storm announced, "Let's stop for a lunch break. I can build a fire if one of you can collect some wood. And later on, there's an abandoned farmhouse further down the road we can take shelter in when night falls." When Clarity gave him a disbelieving look, he added, agitatedly, "It's perfectly safe. I stay there each time I travel to and from my uncle's house."
      "I can collect the wood," Corinna offered. "I think my hands and feet will freeze if I sit in the same place for too long."
      "I'll go with you," I said.
      Storm dropped the satchel he had been carrying on the snow-covered ground before taking a seat next to it. "Great, we'll be here resting."
      Clusters of dead-looking trees surrounded the path, and I followed Corinna through the sludgy snow. When we were far enough away from the rest of our group, Corinna looked at me. "When will you start teaching me how to protect myself with a weapon?"
      "When do you want me to teach you?" I asked lightly as I reached down to collect fallen twigs and branches.
      "As soon as possible would be ideal. From the way you countered the masked man, you seem to know a lot about self defense," Corinna noted as she picked fallen branches from the ground. "Were you a knight of some sort before you became a vampire?"
      "A knight?" I let out a laugh. "No. I knew some knights once, but most of these things I only learned after I was turned. Once we reach Storm's uncle's place, I'll show you some routines."
      Corinna's eyes were bright as she beamed. "Thank you!"
      We returned to the rest of our group, and Storm got to work starting a fire. After lunch, we were back on our feet and continuing on our way. As the gray sky gradually grew darker, the abandoned farmhouse Storm had mentioned appeared.
      "We'll rest here for tonight," Storm told us as we veered off the path and made a beeline for the building. "If we wake before sunrise tomorrow, we can make it to my uncle's place before the sun sets. I'll make another fire." Storm set his bag down when we entered the large barn. "When I finish, I can take the first watch."
      I turned to look at him. "I can stand guard."
      "We'll guard too." Phina gestured to Lynden and herself. "The more eyes, the better."
      Storm stifled a yawn, too tired to object. "Fine. But if you kill me in my sleep, my uncle will murder all of you when he finds out I'm dead."
      I watched Corinna and her family huddle around the fire together. They talked quietly before eventually nodding off to sleep. I didn't know how I felt about leaving Storm with them, but I doubted the dark-haired boy would do anything to hurt them.
      As I walked outside, I found myself eyeing my fellow vampires. I needed to keep a close eye on the two of them. Phina's name hadn't rung any bells, but when we first met the vampires, something about the name Lynden had sounded familiar. I just couldn't recall where I had heard it.
      I frowned and furrowed my brow as I tried in vain to remember.
      "Is everything alright, Talon?" Phina asked worriedly.
      I looked at the ginger-haired vampire. "I want to ask you something. Do you know when exactly Lynden was turned?"
      Phina pursed her lips, deep in thought. "If I remember correctly, I think it was nearly a hundred years ago."
      A hundred years ago. That must have been around the same time I was turned.
      "Why do you want to know?" Phina inquired as she tilted her head to the side like a curious puppy. Her blood-red eyes glowed in the inky night.
      I twirled a strand of my long hair around my finger. "I've heard his name before. It was around the time I was turned into a vampire."
      Phina looked surprised. "You still remember that far back? I can't remember much of my life before I was turned." Sadness flicked across her face. "Sometimes I can't remember who I was or who I was loved by."
      I looked up at the night sky. "Sometimes I think back to the past. Sometimes I choose to forget it. But even when I do manage to forget, it always comes back eventually. No matter how hard I try, some things can't be forgotten that easily. Some things aren't meant to be forgotten."
      Phina nodded her head. "I know what you mean."
      We fell silent, and there was a long pause in which neither of us said anything.
      Finally, the ginger-haired vampire gave me a smile. "I'll go check in on Lynden. He's probably worrying about me."
      "Wait," I said. "Do you trust Lynden?"
      Phina blinked. "Of course!" Then her expression melted into a sad smile. "I hope you can come to trust him too. He may come across as cold, but at the end of the day, he's just been broken like the rest of us." And with that said, Phina turned and skipped away.
       
~
       
      The next day, we were back on our feet and continuing down the snow-covered road. Our journey became a steady ascent as we reached the towering mountains at the far corner of the inner kingdom.
      "It's a good thing that the weather is better today," Corinna noted from where she was walking next to me.
      I nodded. Even though it wasn't snowing, the sky was still clouded over, and the sun hadn't shown its face in days.
      "Come to think of it," Corinna said quietly, "you never told me why you wanted to know if Storm's uncle was immortal."
      I looked around at the mountains surrounding us. We were nearly at the summit. "Think about it-Storm got the title Storm the Dragonhearted for a reason."
      Corinna sucked in a breath. "Are you telling me that his uncle really is a dragon?"
      "I think it's a safe assumption," I said lightly. Suddenly I paused.
      I remembered now.
      Lynden. A hundred years ago, there had been an incident where a single vampire had slaughtered a duke and his family in one of the eastern kingdoms-and that vampire's name was Lynden.

Chapter Seven
       
Dragon.
      The word echoed in my suddenly empty head. That can't be possible, I thought. Weren't the dragons hunted to extinction centuries ago?
      I turned back to Talon but found that the vampire had fallen silent. Her expression was unreadable.
      "Is everything alright?" I asked quietly.
      "I just remembered something," Talon said darkly. "Have you ever heard about the downfall of the Winfielde's duchy?"
      I shook my head in bewilderment.
      "If I recall correctly, the duchy was governed by a very well-off family," Talon explained. "Since slaves only became big in the western kingdoms about twenty-five years ago, they had a lot of indentured servants at their estate. One day the entire family was found dead. Well, their bodies had been difficult to identify at first-all of them had been torn to shreds."
      My stomach churned. "Was there a reason that provoked such an attack?"
      "I don't know. But the person behind the murders wasn't human. They were a vampire."
      "I don't think I understand-"
      "That vampire is with us right now."
      My eyes widened as my head snapped over to watch Lynden and Phina. The two vampires were walking at the front of the group, talking quietly among themselves. "Who?" I whispered.
      "Lynden," Talon said grimly.
      "Lynden?"
      Talon's expression was grave. "We're traveling with dangerous people. And as of now, we don't know what they're capable of."
      "Even if that's the case," I said slowly, "both Lynden and Phina have made their intentions clear; they want to try to take down Queen Karmen."
      "You're right. If they wanted to hurt us, they would have already."
      "Besides," I continued quietly, "it probably isn't a good idea to ask Lynden about the incident. If he wants us to know, he'll tell us himself."
      Talon nodded.
      "Look," I said suddenly. As we rounded the corner, a wooden structure slowly came into view. The two-story building had been built into the side of the mountain and was completely hidden from view of anyone who would observe the stretch of mountains from afar.
      "Here we are," Storm said proudly.
      "Just in time too," Phina added. The sun had just begun to set, and the gray sky was growing darker by the minute.
      I pulled my cloak tighter around my body as we drew closer. On closer inspection, the wooden structure looked like a very normal house. If this really was where Storm lived, where was his uncle? From what I had heard about dragons, I was positive that one would not be able to fit into a house of any sort. Dragons were said to have been the size of houses, with great wings even larger than that.
      When we reached the house, Storm pushed open the door before beckoning us into the room beyond. Warmth washed over me the moment I stepped inside. It thawed my frozen body, and I looked around the room in awe. The room looked ordinary aside from large glass windows revealing a gorgeous view of the sky.
      "Hey," Storm called out, stopping us before we could move further into the house. "Remember to take your shoes off before walking around. I'd rather not have to clean up your dirty shoe prints later."
      I quickly slipped off my boots and set them down by the door.
      "Well, what are you all waiting for?" Storm pushed open a wooden door at the other end of the room. "You can either stay here in the house or come with me to greet my uncle."
      I walked over to Storm and peered into the darkness beyond the rectangular opening in the wall. All I could make out were the first few steps of a stone staircase leading down into the heart of the mountain. Of course Storm's uncle didn't live in the house on top of the mountain. The dragon lived inside the mountain itself.
      Storm picked up a lantern before leading the way into the dark. "If you want to come with me, hurry up."
      I watched apprehensively as Storm began his descent. His lantern was the only source of light. Lynden and Phina quickly stepped onto the staircase to follow Storm into the depths of the mountain. Clarity, Cameren, and Mother were next, and the former helped the others down the steps.
      "Are you scared?" Talon asked softly from behind me. "You don't have to go."
      I turned to face her. "I'd be a fool if I wasn't afraid. But have you ever met a dragon before?"
      Talon's eyes were gentle as she offered me a smile. "I haven't, but there's a first time for everything, right? Besides," she reassured me, "even though their appearance may be intimidating, dragons are said to be gentle and wise creatures."
      "I'll take your word for it then. I've been curious to see a real dragon." I turned back to the doorway and the looming darkness beyond. After taking a deep breath, I stepped onto the stairs.
      Even though the steps were made of stone, there seemed to be a heat in them that seeped through my socks and warmed my feet. I could sense Talon walking a few paces behind me, and her presence calmed my nerves.
      From somewhere far ahead, Storm's voice echoed off the stone. "We're nearly there," he said. "Do you see that light ahead?"
      I quickened my pace, with one hand pressed against the cool stone wall so as to not trip in the blinding darkness. Just as Storm had said, as we went further down, a light at the end of the tunnel blossomed into existence.
      "Storm!" a deep voice rumbled. "You are back!"
      "Uncle!" Storm's voice said excitedly.
      "My dear boy," the voice rumbled again. "Look at yourself! You have become so skinny! Have you lost weight?"
      I jumped down the last couple of steps and held my breath as I rounded the corner. My eyes widened as I took in the sight before me. I was standing in a large cavern illuminated by hundreds of glowing lanterns. The ceiling of the cavern seemed to stretch infinitely and the sound of the bubbling stream that ran along its far side echoed through it. Vines snaked up the walls, and their green and oranges gave the cavern a homey feeling.
      But out of everything in the cavern, the dragon himself was the most breathtaking. He was covered in green scales flecked with gold and stood the size of a house-maybe even multiple houses. He had magnificent gold-amber eyes, and his leathery wings were folded neatly at his sides.
      Lynden, Phina, and my family had frozen in place with their mouths open in a mixture of shock and awe.
      Storm crossed his arms over his chest as his uncle looked at him. "I'm not that skinny."
      "I see that you have brought guests," the dragon said good-naturedly as he turned to survey the rest of us. "It would be rude of me if I did not introduce myself."
      Storm gave us a sideways glance. "Oh yeah, I picked them up along the way. They said they needed my help, and since I told them you were expecting me to return, they could rest in the house upstairs. I think all of them were curious to meet their host."
      "I hope the journey here was bearable," the dragon said as he addressed us. "When Storm is away from home too long, he tends to forget his manners. I am Andreus-Storm's uncle."
      "Hello," Phina squeaked excitedly. "This is Lynden, Clarity, Cameren, Meyrah, Corinna, and Talon. Oh, and I'm Phina."
      Andreus's large eyes swept over us. "Vampires. And people from the southern continent. A very rare combination, if I do say so myself. Tell me, what brings you here?"
      "We're here because we need help taking down Karmen, the queen of the vampires," Lynden said. His observant eyes watched the dragon's every move.
      Even though Andreus towered over us, Clarity still managed to look down her nose at the dragon, not intimidated in the slightest. If she was nervous, she hid it well. "We're here because we need help saving my sister."
      Andreus blinked in mild amusement. "And what made all of you decide to work together?"
      "We suspect that Karmen is in the capital city," Phina piped up. "Originally Lynden and I were going to go there by ourselves, but then we ran into Talon. We figured that Talon would be interested in hunting down the queen, but she happened to be traveling with a group of humans. And now all of us are traveling together!"
      "Why do you want to hunt down the queen?" Andreus asked lightly.
      Phina and Lynden exchanged a glance, but it was Talon who spoke up. "We have our personal reasons."
      "Does one of you want to take over as ruler of the vampires?"
      "No," Lynden said shortly. "Karmen was the one who turned us. It only makes sense for us to be the ones to stop her for good so no one else has to suffer at her hands."
      Phina folded her slender arms over her chest as she nodded in agreement. "Karmen is dangerous. Who knows what will happen if she continues to stick around."
      Talon walked over to stand at my side. "Karmen has been killing vampires."
      Andreus sighed. "I know."
      "You do?" Storm's eyes were wide with surprise. "Uncle, why didn't you tell me about this?"
      The dragon sighed again, heavily this time. "Storm, you and I both know that the queen of the vampires is someone you should never cross. I did not wish to alarm you with the news."
      "I-" Storm started, but then he fell silent at the tired look his uncle gave him.
      "I do not know what Karmen is planning to do," Andreus said as he turned back to us, "but what I do know is that the queen could be worried that her death is drawing near."
      "Her death?" Talon asked quickly.
      "Have you heard of the ancient prophecy and the legend of the four queens?"
      Talon shook her head. Lynden and Phina looked equally bewildered.
      "The prophecy states that four queens will rise up and change the known world forever," Andreus recalled. "By the end of the ninth century, all four queens will return to the earth in eternal slumber, their duty fulfilled."
      "Is Karmen one of the four queens?" Lynden asked sharply.
      Andreus adjusted his great wings. "I think it is safe to assume that Karmen herself thinks that she is one of them."
      Phina furrowed her brow. "The ninth century." Then her eyes widened in realization. "It's the ninth century now, isn't it? Year zero was when the last of the ancient magics were eliminated."
      "If I remember correctly," I spoke up, my voice a lot stronger than I felt, "it's year eight-eleven."
      Storm frowned. "Eight-eleven. So there are just about ninety years left until she dies."
      "We do not know for certain if Karmen is one of the four queens from the prophecy," Andreus said lightly. "But then again, we do not know any other queens, do we?"
