      "Karmen must believe in whatever this prophecy is," Talon said quietly. "That's why she's taking action now-to prevent it from happening."
      Phina tapped her chin, deep in thought. "But then what does that have to do with killing vampires?"
      "Maybe she thinks a vampire is going to cause her death?" Storm offered. "And if that's the case, maybe she wants to kill them all before they get to her?"
      Lynden's frown deepened. "Vampires are the only ones who have a chance at taking down the queen. No human would stand a chance against her."
      "Queen Karmen despises both humans and vampires alike," Phina said solemnly. "It's her hatred for this world that continues to make her one of the most dangerous creatures that have ever set foot on it. I don't think she'll die that easily."
      "And this is why we need to find her," Lynden concluded with a sigh. "After she finishes with the vampires, I fear she'll turn on the humans."
      Clarity gave Lynden a sideways look. "Don't tell me that you actually want to stop her for the sake of us humans? I thought you felt that humans are unworthy."
      Lynden's blood-red eyes flashed. "I do. But even so, there are still innocent people out there who don't deserve such a fate. You despise humans as well, don't you, Clarity? You hate what you had to go through to keep your family safe-to keep your family alive. And yet you still know that there are people out there who still deserve a better future. I can see it all on your face."
      Clarity's eyes were steely. "It's funny how in a world of monsters, the human can be the most monstrous of them all."
      "Exactly," Lynden said quietly, and traces of sadness flickered across his face.
      Andreus looked at my family and me. His large glassy eyes reflected the lanterns' glow. "You must be exhausted from your journey. It is getting late. You should have Storm show you upstairs. We have a vacant bedroom."
      I bowed to the dragon. "Thank you for everything."
      Andreus inclined his head. "I will light the stairs for you now. Since I did not want to ruin my nephew's grand reveal, I did not light them up earlier."
      Storm let out a yawn. "We'll start preparing for our trip to the capital city tomorrow. I'll show you where you can stay for the night."
      "Have Storm get you something to eat as well," Andreus called after us as we turned to leave the cavern. "All of you could definitely do with some food." Suddenly, there was a flash of fiery light as every torch lining the walls of the stone staircase burst to life.
      "You have one interesting uncle," Cameren said weakly as we made our way back up the stairs.
      "He is interesting," Storm agreed. "He's old and big and tries his best not to set the house on fire. But that aside, he's the best uncle anyone could ever ask for. If it weren't for him, I probably would have died years ago."
      "Died?" Cameren asked in mild surprise.
      "My uncle's the one who found me," Storm explained as we continued our climb upward. His inky hair practically absorbed the light from the flickering torches. "I had no choice but to run away from my village when I was five years old. My uncle took it upon himself to raise me after that."
      "Is Andreus the one who gave you the name Storm?" Cameren inquired curiously.
      Storm shook his head. "No. Actually, I came up with the name. My father was a horrible man, you see. My mother died because of him. And if I hadn't run away, I probably wouldn't have lived very long. Anyway, my father named me after himself. I couldn't stand that name, so I changed it."
      "Oh." Cameren fell silent.
      "Uncle found me in the middle of a forest," Storm went on, lost in remembrance. "He asked me if I was lost and if I needed help finding my way back home. I told him that I had no home, and everything just kind of happened after that."
      "You weren't afraid of the dragon?" Lynden questioned.
      Storm's eyes darkened at that. "Between the dragon and my father, I would pick the dragon any day. Besides, after people meet him, who would actually be afraid of my uncle?"
      Before I knew it, we were back in the house. Storm led us to the second level, then directed us to the door at the end of the hallway.
      "We only have one extra bedroom," the dark-haired boy told us as we halted in front of the door. "I'm going to bed, so the seven of you work it out between yourselves. Oh," he added, "there's probably some sort of food downstairs if you're hungry." And with that said, Storm marched back down the hallway and disappeared into another room. There was a loud thud as he shut the door behind him.
      "The four of you can take the room." Talon gestured to my family and me. "Vampires don't need sleep. If you need anything, we'll either be downstairs or outside."
      I nodded my head. Clarity pushed open the door to the room, and Mother and I followed her inside. Cameren had gone back downstairs so Lynden and Phina could check on his injuries.
      "Clarity and I can sleep on the floor," I said as I turned to my sister.
      Mother nodded her head. "When Cameren gets here, he can have the bed."
      Clarity just glanced around the room. "I'll go look around for extra blankets."
      The room was fairly small, with one bed next to the window in the corner. But it was warm, and though I was confident Andreus himself didn't come into the house above his cave, the room was completely free of dust.
      I lay down on the floor after pulling off my cloak and folding it into a neat square. This would work as my pillow. I was exhausted, and a little sleep wouldn't hurt . . .
       
~
       
      I awoke in the dark. Clarity was fast asleep next to me, and I carefully sat up so as to not wake her. I quietly made my way out of the room and pulled on my cloak as I went. When I reached the front door, I pushed it open and stepped into the night beyond.
      A cool wind kissed my face as I lifted my head to the stars. My breath puffed out in front of me. The clouds had finally cleared, and the stars glittered as pinpricks of light against the infinite dark.
      "Can't sleep?" Talon's voice asked.
      I turned to find the vampire standing behind me. Her own face was tilted up to the stars.
      "I wanted to see the sunrise," I said. "So I decided to come out here."
      Talon smiled. "You're in luck. Sunrise is minutes away."
      "The sky finally cleared up," I noted. "I haven't seen it this clear in forever. Hey . . ."
      Talon turned to me and arched a brow as she waited for me to go on.
      "Do you hate humans like Lynden?"
      Talon held my gaze as her hair danced lightly in the breeze. "No. Once, maybe. But not anymore. I realized that when you live a life full of hatred, everyone suffers. And that includes yourself. When Karmen first turned me, it's true that I was very hateful. I was ready to hunt down the people who had caused all my pain and suffering but found that they had already died at the hands of someone else. After that, I realized that not all people were as horrible as I thought. A group of them had avenged me after all."
      I nodded my head. "You know, I should probably hate humans as well after what they did to my family and me. But at the end of the day, I am human too. For me, life is short. I can't spend what precious little time I have consumed by rage and hatred. I had to decide what the most important thing to me in this life is. And right now, that's my family. Once my family is safe, then I can focus my efforts on everyone else."
      Talon smiled. "Wise."
      I smiled back.
      The sky was slowly beginning to brighten, and I looked out over the mountains. My breath caught in my throat as I watched the sky change from deep indigo to gold to rosy pink. Light crept over the land and embraced everything in its brilliance. And then the sun appeared on the horizon. Its golden rays painted both heaven and earth in vivid color.
      I had never seen such a sunrise before. Back at the farm, we had always been too busy working to pay attention to the colors. I stood there on the edge of the mountain for a very long time, gazing out into the distance.
      Chloe-Jane was out there somewhere. I wondered if she could see the same sunrise.
      "Hey, Talon," I said suddenly. "Do you think . . ." I looked over my shoulder only to discover that I was alone on the snow-covered mountain. The vampire had vanished along with the night.
      I stared at the place where she had disappeared. How could one live for so many years without seeing the sun? I shivered and pulled my cloak tighter around myself as I made my way back into the house.
      "Corinna!" Phina called excitedly as the door swung shut behind me. "Did you see the sunrise? What did it look like?" She was sitting at the dining table between Lynden and Talon. Talon caught my eye and offered me a smile. I shrugged off my cloak and took the seat next to the dark-haired vampire.
      "The sunrise was beautiful," I told them as I pictured the breathtaking sky in my mind. "It was full of color and light and hope. It was the dawn of a new day."
      "It sounds lovely," Phina said wistfully.
      Talon's eyes sparkled. "It sounds magical."
      Lynden just stared at the table. "I've never seen the sunrise before. When I was human, I never got the chance."
      "Is it not possible to watch it from inside?" I asked.
      Phina's expression turned sad. "We can't see the colors. It's just a blinding light."
      I fell silent at that. It took me a moment to notice that all three vampires had cups on the table in front of them. "What's in there?"
      "What do you think?" Lynden said flatly.
      I felt my stomach churn unpleasantly. "Blood."
      Phina gave me a guilty smile. "I'm sorry, Corinna. Lynden and I didn't think anyone would be awake this early."
      I removed my gaze from the cups. "It's fine. The three of you should do what you need to do. I shouldn't be one to judge. Is blood really the only substance you can consume?"
      Talon nodded. "We can't consume anything else without our bodies rejecting it. As vampires, we're technically dead. We don't need food or water. But since we are dead, we can't create our own blood. And as a result, we can only sustain ourselves off the blood of others."
      Lynden grimaced. "It's disgusting, really."
      Phina nodded along in agreement.
      "That isn't human blood, is it?" I asked in a strained sort of way.
      "No," Talon answered. "Most vampires prefer not to drink the blood of humans. It tastes vile."
      "You can taste their greed and envy and hatred." Phina wrinkled her freckled nose. "You can taste their fear and sadness and desperation. It's awful. Other animals don't tend to have such emotions, or at least not to such an extreme extent. But then again, there are some vampires who are just as greedy and hate-driven. And those sorts of vampires don't have any problem with feeding off humans."
      "Does feeding off an animal or human kill them?" I shuddered slightly at the thought.
      Talon sighed. "If a vampire doesn't drain them entirely, they can still live."
      I stared down at the table in front of me as I clasped my hands together on top of the wood. "I can only imagine what it would feel like to have one's very life force stripped away like that. It must be awful."
      Phina tugged at a strand of her ginger hair. "It's quite the opposite, actually. Let's just say it isn't a very painful death."
      I fell silent again and looked up as Storm appeared on the stairs.
      "Good morning," Storm said with a yawn. His dark hair was disheveled and sticking up in all directions. Storm walked right by us and into the kitchen without a second glance. I noticed that the cups in front of my tablemates had vanished but decided it was better not to say anything.
      Clarity, Cameren, and Mother came down the stairs shortly after and took seats at the table as well. It was a tight fit, but somehow we miraculously managed to get everyone around the table.
      Storm returned with a bunch of bowls. "I hope you don't mind porridge."
      "Can I really have all of this?" I asked in surprise as Storm slid one of the bowls to me across the smooth surface of the table. Back at the farm, we were only given enough food to sustain us. Every day, it was the same flavorless meal.
      Storm blinked. "Of course."
      I carefully dipped my spoon into the bowl. Faint tendrils of steam drifted lazily through the air. After lifting the spoon to my mouth, I took an eager first bite. "It's good."
      "Well, I'm glad you think so," Storm said as he returned to the kitchen, "because it's the only thing I know how to make." He reappeared later with a bottle of amber liquid.
      "Don't drink that," Lynden said sharply as he stood up.
      Storm scowled. "I-"
      "Sixteen-year-olds can't drink!" Phina stood up as well. Her hands were on her hips as if she were a mother about to scold a small child. "Does your uncle know about this?"
      "Neither of you gave me a chance to explain myself," Storm said irritably as he looked from Lynden to Phina and then back again. "My uncle told me to be hospitable. It's not for me."
      "Good thing you know not to drink it," Clarity said shortly. "Drinking makes you an easy target for manipulation. I would know as I've manipulated intoxicated people myself."
      Storm fell silent as he eyed my sister suspiciously.
      Cameren turned to Clarity in an exasperated sort of way. "He said he isn't going to drink it. You don't have to frighten him." Then Cameren turned back to Storm. "We appreciate that you're thinking about us, but none of us here drink either."
      Lynden sighed. "Clarity's right, though. What's more is that too much alcohol leads to bad decision after bad decision. I learned that the hard way. And look where I am now because of it."
      I waited for him to continue. But he didn't.
      "Storm," Talon said as she changed the topic, "if I remember correctly, you're the only human to have single-handedly killed a vampire before. Would you care to enlighten us on how it happened?"

Chapter Eight
       
Storm's expression turned serious as he ran an agitated hand through his dark hair. "Look, it's not as impressive as you probably think or heard from whoever told you that story."
      I arched a brow as I waited for him to go on.
      Storm clasped his hands together. "I wouldn't have found that vampire if it wasn't for my uncle. It was about four years ago, back when Uncle still left the mountain. We were flying over a desert when we saw a vampire. It was daytime, and he was just lying there. Uncle landed, and the two of us went to check on him. He was barely conscious. All of his skin had flaked off too. We flew him to the closest forest and waited for him to wake up. When he did, he was, well, sad. He asked why we had saved him and then told us that he wanted to die. I didn't want to kill him, but I also wanted to help him."
      I listened to Storm's story in silence. Four years ago. The boy was only twelve years old at the time.
      "My uncle could have easily ended him, but I don't know what made me decide to do it." Storm stared unseeingly at the wall. "I just felt so bad for him. After that, word got out somehow that I successfully killed a vampire, and people kept changing the story until it was as far from the truth as it could get. Even when I tried to correct them, they refused to listen. Do you still want me to work with all of you after you heard my real story?" Storm asked tiredly. "I won't blame you if you don't."
      Phina looked in my direction. "I don't know about you, but Lynden and I have never been to the capital city before-at least not in the very heart of it. We still need a guide."
      I nodded. "I haven't been to the capital city in years. I can only imagine how much it's changed since then."
      Cameren offered Storm a smile. "Would you still consider it?"
      Storm broke into a genuine smile. "I'll be your guide. And I'll do my best to be the best guide there ever was!"
      Phina beamed. "That's the spirit!"
      Storm nodded his head. "So you're looking for Queen Karmen?"
      "First we find the sister," Lynden said. "Then we'll look for Karmen."
      "You're okay with that?" Clarity asked with raised brows.
      Lynden looked at Clarity. "Karmen can wait. Right now your sister's well-being is more important."
      "With all of us looking, I'm sure we'll find her in no time," Phina said reassuringly. "And who knows, maybe while we're searching, we'll run into Karmen along the way."
      "Chloe-Jane was taken to the capital to be a seamstress," Corinna explained. "Do you know all the places where a seamstress could end up working?"
      "I'll go through my maps with my uncle and find all of the places she could be," Storm declared determinedly. "All of you are welcome to start looking through our stash of weapons," he added over his shoulder before he dashed upstairs.
      "Weapons," Corinna said quickly as she turned to me. "That's right-Talon, you said that you'd help train me. When do we start?"
      I found myself smiling at Corinna's eagerness. "Let's go look at some weapons now, shall we?" I stood up from my seat, and Corinna followed closely as I opened the door to Andreus's cavern. "When we came down here yesterday, I noticed a door with a sword hanging over it," I explained as I led the way down the steps. "I'm positive that's where the weapons are kept."
      Sure enough, a short distance down the staircase, the door made an appearance. I pressed my hand against the wood and the door swung open with ease. Inside was a large stone room. Shelves of different blades lined the room, along with shelves of bows, spears, shields, and other miscellaneous weaponry.
      Corinna sucked in a breath. "I've never seen so many weapons in one place before."
      "Me neither." I pivoted on my heel as I took in the entirety of the room in all its glory. As an immortal, Andreus must have spent his whole life collecting weapons. I only needed to glance at the collection to know that some of them dated back hundreds of years ago. Not only that, but Andreus had been alive hundreds of years before I had even been born. Who knew how ancient some of these weapons were.
      A chunk of the morning was spent setting Corinna up with a set of daggers. When she had finally decided on her weapons, Corinna stared down at the blades in her hands.
      "Now that you have your own weapons, what will you do with them?" I asked softly.
      "I will use them to defend and protect," Corinna vowed. Determination sparked in her eyes. "I've never liked weapons. But I will take them up if it means I can keep my family safe."
      The two of us spent the entire morning in the weapons room running through different motions and exercises.
      "It's time for a break," I announced after a while.
      "A break?" Corinna stared up at the high ceiling in a daze. "I think I finally got the hang of it, though."
      I laughed. "Pushing yourself is good, but pushing yourself too much can lead to injuries. And for someone who doesn't have limitless stamina, you need to take the time to rest and recover."
      Corinna looked over at me. "You're a very good teacher." Even though she had braided her hair back from her sweat-slick face, loose curls had still managed to escape. "Something tells me that I'm not your first student."
      I sighed as I took a seat on the ground. "I had two students before. If I remember correctly, it was about forty years ago. They were sisters. Twins, actually."
      Corinna sat down across from me. "What happened to them?" she asked quietly. From the look in her eyes, I could tell she already knew how the story was going to end.
      "We met in one of the smaller towns on the outskirts of the capital city," I recalled. "The girls were young at the time-both of them no older than fifteen. I just happened to be walking by when I saw a group of men trying to abduct them. After I knocked out all of their would-be kidnappers, the girls begged me to teach them how to defend themselves. I agreed. The three of us journeyed together for four years." I found myself smiling wistfully. It had been a while since I had last allowed myself to think of the past. "They didn't care that I was a vampire. They just respected me as both their teacher and an older sister. I taught them everything I knew, and they were fast learners.
      "The three of us bought a house close to the capital city. The two sisters took it upon themselves to watch the streets during the day, while I would patrol during the night. They saved and helped countless people. But even with all the good they did, there were quite a few people who felt threatened by the sisters. They didn't like that they couldn't get away with things as easily anymore, so they rallied against them-shortly after, the sisters were accused of being witches and were burned to death in front of the castle for all to see. I was away at the time, but when the news reached me that the sisters were dead, I rushed back to the capital as fast as I could. All that was left of the sisters were their ashes."
      I shook my head as I concluded my story. My chest was hollow and empty. If I was still human, I probably would have shed a tear at this point. But I wasn't human. I couldn't cry. I couldn't express my pain properly-couldn't mourn the sisters properly.
      Before I could blink, Corinna wrapped me in a tight hug. "I'm sorry," she whispered.
      There was something about the embrace that settled all of the emotions gnawing away at me. And for a brief moment, there was warmth.
      "You helped those sisters." Corinna pulled away a few moments later. She took my hands in her own and gave them a reassuring squeeze. "Who knows what would have happened to them if their kidnappers had managed to successfully abduct them."
      I nodded as I returned Corinna's gentle smile.
      Corinna let go of my hands. "I noticed your ears, by the way."
      "My ears?" I reached up to tuck my hair behind an ear. Unlike Corinna's rounded ears, mine ended in a delicate point. "All vampires have pointed ears," I explained. "They allow us to hear different frequencies than humans. But that's enough about me for now-let's get you back upstairs to rest."
      Upstairs, Corinna's mother and sister were sitting at the table, talking quietly. All the curtains were drawn over the windows, leaving the room to be illuminated by flickering lanterns. Lynden and Phina were sitting on the couch, looking over a large pile of maps. Cameren and Storm sat opposite them on the floor, playing a game of cards. Cameren was smiling faintly as he looked up from his hand of cards. "It looks like it's a tie again."
      "Good game!" Storm grinned. He set his cards down before extending a hand for Cameren to shake. Out of everyone, Storm seemed to have connected the most with Corinna's brother. Maybe it was because Storm liked to talk, and Cameren, being the big brother he was, was willing-and had enough patience-to indulge him.
      "Corinna." Cameren waved his sister over when he noticed the two of us had entered the room. Corinna hurried over to take a seat beside her brother, and Storm eagerly shuffled the cards for a new round.
      I took a seat on the floor in front of the couch before picking up one of the maps from the pile. I scanned the paper and frowned slightly when I noticed how outdated it was.
      Phina reached for another map. "All of these are at least over a hundred years old. Who knows if some of these buildings are still around."
      As I looked through the maps, Corinna and Cameren eventually migrated to join Meyrah and Clarity at the dining room table. Storm brought out more porridge for lunch, and I found myself listening in on their conversation.
      "Mother and I decided that we're going to stay here with Andreus," Cameren explained to Corinna. "As much as we want to help in finding Chloe, we agreed that it would be better if we didn't slow you down. Andreus said that he could help heal my injuries."
      "He did?" Corinna asked quickly. My own ears perked up. Could Andreus really heal all of Cameren's injuries?
      "Andreus was actually the one who offered," Meyrah added. "We went to visit him with Storm earlier this morning."
      "What do you think of Andreus?" Corinna asked lightly.
      "I trust him," Cameren said confidently. "If he can really heal me . . . this is an opportunity I can't afford to pass up. While we're here, I bet Andreus also has countless stories to tell about his adventures as an immortal. That's an opportunity I can't pass up either."
      "I think that's actually a good idea." Corinna looked from her brother to her mother and then back again. "The journey to the capital city will be a long one, and I'll be reassured knowing that the two of you will be safe and comfortable here. What about you, Clarity? Are you planning to stay here too, or are you coming with us to the capital city?"
      "Of course I'm coming along," Clarity said stiffly. "Chloe-Jane is my sister. I'm going to help with getting her back."
      Corinna let out a breath. "I'm glad. Chloe would be overjoyed to know that."
      When they were done eating, Corinna hurried back over to me, and we returned to the weapon room to continue training. We stopped when it was time for dinner and then returned downstairs for a couple more hours after that.
      By the time we decided to call it a night, the moon had risen in the sky outside the living room windows. After Corinna and I bid each other goodnight, I exited the house.
      Alone in the night, I tilted my head upward to take in the ocean of stars above the snow-capped mountains. Then closing my eyes, I let my mind wander.
      I heard the voice: I can give you the strength you need to take your revenge-I can give you the power you desire.
      This time, the Karmen in my mind was more than a pair of glowing red eyes; she was a woman with pale skin and long brown hair. Elegant yet cold. Just as Phina had described.
      After opening my eyes, I leaped up into the sky and landed lightly on the roof of the house. The pearly moon hung low. And there were so many stars. Whenever I found myself questioning whether there was beauty left in the world, I'd just have to look up at the night sky and the stars would answer. Always, always, always.
      "Lynden," I said without turning around. I had sensed his presence. "What brings you here?"
      "Talon," Lynden replied curtly. "I can go wherever I please, can't I?"
      I glanced over my shoulder to look at the other vampire. "Since you're here, I have a couple of things I'd like to ask you."
      I took Lynden's silence as an indicator for me to continue.
      I turned to face him. "What's your relationship with Phina? Do you trust her?"
      Lynden paused for a moment before folding his arms over his chest. "Phina and I met while we were working for Karmen. And as a matter of fact, I do trust her."
      "What's Phina's story?" I watched Lynden's expression. "For that matter, what's your story? I know what you've done, Lynden. What happened at the Winfielde's estate was your doing. Do you deny it?"
      Lynden's expression didn't change. "I don't deny it."
      "Then how can I trust you? You slaughtered an entire house of humans."
      "You've killed many people yourself in that forest, Talon." Lynden's tone remained unchanged. "I don't need your trust. Why would I want yours when I can't even trust you?"
      "Don't trust me, then. But for the sake of Corinna and Clarity, let's be civil until we get their sister back."
      "Who are you really, Talon?" Lynden refused to look away. "You seem to already know my story. What's yours?" When I didn't answer, Lynden let out a snort. "Fine. If you're not going to tell me, I won't ask again." There was a rush of wind as Lynden leaped down from the roof and vanished into the night.
      Frowning slightly, I turned back to look out over the mountains. I clasped my hands together behind my back as a soft breeze set my long hair dancing.
      Who am I? I wondered. Lynden had posed a very good question. But who I was in the past didn't matter now. That girl died the moment she was turned by Karmen.
      Who am I now? I was a monster of claws and fangs and darkness.
      Karmen. Why did Karmen turn Lynden and Phina? I asked myself. What did the two vampires mean to her? Why did she turn me? In all of these years, Karmen was rumored to have only turned ten vampires. But I didn't know what to believe at this point. I hadn't met any other vampires turned by the queen herself until stumbling across Lynden and Phina.
       
~
       
      "What are you going to be teaching me today?" Corinna asked eagerly.
      I took a seat on the smooth floor of the weapon room. Corinna followed my lead and winced slightly as she sat down.
      "Sore?"
      Corinna nodded but flashed me a smile all the same. "It's not that bad. I want to learn as much as I can as fast as I can. I don't want to keep Chloe-Jane waiting if I can help it."
      I picked up a nearby weapon. "How about we start with learning how to use a dagger, then?"
      The two of us spent a good hour going through the motions over and over before working on different exercises. We took a break when lunchtime rolled around and joined Corinna's family and Storm upstairs.
      "Good news," Storm announced as we gathered around the table. "We were able to pinpoint all of the locations where Chloe-Jane might be."
      Corinna let out a breath. "That's wonderful."
      "We'll find your sister in no time," Storm said confidently. "When we get to the city, I'll find us a current map and add any new shops to our list of locations. If we split up in the capital, we can cover all of the locations in a little less than a month."
      "A month?" Clarity asked incredulously. "Is the capital city really that big?"
      "Of course it is," Storm replied, frowning. "Look, I'm doing the best I can."
      Corinna shook her head. "This is great news. I don't know how to thank you enough. When do we leave?"
      "Tomorrow morning," Storm answered. "We'll leave tomorrow morning. My uncle has been helping me get ready."
      Phina jumped to her feet. "Lynden and I will go collect more plants that we can make into medicines later," she declared. "You never know if someone will get hurt."
      Lynden nodded in silent agreement.
      Suddenly, Clarity surprised everyone in the room. "Can I come along?" she asked.
      Phina blinked before her expression melted into a smile. "Of course!"
      Clarity got to her feet and brushed invisible specks of dust from her skirts. "My brother was suffering right in front of me for so long and there wasn't anything I could do. I just felt so useless. If I knew about medicine, I could have helped my brother out myself. I want to be able to help."
      "Lynden and I can teach you what we know about medicine," Phina said excitedly. "I think the knowledge will be more useful to you than us vampires."
      I watched as the three of them left the house. The afternoon sky was dark, with gray clouds streaking through it. Another storm was approaching, and all I could do was hope that things would clear up before our descent down the mountain.
      After lunch, Corinna and I returned to the weapon room. We spent the rest of the day there before climbing back up the stairs for a late dinner. At that point, Corinna's family had already gone to bed, and Lynden and Phina were somewhere outside, keeping watch over the silent mountains.
      Corinna turned to me after she had finished washing her bowl in the kitchen. "I guess this is where we say goodnight."
      I nodded. "You did a good job today."
      Corinna beamed. "Goodnight, Talon."
      "Goodnight, Corinna." I watched her climb the stairs to the second floor and vanish around the corner. Once she was gone, I stood up from the table. I slowly unbraided my hair as I gazed out the window at the night beyond.
      "Talon." Storm's voice called. "My uncle wants to speak with you alone."
      "He does?" I asked mildly. I looked over my shoulder at the dark-haired boy.
      Storm nodded. "I'm not completely sure what it's about, but I think he wants to give you some useful information."
      I sighed. "Let's see what Andreus has to say, then."

Chapter Nine
       
I awoke the next morning to a flood of sunlight pouring in through the window. And ever so slowly, I sat up from where I had been lying on the floor. It looked like the storm had blown over after all. My stiff back whined as I climbed to my feet, and I winced.
      Clarity was already awake. She was standing next to the window as she gazed out over the mountains. Quietly, so as to not wake Mother and Cameren, I tiptoed over to admire the view as well. The sky was a clear blue with long streaks of white clouds carefully brushed onto the surface. "We're going to get Chloe-Jane back," I said quietly. "I believe we can do it."
      "And what if we don't find her?" Clarity gave me a sideways glance. "Then what?"
      "Then we keep trying."
      Clarity turned back to the window. "Why are you so confident?"
      "I have to have enough confidence for the both of us, don't I? You've just got to believe."
      "What has believing ever got us? Even if we do find Chloe, what do we do then? Where do we go? It will be tricky to stay in this kingdom."
      I stared out over the horizon. "We'll go somewhere far away. You, me, Chloe-Jane, Cameren, and Mother. We could go to the southern continent, but we've been cut off from the language and culture for far too long . . . We'll think of something."
      "And what about the vampires?"
      I blinked. "What about them?"
      "Once we get Chloe back, will you really be okay parting ways with them just like that?"
      I let out a soft sigh. It wasn't something I wanted to think about right now.
      Clarity met my gaze. "I'm just asking because even if I personally can't stand them, I've noticed that you seem to be enjoying their company."
      I averted my eyes. My sister noticed everything. I could never seem to hide anything from her.
      "Clarity, Corinna," Mother called out to us. We turned to find her and Cameren watching us from the bed. "Have the two of you eaten breakfast yet?"
      "Not yet." I quickly shook my head. "We were waiting for you and Cameren to wake up."
      Clarity inclined her head in Mother's direction. "We're leaving after breakfast."
      "Corinna." Mother smiled at me tiredly. "Come here."
      I walked over to Mother and looked down at her expectantly. Mother stood up and gently placed her hands on my shoulders. She turned me around so that my back was to her, and I held still as she skillfully braided my hair away from my face.
      When she finished, she turned me back around to face her. Her eyes sparkled with a mixture of sadness and joy as she gazed at me. "That's my beautiful little girl. If only your father could see you now. You've grown up so fast. And look at your sister-she's already an adult!"
      Clarity flashed Mother a rare smile. The usual hard lines of her face were briefly softened. I found myself smiling faintly as well. Mother was the only person Clarity ever smiled for-not me, not Cameren. As a matter of fact, she didn't even smile for Chloe-Jane. But that was fine. That was just how Clarity was. If she couldn't find anything to smile about, she wouldn't go out of her way to fake it. She was harsh at times, but her harsh nature was usually balanced by Chloe-Jane's carefree personality. Now that Chloe-Jane wasn't here, something felt unbalanced.
      "Corinna isn't a little girl anymore," Cameren said as he grinned at me. "She's a young woman now. It's crazy how time flies. Let's go get some breakfast now, shall we? Even after stuffing myself last night at dinner, I'm already hungry again."
      I smiled at my older brother. It had been a while since I had seen him so content. He was hopeful too, I realized. Now that Andreus had presented him with the possibility of healing his injuries, Cameren's own hope had rekindled.
      Mother and I each took one of Cameren's arms and helped him to his feet. We helped my brother down the stairs and onto the chair next to Storm at the dining room table. Lynden, Phina, and Talon were sitting on the couch, and each of them was dressed head to toe in heavy fabric as they talked in lowered voices. When Talon noticed me, she turned and waved. "Good morning, Corinna."
      I smiled and waved back. "Good morning."
      "I was just telling Lynden and Phina how I was talking with Andreus last night," Talon informed me as she stood up from the couch. "Apparently Andreus has a house that he keeps for friends on the east side of the capital city that we can stay in."
      "What friends?" Lynden turned to Talon with raised brows. "He keeps a house for friends but sits around in a cave all day?"
      "My uncle says it's for the friends he hasn't met yet," Storm said as he gave Lynden a look. "I've only been to the house a few times before, but I know the way. We'll be taking the main road to the capital. On foot, the journey takes over a week. Lucky for you, though, I know where we can rent a wagon and horses. I've got all of the weapons, food, and other supplies we need for our trip there." Storm pointed at a large crate next to the door.
      "Is that much stuff really necessary?" Clarity asked as she eyed the crate.
      "I said the same thing earlier," Lynden said with a frown. "But he insisted that it was important."
      Storm crossed his arms. "It's very important. My uncle and I spent all night putting it together. Uncle found some clothes suitable for the capital city in one of his many storage rooms. If we walk around there as we are now, we'll certainly attract attention. Especially the three of you," Storm said with a nod to the vampires.
      It was true; the three of them were wearing so many layers that it looked like they were preparing to walk into the middle of a snowstorm. Each of them wore a hooded cloak and numerous scarves over their faces.
      Phina placed her hands on her hips. "We've got to cover up if we don't want our skin to flake off!"
      "How does that work anyway?" Storm raised his brows.
      "It's part of our curse," Lynden answered flatly. "Vampires are creatures of the night. We're not allowed to enjoy the sun. The ancient magic prevents us from going out in the day without consequence."
      "Oh, that's right," Storm said. Then he turned back to address Clarity and me. "The two of you would look suspicious as well-people from the southern continent are only rarely seen in the capital city, and when they are, they're usually enslaved and trailing their masters around."
      Well, he did have a point.
      "Let's just focus on finishing eating right now." Storm shook his head, then his expression turned serious. "We want to make good time before night falls."
       
       
~
       
      After we finished eating, the six of us bid Andreus, Mother, and Cameren farewell before starting down the mountain. Lynden and Phina took turns carrying Storm's crate of supplies. Neither of them were particularly thrilled about the job. Storm was at the front of the party, talking to himself in a string of seemingly incoherent sentences. I had long given up on trying to understand him and was now trailing him from a good distance.
      Talon came up by my side. Her face was completely hidden behind layers of dark scarves. "You could definitely pass for a bandit of some sort," I said lightly.
      Talon laughed. "A bandit?"
      I nodded as the frosty winter wind bit at my exposed face. "Yes-a mountain bandit that needs to wear as many layers as possible so as to not freeze to death."
      Talon looked around at the piles of glistening snow covering every flat surface. "It does get quite cold in the mountains this time of the year."
      I pulled my cloak tighter, and my breath puffed out in the frozen air in front of me. "Even though it's not snowing now, today feels like the coldest day yet."
      "Look there," Storm called out from the front of the group as we rounded the corner. "You see that all the way in the distance? That's the capital city."
      My eyes widened as I gazed out at the horizon. Without the clouds obscuring my view, I could now see for miles and miles. If I looked carefully, I could make out the hundreds upon hundreds of buildings that made up the city. And if I strained my eyes, I could almost make out the turrets and towers of the royal castle.
      "We'll be there soon," Talon said quietly. "You won't have to wait much longer."
      We spent the first half of the day carefully descending the icy mountain and the second half of the day retracing our steps to the abandoned farmhouse we had previously spent the night in. Along the way, Talon shared her knowledge of daggers and other knives with me. By the time we stopped for the night, I could recite almost everything she told me.
      The next day, we arrived in a small town sometime in the late afternoon. Storm made quick work of renting a wagon and two horses. The six of us climbed into the wagon, and the dark-haired boy took the reins.
      The journey blurred by in a flash, and the days and nights melted together in a rush of color and sound. Before I knew it, we had arrived at the house. It was midday, and the sun was hidden behind a layer of dark clouds. I stiffly climbed out of the wagon and stared up at the building. The house was located near the edge of the capital. It was about two stories tall with a simple but elegant design. Judging from its appearance, it must have cost a good amount of money.
      Storm unlocked the door to the house, and we followed the dark-haired boy over the threshold. The inside of the house was dark, and Storm quickly walked around lighting the lamps. The room was slowly illuminated and I found that we were standing in the middle of an elegant living room.
      "Andreus had an old friend help him buy the house completely furnished from its previous owner," Storm explained when he noticed me staring at the expensive furniture. "The owners were leaving the kingdom at the time and would rather sell everything than take it with them."
      I shook my head as I snapped myself back to reality. I didn't want to think about how much money it took to purchase the furnishings in this room alone.
      Storm opened the wooden crate Phina had just set down and pulled out multiple outfits. "Let's change quickly-we only have so many hours before night falls and the shops close."
      Storm handed me one of the outfits. I unfolded the dress and held it out in front of me. Even though it was a maid's dress, it was still fancier than anything I had worn before in my life.
      "You can change upstairs," Storm continued distractedly as he sorted through the remaining contents in the crate. "There should be three bedrooms."
      Clarity and I headed upstairs together and took one of the rooms. When we had finished changing outfits, Clarity looked down at her dress in distaste. "I'll consider myself lucky if I don't have to be anyone's servant ever again."
      I sighed as I braided back my hair. "I know, but we're doing this for Chloe-Jane. Standing out won't end well for any of us. And we've got to be especially careful too. Who knows how many people will try to send us back to the farm."
      "Here," Clarity said suddenly before pressing a marble-sized ball into my hand.
      "What's this?" I blinked as I examined the tiny sphere. On closer expectation, it was made entirely out of plant fibers all bound together with a single blade of grass.
      "Phina has been teaching me about how to use herbs as both medicine and weapons." Clarity's expression was grim as she held my gaze. "If you add water to it, it will create something like a screen of smoke. If you're ever in trouble, hopefully it might give you an opportunity to escape."
      "Thank you." I carefully pocketed the sphere. I was both happy and surprised that Clarity had decided to look out for me. "I hope that it won't come down to me having to use it, though. Also, I have this." I lifted my long skirts to show my sister the dagger strapped to my leg. "Well, I hope I won't have to use it either."
      "Be careful, Corinna," Clarity said stiffly.
      I nodded. "You too."
      We returned back downstairs to find everyone waiting for us in their own change of clothing.
      "Good," Storm said as he looked over at Clarity and me. "We're all here."
      "Where did your uncle get these outfits?" Talon spoke up. The vampire was dressed in a coal-colored gown complete with matching gloves and a veiled hat that masked her blood-colored eyes. She had cut her hair as well; the inky strands were twisted into an elegant knot at the back of her head. Her lips were painted a deep shade of red, a striking contrast to her porcelain skin. She was a noblewoman through and through.
      "My uncle likes to collect things like the latest weapons and clothes." Storm picked at the lace on his own outfit. "He has me buy them and then proceeds to hoard them in his cave. He's a dragon after all. Dragons like sparkly things. Anyway, my point is that if we didn't use the clothes, I'm not sure anyone ever would."
      Lynden frowned. "We should get a move on." He, too, was dressed in the outfit of a noble. Phina, on the other hand, was wearing the same maid dress as Clarity and me.
      Storm handed each of us a map and a scrap of paper with a list of shop names scrawled onto it in neat print. "We'll try to cover these today. If we move quickly, each of us can hit two or three per hour. Got it? Okay, let's go."
      We exited the house in pairs. Storm and Clarity went first and took our two horses with them. Lynden and Phina followed five minutes later, and finally Talon and I another five minutes after that.
      The two of us walked down the street in silence. The only sound that cut through the still air was the tapping of Talon's high heels on the cobblestone path.
      "Where is everyone?" I asked quietly, slightly alarmed by the eerie quiet.
      Talon looked around at the buildings, and her dark veil swished with the movement. "This area appears to be residential only. I assume everyone is either indoors because of the weather or at work."
      A silence fell between us again, and at least ten minutes had passed before I mustered the courage to break it. "You didn't finish the story you were telling Phina and me on the ride to the city. I really would like to hear the ending."
      As we walked further into the city, Talon resumed the story of how she thought she had a close encounter with Queen Karmen. The streets gradually became busier and busier, and the buildings began to press closer together as the sound of chatter filled the air.
      "And that was when I discovered that the entire ball was a setup," Talon was saying as her heels tapped over the stones. "It turned out the whole thing had been a trap all along. Someone had tipped off the knights that a vampire was going to be there. I had heard that Queen Karmen was going to be there, but it turned out that wasn't the case."
      "Why do so many vampires want to see Karmen dethroned?"
      "Apart from the fact that she's a female, she doesn't allow vampires to turn humans into vampires," Talon explained. "If a vampire does decide to turn a human, she'll hunt both vampires down and put an end to them."
      "Do you think she's worried that too many vampires will pose a threat to her?"
      Talon frowned slightly. "I can't tell for sure. Karmen is known for being unpredictable."
      "If you don't mind me asking," I asked mildly, "what does it feel like when you're transforming into a vampire?"
      "When Karmen turned me, it felt like I was dying. It's like the very structure of your being is being rearranged as you burn from the inside out. Then when it's over, your human body has died while your mind continues to function as if nothing changed. Some vampires can't accept the fact that they're no longer living and go insane."
      My voice dropped to a whisper. "I'm so sorry."
      Talon absently opened the lace fan she was holding and fanned herself lightly. "Don't be-I was dying even before I accepted Karmen's offer."
      I arched a brow as I waited for her to go on.
      Talon just shook her head. "Oh look-we've arrived."
      I blinked as I looked up at the building in front of us. I hadn't even noticed that we had reached our first destination.
      "Ready?" Talon asked.
      "Of course."
      Talon stepped forward and picked up her lacey skirts as she climbed the single step to the door. The tinkling of a bell sounded as the door swung open. I quickly scanned the room. The shop was fairly large, and racks of dresses lined the walls, forming neat aisles down the length of the room.
      "Welcome," a man's voice called from the corner of the room. Its owner was hidden away behind the lines of clothes. "What can I help you with today?"
      Talon strode over to the source of the voice. "I'm looking for a dress."
      "I have plenty of dresses here," the man at the counter said proudly as he finally came into view. He was middle-aged, slightly balding, with straw-colored hair and one of the thickest mustaches I had ever seen.
      Talon angled her head to the side as she gazed down her nose at the clerk. "I'm not just looking for just any dress. I want the best-the most expensive dress-you have to offer."
      The clerk eyed Talon up and down. Finally the clerk nodded to himself, liking what he was seeing. "Of course, of course! Anything for a lovely young lady like yourself."
      Talon pulled out a large pouch of coins from her embroidered handbag. "How much for a custom gown?"
      "Fifty gold pieces." The clerk's gaze went immediately to the pouch, as if he could see all the money inside of it.
      Talon returned the coin pouch to her handbag. "I'd like to take a look at your seamstresses first. After all, I'll only settle for the absolute best. Show my maid to the back room, will you?"
      The clerk blinked back to reality, and his head snapped up to look at me as if he had suddenly realized that I was present too. He didn't even bother to hide his distaste. "Of course," he said, then he turned on his heel and pushed open the door behind the counter. "Follow me, girl."
      I quickly hurried after the clerk and cautiously peered around the door before stepping into the room beyond. The room was large, with tables, chairs, and mannequins filling every empty space. Racks upon racks of cloth lined the walls, and there wasn't a single window in sight. My eyes widened as I took in all of the girls crowded around the tables, busily sewing away. All of them were dark-skinned like me, and not one of them had looked up from their work when the door swung open.
      "Knock on the door when you're done," the clerk said blandly before leaving me on my own.
      I took a deep breath. Ten, twenty, thirty. There were thirty girls here. And all of them were younger than me. "Excuse me." I slowly walked over to the closest girl so as not to startle her. "Do you know if there's someone named Chloe-Jane working here?"
      "Chole-Jane," the girl echoed quietly. Her head was bent as she refused to meet my gaze. "No, there's no one here with that name."
      I nodded. It wasn't likely that we would find my sister in the first shop we checked anyway. "Thank you."
      The girl just bowed her head. My heart tightened in my chest as I scanned the crowded space one last time before forcing myself to make my way back to the door. If I had the power and ability, I would help get all of these girls out of here. Even if Talon took the shop owner out of the equation, there was no way to guarantee the girls' safety once they were out on the streets. Later, I vowed. Once Chloe-Jane was back at my side, I'd come back for the rest of them.
      I rapped on the wooden door. The clerk opened it a few seconds later, and I looked past him to Talon, who was waiting expectantly on the other side of the counter. Her eyes met mine immediately from behind her veil. There was a silent question written on her face.
      I shook my head. This was not the right place.
      "Well?" the salesclerk asked impatiently.
      "It seems as if this is not the right place." The corners of Talon's red-painted lips curled into a smile. "Good day."
      "Hey!" the clerk sputtered as Talon glided out the door with me close at her heels. "Wait!" As the door swung shut behind us, I heard the clerk mutter something under his breath that sounded like "good-for-nothing women."
      "Are we allowed to just walk out of there?" I asked quizzically.
      Talon's eyes sparkled as she hid her smile behind her fan. "I don't see why not. We weren't going to buy anything after all. Where next?"
      I pulled out the roll of map I had stuffed into my skirts. I opened the map and pointed to a circled spot. "Here."
      Talon leaned over to examine the series of complex lines that made up the city's streets. "That's about a thirty-minute walk from where we are right now."
      Talon and I continued on our way. Had we been here in the capital city for another reason, I would have found it amazing. But I could only see it as nothing more than a maze of streets and buildings hiding my younger sister somewhere in its midst.
      The second shop we visited was smaller than the first, and when I pushed open the door, a woman's voice greeted us. "Welcome," she called out. Her eyes went immediately to Talon. "What can I get for you today, Lady . . . Lady . . .?"
      "Falon," Talon said distractedly as she looked around the room.
      The young woman stepped out from behind her counter. "Lady Falon."
      "I'm looking for a dress," Talon said. Then she went through the same speech she had presented in the previous shop. Like last time, the clerk led me into the back room, and again none of the young seamstresses had heard of a girl named Chloe-Jane.
      The next three shops we went to were the same. By the time we exited the fourth, the sky was beginning to darken. Shops were closing left and right, signaling that it was time for us to head back. I shook my head tiredly. I was finally starting to feel the pain in my feet. I hoped the others had better luck than us.
      Talon and I silently retraced our steps back to Andreus's city house. Even though it was late, the streets were brightly lit by high-hanging lamps and even more glass lanterns hanging over every house's door. It had to have been midnight when we finally arrived at the house.
      "Welcome back!" Phina exclaimed as we walked inside. The ginger-haired vampire was sitting on the couch, and Lynden was standing a good distance away from her.
      "Any luck?" I asked hopefully.
      Phina shook her head sadly. "Not today. Storm and Clarity just got back half an hour ago. Both of them are asleep upstairs. Your sister is in the farthest room down the hall."
      I just nodded my head, too exhausted to come up with a response.
      Talon smiled softly. "You should get some sleep as well."
      I didn't need to be told twice before I climbed the stairs, stifling my yawn. "Goodnight, everyone," I called, then made my way through the dark hallway to the last room and quietly pushed open the door. Clarity hadn't bothered to draw the curtains, and the room was illuminated by the moonlight cutting through the dusty air.
      My sister was fast asleep on the bed. I stared down at Clarity for a long moment. Her hair was still in its thick braid, and in sleep, her expression was almost peaceful.
      I drew the curtains and let the room fall into complete darkness. Finally, I lay down on the carpeted floor on my side before drawing my knees to my chest. The room was surprisingly warm, and a blanket wasn't necessary-it also just so happened that the only blanket in the room was the one Clarity was using. I didn't want to disturb my sister. Clarity was a light sleeper when she allowed herself to fall asleep.
      I closed my eyes and let my exhaustion wash over me. As I began to drift off, I found myself thinking about Mother and Cameren-and Chloe-Jane. We had never been apart before. Not until now. So many things were changing that it was becoming more and more difficult to wrap my head around them.
      I was scared, I realized-scared of what would happen if I lost them. First Father had been taken away. Now Chloe-Jane. But this time, unlike with Father, we knew about Chloe-Jane's whereabouts. Unlike Father, she was still in this kingdom. And she was still alive. That was more than I could say about Father. I drew my knees to my chest. I missed him so much sometimes that it would hurt.
      I would do everything in my power to keep this family together. Cameren and Clarity had lost hope long ago-I could see it in their eyes whenever I looked at them. But back at Andreus's place, their spark had rekindled.
      Clarity didn't hold on to hope, but she was always ready to fight for her family-to protect them and keep them alive, if only for one more day. She would sell her mind, body, and soul if it meant we wouldn't hurt anymore.
      And Chloe-Jane . . . Chloe-Jane believed in the Immortal One. She believed that if she worked hard enough, the Immortal One would save her and take her to a better place. That's what all the overseers had told us, at least. But if it kept her going, I would gladly let her continue to believe in whatever she wanted.
      Tomorrow, I reassured myself. Tomorrow is a new day. Tomorrow will be full of new possibilities. Maybe I'll get lucky and find my sister.

Chapter Ten
       
I was lounging in the living room with my fellow vampires as we waited for the sky outside to darken. I hadn't bothered to change out of my dress-Corinna and I would be back out in a few hours anyway.
      I blinked once and allowed my eyes to adjust to the darkness. Lynden and Phina did the same, and their eyes glowed crimson. Phina stood up from the couch a moment later and extinguished the lamps placed around the room. "Talon," Phina said in a low voice, "did you notice that this house has a basement?"
      "A basement?"
      "Over here," Phina whispered excitedly. She tugged her ginger hair from her braid as she hurried over to the corner of the room. "You should see this too, Lynden. Well, it's not quite a basement. It looks like it could be a cellar of sorts." Phina dropped to her knees and pushed the carpet aside. Her slender fingers closed around a metal handle, and she carefully pulled open the panel of floor, revealing a ladder that descended to a stone room beneath the ground.
      "It looks like some kind of wine cellar," Lynden observed as he knelt down as well. "Except there's no wine."
      In one graceful movement, Phina hopped into the room and landed silently on her feet. "You're right," she called up. "It's completely empty."
      After exchanging a glance with Lynden, I hoisted my skirts and jumped down into the cellar. Lynden followed close behind. The room was roughly three-quarters of the size of the living room above it, and its walls were lined with empty wine racks. I looked around, eyeing the stone space thoughtfully. If we just pushed the wine racks to one side of the room, the cellar would make a great training room. It was spacious with plenty of room for sparring.
      "Do you mind if I tell Corinna about this tomorrow?" I asked lightly.
      Phina turned to climb back up the ladder. "Not at all. I wonder if everyone in the capital city has a wine cellar in their house. Or maybe only the rich do."
      "Think about it," Lynden said as he climbed up after her. "Who has the money to buy an entire cellar's worth of wine?"
      "The wealthy," Phina said thoughtfully.
      I looked around the wine cellar again before joining my fellow vampires back in the living room. I carefully slid the floor panel back into place, then rolled the carpet back over it.
      "I can take the first watch," Lynden offered.
      I nodded absently before I tugged off my high heels and set them down next to the door. It had been a while since I last wore expensive clothes. In fact, I tried my best to avoid it whenever I could. It wasn't that I didn't like the clothes-I very much did-rather, I wanted to prevent any old memories from resurfacing. I knew I couldn't hide from myself forever. But I had been able to run for this long. A little longer wouldn't hurt.
      I watched Lynden fasten a long cloak over his shoulders before leaving the house without a second glance. Phina returned to the couch and absently swung her legs. Her eyes were blank and glassy as she stared at the wall across the room.
      After I pulled my hair free from its knot, I left Phina in the living room and silently made my way up the stairs to the second level of the house. I could sense multiple human presences behind the doors. One presence in the first room, two in the farthest room-Storm, Clarity, and Corinna.
      As I made my way down the hall, I almost immediately noticed that the door to the sisters' room hadn't been shut properly. I walked over to close it, but my fingers paused on the handle as I peered through the slim opening. Both women were fast asleep, but my gaze immediately went to the floor where Corinna lay.
      I quickly dropped my hand from the door and glided over to the vacant bedroom in the middle of the hall. I knew there had to be an extra blanket here somewhere, and it didn't take me long to find one folded neatly on the floor of the large closet.
      I triumphantly made my way back to Corinna's room, blanket in hand, and carefully pushed open the door. Kneeling down, I unfolded the blanket before gently placing it over Corinna's sleeping body. Then with my work complete, I stood up and exited the room. I closed the door as quietly as I could behind me. Sunrise was just a few hours off.
      I returned to the living room to find Phina exactly as I had left her: staring blankly at the wall. The ginger-haired vampire didn't even look up when I walked in. Frowning to myself, I sat down at the table on the far side of the room to study the stack of maps. Between Lynden and Phina, I still couldn't decide which vampire I found stranger.
       
~
       
      Morning came quickly, carrying snowy weather with it. The little white flakes drifted down from the gray sky to dance and twirl outside the windows. Fortunately, the snowfall wasn't heavy.
      Corinna, Clarity, and Storm had come downstairs for breakfast, and the three of them were sitting around the dining room table.
      Corinna walked over to me after she had dropped off her bowl in the kitchen. "I ran through your training exercises upstairs before I came down to breakfast. I'm ready to head out when you are."
      I offered her a smile. "Alright. It's snowing outside right now. You should take one of the cloaks."
      Corinna nodded her head. "You should make sure to get one too. Even noblewomen are vulnerable to the cold, after all."
      "Of course. I'd be blowing my cover otherwise."
      Phina bounced over to me. "Talon, let me help you with your hair."
      Before I could even blink, she was standing behind me as she skillfully braided my now knee-length hair into a wreath around my head. I tensed.
      The ginger-haired vampire must have noticed my reaction because she giggled. "Relax. I know you still don't trust me, but you really think I'd take this opportunity to kill you?"
      "Could you?" I asked as I forced myself to relax.
      "Is that an invitation?" Phina continued fixing my hair as if our conversation was no different than talking about the weather.
      I kept my head straight. "It's a question."
      Phina sighed. "I don't know. If Lynden and I worked together we might be able to take you down. But hear me out; we don't want to kill you. We want to work with you."
      "Lynden doesn't trust me," I said lightly. "What about you?"
      "Trust in what? That you'll try to kill the two of us when you have the chance? That you'll run away when we find Karmen and leave us to fend for ourselves? That you'll sell us out to the queen? I don't think you're that kind of person. At least, that's not the impression I've gotten from you."
      "And what kind of person do you think I am?"
      Phina dropped her hands. "I think you're a good person. A much better person than I could ever be. Anyway," Phina said cheerfully, "I finished with your hair." She was smiling brightly, and her face gave nothing away.
      Phina, I decided-between Lynden and Phina, the latter was definitely stranger.
      I carefully fastened my veiled hat to my hair, and the black gauze fell over my eyes. As Corinna had suggested, I selected one of the cloaks hanging over the stair banister and draped it over my shoulders.
      "Hey," Storm called from the table. "Don't forget to bring money with you. We won't be returning here for the next few days, so bring enough for inns and food."
      "Inns?" Clarity's head snapped up from where she was sitting next to the dark-haired boy.
      Storm folded his arms over his chest. "Yes, inns. We went over this already, remember?"
      "I'm not sleeping in the same room as you," Clarity said coldly. "I'd rather partner up with Phina this time around."
      Storm choked on his porridge. "What? I wouldn't-"
      "Storm," Corinna started. Even though her voice was tired, her tone was firm. "I think you'll have to let it go. Don't take it too personally-it's just that Clarity's gone through her fair share of unpleasantries after all."
      "Oh," Storm fell silent as his expression turned solemn. "I-I'm sorry, Clarity."
      "Looks like we'll be working together, then," Lynden said to Storm.
      Storm grimaced, clearly not thrilled by the new development.
      Corinna put a hand on my arm and gently tugged me toward the door. "We'll head out first. The sooner we leave, the sooner we'll find Chloe-Jane."
      "Remember our meeting spot!" Phina called after me.
      I nodded my head as Corinna pushed the door open. A thin layer of snow coated the cobblestones in a fine powder. Corinna's breath puffed out in front of her as the two of us made our way down the path. It was going to be a long walk. Hopefully we'd be able to pay someone for a carriage ride.
      We arrived at the first shop sometime in the afternoon only to find that Corinna's sister was not there either. Now the sun had long dropped from the sky, and the temperatures dropped along with it. I could tell that Corinna was disappointed, but we had to find a place to stop for the night. Even though all the shops had closed, the streets were still full of people. I scanned the crowds through my veil.
      Karmen was brilliant; the capital city was the perfect place to hide out. It would be impossible to sense an immortal presence in the midst of all the human ones. The sheer number of humans was overwhelming. But all of these people would hide our presence, too. The queen would never know that we were coming-well, if we could even find her, that is.
      "According to the map"-Corinna squinted down at the map she was holding-"there should be an inn right here." She looked up, and I followed her gaze to a large building at the end of the block.
      "Perfect." The two of us made our way into the building, and I booked us a room for the night. We were on the second story of the building, and the city lights were a glittering maze outside the small window.
      Corinna immediately hurried over to the window and pressed her hands and nose against the glass. "It's so bright!"
      I smiled faintly at her reaction as I looked around the room. It was slightly larger than the last inn we had stayed in, and nicer too. More expensive. But that's what was to be expected from the capital city and all its riches.
      There was a wooden vanity with a lit glass lantern on the left side of the room, and I took a seat on the stool before unpinning my hat from my hair. The veil fell away, and my crimson eyes stared back at me from the mirror.
      I tilted my head to the side and silently watched the vampire in the mirror-the monster in the mirror-copy my every movement.
      "Talon?" The sound of Corinna's voice drew me back to reality.
      I turned away from the mirror to face her. "Is everything alright?"
      Corinna bit her lip. "I was about to ask you the same thing." Then she offered me a smile. "I'm fine. Just a little tired, that's all."
      I returned the smile before turning back to the mirror and got to work tugging out the hairpins Phina had placed in my hair. I blinked in surprise as I watched Corinna's reflection make her way toward me. She stopped directly behind me, and I turned in bewilderment.
      "May I?" Corinna asked hesitantly.
      I nodded my head.
      Corinna gently reached up and ever so carefully pulled the pins from my hair. I turned back to the mirror yet again, sitting as still as I could. "Is it weird that I'm a little surprised that you have a reflection?" Corinna met my eyes in the glass. "I heard that vampires aren't supposed to have reflections."
      "I don't know who started that silly rumor. Everything visible is going to get reflected."
      Corinna's eyes sparkled as she smiled faintly. "I suppose you're right. But I also heard that the reason why vampires can't be reflected is that they don't have souls-which is very ridiculous too because if that was the case, many humans wouldn't have reflections either."
      I burst out laughing at that. "And who told you that?"
      "One of the overseers back at the farm." Corinna skillfully twisted another pin from my hair. "I didn't believe him for a second. I would have told him that too if I hadn't been so intimidated by the sword at his side." She plucked the last pin from my hair, and my braid tumbled down my back. "Unfortunately, I don't have a comb," she said as she began untangling the messy braid, "but I'll do the best I can."
      "I can take it from here," I offered. "You should get some sleep."
      Corinna shook her head. "I don't mind. My younger sister used to have me braid her hair late at night, and I've been starting to miss it."
      There was a brief pause before I decided to ask a question that had been on my mind for some time now. "If you don't mind me asking, what exactly happened to your sister? Clarity, I mean."
      Corinna let out a heavy sigh. "Clarity's had a difficult time. There's not a lot one can do at the farms to get favors from the overseers. But by 'accompanying' an overseer at night, a slave woman can ask him for small things like medicine and bandages, for instance. I've never done it," she added quickly. "But Clarity has multiple times. Originally she had no plan to do so until she was asked by one of the overseers. She had no choice in the matter. Once, an overseer's wife was visiting the farm. When she caught Clarity with her husband, she tried to kill her. Even though Clarity doesn't admit it, my sister's never been the same."
      I felt a hot surge of anger bubble through my veins. "No one should have to go through that."
      "No one should," Corinna echoed darkly, "but they do. For my sister, I'd personally kill each and every overseer that laid a hand on her. My sister isn't the only one they've hurt. Countless others have suffered because of them."
      "Even if you are driven by revenge"-I lifted my eyes to meet her gaze in the mirror-"you shouldn't have to become a murderer because of it. Your hands are still clean. I'm already a monster. Leave the killing part to me."
      "You're not a monster."
      "I've killed people before, Corinna," I said as I turned to face her.
      "I know," Corinna said solemnly. "But I can see the pain in your eyes. Do you ever regret it?"
      I held her gaze. "Sometimes I do. Sometimes I don't. But it haunts me."
      There was a silence as Corinna gently turned my head back to the mirror and neatly finished my braid. Only then did she speak again. "Even though I want the overseers to suffer-to feel all the pain they've inflicted-I won't let that control my life." Corinna finally dropped her hands. Her voice was tired. "It's complicated. Even though I despise them for what they've done, I also believe in second chances. If I were ever in a situation where it was up to me to decide whether to let them live or die, I don't think I could actually kill them. I think I'd get more satisfaction knowing that they were locked up for life."
      I swiveled around to look up at Corinna. "That's what makes you different from them. Good people shouldn't have to do bad things. Because once you kill someone, there's no going back. Your hands will be stained with their blood forever."
      "The night we first met, you killed those two overseers."
      "I did," I said simply. "It's true that I didn't have to end their lives. I'm not trying to make excuses for what I did, but if I had left them alive, who is to say that they wouldn't try to do the same thing that they were planning to do to me to someone else?"
      Corinna sighed softly. "It is complicated. I just wish things didn't have to be this way. Why does there have to be so much hate and pain and death?"
      I dropped my gaze. "When it comes to power and absolute control, people stop seeing their fellow human beings as humans. Instead they view them as obstacles-or view them as puppets ready to manipulate into doing their bidding."
      Corinna's skin glowed gold in the light from the lantern. "I think that's the harsh reality. In such a world, have the humans become the monsters?"
      "The monster isn't always the one with the claws and fangs," I said darkly. Then I let out a sigh. "I hope I can find Karmen soon."
      "Karmen?"
      I lifted my head. "I'll finally be able to get some closure after all these years. She can end what she started. I want to be able to feel what it's like to be human one last time before I leave this world for good. And isn't death the most human thing?"
      Corinna shook her head firmly. "No. The most human thing is to live."
      Live. The word rang through the fog in my mind. Live, live, live.
      "Would you like to sit?" I stood up from the stool and hastily straightened my skirts. "It would only be fair if I helped you with your braid as well."
      "I'm afraid we'll have to save that for another time. I think I should get to bed."
      "That's probably for the best. I've got to meet Lynden and Phina soon anyway." I picked up my cloak from where I had dropped it by the door and fastened the heavy fabric over my shoulders. "I'll be gone for an hour at most."
      "Wait," Corinna called as I placed my hand on the door. I turned around with silent, questioning eyes. "The blanket last night . . . was that you?"
      I nodded. "Did I wake you?"
      "No, no." Corinna shook her head. A smile played on her face. "It makes me feel, well, it makes me feel happy."
      I found myself smiling too. "I'm glad."
      "Goodnight, then."
      "Goodnight, Corinna." I pushed open the door and glanced back over my shoulder before gently closing it behind me. Standing alone in the quiet hallway, I pressed my hands to my face. I was smiling.
      After shaking my head rapidly in an attempt to center myself, I forced myself to walk to the end of the hallway. I lingered there for a moment. My attention was caught by the snippets of conversations floating out from behind the closed doors. After meeting Lynden and Phina, there was one more stop I would need to make.
      I carefully opened the window. The wind rushed in, and snow caught in my hair as I quickly stepped out onto the window ledge. In one swift motion, I leaped up soundlessly onto the roof of the building. I looked down at the city lights spreading out for miles before me. This was the capital city. In the distance, the turrets of the royal castle cut through the night. Each glowing window was a prick of light the size of a candle flame.
      I sprung from where I stood and landed nimbly on the neighboring rooftop. I moved quickly, bounding from building to building. I was faster than the wind, faster than the night. The humans wouldn't notice me. To them, I was no more than a blur-a smudge against the midnight sky.
      As I flew across the city, the lights and sounds and colors passed me by at an almost dizzying pace. At last, I gracefully jumped down from the rooftops and landed in the middle of a dark alley.
      "Talon," Phina said excitedly as I faced my companions. The two of them seemed to have been in the middle of a quiet conversation before I joined them.
      "Greetings," Lynden said stiffly. The two vampires stood side by side with their blood-colored irises glowing. Phina was wearing one of the extra noblewoman dresses, and her ginger hair was in an elegant half-up, half-down style. I almost didn't recognize her.
      I dipped my head in acknowledgment. "Any luck?"
      Phina's face fell as she wrung her hands together. "No. There doesn't seem to be a Chloe-Jane anywhere."
      "We're going to keep looking." Lynden's tone was determined. "Who knows? Maybe the next shop we check will be the one."
      I arched a brow. "You sound oddly optimistic. Or are you just happy to get away from Storm?"
      Lynden frowned but remained silent.
      "We'll meet here again tomorrow night," Phina said. "Best of luck to both of you."
      "Likewise," Lynden replied. He vanished into the night with a rush of wind. Phina flashed me a sympathetic smile before disappearing.
      I wasn't sure what I had expected, but either way it looked like we had another long day ahead of us.
       
~
       
      "Welcome, welcome." The salesclerk waved us over from behind the counter of his shop. "Are you looking for anything in particular?"
      I glanced around the shop, pretending to take interest in the dresses hanging on the walls. Finally I flicked open my fan and stared down my nose at the clerk. "I'd like to take a look at your seamstresses."
      "My seamstresses?" the clerk repeated, taken aback.
      I exchanged a glance with Corinna. She inclined her head slightly, ready to search the back room for her sister.
      "If that's what you want, milady"-the clerk bowed-"your wish is my command."
      "My maid can-" I started, but the clerk cut me off.
      "Girls," the clerk hollered into the back room annoyedly. "Get out here! All of you!"
      Ten young girls filed out of the room. All of them had sunken heads and averted eyes.
      The clerk folded his arms over his chest. "Take your time. I've got some work to attend to in the back." I watched as he shuffled off into the back room.
      "Well that was-" I began, but when I turned to Corinna I found her staring at one of the young seamstresses in disbelief. I followed her gaze to the girl, who couldn't have been older than ten.
      I quickly put the pieces together in my head. "Is she the medicine girl you used to visit?" I asked quietly.
