      Corinna's eyes were wide as she nodded. Slowly Corinna made her way over to the girl and crouched down in front of her. I stood back and watched the girl slowly look up at Corinna. She blinked.
      Corinna, the girl mouthed.
      Corinna nodded, still in a state of disbelief. The girl glanced over at me before turning back to Corinna. "She's a friend." Corinna's voice was a breathy whisper. "We're looking for my sister."
      "Chloe-Jane," the girl said.
      "Yes." Corinna nodded vigorously. "Does she also work here? Do you know anything about what happened to her?"
      The medicine girl averted her gaze. "Chloe-Jane is here in the capital city, but she's not working as a seamstress." Corinna sucked in a breath as the medicine girl continued, "At first we were working together here at this very shop. The very next day, the king showed up."
      "The king?"
      "The king." The medicine girl nodded. "He came in with his knights and took her away."
      Panic flashed across Corinna's face. "The king took her away? Where is she now?"
      "She's at the castle." The medicine girl slowly looked up to meet Corinna's frantic gaze. "Haven't you heard? The king married Chloe-Jane just a few days ago. She's our queen now."
    

Chapter Eleven
       
"No." I shook my head as a dull ringing clouded my thoughts. Chloe-Jane married the king?
      The medicine girl wrung her hands together. "I know it sounds crazy, but it's true."
      "What was the king thinking?" My voice came out as a breathy whisper. People of high status wouldn't even think about mingling with slaves. "He married a slave girl. A slave."
      The medicine girl frowned. "I don't know what the king was thinking. But with that aside, do keep in mind that he was the one who ordered us to work as seamstresses here in the capital. He was the one who wanted to separate our families. If you want to see your sister, you're going to have to be very careful."
      I turned to look at Talon. I was still trying to process the new information. The vampire looked just as surprised as I felt, and her eyes were wide behind the veil.
      "You seem to be traveling with an interesting companion," the medicine girl said quietly. "You've got to be very careful or someone's going to end up seriously injured."
      "Don't worry. I know what I'm doing. And once I get my sister back, I'm going to help all of you as well." I wasn't sure who I was trying to reassure more-the medicine girl or myself.
      The medicine girl held my gaze. "I wouldn't make such a promise if I were you. Besides, once you get your sister, you're going to want to take your family and go somewhere very far away."
      The medicine girl was right. My family and I would be in danger if-when-we got Chloe-Jane out of the castle. But if we ran . . . running away would only help my family to be safe. Maybe my family and I could live freely, but could I really be happy knowing that others were still suffering with their own families torn apart?
      "Running away is always an option," I admitted. "But is it right? I don't think I'd be able to live with myself if I left all of you here at the mercy of the king. No one's going to get left behind. If I'm going to leave this kingdom, I'm going to take everyone with me. There must be a way."
      The corners of the medicine girl's mouth curled upward into a small smile. "Most of us gave up years ago. But your spark hasn't died."
      The door to the backroom flew open as the salesclerk reemerged. "Well? Is there anyone in particular that you have your eyes on?"
      "No," Talon said. She had replaced her surprised look with a mask of cool boredom. "We'll be on our way."
      "Hey!" The clerk protested as Talon turned on her heel. "You're not going to buy anything?" As the clerk continued to call after her, I slowly climbed to my feet and bowed my head to the medicine girl. She returned the gesture. I was reluctant to leave her here in the shop, but I forced myself to hurry after Talon.
      My head was spinning from my new knowledge. If Chloe-Jane had been in one of the shops, it would have been easy to sneak her out under the cover of night-getting her out of the castle was a completely different story. The castle was said to be the most secure place in the entire kingdom, with hundreds upon hundreds of knights guarding every entrance.
      Talon and I sat across from each other in silence. She was able to pay a carriage driver to take us all the way back to Andreus's city house, and now all I could do was stare blankly out the window and watch the rows of buildings roll by.
      "Think about it this way," Talon finally said. "At least now we know Chloe-Jane's exact location."
      "We know that she's in the most protected place in the kingdom." I turned to Talon as I pinched the bridge of my nose in an attempt to ward off a headache.
      "Just because it's a secure place doesn't mean that we can't break into it." Talon's eyes sparkled reassuringly as if she could sense my helplessness. "We'll come up with a plan."
      "You'll help me?"
      Talon nodded. "We've gotten this far. We're going to get your sister back."
      I let out a breath I hadn't realized I had been holding in. "Thank you."
      Talon's smile faded. "There is one problem, though. What if Chloe-Jane doesn't want to be saved? What if she likes being the queen?"
      I shook my head. "Chloe isn't like that-she's never thought about being a person with power before in her life. She has a carefree personality. She loves to run and laugh and smile. Royal life will suffocate her. But now that Chloe-Jane is queen," I continued slowly, "what kind of power does she hold? If she wanted to, would she be able to set all of those enslaved free?"
      Talon let out a soft sigh. "If it were just her ruling the kingdom, she'd be able to do it in a heartbeat. Right now, she's still second to the king. He can easily dismiss any of her proclamations if he doesn't like them."
      I felt my lips tug into a frown. Would it be better to leave Chloe in the castle? As queen, she'd get all the food and clothes she could ever ask for . . . No-she might be well off, but she wouldn't be happy. I know my sister well enough to determine that much.
      "Why Chloe-Jane?" My voice broke as I finally put that thought into words. "Of all the people the king could have married, why did it have to be my sister?"
      Talon squeezed my hands reassuringly. "Your sister is going to be alright. As the king's wife, no one can lay a hand on her."
      "No one except for the king himself." I dropped my gaze. Even though Talon's hands were neither warm nor cold, something about her touch made me believe that everything was going to be okay. "We don't know what kind of person the king is yet. He separates families and forces the slaves to work harder than ever in fear of punishment. And yet he still decides to marry a slave girl."
      "I heard that the first thing the new king did when he took over from his father was call for a stop to the war on the southern continent," Talon said slowly. "They have been fighting a pointless battle for years, and thousands on both sides have died. Those who didn't perish are going to return to the kingdom within the next couple of months."
      "The king put a stop to the war?" I looked up in surprise. "Where did you hear this?"
      Talon held my gaze. "Last night. I overheard someone talking about it at the inn, so of course I had to confirm it for myself after I met up with Lynden and Phina."
      I shook my head in bewilderment. "What was the war even about?" My father had been sent away all those years ago to fight in the name of the kingdom-to fight against the very people he had been stolen away from. "Both my father and brother had no choice but to go serve. Even when my brother returned, he had no clue what the fight had been about. I remember hearing it started due to arguments about trading, but I don't buy it."
      Talon sighed again as she released my hands. "It's not common knowledge to the public, but the war was about conquering the southern continent. The former king was hellbent on taking the territory for himself."
      "So the new king"-I furrowed my brow as I tried to piece everything together-"he's putting a stop to what his father started? Is that why he chose to marry Chloe? Because he wants to improve the kingdom's relationship with the southern continent?"
      Talon leaned back in her seat and crossed her arms over her chest. "It's hard to say. I'd like to think that's the case, but his orders for the farms contradict that statement, don't you think?"
      I nodded. "If he wants to improve his relationship with the people of the southern continent, he's not doing a good job. Instead of freeing the slaves-all of us being people from the southern continent-he had us work even harder than ever."
      Talon's frown deepened. "Not everyone knows that, though. In the eyes of the kingdom's citizens, it looks like he's doing good by putting a stop to the war."
      "All I can do now is hope that he doesn't do anything to Chloe-Jane." I closed my eyes for a brief moment.
      There was a long moment of silence until Talon spoke. "We'll be back at the house soon.  Tonight, I'll go let the others know that they can return to the house, and we can figure out what the best course of action will be from there."
      I exhaled through my nose before turning to look out the window. Chloe-Jane, please be alright.
       
~
       
      We arrived at the house a couple of hours before sunset. In an attempt to distract myself from the problem at hand, I headed down to the basement to practice swords with Talon. As our blades clashed together again and again, I found myself wondering through my daze whether the neighbors could hear the metallic ruckus.
      After calling it a day, Talon and I returned to the living room. And to my surprise, the vampire offered to let me try on her high heels in another attempt to take my mind off everything we had discovered about my younger sister's situation.
      But just ten minutes later, Talon and I sat next to each other on the living room couch with the high heels discarded on the floor a good distance away. I had examined my feet to find that the back of my ankles had become red and tender. I gingerly touched the raw skin and hissed quietly as pain blossomed from underneath my fingertip.
      Talon grimaced as she eyed my ankles. "I forgot that could happen. I'm sorry, Corinna."
      "Don't be sorry. I'll admit, the heels were actually quite fun." I looked over at the vampire. "On a more serious note, how can I ever repay you for your help?"
      Talon just shook her head, smiling softly. "Don't worry about it."
      "I'd be dead if it wasn't for you." I held Talon's gaze. "I never would have thought that I'd end up here in the capital city. In fact, I thought I'd work on the farm for my entire life. I honestly didn't think I'd live very long. Maybe I'd reach thirty or forty years, but that was about it. Now that I'm here, I'm finally allowing myself to think about the possibility of a different fate."
      Talon turned to gaze across the room, and her eyes grew distant. "Fate is an interesting thing. My fate led me to immortality. But what's the point of living forever? The pain of one lifetime is more than enough."
      "If you had someone to share immortality with, wouldn't it be nice to live with that special person forever?"
      "That would be nice." There was a distant look in Talon's eyes as she gazed across the room.
      "Did you have a special person in your heart at one point or another?" I asked softly. "Do you miss them?"
      Sadness flickered across Talon's face. "My parents. The way they were killed still haunts me until this day. Sometimes I wonder what they'd think if they saw their daughter now."
      "Did you choose to become a vampire to avenge your parents?"
      Talon laced her fingers together on her lap. "Yes and no. When Karmen found me that night, I was dying-bleeding out on the ground. I was scared. I felt so weak. So helpless. When Karmen made her offer, I didn't think twice when I accepted."
      I slowly nodded my head in understanding. "You want to know the reason why Karmen showed up that night to spare you from death."
      Talon dipped her chin. "Exactly. Why did she choose me? I wasn't the only one on the verge of death. And something tells me that Karmen doesn't just turn anyone into a vampire. I've never wanted to be associated with the queen-ever since she turned me, my existence has felt so wrong."
      "Do you know how many vampires Karmen turned-how many vampires are there exactly on the northern continent?"
      "No one's quite sure how many vampires the first progenitor turned besides Karmen," Talon explained. "It's rumored that the number is ten, but of course that rumor is questionable. As far as the total number of vampires here, I think it's safe to assume that there were somewhere around five hundred vampires on the northern continent the last time someone tried to count."
      "Only five hundred?" I wasn't sure what I had expected, but five hundred seemed like a very small number in the grand scheme of things. "But what about in the southern continent? Are there vampires there too?"
      "You won't find any vampires in the southern continent-there's too much sun there."
      "Did you ever consider the possibility that Karmen could have decided to hide there?" I questioned.
      Talon slumped down in her seat. "I definitely considered it. After all those years of searching for her, I was beginning to come to that conclusion. But then I found the body of that vampire in the forest. That was when I realized that Karmen was still here. She probably hadn't even left at all for that matter. It kind of clicked after that-the only place I hadn't searched for the queen was the capital city. I had been avoiding the capital city if I could help it. But it turns out she is probably here after all. Oh, look outside. It's already dark."
      I turned in surprise to the window. Talon was right-the curtains were no longer glowing with the light from the fading sun.
      "I better go." Talon stood up from the couch, and her long hair cascaded to the floor. "I'll be back before morning."
      I nodded silently as Talon fastened her cloak.
      Talon turned to face me. "Lynden and Phina will likely return with the others sometime tomorrow afternoon. We'll get your sister back one way or another. I promise."
      I stood up as well, and my feet protested as I walked over to meet Talon by the front door. "Be careful out there."
      Talon's delicate features softened as her face melted into a smile. "Of course." And with one last glance back at me, Talon pushed open the door and slipped out onto the snow-covered street beyond. I lifted a hand in farewell as I watched the vampire disappear into the night.
      Sighing, I gently closed the door. The silence was beginning to press down on me as I wandered aimlessly through the empty house. I found myself in the kitchen a few moments later; the rumbling of my stomach told me that I needed food. After I had found myself something to eat, I made my way up the stairs to the bedroom Clarity and I had shared. I was exhausted-both mentally and physically.
      I drew the curtains, then collapsed onto the bed and stared up at the dark ceiling. We now knew Chloe-Jane's exact location. How difficult will it be to break into the castle? I wondered. I didn't know myself, but something told me that between Lynden, Phina, and Talon, at least one of them would be able to figure something out.
      If I couldn't break into the castle like the rest of them, maybe I could somehow  sneak in. No. What was I even thinking? Breaking into the castle meant that I would become an enemy of the kingdom-an enemy of the king himself. I'd have to take my family and go somewhere very far away.
      I let out a dry laugh. I was already an enemy of the kingdom, wasn't I? I had never belonged here. People from the southern continent had been seen as outcasts only to be used from the very beginning. I belong in the place where my mother and father were born-in the southern continent I had yet to see with my own eyes.
      But did I? I wasn't born there. Would the people of the southern continent even accept me? I didn't belong here nor there. So if that were the case, where did I belong?
      I watched the dust as it lazily swirled through the air, illuminated by the pearly light filtering in through the gap in the curtains. For the first time in a very long time, I felt alone.
      There was no Mother or Father here. No Cameren, Clarity, or Chloe-Jane by my side. No Storm, Lynden, Phina, or Talon. I felt my chest tighten, and I flipped over onto my side. I drew my knees to my chest as if they could ease the sharp pang. Then squeezing my eyes shut, I took a deep breath. Even if Mother and Cameren weren't here with me now, they were safe. Clarity was safe too. I trusted that Phina would make sure no harm came to my sister. Chloe-Jane was the only one I needed to worry about right now. My sister's scared face flashed across my mind, followed by the sound of her scream when she pushed me away from the overseer's sword.
      I opened my eyes, suddenly no longer tired. I slowly sat up and brushed my fingers over the soft blankets on top of the bed. Compared to the tiny house my family and I had been living in just a handful of weeks ago, this house was a complete luxury.
      I walked over to the window, pushed the curtains aside, and let the moonlight spill into the room. I rested my arms on the windowsill and my chin on my arms. And for a while, I just stared out at the silent night sky beyond the icy glass.
      They were all out there somewhere. My family. My new allies. Talon.
      It was strange to think that even though we were so far apart, we were all under the same sky. I wondered if Father was out there somewhere-if he was somewhere on the southern continent or in the sky itself.
      I let out a soft sigh as I watched a lone snowflake spiral past the window, carried on a gust of wind. In a blink of an eye, the snowflake disappeared into the dark. Even though I could no longer see it, I knew it was still dancing. And it would continue to dance-continue to fight-until it was no more.
      The snowflake's story is a tragic one. It was only a matter of time before it hit the ground, and then only a matter of time after that before the sun would reduce it to nothing.
      The snowflake and I were very similar. But unlike the snowflake, I was not alone.

Chapter Twelve
       
I landed in the middle of the dimly lit alley in a flurry of snow. The sounds of the bustling city outside floated in from beyond the walls, and I didn't have to wait long before Lynden and Phina appeared. Their faces were hidden in the depths of their hooded cloaks.
      "No one seems to know anything about her." Phina pulled back her hood with a worried expression on her face. "None of the shops we checked today have a Chloe-Jane."
      Lynden lowered his hood. "No luck here either."
      I tugged my hood off too and shook out my long hair. "Well, I have news for the two of you."
      "Good news?" Phina asked at the same time Lynden said, "It has to be bad news."
      I folded my arms over my chest matter-of-factly. "Chloe-Jane is at the castle. She's the queen now."
      "The queen?" Phina blinked as if she couldn't believe what she was hearing. "But-but she's fourteen years old, isn't she?"
      "What was the king thinking?" Lynden shook his head in disbelief. "The royal family never married anyone who wasn't of high status. Even regular servants were out of the question."
      "Something big is going to happen," I said grimly. "Things don't change drastically without a reason behind them. And we need to get Corinna's sister out of harm's way before they do."
      "We'll head back to the house first thing in the morning," Phina said faintly. She tugged absently on a strand of her hair. "The poor girl. The royal family is known for despising people they deem as inferior to their noble blood. This new king can't be any different than those who came before him."
      Lynden let out a tired sigh. "I agree fully. But what if the new king really does want to change things for the better?"
      I leveled Lynden a look. "Do you believe that? It's difficult to say what the king wants. His actions so far have contradicted each other. First he ordered the slaves to work harder than ever, then he decided to stop the war on the southern continent and take a slave girl as his bride."
      Lynden frowned. "It doesn't quite add up. But as long as Chloe-Jane is at the castle, she's at the mercy of those around her, even if she is the queen."
      "Exactly."
      "We could break into the castle," Lynden said slowly. "The three of us could do it."
      Phina elbowed Lynden halfheartedly. "Don't you know that the castle has anti-vampire defenses?"
      "What kind of anti-vampire defenses?" Lynden arched a brow. "What even are anti-vampire defenses? I've never heard about them before."
      Phina sighed. "That I don't know. But I do remember hearing about them adding something of the sort when they did renovations about twenty years ago. I don't know if said measures even work, but we shouldn't take our chances. What we need is a map of the castle, its layout, and where all of the defenses are."
      I looked over at Phina. "Now that you're mentioning it, I do remember there being talk about methods to prevent vampires from entering the premises. That would mean that these so-called traps are likely somewhere outside. They wouldn't want vampires to get inside, would they?"
      Lynden nodded slowly. "The windows and doors seem like a very likely place for traps. If there is such a thing, our best bet would be to have someone disable them from the inside."
      I tucked a loose strand of hair behind one of my delicately pointed ears. "Let's not be too hasty about this. Before we do anything, we'll need to covertly get our hands on a map of the castle. If there really are traps, we'll have to be extra careful. If the king somehow manages to connect us to Corinna and her family-or even Storm for that matter-we'll be putting them in constant danger for the remainder of their lives."
      Phina scrunched her freckled nose, deep in thought. "You're right. We should try to learn as much about the new king as we possibly can-hear what the public has to say about him."
      "And if we're lucky," Lynden added, "find someone on the inside who can provide us with information."
      Suddenly, I felt a shiver run down my spine. Amid all the human presences, I could sense an immortal in our midst-a vampire. And for me to be able to sense them among that many people, they had to be close.
      I exchanged a glance with Lynden and Phina. Both of them nodded gravely. They had sensed it too.
      Phina's eyes widened as they landed on something-or someone-over my shoulder. "Who's there?"
      I whirled around, but whoever had been there was gone. My eyes briefly snagged on the tail of a long back cloak fluttering in the wind.
      Lynden narrowed his eyes as he stared at the spot where the figure had vanished. "That was a vampire. There's no doubt about it."
      "Did either of you see their face?" I asked as I turned to my companions.
      Phina's expression was uncharacteristically serious. "I couldn't see under their hood."
      "Could it have been Karmen?" Lynden mused quietly, voicing the exact thing I had been wondering.
      "It must be," I said darkly. "What other vampire would be wandering the city?"
      "That I can't say for sure." Phina's frown deepened. "But what I do know is that whoever they were, they saw my face and Lynden's face too. I don't think they saw yours, though, Talon."
      "Should we chase them?" Lynden asked sharply. "If we go now, we could still catch up with them."
      "No," I said tiredly. "If that really was Karmen, we don't want to engage her right now. Chloe-Jane is our top priority at the moment, not the queen of the vampires."
      Lynden and Phina nodded.
      "I'll take my leave," I said. Then I tugged on my hood, sprung into the air, and landed silently on a snow-covered rooftop.
      "Please be careful out there," Phina called after me.
      "I'll try to find information on the castle," Lynden added. "We'll make our way back to the house first thing in the morning."
      I just nodded down to them, then leaped into the night.
      Karmen was here. She was in the capital city. But that didn't come as a surprise; we had all known that coming here. It had to be Karmen, I thought. Because if the vampire who we had seen in the alley wasn't the queen . . .
      After landing on another building, I glanced down at the sea of lights flickering and dancing along the streets. Even in the night, the city never saw the dark.
      I arrived back at Andreus's house in no time, and I lowered my hood as I perched on the roof. I found myself looking out at the darkness of a familiar forest. It had been years since I had been back there, but I figured a short detour wouldn't hurt.
      I soundlessly jumped from the roof, then hurried down the empty street. I traversed the city until the streetlamps disappeared completely, and I found myself taking my first step into the woods. The moon disappeared behind the trees, and I was bathed in complete darkness. I couldn't have been more than a mile away from Andreus's city house, but somehow I felt as if I were in a completely different place.
      I slowed to a walk, and my feet moved on their own accord. I could hear the bubbling of water before the small stream even came into view. Something tightened in my chest as I kept moving forward.
      Before I could second-guess myself, the house came into view. Sitting on the edge of the large clearing, the little wooden house was exactly as I remembered it. Well, almost exactly as I remembered it-vines had snaked up the sides of the building, and the weeds had completely hidden the front porch steps.
      A wistful smile tugged at my lips as I stared at the house. This was once my home with the sisters Miah and Dahlia.
      But the sisters were gone now. Out of the three of us, I was the only one still alive. For those seven precious days, I really believed that we would be able to live a peaceful life together.
      I closed my eyes as I tucked all my thoughts and emotions into the furthest corner of my mind. It wouldn't do me any good to dwell on them for too long-because if I did, the insanity would start to creep in. I knew that after it sunk its claws into my being, it would rip me apart.
      I slowly opened my eyes as a soft breeze sent strands of my hair flying. The moonlight bounced off the small stream running through the clearing, and its light stained the water silver.
      In one swift motion, I leaped onto the front porch of the house. I tapped my foot a few times, and when the wood didn't crumble under my weight, I tried stomping. It was solid; the wood was still holding up.
      I felt some of the weight lift off my chest. Good.
      Next I reached for the door handle, and ever so carefully, I pushed the door open and peered into the familiar room beyond. All the furniture was exactly as I had left it. The house was still fairly empty because we hadn't bought much during our seven days living in it. As I made my way further into the living room, I ran my hand lightly over the back of the couch and then over the glass lamp beside it.
      Before I knew it, I found myself facing the back wall of the living room and the doors leading to the two bedrooms beyond. The sisters' room was on the right, and mine was on the left.
      I hesitantly placed my hand on the handle of the right door, but my nerves got the better of me, and I pushed open the door to my room instead. A bed sat in the corner of the room, pressed up against the curtain-drawn window.
      A vanity sat on the opposite side of the room with its mirrors covered in heavy layers of dust. I walked over to the vanity, dragging the hem of my cloak over the dusty ground as I went. I carefully pulled open the first drawer beneath the wooden surface. Rows of daggers and knives glinted back at me. Their blades were dull and dusty.
      I let out a dry laugh as I gently shut the drawer. What did I need so many knives for? The second drawer revealed sticks of charcoal and boxes of powder, and the final drawer was completely empty.
      I shook my head as I exited the room. Then finally mustering the courage, I silently opened the second door and stepped into the room beyond. A wave of emotion washed over me at the sight of the sisters' room, and I stilled. All of their belongings were still arranged neatly on the shelves on either side of their wooden dresser. And if I blinked my eyes, I could almost see their smiling faces swim across my vision for a brief moment.
      I dropped to my knees.
      Happiness is fleeting, Miah once told me. You've got to enjoy what you have whether it lasts for a minute, or a day, or a year.
      My sister's right, Dahlia had added. Our lives could end at any moment. So with that in mind, we should spend all of our time together being happy.
      I stared unseeingly at the faded carpet. Even though I was completely immune to the cold, I found myself shaking. But whether I was shaking with sorrow or fear or anger, I couldn't tell. Either way, I couldn't stay here for long. I needed to get back to Andreus's house. Corinna was waiting for me.
      After slowly climbing to my feet, I backed out of the room and gently shut the door behind me. The sisters were right: happiness is indeed fleeting. The years I spent in the forest after their deaths were not especially happy ones. But now I was traveling again with a new group of individuals-traveling alongside both humans and vampires. Even if I was still wary of the latter, I felt more alive now than I had been in years.
      I stepped back into what had been my room and made my way to the vanity again. After pulling open the first drawer, I began sorting through the blades and picking out the ones that could fetch a high price. As I was rummaging among the blades, my fingers brushed up against what felt like a scrap of paper.
      I set the daggers aside and carefully picked up the paper. I unfolded the scrap and took a seat on my bed as I smoothed out the crumpled corners. It was a letter.
      To our dearest Talon, Dahlia's curly handwriting read. I quickly brushed my hair over my shoulder and began to read:
       
      When you find this note, Miah and I will probably already be gone. We don't want you to blame yourself, Talon. We know that you will, so let us tell you right here and now that it is our decision to return to the capital city. The guards have planted eyes everywhere in the city and are keeping a lookout for us. The message is clear: they want us to stay out of the city. But we will not leave.
      While people are still suffering, we cannot turn a blind eye. Staying here in this house would be the easy way out. Fleeing would also be the easy way out. Maybe we would get to live a little longer, but at whose expense? Maybe we would get to experience happiness for a little longer, but who will suffer in our stead? You have trained us to be warriors, and with our blades we will protect and defend those who need us the most.
      Maybe it's my fault for falling in love with that boy. Maybe I'm to blame for how he eagerly sold our names and identities to the royal guards. Either way, Miah and I are bound to get arrested or worse sooner than later. That much is inevitable.
      They say love makes someone a fool. And fools are destined to meet a tragic end, aren't they? Miah was always the romantic one out of the two of us, not me. I never would have thought that I would end up being the one to have my heart broken.
      Miah and I are heading out again tonight. This time, I fear we won't be returning. Do you hear what they call us? Witches. They won't hesitate to take us down. We can't go on like this. You staying around us is just putting yourself at risk. I know you can easily take down dozens of armed men, but can you handle an angry mob of hundreds upon hundreds of people?
      My sister and I don't kill people. We never have. Knocking out that many people is an impossible task even for the three of us. These aren't people who will settle for knocking us out. These people won't hesitate to kill us.
      Talon, I'm so glad I got to meet you in this short life. You've always been like a sister to Miah and me. We love you dearly, you know. We're sorry for sending you out of the city, but neither of us regret that decision. If we don't end up seeing each other again, promise us one thing: promise us that you'll spend your life being happy. Live, Talon. Live for the three of us.
      From the bottom of our hearts, we thank you for everything. Thank you for giving us a chance at life.
       
      Dahlia & Miah
       
      I reread the letter. Once. Twice. Three times.
      This letter had been here in my drawer for years.
      I clutched the scrap of paper to my chest. My hands and shoulders were shaking. When I had rushed all the way back to the capital city, all that remained of Dahlia and Miah were their ashes. I could still remember the lingering scent of smoke and the even more nauseating smell of burning flesh. In the end, it seemed like I had saved the girls from one miserable fate just to condemn them to another.
      After finally setting the letter down on the dusty blankets beside me, I turned to the window and pushed the curtains aside. Silver moonlight streamed into the room as it filtered through the numerous vines spiraling up the glass outside.
      I let myself fall backward onto the bed and stared up at the ceiling. I had failed the sisters. I had failed myself as well. For the longest time, I had been neither dead nor alive. I had just existed. Existed somewhere in my own dark world of misery and regret-a world gifted to me by the queen of the vampires.
      But things were different now. Now I had a purpose. I had been given the chance to unite a family that had been torn apart.
      I lifted my hand to my face, and my skin glowed silver in the moonlight. Even after all of these years, I hadn't changed. And at the same time, I was a completely different person.
      When I closed my eyes, I could almost picture my homeland with the vibrant grass that seemed to extend forever. I could almost smell the sweetness of the flowers-could almost see Mother's laughing face and radiant smile that made her appear much younger. But her face was blurring in and out of focus. The memories were slowly fading. All of them were.
      My name. My name was on Mother's lips, but all I could hear was silence.
      What was my name?
      I pinched the bridge of my nose, furrowing my brow as I tried to remember. Even though it hadn't been something I used or heard in years, how could I have forgotten such an important part of myself?
      After opening my eyes, I slowly sat up and climbed to my feet. I carefully tucked the letter into one of my coat pockets before filling my others with daggers. It was time for me to head back. I silently made my way out of my room, through the living room, and out of the front door. And then with one final glance back over my shoulder at the little house, I leaped into the night.
       
~
       
      The stars were still glittering in the slowly brightening sky, and I arrived back at Andreus's house in a matter of minutes. I quietly pushed open the door, but then froze with my fingers wrapped around the handle as the scent of blood shoved itself up my nose.
      I dropped my cloak, and the metallic thud from all the daggers sounded in my ears as I flew up the stairs. Has something happened to Corinna? In my state of alarm, it was only when I was at the top of the staircase that I realized Corinna's presence was in the backyard and not her bedroom. I spun on my heel and hurried back down the steps. I threw open the door to the yard and skidded to a stop on the wooden deck.
      Corinna's hair glowed in the silvery light as she turned to look at me in surprise. She was in the middle of attaching a blanket to one of the clothing lines stretching from fence to fence. Corinna clutched her chest with her free hand. "You startled me."
      Relief swept over me. "You're okay."
      "Of course I'm okay." Corinna blinked again, clearly bewildered as she went back to hanging up her blanket.
      "I smelled blood." I took a seat on the wooden porch with my feet dangling over the tall grass. "In fact, I still smell it on you."
      Corinna let out a laugh as she walked over to take a seat next to me. "I was a little confused at first, but then I realized that I had gotten my cycle. Even though this was the first time, I kind of knew what to expect." She spoke with no trace of embarrassment, and her eyes were clear as they watched the moon's slow descent across the sky. "My mother told me that most girls get theirs between the ages of ten and sixteen, but I think my sisters and I were too malnourished on the farm."
      "I see." I lifted my head to the stars as well. "I think I first got mine when I was twelve or thirteen. But once I became a vampire, that was the end of it."
      Corinna tapped her chin thoughtfully. "I guess that would make sense. Vampires and humans don't reproduce in the same way, after all."
      "All a vampire needs to do to turn someone is have that person drink their cursed blood. Vampires are like corpses-and corpses don't menstruate."
      "I don't think comparing vampires with corpses is fair." Corinna glanced at me. "The more I think about it, vampires aren't like corpses at all. When it comes down to it, the vampire is still alive in some sense. Corpses, on the other hand, have lost the ability to think for themselves."
      I let out a weak laugh. "You're right. Anyway, do you need help finding something to use as a liner?"
      "I was able to find some cloth in the washroom. I should be okay for the time being." Then she climbed to her feet. "We should head back inside. Sunrise is only minutes away."
      I followed her lead, and the two of us walked into the living room. Corinna shuffled over to where I had dropped my cloak on the floor and bent down to pick it up. A metallic clank sounded as she attempted to lift it.
      Corinna stared at the cloak. "What did you put in here?"
      "Daggers." I knelt down at her side and emptied the contents of my cloak onto the carpeted floor. "They don't look like much right now, but after I restore them to their former glory, we can sell them for a good price."
      "Do I want to ask where they came from?"
      "Don't worry." I carefully folded the daggers back into the fabric of my cloak. "They're mine. Do you remember those two sisters I was telling you about back at Andreus's mountain house? The three of us bought a house outside the capital city. I hadn't been back there in years and decided to check it out. I bought these daggers years ago and have little use for them now." As I rolled the daggers tightly up into my cloak, the letter from the sisters fluttered out of one of the pockets.
      "What's this?" Corinna asked curiously.
      "I found it at the house." I stared down at the letter. My feelings were still a mess. "It was the goodbye letter to me that I never saw until today."
      "May I take a look?"
      "Go ahead."
      Corinna gingerly picked up the letter and unfolded the paper. Her eyes slowly traveled down the page as she silently mouthed the words.
      "If you don't mind me asking, where did you learn to read?" I asked. "I know for a fact that the overseers don't take it upon themselves to educate their slaves."
      "My mother taught my older siblings and me when we were younger," Corinna recalled. "At the time, she was still working in the master's house. I'm not too sure where or who she learned the alphabet from, but she would come home to us and teach us the letters. I don't think I was older than six or seven at the time, but Clarity and Cameren helped me practice when Mother couldn't be there. Reading is quite easy, actually. Once you know the letters, everything else is phonetic. So even if I'm not sure what a word is, it doesn't take much for me to sound it out."
      I sucked in a breath. "Did your mother ever get caught?"
      There was a distant look in Corinna's eyes. "Fortunately she never did. She even managed to smuggle out a book for us to look at once-well, granted that she had to smuggle it back into the master's house the following day to avoid anyone noticing that it had gone missing. The punishment for a slave knowing how to read or write is having the fingernails in one's right hand torn off. They'll whip us, beat us, and do other horrible things, but they're hesitant to kill us. Ever since the war started, all shipment of people from the southern continent was halted.
      "My mother eventually was kicked out of the master's house and demoted to a field worker-not because they figured out she had learned to read, but rather because she had gotten pregnant, and the master didn't want to take responsibility for the child. Sadly enough, this type of situation is quite common, though. We don't dare to disobey our master's orders for fear of what would become of our family otherwise. Dahlia and Miah," Corinna said as she reached the end of the letter. "I know I've never met them before, but I can tell from their words alone that they truly loved you."
      "They were like sisters to me," I whispered. I didn't trust myself to speak as my voice broke. "I just wish I could have had more time with them."
      Corinna stood up from the ground before carefully refolding the letter. "Would you tell me about the first time you met them? You could tell me about all the adventures the three of you went on together. You can relive their story. If you feel up to it, that is."
      I stared up at Corinna as she offered me a soft smile. "I'd like that, actually."
      Corinna offered me a hand, and I took it. I interlaced my fingers with hers as she pulled me to my feet.
      "We can get to work polishing up the daggers as we talk," Corinna said as she led me over to the dining room table and took a seat. "How does that sound?"
      "I'll go grab what we need."
      Five minutes later, the two of us were sitting at the table with all the knives neatly laid out on the wood in front of us. The sun had just risen outside, and the curtains over the windows glowed faintly with the golden light.
      I picked up the first dagger and turned it over in my hands. "The story starts many years ago."

Chapter Thirteen
       
I listened intently as Talon spoke about Dahlia and Miah. Each tale was more fascinating than the one before it, and I found myself completely drawn into the stories. It was only a matter of time before the two of us had all the blades on the table polished to a gleam.
      I wasn't sure how long I listened or how long Talon spoke, but it must have been hours because our conversation was cut short by the sound of a knock at the door. I exchanged a glance with Talon. The vampire nodded before she rose from her seat and glided across the room to the door.
      "It's Phina," Phina's voice sang from the other side of the wood. "And Clarity."
      Talon pushed open the door, and Phina hopped over the threshold with Clarity close at her heels. I let out the breath I hadn't realized I had been holding in as I stood up to greet them.
      "Is it true?" Clarity demanded immediately as she marched over to me. "Is it true that Chloe-Jane is the queen?"
      "Yes," I answered seriously. "I found it hard to believe at first, but it's true."
      Clarity's shoulders slumped as she shook her head. "How did this even happen?"
      "Your guess is as good as mine," I said tiredly. "You must be exhausted from your trip. I'll go find you something to eat-"
      "Don't bother," Clarity said shortly. "I'll go find something myself." And with that, I watched my sister turn and disappear into the kitchen without a second glance. Clarity seemed more irritable than usual, but that was only because she was tired.
      "I don't think she slept at all," Phina said quietly as if she could tell what I was thinking. Her expression was sad. "She was too apprehensive of me the entire time we traveled together. Honestly, I think she would have been better off traveling with Storm. At least he's a human."
      I sighed. "Don't take it too personally. Clarity isn't exactly the most trusting person."
      Phina offered me a tired smile before walking over to take a seat on the vacant couch. She was still dressed in her noblewoman outfit, and I looked on as she kicked off her high heels before absently pulling pins out of her wavy hair.
      We didn't have to wait long before Storm and Lynden arrived back at the house too. The former had a look of annoyance on his face, and the latter had an expression of austerity.
      "I did some wandering through the city last night," Lynden explained to the quizzical looks cast in his direction. "It seems like Queen Chloe-Jane is the talk of the town. And not in a good way."
      "Long story short," Storm cut in, "she's not very popular among the people. They don't think very highly of her at all."
      Lynden narrowed his eyes. "They're not happy with the king either. They don't understand how or why he could have married a slave girl. And they've made it clear that they certainly don't want a slave girl as their queen. Do you know what they've been saying about Chloe-Jane?"
      "What?" I asked as a feeling of dread slowly seeped in.
      "They're calling her a witch," Lynden said grimly. "They're saying that she bewitched the king into marrying her."
      "But she did no such thing!" Phina frenziedly jumped up from the couch. She nearly tripped over the shoes she had discarded in her haste. "How sick do they need to be to accuse a little girl of witchcraft?"
      Bewitched the king into marrying her? The people of the capital city would go as far as accusing a fourteen-year-old? I turned to look at the dining room table where Clarity sat. My sister's lips were pursed as if she had just eaten something sour. Her back was stiff, and her hands were clenched together on the wood in front of her.
      After a long moment of silence, Storm said, "So, are we actually gonna break into the castle?"
      "There has to be a better way." Phina wrung her hands together in front of her frilly skirts. "Can't we find a time when Chloe-Jane is outside the castle to take her away?"
      "Do the royals here ever leave their castles?" Lynden asked. "The previous queen was said to have never made a single public appearance. Even her funeral was kept private."
      "The only time royals leave their castles is to attend events such as meetings and balls," Talon added. "But trying to kidnap Chloe-Jane in front of all of those people will be problematic."
      "If I break into the castle," Storm said slowly, his face paling, "I'll become an enemy of the kingdom."
      "That's right." Clarity's tone was cold. "You'll no longer be the beloved hero."
      Storm crossed his arms over his chest. "I don't need that title anyway. They're just words after all. I want to help reunite your family. You asked me for help and I want to see it through. Besides, if I do become an enemy of the kingdom, I'll just go hide out with my uncle for some time. He can protect me."
      "No one said that you need to break into the castle," Lynden said, vaguely amused.
      Storm frowned distastefully. "I want to help."
      "We'll need people on the outside in case something goes wrong," Lynden continued. "You're more than welcome to take that job."
      "Perfect." Storm clapped his hands together. "I reckon I can do that."
      Lynden inclined his head. "We'll also need someone to find us an informant. Theoretically they would be someone who knows a lot about the castle and isn't afraid to give us the information."
      "I can find a person," Storm said quickly. "I think I know where to look."
      "Perfect." Lynden's expression remained the same. "Then what are you waiting for?"
      Storm's head snapped up to look at Lynden. "You want me to go right now? But-but we just got back."
      "Will you be alright out there by yourself?" Phina asked with large eyes.
      "Wha-?" Storm turned to the ginger-haired vampire. "Yes! Of course I'll be fine!" Storm stomped up the stairs and returned minutes later dressed in traveling attire. He muttered angrily under his breath on the way to the door. "I'll find someone by the end of the week," he said. "Just you wait!" And with that, the dark-haired boy marched out of the house and slammed the door shut behind him.
       "I know you don't like him, but you could have at least let him rest," I said with a glance in Lynden's direction.
      Talon nodded in agreement.
      "Do you think he can really find someone?" I asked uncertainly. "I'm not sure how easy it would be to find someone who would willingly spill their knowledge of how to infiltrate the castle."
      "Oh, I'm confident he can do it," Phina said brightly. "We wouldn't have given him such a task otherwise." Then Phina turned to look at Talon. "Last night I tried to track down the vampire we saw. I followed their trail to the city square, but then I lost them."
      "Vampire?" Clarity asked sharply.
      "We saw a vampire last night," Lynden explained. "Whoever they were, they seemed to be spying on us."
      My voice dropped to a whisper. "Karmen?"
      Phina's expression was serious again as she tugged on a strand of her hair. "We don't know. None of us saw their face. But they saw ours."
      Clarity's mouth was a hard line. "Is that going to be a problem?"
      "No," Talon answered her. "Considering that they ran away when we noticed them, they aren't interested in engaging us. Not right now, at least."
      Here was yet another variable that we needed to account for: what did the presence of other vampires in the city mean for us? Would they interfere with the rescue mission? I knew that whoever that vampire was, they couldn't care less about my sister. But would they try to drag Lynden, Phina, and Talon away?
      "We're not going anywhere, Corinna," Talon reassured me as she read my expression. "We shouldn't worry too much about that vampire right now. It isn't unheard of for vampires to live in the capital city. Maybe they just sensed our presence and were curious to see what other vampires were doing in the city."
      I nodded, but the uncertain feeling remained.
      There was a brief pause, then Lynden spoke up. "Now that that's out of the way, it wouldn't hurt to try to get some information about the outside of the castle. We're going to need an escape route after all. And a backup plan in case things don't go as expected. I can go look around. I saw a library earlier on the way back to the house. Maybe there will be something useful there."
      "I'll join you!" Phina said energetically.
      Lynden sighed as he offered Phina the faintest trace of a smile. "There's no need for that. I want some time to myself."
      Phina's face fell. "Alright, then."
      "I'll be back before sunset." Lynden turned on his heel and disappeared out the front door.
      "What now?" Phina looked from Talon to me, then finally to Clarity.
      "We wait," Talon said simply.
      Phina wrinkled her freckled nose. "I want to make myself useful as well."
      "I have an idea." Talon hurried over to the table where all of our newly polished knives glimmered in the flickering lamplight. "You can sell these for us."
      "Okay!" Phina perked up excitedly. Then she hesitated as she gave Talon a suspicious look. "Where did you get so many daggers from?"
      Talon flipped one of the daggers over in her hand to examine its blade. "They're mine. I bought them the last time I was here in the capital city. I don't need that many knives."
      "If you say so." Phina took the blades from Talon and carefully packed them away into a bag. Shortly after, she was skipping out the door.
      "I'm going to bed," Clarity announced once the ginger-haired vampire had vanished.
      I watched my sister stand from the table and make her way upstairs, leaving me alone in the living room with Talon. "I guess it's just us again."
      Talon set down the dagger she was holding. "I guess so."
      "Do you think we could do some training?" I asked. "This time I might be able to keep up with you."
      "Are you sure you feel up for it? It won't hurt to take a day off to rest."
      "I appreciate the offer, truly," I said, smiling. "But I want to keep doing my part to get stronger."
      The corners of Talon's lips tugged upward. "Okay. If you really want to continue training, I won't go easy on you."
      I laughed. "I'm counting on it."
       
~
       
      The sun had just dipped below the horizon when I climbed back up the wine cellar's ladder to the living room, completely spent. Even though I felt like I could collapse at any moment, I was still standing. That itself was definitely an improvement from our past training sessions.
      Talon beamed as she extended a hand to help me up the last few rungs of the ladder. "You're getting better!"
      I found myself smiling despite my exhaustion as I reached up to take it. "I'm still no match for you."
      "Strategy is key." Talon's eyes sparkled knowingly as she pulled me to my feet. "Even if your opponent is stronger than you are, with the right strategy you can still take them down."
      "Maybe that's the case with other humans, but I doubt I could ever go up against a vampire-with or without a strategy." Then a knock sounded on the door.
      Talon turned at the sound. "It looks like Lynden's back."
      The two of us made our way over to the door, and opened it. Lynden stood in the doorway. His face and eyes were hidden in the shadowy depths of his cloak, and a large bag was slung over his shoulder, filled with rectangular shapes.
      "Don't tell me that you've got the entire library in there." Talon's tone was that of mild amusement.
      "I don't," Lynden said stiffly as he crossed the threshold. He let the bag fall to the floor with a loud thump. "These are all I could find about the castle."
      I eyed the bag. "On one hand, I'm surprised that there are so many books about it; if people know too much, wouldn't that make it a target? But then, on the other hand, it is the most important building in the capital city; of course people would want to know about the place the royal family resides."
      "I'm sure they left out anything that could be used against them," Lynden said flatly as he folded up his cloak and placed it on the floor next to the door. "They won't say anything that would make them look bad either."
      "I would be surprised if that wasn't the case." Talon flipped her braid over her shoulder. "How long will it take us to get through that many books?"
      Lynden frowned. "Between you, Phina, and me, maybe three or four days if we don't take any breaks."
      Three or four days. Things weren't going to happen instantly. They were going to require time and a solid plan. It looked like Chloe-Jane would have to keep holding on for a little longer. I would offer to help read the books, but even though I could read, it took me a while to sound out the words either out loud or in my head. Getting through just one of the books in the bag would probably take me an entire day.
      Talon picked up the bag of books as if it weighed no more than a feather. "We might as well get started, then." She opened the bag, pulled out one of the books, and took a seat on the couch.
      "I think I'm going to head upstairs," I said. "I'm going to bed."
      "Wait," Lynden called as I turned to make my way up the stairs. I turned back around to watch the brown-haired vampire hurry over to the bag and pull out a stack of books. "Bring these up for your sister to look at."
      I took the books from Lynden, and my tired arms burned from the weight. I craned my neck to read the cover of the book at the top of the stack. "Medicine? These are books on medicine."
      "Phina requested that I find them for your sister," Lynden said as he returned to the bag of books. "She claimed that Clarity would find them interesting."
      I carefully began my tedious climb up the stairs, then made my way down the dark hallway with the pile of books swaying dangerously in my arms. With my hip, I pushed open the door to our room and blinked in the sudden light.
      A moment later, half of the books had been taken from my stack. "Books?" Clarity looked inquisitively down at the books in her arms.
      "Yes, books." I walked over to set the rest of my stack down on the dresser. "Why are the lights on? I thought you were going to sleep."
      "I was sleeping a few hours ago." Clarity brushed me off. "Clearly I'm not anymore."
      I gave my sister a look, but she ignored me. "What were you doing in our room all day?" I tried a different take. "Wouldn't you feel better out in the backyard?"
      "It's cold outside." Clarity set her stack of books down next to mine. "On a more serious note"-she turned to face me with steely eyes-"aren't you suspicious?"
      "Suspicious?" I crossed my arms. "Suspicious of what?"
      "Of the vampires," she hissed quietly. "Doesn't it strike you as odd how Lynden left on his own?"
      I shook my head. "No."
      Clarity ignored me again. "Isn't it strange how even though Phina is just supposed to be selling knives she hasn't returned yet?"
      "No."
      "You don't find it weird that Talon goes by such a name?"
      "No," I said firmly. "These people are here to help us get our sister back, Clarity. I-"
      "People?" Clarity scoffed. "They're vampires, Corinna. They're not like you and me."
      "Not like you and me? Clarity-"
      "Is it not true?" Clarity challenged. The flames in her eyes flickered. "They don't care about us."
      I just stared at my sister. "And we're better than they are? Do you remember who put us through hell in the first place? Humans did, Clarity. Not vampires."
      Even though we were just about the same height, Clarity still managed to look down her nose at me. "I don't want to be here in the capital city. In fact, I wouldn't be here if it weren't for the fact that Chloe-Jane is here."
      "I know." I took a breath to steady myself. "I'm asking you to please just bear with us for a little longer. We made it out, Clarity. We made it out of the farm alive thanks to Talon's help. If it weren't for her, I'd be dead."
      Clarity turned away from me. "It's difficult, Corinna. Now that we're finally free, I'm scared. I don't know what I'd do if I were sent back there. Now that I've got a taste of freedom, the thought of being sent back haunts me. I'm worried that the vampires have some sort of alternative agenda they're not telling us about."
      "Look," I said softly. "I don't mind if they do have some sort of alternative agenda that they don't want to tell us about. As long as it doesn't get in the way of rescuing Chloe-which it isn't-they can do whatever they want. I know that Karmen is still on their minds. But that's their business, not ours. I trust them, Clarity. Haven't you been around them long enough to understand their character?"
      Clarity walked over to the window and pulled back the curtains to look out at the night sky beyond. "You trust too easily."
      "That's not the case. I just feel like they can be trusted."
      "Do you, now?"
      "Clarity"-I stepped forward-"I'm trying my best here. I'm trying my best to get along with you. You're my sister."
      "Then you're fighting a losing battle."
      "I know that you don't want to get close with anyone." I met her eyes with my own. "I know that you're afraid that if you get close to someone, the pain will be unbearable if you lose them. Out of Chloe-Jane, Cameren, and I, you were the closest to Father. Even though you didn't show it, you were devastated that he never came back. Now you're trying to distance yourself from us. And I won't let you."
      "Do you really think we'll be able to get Chloe-Jane back, Corinna?" Clarity's expression remained unchanged. "I want to keep our remaining family members together as much as you do, but breaking into the castle? That's impossible."
      "Tell me, Clarity, are you really just going to give up?"
      Clarity folded her arms over her chest. "I never said that I was going to give up. I'm just asking, how much are you willing to give? How much are you going to sacrifice for that unrealistic happiness?"
      I blinked. "What do you mean? I am happy. I'm happy we've made it this far and-"
      "Liar," Clarity said softly.
      "I-I'm sorry?"
      "You were never happy. Back at the farm, you were always the one who kept our family from falling apart. But even though we are supposed to be a family, we're complete strangers to each other."
      "You really feel that way?" I whispered, shaking my head as I looked up at my sister.
      "We barely interact if it isn't related to our survival. You haven't felt alone at all, Corinna? Mother hasn't been the same after Father left for the war. Cameren's still living with the physical and mental trauma of the fighting. Chloe-Jane was always off in her own world, praying to the Immortal One day and night. And I, well, I never went out of my way to talk with you."
      My sister's words struck me into a stunned silence. I opened my mouth, but then closed it again when no sound came out. No. That couldn't be right.
      "So what if we're flesh and blood?" Clarity's eyes were hard. "We're strangers, Corinna."
      "Stop. We're family. I know you won't admit it, but you care for us. We care for each other, Clarity. I care for you."
      Clarity just turned away. "Say what you will."
      Calm. I needed to be calm.
      "I'm going to bed." I walked across the room. I flopped down onto the bed and burrowed myself under the covers. "If you are going to go downstairs, thank Lynden and Phina for the books." I closed my eyes and rolled over onto my side, preparing myself for whatever response Clarity would throw back at me. But it never came. Instead I heard a snuff of the dresser lamp, followed by the padding of footsteps, then the sound of the door opening and closing.
      I slowly cracked open an eye as Clarity's footsteps made their way down the stairs.
      I was alone in the dark.
       
~
       
      I awoke the next morning to the faint smell of smoke. I bolted upright in bed. Nothing seemed to be out of the ordinary, but the distinct odor in the air was still there.
      I threw off the covers and hurried out of the bedroom. I nearly stumbled on the stairs as I took them two at the time.
      "Corinna?" Talon's voice asked.
      I whirled to find the three vampires sitting in the living room.
      "Outside!" I gestured. "Smoke? Fire?"
      "Don't worry," Talon's face relaxed as she offered me a smile. "We just checked. Nothing bad happened. It's just Clarity."
      "Clarity?" I echoed. That was right, I remembered. Clarity wasn't in the room with me when I had woken up.
      "How about you go take a look?" Phina gestured to the door to the backyard. "I'd go with you, but the sun's up now."
      I made my way over to the door and slipped outside.
      Clarity was sitting on the porch. Her back was to me and a large number of books lay open around her. In front of her was a pot full of what looked like charred leaves, and a faint burning scent still clung to it. "Did I wake you?" Clarity asked without turning around. "My apologies."
      Even though she didn't sound very sincere, I just nodded. "It's fine. But what are you doing out here?"
      "I've decided to make myself useful," Clarity said shortly. "Plants have many uses. I've never made medicine by myself before, but I've got to start somewhere, right?"
      I crouched down to examine one of the books. "Medicine is good. But who are you making it for? The vampires can regenerate on their own."
      Clarity finally looked up from her basket of herbs, and her thick hair glowed gold in the morning sunlight. "It's for you, Corinna. When you end up hurting yourself, you're going to need it."
      "Who said I was going to get hurt?"
      "You'll thank me when the time comes," she said, then went back to her work grinding the leaves.
      I smiled faintly down at my sister. Even though she wouldn't admit it, Clarity did care.
      "I'm going to head back inside," I told Clarity. "I'm really glad that you're trying this to help out. But with that said, we are trying to keep a low profile. Too much smoke will draw unwanted attention."
      "I know," Clarity said. "It was a careless mistake on my part. It won't happen again."
      I turned to head back inside. "Be careful out here." I pushed open the door to the house and slipped back inside.
      "Look, Corinna!" Phina said excitedly. She and the other vampires were sitting at the table. "We have a plan!"
      "A plan?" I walked over to examine the large map of the castle they had drawn up. "How are we going to save Chloe-Jane?"
      Phina wrung her hands together. "Well, we still need to figure out that part. We have an escape plan."
      "This mission should take place at night," Talon explained. "According to all of the books we've read through so far, there are balconies outside each room on the ninth floor. If we can find Chloe-Jane inside, we can take her to one of those balconies and jump. As long as we don't exit the castle from the front, we won't be spotted."
      "I'm guessing you can't get in that way." I stared down at the map as I tried to make sense of what all the lines and scribbles were supposed to mean.
      "We can't jump that high," Talon said with a sigh. "Maybe two or three stories at most. The balcony is the best way out because if the guards are alerted, they can't follow us from there."
      "Will Chloe-Jane be alright after that fall, though?"
      "One of us will be carrying her," Lynden reassured me. "She'll be fine."
      Talon leaned over the map. "The best way to get inside would be through one of the windows. We'll have to find one that's either open or far enough away from the guards so they don't hear the sound of the glass breaking. And right now we don't have enough information to know which window that will have to be."
      "That part is up to Storm." Phina leaned back in her seat as she wound a strand of her hair around a delicate finger. "Who knows? Maybe he'll find a castle guard to bribe."

Chapter Fourteen
       
Just as Lynden had predicted, it took us around four days to finish reading through the entire bag of books. Initially I had thought it would take a lot longer until I realized that most of the books were just repeating the same information. Storm had yet to return, and I couldn't help but feel tense. The clouds were beginning to clear to the point where I could no longer go outside during the day without covering up completely.
      I had just finished my training session with Corinna, and the two of us were sitting at the dining room table.
      "I think I'm getting better," Corinna said. Excitement glittered in her eyes.
      I smiled. "You are getting better! It's amazing how much you've improved in such a short time."
      Corinna laughed. "I've tried my best. Maybe I should try sparring with Storm when he gets back. I'm sure he could offer me some tips."
      As if on cue, loud knocking sounded on the door, and Storm's muffled voice called through the wood. "It's Storm! I'm back!"
      Corinna and I exchanged a glance before we both slid out of our chairs and hurried over to the door. Corinna pulled it open and Storm staggered over the threshold, completely winded.
      "Did you run all the way here?" Corinna asked in surprise as Storm collapsed onto the couch.
      "Yes," Storm panted. "Well, actually no. I rented a horse, but I had to return it to the stable on the way back. I ran all the way here from the stable."
      "You're back!" Phina called excitedly from the top of the stairs. She quickly hurried down to join us with Lynden close at her heels.
      "Well?" Lynden asked. "Did you find someone?"
      "I did." Storm puffed out his chest proudly. "He's an information dealer. And get this-he happens to be a former castle guard!"
      Phina tilted her head to the side. "Is he really willing to tell you how to get inside the castle?"
      "Here's the catch." Storm sighed heavily. "He wants money for his troubles. Lots of it. But that's what to be expected from these kinds of people."
      "'These kinds of people?'" Lynden inquired.
      Storm ran an agitated hand through his dark hair. "Look, I know the capital city and where to go if you want to do something that will get you in a heap of trouble. Have any of you been to the north side of the port town before? Well, that's where all the crooks camp out. The crooks, the thieves, and the pirates. If you pay them enough, these people will do any job for you regardless of what it is. You can buy illegal items from them, along with information."
      Lynden frowned. "And how exactly do you know these people?"
      "I don't know them," Storm snapped. "They know me. I've stopped them from doing illegal things in the past. Did I mention that they don't like me very much? Some pirate tried to attack me when I first arrived, and I had to make sure to keep a low profile after that."
      "Is that going to be a problem?" I asked hesitantly as Storm's temper continued to simmer.
      Storm unfastened his cloak. "I'm not sure."
      Corinna stepped forward to rest her arms on the back of the couch. "Did he give you the information?"
      "No," Storm said tiredly. "I didn't have nearly enough money on me. Also, he said he wanted to meet my accomplices before we settled on a price. He knew that I couldn't possibly want to break into the castle by myself."
      "He wants us to meet him?" Lynden echoed suspiciously. "That doesn't seem questionable to you in the slightest? What does he want, to see all of our faces so he can report us together?"
      "It does sound questionable to me," Storm snapped again. "But he's our best source of information at this point. He says he knows all about the traps set up around the castle, where they're located, and how to disable them."
      "It's a gamble, then," I said.
      "It is." Storm tugged at his hair. "If he sees all of us, he can easily describe us to the royal guards, and then not only will they tighten their security, they'll also be on the lookout for us."
      "He never said he needed to see our faces though, right?" I said slowly.
      "That's right!" Corinna's eyes brightened as she caught on. "He never said we couldn't meet him in disguise!"
      I turned to Storm. "Do you know where we can buy armor? If we can get helmets, we can hide our faces."
      "It's perfect!" Phina excitedly clapped her hands together.
      "You're right." Storm looked up. "There are always shady people coming and going from the port town. Most of them are in disguise anyway. Are all of us going? I'm just gonna go ahead and say it: the north side of the port town is really not a nice place."
      Corinna's brows knitted together as she frowned. "If it's really that bad, Clarity wouldn't like it there."
      Storm looked around the room. "Speaking of Clarity, where is she?"
      "Outside." Phina pointed to the back door. "She's decided to start working with medicine."
      "Do you think it's a good idea to leave her here alone?" A crease formed between Storm's brows. "If she catches the neighbors' attention . . ."
      "I can stay behind," Phina offered. "I don't think I'd like the port town either. Besides, while I'm here, I can help teach Clarity what I know about self-defense."
      "Are you okay with coming with us?" I asked quietly as I turned to Corinna. "This trip might not be very pleasant."
      "I'm coming with you," Corinna said determinedly. "I want to explore the capital city. I want to see everything it has to offer."
      "Then it's settled," Storm declared. "If we can get everything we need today, we can set out tomorrow morning." Storm flopped back down onto the couch as we all looked at him expectantly. "Oh, come on, I just got back. Can I at least rest first?"
      "I can go buy the armor," Phina said energetically. "I want to do it!"
      Lynden turned to the ginger-haired vampire. "I know you're enthusiastic about this, but I think it would make more sense for me to go. Don't you think a female buying males' armor would be a little suspicious?"
      "You're right," Phina conceded, and her excitement fizzled out.
      "Why are you so excited to help with the drudge work anyway?" I asked curiously, angling my head to the side.
      "This is the first time in a while that I've got to be part of a good cause," Phina said sadly. "Is it wrong of me to want to help out?"
      I shook my head. "I understand where you're coming from, but you shouldn't feel inclined to do everything by yourself."
      "She's right." Corinna gave a nod in my direction. "We're a team. We work together."
      Phina grinned from ear to ear. "This is so exciting!"
      Lynden gave Phina a slightly exasperated look. "I'll head out now."
      "Wait." I quickly hurried over to the corner of the room where we had stored the money Phina received for the knives. I picked up one of the coin pouches and returned to toss it to Lynden. "Take this with you. It should be enough."
      Lynden nodded and fastened the pouch to his belt. "I'll take my leave, then."
      Once Lynden had vanished, I sighed and took a seat on the couch. "And now, we wait." 
      Storm stiffened and scooted away from me. I offered the dark-haired boy a smile, but my fangs slipped over my lip and he jumped off the couch completely. So much for trying to be friendly.
      "And now, we wait," Corinna echoed as she took the seat Storm had just vacated.
      "I'm going to bed," Storm announced, all too eager to leave the room. He quickly hurried up the stairs and disappeared onto the landing in seconds.
      Phina took a seat on the floor in front of the couch and pressed her hands to the sides of her face. "I wish he was my little brother. Is that too much to ask?"
      I laughed at that. "I don't know how well that will fly with Andreus."
      "Did you have any siblings before you were turned?" Corinna asked the ginger-haired vampire.
      Phina scrunched her brow, deep in thought. Finally, she shook her head. "I can't seem to remember. It's been so long." Then she smiled, and her frown vanished as if it had never existed in the first place. "It must be nice to have siblings." Even though she was smiling now, there was still something sad flickering behind her eyes.
      "I never had any siblings," I admitted to Corinna. "I never felt lonely with my parents, but having siblings wasn't something I got to experience."
      Corinna smiled faintly. "Having siblings has its ups and downs. The good thing about them is that they're family. They're more likely to stick with you through difficult times. Or at least I'd like to think so. My younger sister, Chloe-Jane, was always the cheerful one," she recalled wistfully. "No matter how bad things looked, she would always face life with a smile. But then again, she's the only one in our family who believes in the Immortal One. As the saying goes, 'Those who are hard workers will have a place in the afterlife.' Chloe took that all too literally, and it was up to Clarity and me to make sure she wouldn't work herself to death."
      Phina sighed sadly. "That Immortal One nonsense has people completely devaluing their lives." Her eyes darkened for a brief moment. "The previous kings were smart. They found a way to control their subjects completely. This kingdom is not a kind place. And the people living in it aren't any better."
      "Maybe with Chloe-Jane on the throne," Corinna said slowly, "things can change for the better."
      I pinched the bridge of my nose. "While she's at the king's side, the queen doesn't have much power. He can veto any proclamation she tries to order."
      "On a different note," Phina said seriously, "are you sure Chloe-Jane's going to want to willingly leave the castle with us?"
      Corinna exhaled through her nose. "I want to say she'll come with us, but I really can't tell."
      I placed a reassuring hand on Corinna's shoulder. "I'm sure there's some way we can try to get a message to her. All we need to know is whether she wants to leave the castle or not. If she says yes, then we'll continue planning and go through with the rescue mission. If she says no, then I guess we either stop what we're doing or go ahead and rescue her anyway."
      "If she doesn't want to leave," Corinna said defeatedly, "we should respect her wishes. She's my sister after all."
      "We'll figure something out," Phina said determinedly. "Don't lose hope now." Then she paused as her brow furrowed. "About Storm . . . Lynden and I feel bad about getting him involved in all of this. We were the ones who wanted him to be our guide around the capital city. Well, I was the one who wanted to work with Storm. Lynden never really wanted to, but he followed me when he saw what a big fan of Storm's adventures I was. Neither of us thought that we'd be breaking into the castle. If people find out Storm's been working with us, his reputation will be ruined."
      I crossed my arms over my chest as I leaned back in my seat. "He's the only one of us who knows the ins and outs of the present-day capital city. He's done so much for us already."
      "Yes," Phina said sadly. "And now I can't help but feel guilty. I didn't think things would go this way."
      We all fell silent for a long moment before the ginger-haired vampire sprung to her feet, smiling. "I'll go check our supplies again. You never know if something's gone missing." As she danced off, I felt a pang in my chest. Out of us vampires, Phina was definitely the most cheerful. She was always smiling, always laughing. Did she really not remember if she had siblings? Or did she not wish to tell me? It was a personal question after all.
      Had Karmen done this to her? Or was it the situation the queen of the vampires had saved her from? I'd have to ask Lynden later. Maybe he knew more. Then again, even if he did know, there was a high chance he wouldn't tell me, for both Phina's sake and mine. The two of them had past events they would rather not relive if they could help it. And I didn't blame them.
       
~
       
      Lynden greeted me stiffly as I joined him outside the house. The vampire was standing next to the front door with his arms crossed as he leaned against the wall. "What are you doing out here?" he asked stoically. "I thought we determined that I was going to stand guard tonight."
      "We did. And you are."
