      "What do you want to know?" Lynden looked up at the sky, and his long brown hair glowed gold in the light of the flickering street lamps. "The sooner you ask, the sooner you'll get an answer."
      "Now that we're both aware of my intentions, I guess there's no point to start with small talk." I smiled wryly, more to myself than Lynden. "It's about Phina."
      "What about her?" Lynden continued to watch the sky. I watched his face, but his stone-like expression gave nothing away.
      I lowered my voice. "What happened to her?"
      "If you're so curious"-Lynden finally turned to me-"why don't you ask her yourself?"
      "Ask her myself? I purposely came to you to save her the trouble of reliving the horrors she has undoubtedly gone through."
      "At least you're considerate. But no matter how hard I try, I can't understand you at all, Talon."
      I just raised a brow.
      Lynden let out a sigh. "As you already know, Phina and I both worked for the queen. The two of us lived at her manor. Anyway, the longer Phina and I worked together, I began to open up to her about my past and she listened. Even though I've known her for years, she's only told me bits and pieces of her own past. It's not enough for me to put together the entire story, but it was enough to tell me why she had blocked it out of her memory.
      "Before she was turned, Phina was going to get married. But on the day of her wedding, a jealous man killed the young man she was going to marry. He wanted Phina for himself. Phina was devastated. Karmen eventually found her trapped in the man's manor, and when the queen offered her the power to take revenge on the man who had wronged her, Phina didn't hesitate."
      There was silence as I tried my best to process the new information. "She lost the love of her life," I said finally.
      Lynden nodded regretfully.
      There was a long pause before I broke the silence. "Should I not tell Phina that you told me her history?"
      "It doesn't matter." Lynden's face became expressionless once again. "Phina herself said if you came asking, I could tell you. What about your past, Talon?" Lynden raised a brow. "How long are you planning to keep that to yourself?"
      "My past?" I turned to head back inside. "Right now my past doesn't matter. As long as it isn't impacting us-which it isn't-I see no need to bring it up."
      Corinna, Clarity, and Storm were asleep upstairs, and the house was silent. Phina had gone out to do some last-minute preparations for our journey to the port town. I sat down at the dining room table and rested my head on my hands as I turned to look out the window. The night sky sparkled outside the glass, and the faint stars danced lazily among it.
      As I watched, a single star in the far corner of my vision vanished from the sky. I blinked, straightening in my seat. I stared at the place where the pinprick of light had faded into the inky backdrop.
      I pressed a hand against the glass.
      Can you see the stars? a familiar voice echoed in my head.
      "I can see the stars," I whispered.
      Don't be afraid, the voice said softly, but I could still hear the tears that choked it. Just look up at the sky. That's all you need to do. Don't look at your father. He's just gone to sleep.
      The voice faded as quickly as it came, and I let my hand drop limply back to my side.
      
~
       
      "Remember that I'm going to do the talking," Storm called from his horse. "The three of you just need to stand in the back and look intimidating."
      "What?" Corinna yelled. Her voice was already muffled by her helmet and grew even more inaudible by the second as it was swept away by the wind.
      The four of us had left the house early in the morning, just as the sun had begun to rise. We stopped off at the stable to rent out four horses, then we were off on our way to the port town. According to Storm, at the pace we were going, we'd arrive in about two days' time.
      Now we were racing through the outskirts of the capital city. The cobblestone paths slowly turned to dirt the farther we went from the city's heart. I squinted through the mesh of my helmet, and the brilliance of the light stung my eyes. According to Corinna, the sky was a brilliant blue without a single cloud in sight. Everything was so bright in the day. The sky was so bright. Each ray of sun was alive with flames as they searched for gaps in my armor.
      "I said I'm going to be doing the talking," Storm shouted again. "We'll set up camp when night falls. Let's just hope this doesn't end badly."
      As Storm had predicted, we arrived at the port town in the afternoon of the second day. We had slowed our pace to a steady trot and I took the time to take in our surroundings. The buildings in this part of town had seen better days: the wood was chipped and the paint was peeling.
      The smell of rotting fish lingered in the air, mixing with the strong odor of unwashed bodies. I wrinkled my nose as the stench intensified the farther we moved into the town. People were milling around on all sides; some watched us out of the corners of their eyes, while others made no attempt to hide their stares. There were a lot of downsides to being a vampire-the enhanced sense of smell just being one of the many.
      Storm looked around the buildings. "We're going to want to leave our horses somewhere safe. They want our horses." We followed Storm to an empty lot hidden behind a row of buildings and dismounted. I carefully looped the reins of my horse through an old fence, and the others followed my lead. "This is where I leave my horse each time I come to the port town," Storm explained as he rummaged through his horse's saddlebag. After selecting a couple of knives and fastening them to his belt, Storm turned to face us. "Follow me."
      We followed Storm into a poorly lit alley, which grew narrower and narrower as we made our way to the very back. The stones that made up the floor here were covered in some kind of sludge, and the bones of little rodents crunched unpleasantly beneath our armored boots.
      "You were right," Lynden said in disgust. "The port town is quite an unpleasant place."
      "Of course I was right," Storm said distractedly as he glanced around the alley. "It isn't very likely for the royal guards to come here and make an inspection. But all the towns in the outer kingdom are like this. The capital city is the only one that shines. Anyway, here we are."
      Storm stopped in front of a door hidden behind a clothesline. After ducking under the hanging clothes, Storm knocked three times on the wood. We didn't have to wait long for footsteps to sound from the inside. There was a clicking sound and a tiny square opened in the wood. A deep blue eye stared out of the hole as it took all of us in.
      Storm pulled off his helmet. "I'm here for my information. And this time, I've brought the coins you've asked for."
      "Storm," a deep male voice rumbled. "I should have taken your head years ago."
      "I could say the same about you." Storm's expression was more serious than I had seen before. "Now, are you going to open the door? Or do I need to have my friends here open it for me?"
      "Hold your horses, boy," the voice grumbled. "If you break my door, you're going to have to pay extra for the repair costs."
      The square slid back into place, and the eye vanished. A moment later, the door swung open.

Chapter Fifteen
       
A man with wild brown hair stood in the doorway, with his hands clasped behind his back. "What are you waiting for? The door's open."
      Storm took a step forward, and I exchanged a glance with Talon before we followed him inside. The moment Storm's foot had crossed the threshold, the man darted forward, swinging a wicked-looking sword at the boy's head.
      I instinctively reached for my own blade, but Talon beat me to it. There was a loud clash as metal struck metal.
      "You-" the man hissed as he sprung backward.
      Talon remained silent, her knife at the ready. Lynden and I had drawn our blades as well, and the two of us stood protectively on either side of Storm.
      Storm leaned around Talon's shoulder to frown at the man. "Now, that wasn't very nice. That wasn't very welcoming at all."
      "Yeah, yeah," the man grumbled as he tossed his blade to the side of the room. "It was a joke-a joke. Don't take life so seriously, kid. But taking your head was worth a try though, wasn't it? Come in. Quickly now." He gestured for us to climb up the flight of stairs behind him.
      Storm marched forward without a backward glance at the man, and his armored boots clanked on the wooden steps. I followed Storm, and Lynden and Talon brought up the rear. There was a click as the man closed the door behind us.
      At the top of the stairs was a large room. In contrast to what we had seen of the port town so far, the man's house was surprisingly clean. There was a desk in the middle of the room, and the man took a seat behind it. He stared up at us expectantly. "Well? Where's my money?"
      "Where's my information?" Storm countered crossly.
      "Right here, boy." The man picked up a wooden crate from behind his desk and placed it on the table. "Now, are you going to tell me why you want to break into the castle?"
      "I never said I was going to break into the castle," Storm said as he tapped his foot. "You assumed that yourself."
      The man rolled his eyes. "The only reason someone would ask for this much information about all the entrances and exits is if they were going to sneak inside. And look here, I don't care about what you do. As long as I get my money, I'll tell you anything you want."
      "You weren't this cooperative the last time I met with you." Storm folded his arms over his chest. "Is it because you're feeling intimidated by my friends?"
      "Your friends seem like fine men." As the man spoke, his eyes flitted to the blades at our sides. "And I'm sure fine men like yourselves wouldn't dare to break into the castle."
      "That's right"-Storm casually dropped a hand to the hilt of his sword-"we wouldn't dare. And even if we did, you wouldn't dare tell anyone about it."
      The man let out a shaky laugh. "Of course not."
      "Now that that's out of the way," Storm said with a smile that didn't quite reach his smokey gray eyes, "how about you tell us a little bit about your relation to the castle and the royal guards?"
      "Before the former king passed away," the man said as he leaned back in his chair, "I was one of the castle guards. I spent time patrolling both the interior and exterior of the castle. I know just about everything there is to know about the castle. But once the new king took over his father's position, he fired and replaced all of us."
      Storm tapped his foot. "Is there anything you can tell us about the new king?"
      "King Volin?" The man's brows knitted together as if the mere act of recalling him was painful. "I never liked that boy. I think it's safe to say he isn't the person he and everyone else makes him out to be."
      "Oh?" Storm looked down his nose at the man behind the table. "Tell us more."
      The man lowered his voice as if he were afraid someone outside was listening in. "That boy was the cause of his father's death. No one outside the castle knows about this, but the former king fell ill four years ago. It was poison."
      "Poison?" Storm blinked. "I've never heard of this before."
      "Of course you haven't," the man said matter-of-factly. "I just told you that only those who were inside the castle knew of this, did I not? Anyway, to him, there is no difference whatsoever between right and wrong. He'll do anything to raise himself up no matter if it's at the expense of others. To him, everyone is disposable. I think it's safe to say that everyone at the castle is afraid of him."
      Storm frowned. "Why haven't I heard of this either?"
      "Stupid boy, did you think this was common knowledge?" the man said in exasperation. "I hope you know that you can't openly criticize the monarchy in the kingdom. You know that even talking about the royal family in a negative light could land you a life sentence in jail if the guards catch you. And that's if you're lucky."
      The man fell silent for a moment to look over his shoulder at the thick curtains pulled over the window behind him. When he seemed to determine that there was indeed no one outside listening in, he turned back to Storm. "I tried to avoid King Volin at the castle while he was still the prince." The man's voice had dropped so much I had to strain my ears. "I don't know the full extent of his insanity, and I know for a fact that I don't want to find out."
      "How do you think he would treat his wife?" Storm asked with a subtle glance in my direction.
      The man blinked dully. "The queen? You mean that little girl from the southern continent?"
      "Yes, her," Storm said quickly.
      I held my breath as I waited for the man's response. If the king was as crazy as the man made him out to be, I was terrified to think of what state Chloe-Jane would be in if-when-we found her.
      The man just let out a laugh. "How would I know how he treats his wife? He fired all of us before he decided to marry that witch."
      Witch? I had to take a deep breath to prevent myself from blurting out something I would regret.
      But it seemed like Lynden beat me to it.
      "Witch?" Lynden choked out. We all turned to him in surprise.
      "So you people can talk after all," the man behind the table said in amusement. "As an information dealer, it's a given that I know more than the lot of you on practically everything, but it's rare that my clients are this out of the loop. Haven't you heard? It's what the people have been calling her. She's being called a witch for seducing the king and tricking him into marrying her. Of course, I don't buy it. Knowing the king, he's probably trying to make some kind of statement-probably something directed at the southern continent. But I could be wrong. Maybe the girl just had a pretty little face and he wanted it for himself."
      Disgust surged through me at how casual the man's words were. My head was spinning with the new information. Is Chloe-Jane alright? Can this man even be trusted? I snuck a glance at Talon, but she was still watching the man with her face completely masked by her helmet.
      "I will say that all of the maids at the castle were terrified of him," the man added. "But I don't know if that was because he forced them into his bed or whether the girls merely sensed something was off about him. It's hard to say if the new queen will last very long at the castle."
      Storm inhaled sharply.
      The man raised his brows. "Do you know her? You seem concerned."
      "No," Storm said quickly. "But do I need to know her to worry about her safety and well-being?"
      The man shrugged. "I suppose not. But how old are you now, Storm? What was it? Twelve? I know you're not an adult yet, but look at yourself. Everyone has heard the name Storm the Dragonhearted at least once. You don't need to worry about some little girl in the castle." Then the man let out a laugh. "I think I've figured it out-you like that girl. But the king took her away. So now you have some friends to help you sneak into the castle and get her back. I know I'm right." Storm opened his mouth, but the man cut him off. "Look, I'm warning you now to give up on her. Oh, I won't stop you from trying, but if you get caught, you'd better use that sword of yours to slit your own throat. That's all."
      "You better have given us all of the maps of the castle I asked for," Storm said tiredly. He was clearly more eager to leave than to stay and argue. "Here"-Storm dropped a pouch of coins on the table-"let's finish this deal quickly."
      "I promise you that everything you need is in the box," the man said with a nod to the wooden crate on the table. "You've just given me so much money. How could I not give you the information you asked for in return?"
      Storm eyed the man suspiciously. "I want to take a look. And if I find out you've been lying to us, a certain someone is gonna end up in a world of hurt."
      "Don't worry." The man let out a slightly strained chuckle. "I swear all I've been is honest."
      We all watched silently as Storm flipped open the lid and sifted through the contents inside. When he seemed satisfied that it was indeed everything we needed, he replaced the lid and motioned for Lynden to pick it up.
      "So you didn't lie to us after all," Storm said lightly as he looked down at the man. "Sure, you did squeeze a lot of money out of us, but you actually gave us what we asked for."
      The man crossed his arms. "You really think that lowly of me, boy? This information wasn't easy to come by, and it certainly wasn't free. You should be grateful I'm sharing it with you at all. I hope you don't expect too much of me, though"-the man stood up from his seat-"because the next time I see you, your head will be mine."
      "Yeah, yeah." Storm turned to head back down the stairs. "The next time I see you, you'll probably have rotted away in prison."
      "One more thing," the man called, and Storm looked back over his shoulder. "Have you heard about the ball the king and queen are going to be attending in two weeks' time?"
      Storm paused. "A ball? When was this announced?"
      "Yesterday," the man explained quickly. "I get that you lot wouldn't have known about this one. Apparently the king and queen were invited by the archduke to attend his annual ball. The king has been invited every year, but this one is a big deal since it's the first time the new king and queen are going to make a public appearance together. And everyone is curious about the new queen. This kingdom hasn't had a queen in nearly eighteen years now."
      "Why are you telling me about this?" Storm asked suspiciously.
      "I just thought it might be easier for you to rescue your girlfriend from the archduke's estate rather than the castle."
      "Rescue her at the ball?" Storm let out a dry laugh. "In front of all of those people? That would be impossible. If what you said holds any truth, the ball will be packed full of nobles ogling the new queen."
      The man threw his hands into the air in a gesture of surrender. "I was just putting it out there. Now get out of my house. You've all overstayed your welcome. I'm sure I don't have to show you to the door."
      "We'll take our leave, then." Storm started down the stairs, and his boots clanked on the wood. "Let's both hope that we won't ever see each other again."
      Talon, Lynden, and I followed the dark-haired boy down the steps. We were back in the dirty alleyway in seconds, and I tried my best to keep from gagging as the rotten stench shoved its way up my nose. Even my helmet did little to block it out.
      Storm wrinkled his nose in disgust before he shoved his helmet back over his head. "Let's get out of here. The last thing we want is to find out that that crazy man has a bow and starts trying to shoot us in the back."
      "He didn't seem that bad," Talon said lightly. Her voice was muffled by her helmet. "I've met worse."
      Storm led the way out of the alley. The sky above was as brilliant as ever; it hadn't been this clear in so long that it was almost strange to see a color other than dull gray.
      "About the ball," Talon said slowly. "Wouldn't that be the best time to find Chloe-Jane and ask her whether she wants to leave the castle?"
      Storm paused for a moment as he glanced back at us. "I wasn't about to admit it in front of that crazy man, but I think it would work in our favor to attend."
      "You're going to infiltrate the ball?" I asked in disbelief.
      "Not just us." I could almost hear the smile in Talon's voice. "You'll be there too. Chloe-Jane is your sister after all. She'll be less likely to report you to the king than us."
      "What if we get caught?" I countered. "Then no one's going to be rescuing Chloe. And at that point, we'll just be lucky if someone rescues us."
      "It's quite easy to infiltrate a ball, actually," Talon said with confidence that calmed my ever-growing anxiety. "Forging an invitation is the hardest part. Everything else after that is easy."
      "She's right," Lynden said. "Forging the invitation is only difficult because you need to get your hands on one in the first place. I've infiltrated one as well with Phina. That was back when the two of us were working for Queen Karmen and were tasked with collecting information on certain vampires."
      "What do you think?" I turned to Storm.
      Storm shook his head. "I'm usually invited to balls. I don't have to sneak in."
      "People invite you to balls?" Talon asked in amusement. "Do you attend? You don't strike me as the kind of person who would enjoy such events."
      "You're right." Storm stared up at the sky. "I tend to decline them. I've never liked those kinds of events. For one thing, I despise the clothes-they're uncomfortable and impractical. Everyone is so uptight and rigid. It's . . . uncanny. But that's not even the worst part. The worst part is how judgmental those nobles are. They'll smile at your face and gossip behind your back. They pretend that they aren't watching you, but you can feel their stares when you turn away."
      Lynden nodded in agreement. "And then there's the fact that there are so many rules you need to know so you don't end up embarrassing yourself."
      I swallowed hard. "Maybe you should reconsider bringing me along to the ball." The last thing we wanted was to draw attention to ourselves. "I know I'll be dressing up as a maid again, but what if I still mess something up?"
      "As a maid, you'll have a much lower chance of drawing attention to yourself," Talon reassured me. "We'll talk more about this later. Right now we should probably find somewhere to get something to eat."
      Storm pressed a hand to his stomach. "I don't think we've eaten anything since yesterday. Follow me-I know a place." Storm led us down block after block, each one full of the same battered-looking buildings. Finally we turned the corner, and my breath caught in my throat.
      Waves sparkled in the sunlight, and the ocean spread out in front of me. We had turned onto the dock, and the stone path gave way to a long stretch of wooden planks that made the pier.
      "You've never seen the ocean before?" Storm turned around when he realized I had stopped walking. "How about this, I'll go get us something to eat, and you can stay here until I come back."
      I just nodded as I stared. I couldn't look away from the water. I had never seen this much water before in my life-had never seen how large the ocean really was. I'd heard that the majority of the world was covered by water, but this was the first time I was seeing it with my own two eyes.
      "What do you think?" Talon asked softly as she came up behind me.
      "It's beautiful," I said breathlessly. "Oh! What's that?" I raised my arm to point at the blurry shape in the distance. "What's that there on the horizon?"
      "It looks like some kind of boat," Talon observed. "Maybe it's a pirate ship."
      "A pirate ship?" I repeated excitedly as I squinted against the glittering water.
      Talon laughed. "Or maybe it's just a regular trading ship."
      I gazed out over the water. "I wonder what it's like to sail over the waves. Is it scary? Thrilling?"
      "I'm not sure. I've never been on a boat before."
      "Maybe one day we could go on one together, then," I suggested, smiling beneath my helmet.
      "I'd love that," Talon said wistfully.
      I finally tore my eyes away from the glorious ocean to look at the vampire. "Maybe one day, when this is all over, we could sail away. Far away. We could leave this kingdom behind and explore the world."
      "That sounds like the perfect dream. A dream too good to come true."
      I laughed. "But even if it's just a dream, it doesn't mean we can't fight for it. And then maybe one day that dream will become a reality."
      The two of us fell silent, and we gazed out over the ocean as we stood side by side.
      "I'm back," Storm's voice called, drawing me from my thoughts. I turned to find him jogging toward us with a bag in hand. "Let's go. The sooner we leave, the sooner we can look into the ball. Besides, the sooner we get out of this stink hole, the better."
      I nodded before absently taking the flatbread Storm held out for me. And as I turned away from the ocean, I wondered whether this would be the last time I ever saw it.
       
~
       
      It was late night by the time we stopped at a local inn to rest for the night. Fortunately for us, there was a stable right across the way to let our horses rest up as well.
      Lynden had transferred all of the documents from the crate into a different bag, which he made sure to hold on to at all times. Not only would traveling with a wooden crate be inconvenient for the horses, but it would also make us the target of potential thieves.
      The four of us decided it was probably for the best that all of us stayed together in one room. The more eyes there were guarding our precious information, the less likely it was for something to happen.
      The moment we stepped into our room, I pulled off my helmet. I could finally breathe properly again. And as much as I wanted to undo the tight braid snaking around my head, I knew that it would be too troublesome to redo it in the morning.
      The room was fairly small; it had only a little table, a couple of rickety-looking chairs, a chest of drawers, and a single bed pressed against the back wall.
      "Do you want the bed?" Storm asked me as he pulled off his helmet. His dark hair stuck up in every direction. "I don't mind sleeping on the floor."
      I went to work unfastening my boots. "I'm fine with sharing it. I share a bed with my siblings all the time."
      Storm just shrugged. "As long as you don't mind."
      "The two of you should get some sleep," Lynden said blandly as he took a seat at the table. "I'll start looking over the documents the information dealer gave us. You're welcome to put the lights out. Talon and I can see in the dark after all."
      Talon walked over to the window and drew the curtains, blocking out the glow of the city beyond. Then she moved over to the small lamp perched on top of the chest of drawers. She turned the little knob on the side, and the flame inside flickered out.
      The room was now completely bathed in darkness, and I silently climbed into the bed. I didn't want to think about how risky our plan was-didn't want to think of the consequences if we failed. Not right now anyway. Storm climbed into bed next to me and was fast asleep within seconds. I stared at the wall for a long time, half-listening to Lynden and Talon's occasional whispers as they looked over the maps. How are Mother and Cameren doing at Andreus's place? I wondered.
      I squeezed my eyes shut as I listened to the sound of Storm's steady breathing. I knew there was a large possibility that I'd die before I'd get to see my family again. Lynden and Talon were vampires; nothing was a threat to them. But on the other hand, I was only a human-one wrong move and it would be the end.
      It took me a moment to realize Lynden and Talon had stopped whispering. They had probably sensed my rapidly changing emotions. But I didn't mind. The people in this room were on the same quest as me. I knew that they would stand by me until the end.
       
~
       
      We left early the next morning and were back on our horses before the sun had fully risen in the sky. As we raced through the streets, I found myself thinking about Clarity. It had been almost a week since I had last seen my sister, and I wondered how she had been faring with Phina.
      By the time we arrived at the stables, it was late afternoon, and I was completely stiff as I dismounted my horse. I'd consider myself lucky if I never have to ride in heavy armor again.
      The four of us made our way toward the house, but it didn't take us long to realize something was wrong as we turned onto the street. A group of about twenty people stood outside the front door to Andreus's city house, yelling angrily up at the building. My heart sank as we came to a stop behind the crowd.
      "We demand to speak to the mistress of this house at once!" a woman yelled furiously.
      "I already told you that my mistress is a sickly woman," Clarity's voice snapped back from the other side of the wood. "She's sleeping right now and will see you when she wakes up!"
      "We're not leaving until you open this door!" a man shouted. "Either you get your mistress down here to speak to us right now, or we're going to find a way to get this door open ourselves!"
      "Whoa there," Storm said as he pulled off his helmet. "What are all of you doing in front of my house?" The crowd spun around to look at us, and the suspicion in their eyes was plain as day.
      "Who are you?" the woman who had yelled at Clarity demanded. "Your house? But that wicked wench just told us that it belonged to her mistress."
      Storm frowned. "I'm the mistress's younger brother. And she's right; my sister is quite ill. All this ruckus is not helping her condition. I just returned from a trip with my fellow adventurers. Forgive me if I have no clue what is happening outside my house. Would someone care to enlighten me?"
      "We want to know where your sister found such a maid." The woman curled her lips back in a cross between a grimace and a sneer. "You'll never guess what my husband and I saw today! While I was putting the laundry out, I heard a commotion from the other side of the fence. So I stood on my toes to look into your backyard to find a black-skinned girl! I'd never seen a black-skinned girl before, and I watched with wide eyes as she created smoke with only her bare hands and some leaves!"
      "I saw it too," another woman called from the back of the crowd. "Even though slaves are allowed in the capital city, they're supposed to stay out of sight! This one couldn't care less! That thing is a disgrace to her mistress!"
      Storm tried to calm the angry crowd, but it wasn't working. "If you didn't look over the fence, you wouldn't have seen her in the first place."
      "Nonsense!" the man who had spoken before snapped. "She had it out for us! She looked me in the eyes, and I could have sworn there was a fire in them!"
      "That girl's from the southern continent," another man called. "You've got to be careful of those sorts of people."
      Storm's jaw clenched. It was clear that he was getting more annoyed by the moment. "Look, there's nothing wrong with the maid here. She's been serving my sister ever since we moved into this house."
      "I don't believe it for a second," the first woman said shrilly. "I don't feel safe in my house anymore! Who knows what kind of evil magic that girl would be practicing! You don't know what those kinds of people are capable of! Do you know what else I saw in the backyard when I took the liberty to glance over the fence? Books! That's right, books!"
      Gasps rippled through the crowd.
      "They had to be spell books!" the second woman cried. "This is much worse than we expected! That girl's no maid! She's a witch!"
      "That's right!" the man yelled in agreement. "She's a witch!"
      "No, she's not!" Storm had to raise his own voice to a yell to be heard over the rapidly increasing volume of the crowd. "Please, everyone calm down!"
      "Witch!" another man bellowed.
      "Witch!"
      "Witch, witch, witch!" the crowd chanted.
      "You know what we do with witches here?" The first woman turned to Storm with a crazed look in her eyes. "We burn them!"
      "But she's not a witch," Lynden said angrily as he took a step forward to stand at Storm's side. "You don't want to accuse innocent people."
      "Innocent?" the man demanded. "How can she be innocent?"
      "Where's your proof?" Storm countered furiously.
      "Proof?" the man scoffed as he shook his head in disbelief. "There's so much proof! Don't you see it?"
      "No," Storm snapped. "I absolutely do not see it!"
      As the two argued, I felt myself freeze up. My legs were glued to the ground and my arms were weighed down at my side.
      "If you're so convinced that wench isn't a witch," a man from the crowd said slowly, "how about we do the good old witch test?"
      "Perfect!" The first woman grinned like a fiend. "If we determine that she is indeed a witch, we can still burn her after!"
      "What is this witch test?" Storm said angrily.
      The woman ignored Storm completely. "We'll go make the preparations. We'll be back." And with that, the crowd dispersed, leaving the four of us standing in front of the house.
      "Hey!" Storm yelled after them. "Get back here! You haven't told me what the witch test is yet!"
      "I happen to know." Lynden's tone was grim. "The townsfolk take the woman in question to the well and throw her in. If she floats, she's a witch. And if she drowns, well, then it turns out she wasn't one after all."

Chapter Sixteen
       
"What kind of test is that?" Storm demanded. But I wasn't looking at the dark-haired boy. My gaze was on Corinna. She was frozen with her face hidden beneath her helmet.
      "We can talk more about this inside," Lynden said quietly. "Right now we just want to get off of the street."
      I placed a hand on Corinna's shoulder. "Let's go inside."
      Corinna nodded absently as she let me lead her into the house. We followed Lynden and Storm over the threshold to find Clarity and Phina crouched next to the door. The former's expression was unreadable, and the latter's was fearful.
      "What do we do?" Phina wrung her hands together anxiously. "I didn't know when all of you would get back, and I couldn't go outside, either, since the sun is still out . . ."
      Lynden pulled off his helmet. "We've got to be careful now. Even more careful than before. We could easily stop them from getting to Clarity, but in doing so, we'd put ourselves at risk of exposing our identity. If we don't do anything, there's a high chance that our house is going to get stormed."
      "We can't just turn her in," Phina said defiantly. She clutched Clarity's arm. "I won't let them get you!"
      Clarity stiffened but made no move to shake herself free from the ginger-haired vampire's grasp. "What would happen if I hid? Do you think the neighbors would give up if they couldn't find me?"
      "I don't think that's a good idea," I spoke up. "If we made it look as if you ran away, who knows if they'll send out people to search the entire city for you."
      Storm angrily threw his helmet onto the couch. "We've got to fight back somehow. We can't let them get away with it!"
      "So physically preventing them from getting to Clarity runs the risk of exposing yourselves as vampires," Corinna said slowly. "And in doing so, that puts us at risk of Queen Karmen figuring out that you're here."
      "We don't want to deal with the queen right now," Lynden said stiffly. "If Karmen decides she wants us out of the city-or even dead for that matter-all of the planning we've done so far to save Chloe-Jane will have been in vain."
      "It looks like that isn't an option, then," Corinna said heavily. "And if we make it look like my sister ran away, Clarity would no longer be safe anywhere. We can't let that happen either."
      "What if we send Clarity someplace where no one will be able to hurt her?" Storm asked. "We could send her to my uncle's place."
      "Nonsense." Clarity's eyes flared. "I want to stay here in the capital city. I want to help out."
      Corinna dropped to her knees in front of where Clarity was still sitting on the floor. She had pulled off her own helmet and now looked her sister straight in the eyes. "Clarity, you're in danger here."
      "I wouldn't have been if those nosy neighbors kept a better watch on their laundry! It blew over the fence, and when I tried to hand it back to them, they started acting offensive."
      Corinna took her sister's hands in her own. "We're not blaming you, Clarity. Please, I just want you to be safe."
      Clarity shook off Corinna's hands. "You want me to be safe? What if I want you to be safe? Would you leave with me if I asked?"
      "Clarity." Corinna's eyes flashed as she paused, clearly conflicted. "One of us needs to stay here to make sure we can get Chloe back. Since you've got people out to get you now, I'm the one who has to stay."
      Clarity pursed her lips as she fell silent.
      "Now that we've agreed it's in Clarity's best interest to return to Andreus's place," Lynden said with a frown, "how are we going to get her there in a way that doesn't just seem like she fled?"
      "If I did get captured by the townsfolk," Clarity started slowly, "would you be able to save me?"
      Phina's eyes widened. "But they want to kill you! How would you escape? Fake your death?"
      Clarity nodded, and Phina just stared at her.
      I looked from Phina to Lynden. "We could do it."
      "How?" Corinna's expression was slightly panicked. "Isn't that a little too risky?"
      Clarity's eyes were steely. "We've been taking risks ever since we ran away from the farm. What's one more? This way I'll be able to get away without having to worry about anyone searching for me. Queen Karmen won't be tipped off, and our house won't get burned down either."
      "So you agree to go?" Corinna asked softly.
      Clarity rose to her feet and brushed off her skirts. "What choice do I have? As much as I want to stay, I don't want to hinder you either."
      "We don't know when the neighbors will be back." Phina stood up as well, and she glanced worriedly at the door as if someone would knock on it any moment. "I don't know if we'll have enough time to come up with a plan by then."
      "It's fine if you don't tell me what it is," Clarity said shortly. "As long as you can get me out of here alive, I couldn't care less about what you come up with."
      I tapped my chin thoughtfully. "If you're going to be thrown into the well, one of us vampires should wait inside for you to be thrown in. Since we don't need to breathe, we can wait under the water for as long as it takes. Someone could then cause a distraction, and we can whisk Clarity away in a blink of an eye."
      "I need to finish something," Clarity said suddenly before turning to walk briskly up the stairs. "When the neighbors come back, turn me in to them. I'll let you do the rest." Corinna hurried after her sister, and the two young women disappeared to the second floor. Their footsteps grew softer as they made their way to their room.
      Lynden narrowed his eyes. "This was unexpected. Don't the neighbors have any decency?"
      I shook my head. "Apparently not."
      "On a different note," Phina said, trying her best to muster a smile as she turned to Storm, "you're my little brother now?"
      "No." Storm folded his arms over his chest defensively. "You know I only said that to try to get the mob outside to back off."
      Phina let out a weak laugh. "Of course."
      I walked over to the dining room table, then took a seat. I turned my helmet over in my hands. Lynden was right; things had indeed taken an unexpected turn. But the more I thought about it, the less unexpected it seemed. Chloe-Jane, a darker-skinned girl of southern continent origins, was being accused of seducing the king with her black magic. Of course people would believe the silly rumor and then be angry at all people from the southern continent.
      I despised this kingdom. Even though the world itself had changed and I was far from the beautiful land I had once grown up in, I kept clinging to the hope that I'd live long enough to see it change again for the better.
       
~
       
      Lynden, Phina, Storm, Corinna, and I sat around the table, dreading each passing minute. The sun had just gone down, and the neighbors would come knocking at our door any second.
      Phina had changed into the black lace dress I wore when we searched the city for Chloe-Jane. Her ginger hair was pulled back into an elegant knot, and the look was completed with a veiled hat. All in all, she would have looked quite intimidating if it weren't for the look of pure terror on her face.
      "Are you alright?" Storm gave Phina a sideways look. "It's not like you're the one being handed over."
      "I know." Phina wrung her gloved hands together. "But how am I supposed to act? What if I say something wrong? I'm just worried about Clarity."
      "You'll be fine." Lynden tried his best to reassure the ginger-haired vampire. "Just say that you suspected that Clarity was a witch after all and are happy to get rid of her."
      "I can't say that!" Phina's expression was even more horrified.
      At that moment, a heavy knock sounded at the door. "Is anyone home?" a man's voice called. "We're here to collect the witch."
      "Looks like you'll have to," I said grimly. Then I turned to Lynden and Corinna. "Helmets on. It's better if they don't see our faces."
      Phina flashed us another terrified look before she slid out of her seat. She hastily straightened her skirts and walked shakily to the door. "Good evening." Phina's voice shook slightly as she opened the door. I glanced over my shoulder to make out the crowd gathered outside the house. Even though I couldn't see all of them, I could tell there were at least forty people. Their numbers had doubled since this afternoon.
      The man bowed deeply to Phina. "Good evening, milady. When did such a beautiful young lass move in? This house has been vacant for quite some time."
      "My brother and I just arrived here last month," Phina told the man in a strained sort of way. "Our parents thought it would be good for us to spend some time in the capital city."
      The man looked into the house, and his eyes landed on us. "I see your brother there. He made quite the scene earlier-and has quite the temper." Then the man frowned. "The two of you don't look like siblings."
      Phina let out a shaky laugh. "My brother's adopted. Don't take him too seriously. He's young and will say whatever's on his mind without a second thought."
      "Of course," the man chuckled. "I'm sure you know by now that your maid is a witch?"
      Phina nodded. "I suspected that she was a witch all along, and today just confirmed my suspicions. She's locked up upstairs as we speak. I'm happy to be rid of her."
      The man clapped his hands together. "Wonderful. I knew the mistress here would be a sensible woman."
      Phina turned to us with large eyes. "Bring her out."
      Corinna and I slid out of our seats before hurrying upstairs. Clarity was standing on the landing and gave us a grim nod as we arrived. Corinna and I each took hold of one of Clarity's arms before marching her down the stairs. 
      Phina stepped aside to let us practically drag Clarity out the door. "Here's the witch."
      "Perfect." The man smiled awfully. "Quickly, tie her up."
      A group of townsfolk hurried over, ropes in hand, and quickly bound Clarity's arms and legs.
      "Let me go!" Clarity hissed, her eyes blazing. "You'll regret this!"
      "I'd be careful not to get too close to her if I were you," Phina warned the crowd gathered outside. "As a witch, you don't know what kind of magic she's capable of."
      The man bowed again to Phina. "Don't worry, milady. You're safe now. The witch will be locked in the stable. All of our preparations are almost complete-the witch trial will take place tomorrow at sunset." And with that, the man turned away. The crowd dispersed into the night, taking the thrashing Clarity with them.
      Phina shut the door before turning back to us. Her eyes were wide as if she couldn't believe what she had just witnessed. "It's done."
      I pulled off my helmet, and Corinna and Lynden did the same. "They took her." Corinna shook her head in disbelief. "They really took her."
      "Who's going to wait at the bottom of the well for Clarity?" Lynden asked as we all sat down again at the table.
      "I can do it," Phina volunteered quickly. "I can wait in the well."
      "I'll do it," I cut in. "You're supposed to be Clarity's mistress, remember? It would be a little odd if you didn't show up for her trial, no?"
      Phina sighed heavily. "I guess you're right. Maybe it's for the best we leave this part to you." I half expected Phina to keep pushing to help out, but there was something sad behind her eyes. "What do we do now, then?"
      "Now we wait," Lynden said simply. "Talon should probably get into the well sometime before the sun rises, though."
      I inclined my head in his direction. "I can head out tonight."
      Storm slumped in his seat. "I'm sorry, everyone-I didn't know the neighbors would be so meddlesome."
      "How could you have known?" Corinna offered him a strained smile. "No one could have predicted this happening."
      "Maybe my uncle could," Storm said suddenly. "He can see the future."
      I looked at Storm with raised brows. "So you're telling us that Andreus could see that this was going to happen, and he didn't warn us?"
      "Well, not exactly." Storm ran an agitated hand through his hair. "My uncle can see brief snippets of different possible futures. Even he doesn't know which one will happen. Or so he says."
      Lynden frowned. "He could have at least given us some kind of warning. He told us about the legend of the four queens-which has nothing to do with us-and didn't tell us anything about Clarity's witch trial?"
      Corinna blinked. "The legend of the four queens. Queens . . . queens! Aren't there two queens in the capital city now? Queen Karmen of the vampires and now Chloe-Jane?"
      "You're right!" Phina's eyes grew even larger. "Chloe-Jane is a queen now!"
      "She can't be one of the four queens in the legend, can she?" Corinna said in disbelief.
      Storm furrowed his brow, deep in thought. "I can understand how Karmen can be one of the four queens, but Chloe-Jane was a little sudden though, don't you think? What, are the other two queens suddenly gonna show up as well?"
      "Are you saying that all of the queens are here in the capital city?" I asked slowly. With all the events that had happened today, the legend of the four queens had completely slipped my mind.
      "Maybe." Phina tugged on a loose strand of hair. "If they're destined to meet before the end of the century, we won't have to wait much longer to find out."
      Lynden clasped his hands together on the table. "If it does turn out that Chloe-Jane is one of the queens, we'll no longer have to go looking for Karmen. If we wait long enough, she'll come to us. I think I understand now. Karmen came here to the capital city to look for the queens."
      "If she's just looking for the queens, why has she been killing vampires?" I asked skeptically. "I think there's more to it than that."
      "Maybe she thinks one of the queens is a vampire?" Storm suggested.
      I shook my head. "That wouldn't make sense since the corpse I found was a male."
      Silence fell between us as we stared at the table. If Karmen did find the other queens, what then?
      "I'm gonna go to bed," Storm announced.
      I watched as Storm stood up from his seat. "Once we get Clarity away from the well, you'll have to escort her back to your uncle's place. You're the only one who knows the way."
      "Don't worry. I'll have the horses ready and waiting. When I get back, I'll draw out a map so we can all know the way."
      Corinna rose from her seat as well. "I think I'll head upstairs too-I need some time to think. Goodnight, everyone."
      "Goodnight." I offered Corinna a tired smile.
      Corinna gave me a small smile before she turned to make her way upstairs.
      "I think we're going to run into Karmen sooner than later," Lynden said grimly once Corinna and Storm were out of earshot. "We need to get Chloe-Jane out of the castle as quickly as possible."
      "We can't be hasty either, though," Phina said worriedly. "Haste will lead to mistakes."
      "Let's just proceed as we planned to," Lynden said. "Right now, that prophecy doesn't have anything to do with us. If Karmen really is here for the queens, she won't show up until Chloe-Jane is here with us."
      I nodded. "Listen closely. Here's what we're going to do tomorrow."
       
~
       
      It was a little after midnight when I silently left the house, dressed head to toe in black so as to blend into the night. Lynden had left the house a few minutes before me to check on Clarity, and Phina stayed behind to make sure Corinna and Storm were safe.
      It didn't take me long to reach the well. It was located in the center of the town square; the surrounding buildings formed a large circle around it. Perched on the roof of one of those buildings, I took note of all the entrances and exits. Right now the square was completely empty, and an eerie silence hung in the air. Tomorrow at sunset, this square would be packed with people. All the pathways would be blocked off. And so the best way to go was up.
      I dropped from the roof and landed on the stones below, then made my way over to the well. I placed my hands on the rough stone rim. My hair fell forward and shot ripples across the previously crystal-like surface.
      As the water stilled and the ripples subsided, everything came into a sharper focus. Even though the water's surface was a perfect mirror, I could hardly recognize the face of the young woman that stared back. The long black hair and delicate nose were my mother's, and the eyes and cheekbones were the same shape as my father's. But the blood-red irises that gleamed up at me were not from either of my parents.
      I stared at those eyes for a very long time, and the eyes stared back.
      They were the eyes of a vampire; a creature of the night, a creature forever cursed to flee from the light. They were the eyes of a monster. But they were my eyes.
      There was a faint splash as I dove headfirst into the well-into the eyes staring up at me from its depths. I sunk down, down, down. Everything was silent and dark underneath the surface. Then with a wave of my arms, I was upright again, and I tipped my head back to watch the moonlight above grow fainter the deeper I descended.
      I closed my eyes, savoring the dark. It was almost peaceful down here. All I had to do was watch out for the monster at the bottom of the well. My father had once told me a story about the creature that sat at the bottom of wells.
       
~
       
      "Once upon a time, there was a monster that lived at the bottom of a well. It was a small village with no more than fifty villagers, and each day, a young girl would take a pail and go down to the well to fetch water for her family. One day, a group of village children thought it would be fun to play a trick on this little girl and push her into the well. Little did they know, the girl could not swim. So when they pushed her down, she thrashed around in the water, doing everything she could to stay afloat. But alas, her efforts were in vain. By the time the other children realized what was happening and ran to call the grown-ups, it was too late. The girl had sunk into the well.
      "Now you see, the creature living at the bottom of the well sensed that the girl was drowning and quickly swam up to save her. But when the villagers saw the monster emerge from the well, they grew scared. They fled the village and left the little girl and the monster alone. From that day forth, the girl and the monster slowly but surely became friends.
      "Years passed. Even though the girl and monster had become close friends, the girl was still a girl, and the monster still a monster. By this point, the little girl had grown into a beautiful young woman. One day, a young man from a distant kingdom was journeying across the land and decided to stop off at the girl's village. The moment he saw the girl, he was infatuated by her beauty. The girl treated him as a guest, provided him with food and water, and finally introduced him to her friend, the well monster. But when the young man saw the well monster, being the hero he was, he decided to slay it. It turned out that this young man was a prince, and he took the young girl to his castle to become his wife. The end."
      "What? But Father, that's a horrible story!"
      "I'm glad you noticed. And you are right, it doesn't end happily for everyone."
      "The only one who gets a happy ending is that good-for-nothing prince! What about the girl? What happened to her when she arrived at the castle?"
      "Sadly, no one knows what became of the girl. Not all stories have happy endings."
      "Father, I don't think I liked that story very much. Could you please tell me a happier one next time?"
      "Did you take anything away from this story, at least?"
      "Yes! I know not to be like that idiot prince!"
      "Is that all?"
      "I don't think I understand. What more is there to take away?"
      "It's understandable if you don't get it right now. You're only seven after all. You will understand when you get older."
       
~
       
      Just how deep is this well? I wondered. It felt as if time and space itself had halted as I tumbled in slow motion through the dark water.
      After what could have been seconds or minutes or years, my left foot scraped the bottom of the well. I slowly opened my eyes. There was something surreal about floating there in the water. I looked from side to side and felt my long hair flowing around me with the movement. Where was the well monster? Where was the creature with the claws and fangs?
      Then I let out a humorless laugh, and the sound was silent in the stillness of the water. It's me, isn't it? I'm the monster at the bottom of the well.
      I closed my eyes again. My father's voice was a faint whisper as the words of his story echoed in my head. What I had originally taken away from the story was not to act the same way the prince had. What I could see now was that the monster in the well was only a monster in name-its kindness had shown through in the most important of times.
      Sometimes the real monsters weren't the ones with the fangs and talons.

Chapter Seventeen
       
When I awoke the next morning, Talon was gone. Without her presence, the house felt different. Lynden, Phina, and Storm were already in the living room when I climbed down the stairs in my armor. At noon, Storm would leave to get the horses ready at the edge of the town. He had already prepared food for the journey into the mountains, along with sleeping bags and weapons.
      Phina was still wearing the same black dress from the previous day. She was going to be part of the crowd. Lynden and I were both knights, dressed head to toe in armor. We had concluded that it would be for the best to keep our faces hidden from the townsfolk if we could help it.
      The day dragged out so slowly it was almost as if the sun itself had gotten stuck in the sky. At long last, noon finally came around, and Storm vanished from the house after saying a brief goodbye. By the time sunset was upon us, I was just about ready to pull my hair out. The waiting was by far the worst part. The longer we waited, the more the doubt would sink in. What if something goes wrong? I asked myself. Will Clarity really be able to get out alright?
      "It's time to go," Lynden said stiffly.
      I swallowed hard, then shakily pulled my helmet over my head. I followed the two vampires out of the house to join the crowd of townspeople meandering toward the square where the witch trial was going to take place. When we arrived at the crowded square, the three of us parted ways. I pushed through the crowd and made my way toward the well.
      A thick layer of clouds had covered the sky, and the entire square was painted in an ever-darkening gray as the sun sunk lower and lower. More people spilled into the square with each passing minute, talking in excited voices as if the witch trial were the event of the year. I grimaced, nauseated by all the smiling faces.
      "It's time, everyone!" a loud voice called from the back of the square. A hush fell over the crowd as they turned to face the speaker. It was the man who had knocked on our door the previous day. Clarity stood next to him with her head in a burlap sack and arms bound together behind her back. She had been changed into a ragged-looking dress, and her bare feet were peppered with cuts from having walked over the rough stones that made up the path. But apart from her feet, Clarity seemed otherwise unharmed. It looked as if the townsfolk had taken Phina's warning to heart after all. "Make way, make way!" the man called. "Make way for the witch!"
      The crowd parted, and the man marched over to the well. Two other men grabbed Clarity's arms and practically dragged her forward. Cries of "drown the witch" echoed through the square, and the man next to the well grinned. My stomach clenched.
      The man ripped off the sack over Clarity's head in one swift movement. "Look at her! The girl looks different from the other witches we've caught before, aye?"
      The crowd oohed and aahed as Clarity stood there. Her eyes blazed silently with flame.
      "That's right!" the man chuckled. "She's a black-skinned thing from the southern continent! And you know who else is from the southern continent?"
      "The queen!" the crowd roared in unison.
      "The queen!" the man echoed almost triumphantly. "She's the same as that witch who seduced the king! Today we will show the entire capital city that we won't tolerate witches!"
      "No witches in our city!" the crowd chanted. "Throw her in the well!"
      "Any last words?" the man said to Clarity. "Oh, that's right. I think it's better if you hold that foul little tongue of yours. Push her in!"
      For a moment, my heart stopped beating as I held my breath. The two men on either side of Clarity lifted her up by the arms like a rag doll and dropped her over the rim of the well. Clarity barely had time to scream before she hit the water with a loud splash.
      I hurried toward the well, but the crowd surged forward, and I found myself being pushed and shoved in every direction. In a rising panic, I shoved the people standing in front of me with all my might, but they were like a brick wall. The townsfolk grumbled, reluctant to give up their spots, but eventually moved when they noticed my armor. Holding the little plant pellet Clarity had given me days ago, I finally reached the well, then discreetly dropped it into the water.
      Bam! The moment the pellet touched the water, it exploded. Smoke filled the air, and the townsfolk standing around the well next to me staggered backward in shock. Through the thick screen of smoke, there was another loud splash as Talon rocketed up from the depths of the well with Clarity safely in her arms. She moved so fast that no one would have been able to see her if they weren't expecting her. And with everyone turning away from the smoke, that brief distraction was all that we needed.
      "The witch is dead!" Lynden yelled out of the sudden silence from somewhere on the other side of the square. "It turned out she was a witch after all! Look! She exploded! I've seen this happen before with my own eyes!"
      "The witch is dead?" the man in front of the well repeated in a mixture of shock and disbelief. Coughing as he fanned the smoke away, he slowly leaned over the well to look into the water. He blinked. "The witch is dead. The witch is dead!"
      "The witch is dead," the crowd murmured. Then, a moment later, thundering applause filled the air. "The witch is dead!" they yelled in triumph. "The witch is dead!"
      My task complete, I turned and pushed my way out of the crowd, still shaken. Right now, Storm was probably already escaping the town with Clarity. Even though I was still wearing my helmet, it felt as if I could finally breathe again. A heavy weight had been lifted from my shoulders, and as I made my way back to the house, it seemed as if the color had returned to the streets.
      I reached the house just as night fully set in. I didn't even have to reach for the door handle before it swung open for me. Talon stood in the doorway, smiling. "You did it!" Laughter danced in her eyes despite the fact she was dripping with water.
      "I did it," I said breathlessly as I stepped over the threshold. It took me a moment to realize that there was a smile on my face as I pulled off my helmet.
      "Phina is still in the square indulging the townsfolk," Talon informed me as she shut the door. "Lynden's upstairs changing out of his knight outfit. Lynden and I both thought that it would be a good idea for you to leave this house until the neighbors have calmed down."
      "Leave the house?"
      "I have a house in the forest about half a mile from here," Talon explained. "If the neighbors happened to see you here, I'm certain they'd accuse you of being a witch as well."
      Talon was right. The citizens were so angry at Chloe-Jane for "seducing the king" that they wouldn't think twice about ridding the city of people from the southern continent. I nodded my head. "When do we leave?"
      Talon looked down at her soaking clothes. "We can leave after I change into something dry."
      I hid my smile as Talon gracefully leaped up the stairs. Alone in the living room, I got to work unbraiding my hair.
      Talon returned a few minutes later in a simple dress, and her damp hair hung over her shoulders. She patted the bag at her side. "I've brought you a change of clothes for when we get to the house. Ready?"
      "I'm ready."
      Talon returned the smile, and the two of us exited the house. The streets of the town were empty, as everyone was still gathered in the square. The clouds had cleared and the moon hung low in the clear night.
      Talon led me into the small forest outside the town, and the two of us continued walking until we came upon a clearing. The wind gently rustled the leaves on the surrounding trees, and I paused for a moment to take it all in. There was something peaceful about the clearing and the little stream that ran through it-something peaceful about the wooden house neatly tucked away.
      "Here we are," Talon said as we stepped onto the front porch.
      I looked around with wide eyes. "This is the house you bought with the sisters."
      "That's correct." Talon let out a soft laugh as she pushed open the door. Even though it was clear the house had been vacant for many years, there was still a hominess about it. Talon showed me to the back of the house, where two doors stood against the wall, then opened the one on the left and stepped aside for me to enter the room beyond. "You can stay here. This was my bedroom. Here"-Talon handed me the bag of clothes she had brought along-"you're welcome to any of the clothes in the closet as well. I bought them a long time ago but never actually got around to wearing them."
      I took the bag from her. "Thank you."
      Talon gave me a soft smile. "I'll be here in the living room if you need anything. Goodnight, Corinna."
      "Goodnight." I watched Talon walk over to the couch before I gently shut the door. I went to the lamp sitting on the vanity and turned the knob. The little flame inside sprung to life, and its golden light flickered behind the glass. Even though no one had been living in this room for years, the vanity and all the other surfaces in the room had been dusted. It seemed as if Talon had made sure to clean up the room before I arrived.
      I made short work of changing out of my cold armor and into the warm dress Talon had brought for me. Then I returned to the vanity and took a seat on the stool in front of it. My face stared back at me from the mirrors; my eyes looked just as tired as I felt.
      I dropped my gaze away from the mirror and to the drawers under the vanity. I tentatively pulled open the top one to find an assortment of expensive-looking daggers. A laugh escaped from my lips. I picked up one of the knives and gave the blade a spin before setting it back down. Then I closed the top drawer and pulled open the one beneath it. It was filled with makeup, and I carefully lifted a jar of powder from the drawer. After blowing off a thick layer of dust from its lid, I returned it and closed the drawer.
      Next I made my way to the closet. I gently pulled open the door and blinked in surprise as my eyes fell on all of the dresses. Some of the dresses were casual, while others could pass as ball gowns. Still shaking my head in awe, I shut the door. The ball. I remembered: in two weeks' time, we were going to sneak into the ball at the archduke's estate. There we would see Chloe-Jane. But how would we get everyone's eyes away from my sister long enough for me to have the chance to talk to her?
      I collapsed onto the bed and stared absently up at the ceiling. What happens at balls? Well, dancing of course. Dancing . . .
      I sat bolt upright before hurrying over to the door. "Talon!" I said excitedly as I threw it open. "About that ball-I just had an idea!"
       
~
       
      I dismounted my horse, and my long cape swished around my legs. I pulled my hood back as I looked up at the small shop in front of me. After I had discussed my plan with Talon, she had agreed that it just might work. Right now, Lynden, Phina, and Talon were working to forge our invitations. My job was to pick up a dress.
      After taking a deep breath, I stepped into the shop.
      "Welcome, welcome," the salesclerk called out from behind the counter. Then he blinked at me. "Hey, I remember you! You're the maid of that other young woman who so rudely left without buying anything!"
      I bowed my head. "My mistress sends her deepest apologies. She's decided that she does want to commission you after all."
      "Humph," the man huffed. "Are you sure I should work with you? What if that woman decides to walk out again?"
      "My mistress won't walk out on you," I reassured him. "After looking at all the other dress shops, she's determined that yours is the best."
      "Mine's the best?" Then he broke into a grin. "That's right! Mine is the best! Your mistress has good eyes, girl."
      "As an apology for her behavior"-I reached into my cape-"she wants me to give you this." The man leaned forward as I pulled out a large pouch of coins. "My mistress hopes this will be enough for a single ball gown."
      I set the pouch down and watched the man open it and look inside. His eyes widened. "This-this is enough for three ball gowns! Your mistress is too kind! Come with me."
      The man led me toward the sewing room, pushed open the door, then stepped aside to let me pass. All the seamstresses didn't even glance up from their work as I stepped inside.
      "With all of my seamstresses working on the dress, it will be ready in a couple of days," the man said smugly. "Just tell them what your mistress is looking for. Girls!" All of the seamstresses instantly halted their work and turned to the man with their heads bowed. "You've got a new gown to make. This one is to be finished as soon as possible." And with that said, the man turned on his heel and marched back to his counter.
      I looked around the room, and my eyes fell quickly on the figure I was searching for.
      Corinna, the medicine girl mouthed in surprise. She beckoned me over to her table in the corner of the room, and I hurried over to join her. "What are you doing back here?"
      I sighed. "Long story short, we need a dress."
      "We?" the medicine girl inquired quizzically. "Are you still traveling with that other woman?"
      I nodded. "Have you heard about the ball the archduke is hosting?"
      "I've heard about it."
      "The king and queen are going to be there." I lowered my voice. "Chloe-Jane is going to be there, so we're going to-"
      The medicine girl held up a hand, cutting me off mid-sentence. "Don't tell me, sister. If people come to question me about this later, this way I really won't be able to tell them anything."
      I fell silent as I nodded again.
      "What kind of dress do you need?"
      I held her gaze. "What we need is the most beautiful dress at the ball. What we need is a dress that no one will be able to take their eyes off of. Do you think you could do that?"
      "We certainly can," the medicine girl said simply. "But you're going to need to help me. This dress is for that woman, right? We need to find a theme that complements her."
      "A theme that complements her?"
      "From what I remember when I saw her in the shop," she recalled, "she's quite pale with a slender frame. And she has black hair. I think any dark color would work nicely."
      "What about midnight blue?" I said suddenly. "The night sky. The theme should be the night sky."
      The medicine girl nodded. "Let's get to work, then."
      The two of us spent a good hour playing around with different designs for the dress before finally settling on the perfect one.
      "You can count on me to get this done," the medicine girl reassured me. "With so many hands working on the dress, it will be done in no time."
      "Thank you." I bowed my head. "After I get my sister out of the castle, I'm coming back for all of you."
      The medicine girl nodded. "We'll be waiting."
      With one last bow, I turned and made my way out of the back room. "Done already?" the salesclerk called as I walked toward the door. "Wait, I still need a name for the commission."
      I halted and slowly turned on the spot to face him. "A name?"
      "Yes, yes," the man said impatiently. "A name. Don't tell me you don't have one."
      "You want my name?"
      The man waved his hands in exasperation. "Well? What is it?"
      "Falon." A wry smile played on my lips. "My name is Falon."
       
~
       
      I returned to the shop a week later to pick up the dress. Lynden, Phina, and Talon had gotten us forged invitations, and we were going to leave for the archduke's estate tomorrow. The journey would take us a couple of days, and we wanted to make sure we had plenty of time. Apparently Storm had just returned to the capital city, and I had yet to see him because I hadn't returned to the house in town since Clarity's witch trial.
      The shop bell rang as I opened the door. The clerk was counting money behind the counter, and he paused what he was doing when he spotted me. "Ah, Falon, the dress is ready," he said, then reached underneath the counter to pull out a large box. "It was a pleasure doing business with you. Do come again."
      I stepped forward to pick up the box. After lifting the lid a fraction, I peered inside at the sea of midnight-blue tulle. I let the lid fall back down, satisfied.
      "Good day to you, sir." I scooped the large box into my arms. My back strained.
      "And to you as well," the man said distractedly, having gone back to counting his coins as I staggered out the door.
      Outside, I heard Talon's voice. "It looks like you need a little help with that." She effortlessly took the box from me. "This is it?"
      "This is it."
      "I'll drop this off-you should meet up with the others."
      "Got it." I swiftly mounted my horse before pulling my hood over my head. "I'll see you later."
      Talon offered me a smile before she vanished in a blink of an eye.
      Smiling to myself, I spurred my horse into a gallop. It was time to head back.
      
~
      
      It was late afternoon by the time I reached the house. Careful to keep myself hidden from any watchful eyes, I climbed over the backyard fence before silently slipping inside. As I closed the backdoor behind me, I could hear the sounds of arguing coming from the living room.
      "Come on," Storm was saying, "I don't even like these events. Why can't Phina go to the ball instead?"
      "I want to go," Phina's voice squeaked. "I want to go to the ball."
      I walked into the living room to find Lynden, Phina, Storm, and Talon standing by the stairs.
      "One of us needs to stay behind and watch the house," Talon explained as I looked at her for an explanation. "We don't want the neighbors trying anything while we're away, or we might find that there's no house left to return to."
      Phina's demeanor was limp. "I thought we were all going to go."
      "I'm really sorry, Phina." Lynden sighed regretfully. His expression was almost pained. "I know we did plan for all of us to go, but knowing what the neighbors are like, it's better for you to stay and make sure nothing happens to the house. The neighbors know you as the mistress of this house after all. I'd volunteer to stay, but the neighbors don't know me."
      "I can stay behind!" Storm tried again. "I'm her little brother, remember? There wouldn't be any suspicion if I stayed."
      Talon gave Storm a sideways look. "What would we tell your uncle if the neighbors hurt you while you were guarding alone? You're better off coming with us. Besides, you're still our guide."
      "But . . ." Phina said, clearly disappointed. "The ball . . ."
      Lynden tried his best to comfort her. "We'll have plenty of opportunities to go to balls in the future-if Karmen doesn't kill us first."
      Phina halfheartedly poked Lynden in the arm. "That's not funny."
      "What if I stay behind with Phina?" Storm suggested.
      "Didn't you just hear Talon say that you're coming with us?" Lynden asked. "If you died, I'm sure it would be easy for Andreus to hunt us down and send us to our own graves."
      Storm frowned. "My uncle wouldn't do that. He couldn't do that even if he wanted to. He can't leave the mountains. Didn't he tell you that he used up almost all of his magic to seal himself inside?"
      I blinked. "Andreus can't leave the mountain?"
      Storm's eyes were downcast. "My uncle is old-like, really old. Even though he still has maybe a hundred years left, he's getting close to the end of his lifespan. After his partner died, he was living all alone out there in the world for a long time. As one final good deed, my uncle decided to take me in."
      A silence fell on the room. "I guess it's settled, then." Phina said as she tugged on a strand of her hair. "I'll stay behind and Storm can go to the ball. But I want all of you to know that I want to hear about everything in detail when you get back."
      "We'll be sure to tell you all about it," I reassured her.
      "Thank you." Phina pressed her hands together. "I'll look forward to it."
      Talon walked over to the dining room table, where different papers covered every inch of its surface. "Now that we're all here, let's go over our plan one more time, shall we?"
       
~
       
      When Talon and I returned to the house in the forest, the sun had long set and the night sky was flecked with stars. Talon pushed open the door to the house and stepped inside. I followed close at her heels, and my eyes immediately fell on the box in the center of the living room. Talon and I exchanged a glance before we both hurried over to crouch down next to it.
      "Have you looked at the dress yet?" Talon asked.
      I shook my head as I stared down at the box. "Not yet."
      "Me neither." Talon stared down at it as well. "Would you like to do the honors?"
      "If you don't mind." I gently slid the lid off of the box. Talon and I both leaned in as we examined the sea of midnight fabric. Tentatively, Talon lifted the dress from the box.
      My breath caught in my throat as the dress unfurled into its true state. I had never seen anything like it in my life. It appeared strapless with layer upon layer of flowing skirts; a gown of night and stars. Silver glitter was sprinkled carefully over the deep blues of the skirt and bodice. The voluminous tulle of the skirts was like an ocean, and the silver flecks were like stars drifting over the midnight waves.
      Talon's eyes widened as she held up the ball gown. "It's beautiful."
      "It is," I breathed. Then I pointed to the box. "Look-there's more!" I crouched down to pick up the matching silk gloves from the bottom of the box, still in awe.
      "Hey"-Talon suddenly turned to me, her eyes sparkling-"would you like to try it on?"
      "What? Me? It's your dress."
      "Go on." Talon smiled ear to ear. "I'll be wearing it at the ball anyway."
      I eyed the dress. "I've never worn a ball gown before. As much as I'd love to, I wouldn't want to accidentally mess anything up either."
      "That won't happen-come, I'll help you."
      "Alright." I finally caved. "If you insist."
      Talon tucked the dress under her arm before taking me by the hand and leading me over to the bedroom. We stopped in front of the vanity mirror, and Talon carefully set the dress on the bed. "I'll look for some jewelry in the other room while you change," Talon told me as she skipped back out with the energy of a little girl ready to play dress-up.
      I smiled to myself as I picked up the dress and held it up to my body. There was something magical about it-like it was practically sewn from the night itself.
      I slipped off my own dress before ever so carefully stepping into the ball gown. Then holding my breath, I turned to face the mirror. The girl in the mirror-the girl in the ball gown-was me.
      "Corinna!" Talon exclaimed as she reentered the room with a small box in her hands. "You look beautiful!"
      I beamed. "I can't seem to figure out how the ties in the back work, though."
      "I can help you." Talon set her box down on the vanity table before stepping behind me. She hesitated slightly, and she hovered her hand in the air. "If you don't mind, of course."
      "Not at all."
      Ever so gently, Talon began to lace up the back of the dress.
      I watched in the mirror as Talon paused, her hand stilling on my back. "What are these?" she breathed, tracing one of the still-healing gashes with a shaky finger.
      I smiled sadly. "Lashings are common back at the farm. You don't have to worry, though-the pain has long faded."
      "I'm so sorry," Talon whispered.
      I sighed softly. "You don't need to apologize. It's not your fault."
      There was a long moment of silence before she finally spoke again. "There," Talon said as she finished lacing up the dress. "It's done." She took a step back, and I twisted around to look at the back of the dress in the mirror.
      I just stared, at a loss for words. Never would I have thought I'd get to wear such a dress.
      "You should spin," Talon suggested. "There's nothing more fun than twirling around in a new dress."
      "Okay." I found myself smiling. "Well, here it goes."
      With my bare feet pressing down on the floorboards, I turned on the spot. Even at this slow speed, my skirts flowed out around me. The little stars glittered gold and silver from the combination of lamp light and the pearly moon outside. I spun faster and faster, a whirlwind of midnight tulle.
