      When I finally came to a staggering stop, Talon clapped her hands in enthusiastic applause. "What do you think?"
      "Amazing," I said breathlessly.
      Talon's eyes sparkled as she laughed. "I always loved fancy dresses as a little girl." A moment after the words left her mouth, something flickered behind her gaze. Her expression turned sad as she sat down on the floor and rested her chin on the palms of her hands.
      "Are you thinking about your past?" I asked softly.
      Talon nodded as she drew her knees to her chest. "Not only that. This world is cruel, isn't it? Look what it did to you."
      I dropped to the floor, and my dress flared out around me as I took a seat in front of Talon. "I don't think it's a bad thing that you accepted Karmen's offer. I don't think it's a bad thing that you've become a vampire. I'm sure almost anyone in your position would have done the same. I know for a fact that if it were me, I wouldn't think twice about accepting the strength I'd need to take my revenge. In a way, Karmen gave you a second shot at life. And you've been using it to help out others. You gave Miah and Dahlia an opportunity to live a better life, even if it was brief. Later you even helped the slaves who fled to the forest escape from the inner kingdom. You helped me."
      "Karmen did give me a second shot at life." Talon's shoulders slumped as her hands fell limply to her sides. "Even if I'm now living a cursed life, at least I can try to help other people to a better place."
      I reached out and took Talon's hands in my own. "You don't have to go through this alone anymore."
      Talon's voice was no more than a whisper as she raised her gaze to meet mine. "Really?"
      "That's right." I smiled softly as I squeezed her hands reassuringly. "You have me now."

Chapter Eighteen
       
We left for the archduke's estate early the next morning. Corinna sat next to me, tentatively gazing out the window as the city outside rolled by in a steady hum of color and sounds. Lynden sat across from us, ignoring us completely as he sifted through a large stack of papers. Storm was outside, accompanying the driver on horseback.
      "I feel bad that we couldn't take Phina along," Corinna said as she turned away from the window. "She seemed really excited about the ball."
      Lynden finally set his papers down. "I feel bad too. She's always loved the music and dancing."
      By the time we arrived at the inn, the sun had already passed its highest point and was now slowly descending toward the distant horizon. I pulled my cloak tightly around myself as I stepped out of the carriage. The sky was a raging sea of light.
      We booked two rooms and made a good number of trips back to the carriage to collect our luggage. Lynden had offered to scout out the estate, leaving Storm, Corinna, and I behind at the inn. We had today and the daylight hours of tomorrow to prepare. Then it was showtime.
      Corinna sighed as she took a seat on one of the two beds against the back wall of the room. "I know it's only been a few months since I've seen Chloe-Jane last, but it seems like it's been much longer-years, even. So much has happened in such a short period of time."
      "I know." I unfastened my cloak before taking a seat on the bed opposite her. "But I also know that you've been handling this much better than I ever would if it were me in your position."
      Corinna shook her head tiredly. "There's nothing I can do except to endure. How much longer I'll be able to hold out is another question entirely."
      A knock sounded on the door, and Corinna's eyes looked at me questioningly.
      "It's Storm," I said. "I can go open it." I made my way across the room and pulled the door open.
      Storm stood in the doorway with the stack of papers Lynden had been looking over earlier tucked under his arm. "I thought we might want to look over these again," Storm said. He was looking in every direction except for mine.
      Corinna waved the dark-haired boy inside. "Perfect-the more planning we do, the better."
      Storm scampered past me as quickly as he could, then took a seat on the floor to sort through all the maps. He glanced up at me every couple of seconds as if I'd pull a knife on him.
      I blinked in mild amusement as I shut the door and returned to my seat on the bed.
      "Storm?" Corinna looked over at the dark-haired boy. "You've been traveling with Talon and the other vampires for a little over two months now. You don't have to be so apprehensive around them all the time."
      "Why shouldn't I be apprehensive?" Storm crossed his arms over his chest. "They're vampires."
      "That's funny coming from the person whose uncle is a dragon," Corinna said lightly. "You're not in constant fear of your uncle, now are you?"
      "Well, no." Storm frowned slightly. "My uncle's always trying to keep me out of trouble. He'd never try to hurt me."
      A faint smile played around Corinna's lips. "Then can't that be the same for the vampires? I'm sure many people would be quick to judge your uncle without ever getting to know him. In fact, they might not even want to get to know him. In their minds, Andreus is just a terrifying dragon without anything else to him."
      "My uncle is not terrifying-" Storm started, but Corinna cut him off with a raised hand.
      "Right now, you're doing exactly that to the vampires. You're refusing to even give them a chance."
      "I am?" Storm blinked. Then his shoulders slumped. "You're right. I am. I've just heard so many stories about the infamous Queen Karmen during my years here in the inner kingdom that I think I've developed some ideas of vampires as a whole."
      I rested my chin on the palm of my hand. "Not all stories are truthful. It's true that Karmen is dangerous, and we rightfully should be afraid of her, but that doesn't mean we can't give her a chance, either, if the opportunity presents itself."
      "Would you really give Karmen a chance if you do run into her?" Storm asked skeptically as he finally looked up at me.
      Would I give Karmen the chance? Would I give the queen who killed so many innocents, a queen with blood-stained hands, a second chance? Once I would have said no. Once I said that Karmen needed to die at all costs. But maybe I had just bought into all the stories about the queen like everyone else; maybe there was more to the queen than the rumors. "Yes." I nodded. "I would."
      Storm ran a hand through his dark hair. "I'm sorry, Talon. I haven't exactly been the friendliest toward you. Or Lynden. Or Phina."
      I offered Storm a smile. "It's alright. I'm just glad we're on the same page now."
      "I'm glad, then." Storm broke out into a relieved smile. "I know we didn't get off to a good start, and I'd like to try to start again."
      Corinna was smiling too as she sat next to Storm on the floor. "I'm sure Phina will be happy to hear that when we get back."
      "Your uncle raised you well," I said as I joined the two of them. "If only more people in this kingdom could see things the way you do."
      "According to my uncle"-Storm sighed heavily, and his smile faded-"after the concept of the Immortal One was introduced, people's thinking changed. The Immortal One showed them that there is only one way to be great-and that is by being powerful, no matter how cruel the methods of attaining that power is. I always thought it was ridiculous. According to my uncle, anyone who's different from those living here in this kingdom are considered lesser. I'm from the east. It was definitely a big shock to see it with my own eyes when I first arrived here. My point is that those who don't follow the so-called Immortal One are seen as sinners who deserve to die."
      "Then according to that definition," I said lightly, "all three of us are sinners."
      "That's right," Storm said as he rearranged the maps he had previously laid out. "I'm a sinner for associating with the 'evil' dragons and vampires, Talon is one of those vampires, and Corinna is connected to the southern continent. If people found out that my uncle was a dragon and that I'm working with vampires . . . Well, if they decide that they want my head after all, I can just run home and hide in the mountains with my uncle until things calm down. It will be a little more difficult trying to help out with people out to get me, but I'll think of something."
      I raised a quizzical brow. "You really don't mind risking your famed reputation?"
      Storm shook his head. "It was fun at first, with everybody knowing my name and the stories of my adventures, but that fun was short-lived. There are always people trying to prove that they are better than a kid like me. My uncle taught me that it's much more rewarding doing what's right. I don't need to be a hero. I just want to do what's right. I just hope it will be enough. I just hope I'll live long enough to see this kingdom become a better place."
      I smiled wryly. "I respect you, Storm. I think this kingdom is lucky to have a hero like yourself."
       
~
       
      The next day passed so quickly that the night of the ball was upon us in a blink of an eye. Alone in the room, I stood in my ball gown as I gazed absently out the window. The pearly moon hung low in the sky and painted everything it touched with an ethereal silver glow.
      Corinna and Lynden had left for the estate an hour ago as we had planned. After turning away from the window, I walked over to the mirror above the small dresser. I skillfully applied kohl to my eyes, rouge to my cheeks, and deep red paint to my lips.
      I had already done my hair up in an elegant knot. This style was perfect because it completely hid my delicately pointed ears. Adorning my hair were silver beads-the same ones that hung from my ears and rested over my bare collarbone, which complemented the stars glittering gently on my dress.
      Next I carefully opened a little box of dark-brown lenses. I gingerly placed the first circle in my right eye and blinked until it fell into place over my blood-red iris, then did the same for my left eye before staring in amazement at my reflection. For the first time in years, I actually looked human. Completely human.
      I slid on my midnight-colored gloves and the deep blue heels I had brought along for the occasion. I was ready.
      Less than five minutes later, Storm knocked on the door.
      My heels tapped over the wooden floor as I made my way to the door, and I pulled it open to find Storm standing out in the hallway. He was dressed in the outfit of an attendant, with his dark hair slicked back from his face. "Wow." Storm blinked at me. "You look nice."
      "That wasn't the most creative compliment ever," I remarked as I shut the door behind me. "But I'll take it."
      "Ready to go?" Storm turned to lead the way down the hall. "The carriage is waiting outside. I've got our invitations." I followed Storm outside, and we climbed into the carriage. The driver brought his horse to a trot, and we were off to the estate.
      I gazed out the window as we approached the large buildings. The stars were dancing in the sky beyond, and I watched them flicker during the carriage ride. I could almost see the castle in the distance, silhouetted against the night. We came to a stop behind the line of carriages waiting to pass through the gate in front of the estate's infinite stretch of garden.
      Storm sat across from me, and silence hung in the air between us. I hoped that Corinna and Lynden had managed to make it into the estate without any issues.
      Finally it was our turn as we reached the front of the line. "Invitations, please," the man standing in front of us said in a bored sort of way.
      Storm pushed open his door and hopped out to hand the man our forged papers.
      "Lady Falon and her attendant," the man said, more to himself than to Storm. He glanced over into the carriage, surveying me. When he seemed to deem that I really was the so-called Lady Falon, he tossed the papers into the large box beside him and waved our carriage through. Storm quickly climbed back inside, and we rolled through the gates.
      As we moved into the garden beyond, I couldn't help but admire the sheer number of flowers that bloomed along the path. But as beautiful as they were, only someone as wealthy as the archduke could afford to take care of so many plants.
      When we arrived at the front doors to the main house, Storm jumped out of the carriage and, being the attendant he was, held the door open for me. The moment my heels touched the ground, I could feel all eyes instantly fall upon me. I made a show of rolling out my neck so that my silver beads caught the light. And as our carriage drove away, I could hear the gasps and whispers begin to start up.
      One noblewoman gawked. "Do you see that woman's dress? Where did she get a dress like that? I want a dress like that!"
      "And I thought I had the best dress at the ball," another noblewoman said, sulking. "Who is that woman?"
      "Looks like I won't be getting the king's attention tonight," a third said miserably. "Look at her! She has to be at least a princess."
      Hiding my smirk behind my fan, I made my way up the marble steps and through the front doors with Storm close at my heels. The spacious entrance hall beyond was full of people all walking toward the set of doors at the opposite end of the room. If I craned my neck, I could just make out the elegant staircase beyond.
      "I hate this already," Storm grumbled under his breath. "Do you see how many nobles are here?"
      I glanced around the hall, taking in the majestic chandeliers and hand-painted portraits that lined the walls. "You could at least pretend you're having a good time," I said to Storm. "Everyone's looking at us, after all."
      "I know." Storm put on a strained smile that resembled more of a grimace. "But for the record, they're looking at you. Not me."
      The two of us climbed the stairs to the second floor and finally stopped at the doors to the ballroom. The man standing next to it looked at us expectantly. "Names?"
      "Lady Falon and her attendant," I said.
      "Lady Falon and her attendant have arrived," the man announced loudly before beckoning us through.
      As the two of us passed through the doors and into the ballroom beyond, numerous heads turned in our wake. My skirts swished around my legs with each step, and the tiny silver stars glittered over the midnight backdrop. I lifted my head, the perfect portrait of nobility.
      The ballroom itself was huge. Arching glass windows let the moonlight filter into the room, causing the crystals of the gigantic chandelier on the ceiling of the room to twinkle. The marble floor was polished to a gleam, as was every other inch of the place. The musicians stood off to the side of the room, readying their instruments.
      It seemed as if distinguished guests from all over the kingdom had come to see the new king and queen. I narrowed my eyes ever so slightly as I surveyed the ballroom for the anticipated pair, and it didn't take me long to find them. The king and queen were standing on the far side of the ballroom. There was no doubt that the young man with the golden hair was King Volin and the frail-looking girl by his side was Chloe-Jane.
      Even though both of them wore smiles on their faces, the latter's was obviously strained. Chloe-Jane wore an emerald-green dress, and her hair was pulled tightly away from her face. Something about her seemed off-I just couldn't seem to put my finger on it.
      "That must be Chloe-Jane," Storm said quietly as he followed my gaze. "But look at her eyes. They look . . . dead."
      As I did a double-take, I realized Storm was right. Chloe-Jane's eyes were completely blank as they stared unseeingly out into the sea of faces.
      A nobleman came up beside me. "Are you looking at the new queen?" he asked. "She's a little young, don't you think?"
      "She is young," I agreed as I angled my head to the side. "Do you happen to know why she looks the way that she does?"
      "Look like what? Like a crazy witch that crazy king picked up on his way home from the farms?"
      "No," I said slowly. "Has life as a royal been difficult for her?"
      The nobleman shrugged. "How would I know? Even if I did know, I wouldn't care. The king is crazy to have married someone like her."
      Storm folded his arms over his chest. "He's certainly crazy to have married a fourteen-year-old. I just feel bad for the queen."
      The man looked at Storm distastefully. "And who exactly are you? Oh, you're just some lowly attendant. I was speaking to the lady, not you, boy. You need to learn to speak only when you're spoken to."
      "But weren't you just speaking-" Storm started angrily, but I cut him off with a look.
      The nobleman clicked his tongue as he turned back to me. "That girl's unsuited to be the queen, if you ask me. Our kind aren't supposed to mix with people like her. Anyway, it's clear that you have the most beautiful dress at the ball. Are you hoping to dance with someone special tonight?"
      I turned to gaze out over the crowd. "Who I dance with is none of your concern. But I must say that it certainly won't be you."
      The man opened his mouth, but no sound came out. Finally he sputtered, "Lady, Lady . . ." and he seemed to realize he didn't know my name.
      "Lady Falon," a familiar voice said from behind us. All three of us turned to find Lynden standing there. "It's good to see you here." His expression was more relaxed than I had ever seen it before. "May I have a word?"
      "Of course." I inclined my head, first to Lynden and then the nobleman. "Forgive me."
      The nobleman just stared as I followed Lynden to the other side of the room, with Storm close behind.
      "You came just in time," Storm said once we were far enough away from the nobleman. "That man was crazy."
      "Did Corinna get in safely?" I asked quietly.
      "She did." Lynden's expression grew serious, and his calm mask faded. "She's here right now. Look."
      I followed his gaze to the group of servants lurking toward the back of the ballroom. All of them were carrying trays of food and waiting for the dancing to start so they could set the long table.
      I felt some of the pressure in my chest lighten. "Good."
      "Ahem," a loud voice called. A hush fell over the crowd as they all turned to the announcer expectantly. The man was dressed in yellows and golds, definitely one of the more expensive outfits here tonight. "Ladies and gentlemen, it's time to clear the dance floor. Our first dance is starting."
      "That's the archduke," Lynden informed us quietly. "He's second in the kingdom only to the king and queen themselves."
      The crowd shuffled to the sides of the room, leaving the gleaming floor wide open. The music started, and it didn't take long for couples to make their way out onto the floor. But even with the people dancing, almost everyone's eyes were still glued to Chloe-Jane.
      It was time to make my move.
      With a nod to Lynden and Storm, I made my way around the perimeter of the dance floor and only stopped once I arrived in front of the king. King Volin blinked as I looked up at him, and his deep-green eyes widened slightly as I dipped into a graceful curtsy. "Your Majesty. I was hoping that you'd ask me to dance." At this point, everyone's eyes were on me. I could practically feel them on the back of my neck as I held my curtsy.
      "Whom might you be?" the king asked mildly.
      I lifted my gaze to meet the king's. "My name is Falon, Your Majesty. There is nothing more I desire in this lifetime than to share a single dance with the king."
      "Then it would be quite lamentable of me not to grant you your wish." King Volin motioned for me to rise before gracefully extending a hand. "May I have this dance, Lady Falon?"
      "I would be honored, Your Majesty."
      I rested my hand on the king's and let him lead me onto the dance floor. The dancers parted to let us reach the center of the ballroom, and my midnight skirts swished around my legs. It took all my self-control not to flinch as King Volin slid an arm around my waist. A moment later, we were moving. The silver stars on my dress glittered as we waltzed across the floor, and my feet were light over the smooth marble as I twirled.
      "You're a wonderful dancer," the king praised as his green eyes flickered with amusement.
      "Thank you, Your Majesty," I said, making my demeanor as shy as I could. "You're a marvelous dancer yourself."
      "I think you are definitely the star of this ball tonight," he remarked as we continued to waltz through the ballroom. The other couples who had previously been dancing on the floor had backed up into the crowd to join everyone else in gawking at us.
      Whispers of "who is that girl?" and "no fair!" rippled through the crowd, but I paid them no mind. Just keep your eyes on me. I twirled again and again. That's right, keep watching.
      "Have we met before?" King Volin asked.
      "No, Your Majesty." I let the king lead me across the floor. "This is the first time I've met Your Majesty in person."
      "Is that so?" King Volin arched a quizzical brow. "Are you sure we haven't met before? Maybe at another ball?"
      "If we had met before, I certainly would have taken the opportunity to dance with Your Majesty then."
      The king shook his head in bewilderment. "Then why do you look so familiar? I could have sworn I've seen you somewhere before."
      "Is Your Majesty only planning on having one wife?" I quickly changed the topic. If the king thought about it long enough, maybe he actually would recall where he had seen my face.
      "Only one wife?" King Volin let out an amused laugh. "I don't know. There are many beautiful girls in my kingdom."
      "Then why did Your Majesty choose to marry her?" I pretended to pout as I inclined my head in Chloe-Jane's direction. "She's from the southern continent, is she not?"
      "I have my reasons." The king wouldn't look away from me as we glided over the dance floor. "Maybe I just thought she had a pretty face. But I'm afraid I've been so busy lately that I don't even have time for women. Right now, one wife is enough."
      As he talked, I silently searched his face for any signs of the madman the information dealer had claimed him to be. After some time, I concluded that either the information dealer had lied to us-or the king was just really, really, good at hiding his true nature.
      "What do you think about vampires, Your Majesty?" I asked mildly.
      "Vampires?" King Volin blinked, clearly caught off guard by the question. And for a second-a brief second-crazed insanity flickered through his eyes. It passed so quickly that if I had looked away for only a moment, I would have missed it entirely.
      "I was just wondering how Your Majesty plans to keep them out of our kingdom for good," I continued as if I hadn't noticed his momentary shift. "They frighten me so much that sometimes I can't even sleep at night."
      The king let out an absent sigh. "I don't have a solution right now. But I'm working on it."
      I nodded along. "Of course. With Your Majesty working on it, I can feel relieved."
      Out of the corner of my eye, I watched as Corinna slowly made her way toward Chloe-Jane. All she needed was a few seconds.
      "Does Your Majesty happen to know what this song is called?" I looked up at the king and steered him away from the sisters. The eyes in the ballroom followed our every movement. "It's lovely, isn't it?"

Chapter Nineteen
       
I almost forgot what my task was when I saw Talon. Even from a distance, she looked stunning. She was a graceful butterfly as she twirled with her glittering skirts rippling behind her. Each movement flowed effortlessly like water, and I had to force myself to tear my eyes away.
      Lynden and I had entered the manor earlier in the evening. The vampire had presented me, per our plan, as an extra maid brought from his own estate to help out at the event. The staff in charge of the maids didn't even question the story before handing me a uniform and telling me to get to work.
      I carefully made my way through the crowd and stopped only when I was directly behind Chloe-Jane. "Your Majesty," I said quietly as I extended the tray I carried in my arms. "Would you care for something to eat?"
      "No, thank you." Chloe-Jane turned around to look at me. "I appreciate the offer-" She stopped when her eyes fell on me. Corinna, she mouthed in shock.
      "Chloe," I whispered, my voice breaking.
      Chloe-Jane's eyes were wide with panic. "Why are you here? You're here to save me, aren't you? Oh no, you shouldn't be here! If the king sees you-"
      "Chloe," I said in a hurried whisper, "calm down. I'm just here to ask you a question."
      Chloe-Jane inhaled sharply. "A question?"
      I nodded. "Listen, I met a group of people who have a plan to get you out of the castle. All you need to tell me is whether you want to leave or stay. If you want to stay, we won't go through with our plan and you can remain queen."
      "No!" Chloe-Jane grabbed my hand a little too tightly, and her nails dug deeply into my palm. "Get me out of there."
      "Then all you need to do is meet us on the balcony-"
      Chloe-Jane shook her head quickly. "I'm not allowed on the balconies."
      "We'll meet you in your room, then. You don't share a room with the king, do you?"
      My sister shook her head again.
      "In that case, can you tell me where in the castle that is?"
      Chloe-Jane leaned closer to whisper its location into my ear. I nodded, taking careful note of her words.
      "One week from today," I whispered before slipping back into the crowd. "At midnight. We'll come and get you."
      Chloe-Jane stared after me, wide-eyed.
      I silently resumed my place at the back of the ballroom. My work here was done. I passed the other servants who were currently offering food to the guests, none of whom paid me any heed. All I needed to do now was find Lynden, and then we could leave. Talon and Storm, on the other hand, were going to stay for the entire night. After dancing with the king, Talon didn't have much of a choice.
      Before I could begin my search, I sensed someone's presence behind me. I felt a hand on my shoulder and my heart nearly stopped. Did I give myself away? Was I caught talking to my sister?
      "You, maid," a man's voice said. I turned, keeping my head bowed. I recognized the man; he was one of the people in charge of the event. "Take these to the kitchen, will you?"
      I blinked at the empty trays the man held out to me and hastily received them. I just stood there for a moment after he left while my heart beat rapidly in my chest.
      After my trip to the kitchen, I reentered the ballroom, and I abruptly realized that Talon and the king were no longer on the dance floor. I looked around the room to find that the latter had resumed his place next to Chloe-Jane's side. I scanned the crowd for a glimmer of silver and blue, but Talon was nowhere to be found.
      Suddenly, I caught a glimpse of Lynden's long brown hair outside on the balcony. I silently made my way over to the double doors and slipped into the night.
      Lynden and Storm were standing outside, talking in low voices. "Corinna!" Storm turned to look over at me. "How did it go?"
      I let out a breath. "It was a success. I'm honestly surprised at how well Talon's distraction worked."
      "What did Chloe-Jane say?" Lynden asked seriously.
      I rested my arms against the balcony's railing and stared up at the night sky. "She wants us to help her escape. It looks like we're going through with our plan after all. Do either of you happen to know where Talon went?"
      "She went somewhere down there." Storm gestured to the gardens below. "I think she wanted to get as far away from the king as she could. You should find her if you turn the corner. Lynden and I will let you know if anyone else is coming out here."
      I nodded in thanks before following the balcony railing around the corner of the ballroom. There were no windows on this side of the building. I took a deep breath and let the crisp night air flood my lungs. There was something peaceful about being outside.
      I rested my arms on the balcony's railing again, this time gazing out over the garden as I searched among the rows of silvery flowers, and soon my eyes landed on her glowing figure.
      Talon was standing among the flowers with her head tipped back slightly as she gazed up at the stars. Her gown billowed out around her in a sea of midnight, and the tiny silver stars on her skirts and hair glittered like crystals.
      "Talon," I called softly down to her.
      As she turned to look up at me, her expression melted into a smile, and she waved a gloved hand.
      I smiled and waved back.
      "Should I climb up to you?" she asked.
      I shook my head. "I'll come down to you." 
      After taking off my apron, shoes, and socks, I climbed up onto the railing. In one swift movement, I leaped into the tree on the other side of the rail and clung tightly to the sturdy branches. A soft wind picked up, tugging loose strands of my hair free from my braid. When I had a solid footing, I jumped down to the grass below.
      "Tonight was the first time I actually got to see you in your dress," I said breathlessly as Talon made her way over to me. "You look beautiful."
      "Thank you." Talon's eyes sparkled as she laughed. I noticed that her jewelry had vanished, and when I gave her a quizzical look, Talon held the jewelry out to me. "Would you mind keeping them for me? I feel more like myself without these adornments."
      I nodded as I placed them in one of my pockets.
      "So, what did Chloe-Jane say?"
      I sighed as the two of us set off through the garden. "She wants to be saved. Are you sure it's okay for us to be out here?"
      Talon gave me a reassuring smile as the far-off sounds of the music and the din of conversation from the ballroom drifted down to us. "It's perfectly fine. We're the only people out here. Besides, there are no windows on this side of the ballroom."
      I nodded as my tension eased. "When I was talking to Chloe-Jane, something about her seemed off."
      "Something about her looked off," Talon agreed.
      "When you were dancing with the king, did you manage to get a sense of what kind of person he is?"
      "I'm afraid that he might very well be the person the information dealer warned us about," Talon said grimly, and her eyes darkened. "At first I was doubting whether or not it was true, but when I caught him off guard, he accidentally let something slip. There's an insanity in his eyes, Corinna. And I've never seen anything like it before."
      "Insanity," I echoed. Then I grabbed Talon's arm in a rising panic. "Talon, we've got to get Chloe-Jane out of there. If the king really is a madman, how much longer can Chloe last in the castle?"
      "I know." Talon sighed as we stopped in the middle of the garden. She took my hands in her own. "We're going to get her out of there soon. Very soon. But I'm afraid she'll have to wait a few more days."
      I bit my lip as I glanced toward the looming outline of the castle in the distance. She was right. We had to stick to our plan. If we rushed anything, things could go terribly wrong.
      Talon let go of my hands to remove her heels, then mercifully changed the topic. "I noticed you watching me while I was dancing with the king. I was almost afraid that you would forget to go and talk to your sister."
      I laughed at that. "You're the most beautiful woman at the ball. How could I not look? I'd consider the king lucky to even get a chance to dance with you."
      "Don't tell me that you're jealous." Talon angled her head to the side, smiling. "Are you jealous?"
      "Maybe a little bit."
      "In that case"-Talon extended a gloved hand-"may I have this dance?"
      "Dance?" I blinked at her delicate fingers. "I'd love to, but I'm not a very good dancer."
      Talon laughed. "That's perfectly fine. We're not dancing for anyone but ourselves."
      "In that case . . ." I gingerly placed my hand on top of Talon's. I let her lead me to the center of the garden, and our fingers twined together.
      "Just listen to the music," Talon instructed. "How about a basic waltz? Right foot, left foot."
      I nodded and furrowed my brow in concentration. As I followed her lead, I soon found that I was making my way through the steps. Even though I wobbled around with a fraction of Talon's grace, I was doing it.
      Talon beamed at me as the two of us took turns twirling around. Our bare feet sent the flower petals littering the grass fluttering into the air. "You're doing it!"
      "I am," I said in amazement as we glided over the ground.
      When we finally came to a stop, I realized that we had made our way all the way back to the balconies.
      "I don't believe that you aren't a dancer!" Talon grinned. "You were great!"
      "Back on the farm, there was a dance my siblings and I used to do as a child whenever we were able to hold a rare celebration of any sort," I recalled. "Would you like me to show you?"
      Talon beamed. "Please do."
      "It goes like this." I took Talon's hands. "We hold each other's hands, and then we jump!"
      The two of us jumped up and down, laughing as our skirts bounced with us. As we skipped in circles, it didn't take long for Talon's hair to tumble free of its knot in a cascade of ebony silk. My own hair had come undone from my braid, and the two of us finally collapsed onto the grass under the balcony in a heap of giggles.
      "I think your dance is a lot more fun." Talon laughed as she rolled onto her back to look up at the stars. "If everyone at the ball danced this way, I think those events would be a lot more enjoyable too."
      "I can't imagine the nobles ever dancing like this." I looked up at the sky as well. My heart was pounding away in my chest from all the jumping, and Talon's fingers were still laced through mine. The grass was soft as the two of us lay there under the balcony, and the entire garden was painted in shades of silver. I closed my eyes, listening to the sound of the music wafting down from the ballroom.
      "While I was dancing with the king," Talon said absently, "he kept claiming that he recognized me from somewhere."
      "How could the king have recognized you?" I opened my eyes as I turned to look at her. "This was the first time you've seen him."
      Talon sighed heavily as her eyes met mine. "I know. And I don't get it either. Where could he have seen me before?"
      "Come to think of it," I said slowly, "when we first met that night in the forest, your face reminded me of someone I had seen before."
      Talon blinked. "It did? Do you remember who?"
      "That's the thing." My shoulders slumped. "No matter how hard I think about it, I just can't remember. I know I couldn't have met you before that night in the forest. I'm sure I would have remembered."
      Talon frowned slightly. "If you do happen to recall it, I'd be curious to know where you think you've seen me."
      "If I do remember," I reassured her, "you'll be the first person I tell." I closed my eyes again, trying to remember that night as clearly as I could. What had been going through my head when I met her? Fear. Confusion. "How long are you planning on staying out here?" I asked Talon instead. "Wouldn't people start to notice if you're gone for too long?"
      Talon sighed tiredly. "You're right. I can't stay out here forever." She slowly sat up, and the little silver beads tangled in her long hair as it tumbled over her shoulders.
      "Would you like me to help you with that?" I asked.
      "It's alright." Talon gave me a soft smile as she tugged the sparkling crystals from her hair. "Face the tree over there, will you?"
      With a look of bewilderment on my face, I turned around. There was the sound of rustling skirts as Talon sat behind me, and moments later she carefully placed the silver beads throughout my hair.
      Talon stood up from the ground and brushed off her skirts. "It's done."
      "What about you, though? You don't want your jewelry back either?"
      "I don't need the pins," Talon told me as she twisted her hair back into a knot and hid her pointed ears. "I think they look better on you anyway."
      I opened my mouth, but no sound came out. Talon just smiled before she leaped up onto the balcony. She was nothing more than a smudge against the night sky. Now alone in the garden, I reached up to touch my hair. I smiled to myself as a light wind rustled my skirts and scattered petals into the air.
      Wait. I hurried over the grass back toward the center of the garden. Sure enough, Talon's shoes were still lying on the ground. I shook my head and bit back my laugh as I knelt down to pick them up: she went back into the ball barefoot. But then again, her dress was probably long enough that no one would be able to see her feet unless they were looking very closely.
      I carefully tucked the heels an empty pocket in my dress before making my way back to Lynden and Storm. My shoes, socks, and apron were still lying where I had left them when I climbed onto the balcony, and I quickly pulled them on. Lynden was waiting for me behind the corner, and it seemed like Storm had returned inside with Talon.
      If Lynden noticed Talon's hair ornaments in my hair, he didn't comment. "Ready to go?" he asked.
      I nodded.
      As we made our way through the empty halls of the estate, I couldn't help but smile. The ball was much more exciting than I had anticipated. It was nerve-wracking at times, yes. But it was also fun.
      With everyone so busy attending to the ballroom and its many distinguished guests, Lynden and I were able to walk right through the front doors. As it was already past midnight, the streets were empty and the town was quiet.
      When we reached the inn, Lynden and I climbed up the stairs to our rooms and bid each other goodnight. After changing into my night dress, I carefully set Talon's shoes on the floor next to the door. When she returned from the ball, she'd surely notice them there.
       
~
       
      I awoke the next morning to find Talon sitting at the small table in the corner of the room. She was wearing a casual dress; the ballgown from the previous night was packed away somewhere.
      Talon smiled at me as I sat up and rubbed the sleep from my eyes. "Good morning, Corinna."
      "Good morning. You left your shoes in the garden, you know. I had to bring them back for you."
      Talon laughed. "Looks like I forgot them." She had removed the brown lenses from her eyes, and her irises were back to their normal crimson.
      "You're lucky I remembered. It would have been a shame if you left them there," I said, and Talon nodded in agreement. "When did you get back? I don't think I heard you come in."
      "We only got back a couple of hours ago," Talon said before standing up from her seat to collect her shoes. "I felt a little bad for Storm. When we finally did leave, he fell asleep in the carriage out of sheer exhaustion."
      "He did tell us he doesn't like these kinds of events. I'm honestly surprised Phina enjoys them."
      Talon absently tucked a loose strand of hair behind her ear. "The way all the nobles gossip behind each other's backs isn't something I can say that I enjoy much, either. Only nobles are hot-headed enough to criticize the king while he's in the same room as them."
      "Is it true that they don't think very highly of him?" I looked over at Talon from my bed. The sun had just started to rise outside the window, and the closed curtains took on a faint golden glow.
      "They don't like how he married your sister." Talon tucked her high heels into one of her trunks, then sat cross-legged on the bed opposite me. "They have even less respect for Chloe-Jane, and they don't even try to hide it."
      "I'm not surprised. People here have always been wary of the southern continent."
      "Speaking of the southern continent," Talon said suddenly, "I overheard that the king is planning to invite representatives from the southern continent to his castle to discuss peace and the end of the war."
      "Invite representatives from the southern continent?" I echoed in disbelief. "But people from the southern continent have never been invited to this kingdom before."
      "Exactly. I'm worried that the king is up to something."
      "It does seem that way, doesn't it? First he withdrew his troops from the war his father started, next he married Chloe-Jane, and now he's even inviting people from the southern continent here for negotiations. If the information dealer's information was correct, that seems a little out of character for him, don't you think?"
      "I completely agree. The king wouldn't be doing any of this unless he personally benefits from it."
      "But how is he benefiting from any of this? All he's accomplished so far is turning his subjects against him."
      "King Volin was ambitious enough to kill off his own father and take his position," Talon said slowly. "I wouldn't put it below him to want to take the southern continent for himself as well."
      I inhaled sharply. "Do you really think so?"
      "I'm not sure what he's planning, but we've got to get Chloe-Jane away from him. Since he married her, I think it's safe to say that she's an integral part of his scheme. Also, another thing that I can't stop thinking about is the king's reaction when I brought up vampires. I think he knows something about them that he isn't letting on."
      "Do you think he really did manage to come up with some method to counter them?" I mused.
      "Let's say he does want to become the most powerful person in the world." Talon rested her chin on the palm of her hand. "Until all vampires are gone, he's still vulnerable to them."
      "Would the king want to have the vampires killed off?" I said slowly. "And if he did, who has enough power to actually kill a vampire with ease?"
      Talon sucked in a breath. "Karmen. But-but the king can't be working with her. If Karmen really is in the castle as we speak"-Talon flopped over onto her bed to stare up at the ceiling-"that is going to be a problem. Karmen despises people like the king, though. It doesn't make any sense for her to work with him."
      I let out a sigh. "We should ask Lynden and Phina about this later. The two of them would know Karmen a lot better than we do."
      Talon stared blankly, and she reached her hands skyward as if the answer was just out of her grasp. "We should head back to the house once Storm wakes up," Talon said after a while. "The sooner we get back, the sooner we can figure out what to do."
      I nodded. Is Chloe-Jane in the hands of both King Volin and Queen Karmen? I asked myself. Is that why she was so terrified when I spoke to her at the ball? Did she see a vampire?
      There was a knock at the door, and Talon and I both turned to look at each other. "Lynden," Talon said at my quizzical look. "I can get it."
      She stood up and hurried across the room to pull open the door. Lynden stood in the doorway with his brown hair pulled back from his face. "I couldn't help but overhear your conversation," Lynden said. "I don't think Karmen is working with the king, either."
      "And just how long have you been eavesdropping on us?" Talon arched a brow as she stepped aside to let Lynden into the room.
      I looked over at Lynden. "You really don't think Karmen is working with the king?"
      "I don't think so. It's people like him who she despises the most."
      "That sounds about right." Talon sat down next to me so Lynden could have her seat on the second bed. "When my parents were murdered, Karmen appeared and offered me a chance to get revenge. You could say that the man who killed them and the king shared the same lust for power."
      "Karmen appeared and saved me from a similar sort of character." Lynden's expression was flat. "But even though I was able to tear everyone who had wronged me into shreds, the damage had already been done."
      Talon tilted her head to the side. "This was at the Winfielde family's estate. You had a sister. And they killed her."
      The Winfielde family. Talon's words came back to me. I quickly looked up at Lynden; he was connected to the murder of an entire house of humans. Phina's words came back to me next. She had mentioned that Lynden had a sister once. It seemed like Talon had put the pieces together.
      "They killed my sister," he said, and the corners of his lip curled away from his teeth in disgust. "But it didn't take me long to realize that even all of their lives combined couldn't bring her back. She was my only family."
      "I'm so sorry," I said quietly.
      Lynden's eyes were blank and his gaze was downcast. "You can't bring the dead back to life. But sometimes I think that it's better this way. In death, all the pain of living can be forgotten for good."
      "You remind me a little of my sister Clarity." I inclined my head in Lynden's direction. "As a coping method, she shuts everyone out and refuses to let anyone get close. Both of you have lost someone in the past, and you don't want to lose anyone else." Lynden remained silent as I continued, "But what Clarity doesn't realize-what she refuses to realize-is that she doesn't have to go through this by herself. You don't need to go through this by yourself."
      Lynden opened his mouth to respond, but a knock at the door cut him off.
      "Hey," Storm's voice called from the other side of the door. "You're all here together. Why didn't anyone wake me up?"
      Talon glanced up. "The door's unlocked. But now that you are awake, we can head out."
      "Fine. I'll go get the carriage." Storm stomped off down the hall.
      "I'll get the luggage ready," Lynden announced. He strode across the room and disappeared out the door.
      Alone in the room with Talon, I reached up to pull the crystal-like beads from my hair. "I should give these back to you." I took one of Talon's hands and gently pressed the beads into them. But before I could withdraw my hand, Talon's fingers closed around mine.
      "You should hold onto them. The other jewelry too. They're too fancy for me to wear normally, and I doubt I'll be going to another ball any time soon. You can sell them, if you want, and buy something of more use."
      "Are you sure?" I asked hesitantly.
      Talon nodded as she pressed the beads back into my own palm. "I'm definitely keeping the dress, though."
      "I'd hope so-it would be such a shame to sell it."
      Laughter danced in her eyes. "Definitely." 
      I carefully tucked the beads into the pocket of my skirt. "I'll keep these, then."
      "Good." Talon stood up and shook back her inky hair. "Storm should have the carriage ready soon. Are you ready to go?"
       
~
       
      For some reason, the carriage ride back to our part of the city seemed longer than our journey to the inn. Maybe it was because all the other nobles who had come to the ball were now heading home, and the streets were packed with more carriages than usual.
      All four of us were inside the cabin this time, and our faith was in the generous amount of coin we had given the coachman. Storm had fallen asleep shortly after we departed with his head resting on the curtains covering the glass windows.
      We arrived back at the house by early afternoon, which was fortunately still intact, and we quickly dragged our trunks inside.
      "You're back!" Phina's overjoyed cry greeted us. The moment we closed the door behind us, the ginger-haired vampire bounced over to us and looked from face to face expectantly. "I'm so jealous-I want to hear all about the ball! What was it like? Did Talon have the prettiest dress?"
      "I can tell you all about it," Storm said with a yawn. "Let's go sit down first."
      "Did something happen to him?" Phina whispered as she watched with wide eyes as Storm made his way over to the living room couch. "The last time I saw him, he was still doing everything he could to avoid us vampires."
      "I think he might have had a change of heart," I said knowingly.
      "A change of heart?" Phina thoughtfully tugged on a strand of her ginger hair. "Are you sure someone didn't beat him senseless? Or maybe he's just tired. He looks pretty tired to me."
      The four of us joined Storm in the middle of the living room and quickly filled Phina in on what had happened and what we had learned. When we got to the part about whether Karmen was working with the king or not, Phina shook her head. "I don't think Karmen is like that," she said with a frown. "The man she saved me from was very much like the king in how he did whatever he could to obtain and keep what he thought was his."
      "So are we in agreement that she isn't in the castle?" Talon asked.
      We all nodded. The vampires knew Karmen better than I did, and if they didn't think the queen of the vampires was working with the king, I'd believe them.
      When the sun finally dropped from the sky, Talon and I got ready to leave for the forest house. The stars twinkled lazily in the night above, and I turned to Talon once we were on the street outside. "You can head back to the house first. There's something I need to do."
      Talon gave me a quizzical look but nodded all the same. "I'll be waiting for you at the house, then."
      I smiled as I pulled the hood of my cloak over my head. "I'll see you later."

Chapter Twenty
       
The next few days seemed to fly by too quickly, and before I knew it, there were only four days left until the start of our rescue mission. Corinna and I had been training together every day, and I was proud that she was rapidly progressing.
      At night, Lynden, Phina, and Storm would join us in the forest house to plan how we were going to break into the castle. Some part of me hoped that Karmen really was in the city, if only so the queen of the vampires could take the king out before we attempted sneaking into the castle. But that was just my wishful thinking. Ever since that night in the alley, I hadn't sensed any other immortal presences in the city.
      Lynden, Phina, Storm, Corinna, and I sat in the small living room of the forest house, going over the castle maps. In the past few days, Storm had considerably warmed up to Lynden, Phina, and me. A small smile crossed my face. We had Corinna to thank for that.
      "I think we should stop here for tonight." Phina was lying face down on the floor with her ginger hair in tangles. "My head can't take it anymore."
      "I agree!" Storm said rapidly from where he was lying next to her. "We've been here for hours. Planning is important, but none of it will stick if we're tired."
      Lynden frowned down at them. "When did the two of you get so unprofessional?"
      Phina just faked a yawn, and her fangs gleamed in the lamplight like a cat.
      Corinna and I sat shoulder to shoulder on the floor with our backs pressed against the couch. Corinna was smiling at the interaction taking place between our three companions, not tired in the slightest. After we had gotten back from the ball, Corinna changed her sleep schedule so that she could stay awake with me longer during the night. Winter had gradually melted into spring, and now the sun shone brightly in the sky every dawn to dusk.
      Lynden stood up, still frowning at Storm and Phina. "We'll take our leave, then. Don't make me carry the two of you back."
      Storm climbed to his feet, and Phina followed his lead. "We can walk."
      "Bye, Corinna. Bye, Talon." Phina waved as the three of them made their way to the door. "We'll be back tomorrow."
      I lifted my hand in farewell as they disappeared outside. Once they were gone, I turned to Corinna. "Are you sure you don't want to go to bed as well?"
      Corinna shook her head, smiling. "I'm not tired. Let's go outside, shall we?"
      The two of us left the house and stepped into the grassy clearing beyond. Apart from the sound of the bubbling stream that snaked through the clearing, the night was quiet.
      Corinna clasped her hands behind her back as she looked up at the sky. The light from the moon painted her in an ethereal glow. Corinna smiled faintly, and there was a wistful look in her eyes. "Whenever I look up at the sky, it always reminds me of how small I am in the grand scheme of things. There's an entire universe out there. A universe filled with stars."
      Corinna took a seat on the grass and patted the ground beside her. I smiled as I sat next to her. I leaned back to look up at the night sky. And for a while, the two of us sat there, gazing up at the thousands of twinkling lights.
      After some time, Corinna rose to her feet. "Let's head back inside. It's starting to get a little chilly out here." Corinna offered me a hand. I took it, and the two of us laughed as she pulled me to my feet.
      Hand in hand, we went back into the house. In the bedroom, Corinna sat me down at the vanity and turned me to face the mirrors. She gently brushed my hair to the side before she carefully fastened a necklace around my neck. My eyes widened as I reached up to touch the delicate string and the silver crystal-like beads that decorated it.
      Corinna leaned forward to meet my eyes in the mirror. "What do you think?"
      "It's beautiful," I whispered.
      Corinna pulled a matching necklace out of her pocket before fastening it around her own neck. "Look-I have one too!"
      "So this is what you were doing the other night."
      "I attached the beads myself, so I hope it doesn't look too bad. It probably wasn't the best use of the beads but-"
      I swiveled around to face her. "I think it's perfect!" 
      Corinna beamed.
      "Would you like to hear a story?" I asked, trying to think of something I could share in return.
      Corinna nodded energetically, and the two of us sat across from each other on the floor. "What's this one about?" Corinna tilted her head to the side in curiosity.
      I rested my chin on my hands. "This is a story my father told me many years ago. It's the story of a girl and a monster that lives in a well."
      When I finished the story, Corinna looked stunned. "Your father told this to you as a bedtime story?"
      "I should have given you some sort of warning that the story didn't end happily," I apologized, suddenly worried I shouldn't have shared such a tale. "I'm sorry."
      Corinna shook her head. "No, I thought it was interesting. I liked it."
      "You liked it?"
      "Every story has a moral. This story shows that even though it was met with a tragic fate, monsters can form friendships. Monsters can love. The monster in the story was only a monster in name. Sometimes the real monsters aren't the ones with the claws and scales."
      That was the message my father had wanted me to understand.
      "Just look at Andreus. He's a dragon, but he loves Storm like his own son." Then Corinna turned to look out the window. "It looks like the sun is rising."
      The sky outside was slowly lightening, and the darkness gradually melted away with the stars and moon. Corinna stood up and made her way over to the window before quickly pulling the curtains over the glass.
      "You don't have to do this, you know," I said as Corinna retook her seat next to me and arranged her skirts around her legs. "I feel bad that in deciding to stay inside with me, you can't see the sun."
      "I don't mind." Corinna's fingers brushed lightly against mine, and I interlaced them together. "I think I've gotten better at sparring recently." She used her free hand to unfasten the dagger strapped to her leg. She twirled the blade around her fingers before setting it down on top of her skirts. "I'm curious to see how I'd fare against Storm."
      "You can ask him if he's willing to take you on later today." I leaned into Corinna's side, and my long hair picked up dust along the floor with the movement. "That said, he's been studying swords for a lot longer than you have. His teacher is a dragon too. You'll have to be careful-Storm is quick on his feet."
      Corinna turned to me, and her eyes were bright with determination. "I'll ask Storm once he arrives later. Maybe he can give me a few tips."
      I stood up from the floor before helping Corinna to her feet. "You should get some sleep. You've got a fight to rest up for."
      Corinna gave me a tired smile. "I suppose you're right."
      I slipped back into the living room and gently closed the door behind me. I stood there for a while, lighting touching my necklace.
       
~
       
      "You want to fight?" Storm blinked at Corinna. It was sunset, and the two of them were standing on the porch of the house.
      Corinna nodded. "I'd like to try."
      Storm raised his brows. "Are you sure?"
      "I really don't mind if I lose. I just want to get some more practice in."
      "Okay, okay." Storm gave in as he unsheathed his sword. "I'm warning you now that I won't go easy on you just because you're my friend."
      I looked on from the doorway, and Phina was standing on her tiptoes to peer over my shoulder. Lynden had gone straight inside the house without a backward glance.
      Corinna flicked her daggers in her hands. "I'm counting on it." The two of them walked onto the stretch of grass before taking their positions. Their blades gleamed in the dying light.
      Storm made the first move, leaping forward, and his sword was nothing more than a blur of silver. Corinna dodged with ease as she sprung backward.
      "I knew you were training with her every day," Phina said excitedly, "but for her to make this much progress in such a short amount of time is really impressive, if I do say so myself!" The ginger-haired vampire rocked back and forth on the balls of her feet. "Even though Corinna seems to be doing well right now, Storm is going to be the winner of this duel."
      "Why do you say so?" I arched a brow as I finally turned to look at the ginger-haired vampire.
      "Look." Phina nodded in Storm's direction. "Storm knows what he's doing. He might be young, but you can tell he's practically had a sword in his hand ever since he could walk. He's the kingdom's legend for a reason."
      "How long have you been practicing with blades?" I asked mildly. "You seem to know quite a lot."
      "I'll admit I dabbled in the art of swords for a few years," Phina said proudly, and she crossed her arms as she puffed out her chest. "I also practiced blades with Lynden for some number of years after that. Lynden's actually very skilled himself! If you ask him, he'll say that it's because I was a good teacher, but he's just being modest." Then her eyes brightened as she jumped up and down. "Look!"
      I turned back to the fight just in time to watch Storm dodge past Corinna and point his sword at her throat. Corinna raised her hands in surrender and the two of them sheathed their weapons.
      "Even though you slipped up a few times, you did a really good job, Corinna." Storm extended his fist and Corinna met it with her own. "It was a good fight."
      "I want to fight too!" Phina called out to them, waving enthusiastically.
      "No you don't," Lynden called. "The last thing we want is for you to get a little too over-enthusiastic and accidentally take someone's arm off."
      Phina just sighed disappointedly.
      "Are the four of you done?" Lynden asked in annoyance. "We have a plan to go over."
      "Yeah, yeah." Storm made his way back over to the house. "We're coming."
      "How did I do?" Corinna's eyes were bright as she stopped in front of me. Even though she had just lost, she was still smiling, and I found myself with a smile on my face as well. "I think I surprised myself with the number of strikes I was able to deflect."
       
~
       
      It was late at night, and both Lynden and Phina had left to get supplies. Storm was sitting on the couch, staring blankly at the wall.
      "You should go outside," Corinna suggested as she looked up at Storm from the pile of maps. "Get some fresh air and take a look at the stars."
      "The view of the sky here is nothing compared to the view of it from my uncle's house," Storm said tiredly as he stood up. "Once this is all over, if I'm still alive, I'm going back to visit my uncle. I wish I could stay in the mountains with him, but as long as there are problems in the kingdom, I need to stay here and protect those who are vulnerable. So far I've been careful enough that the kingdom has let me be, but now that I'm going to break into the king's castle, there's no saying how quickly it will take for them to have me publicly executed. If I get thrown in prison, even my uncle won't be able to save me."
      Corinna and I watched as Storm made his way outside. "Going against the kingdom is practically asking for death," I said as I lowered my voice. "If you successfully escape the castle, you'll be hunted for the rest of your life, Corinna."
      Corinna held my gaze. "I know. But I need to do this for my sister. And this kingdom . . . I won't leave it just yet. There's still so many people I want to try and help."
      Suddenly, there was the sound of footsteps, and both of us turned as the door flew open. We exchanged a glance as Phina hurried into the room with a worried expression.
      "What is it?" Corinna asked, alarmed.
      Phina pulled what looked like a crumpled poster from her cloak. "Lynden's still out, but we found something you might want to see. That crazy king is inviting representatives from the southern continent to his castle next week!"
      "Next week?" I gingerly took the poster from the ginger-haired vampire. At first glance it was an ordinary advertisement for a weapon shop.
      Phina nodded as she wrung her hands together. "Next week."
      "What's this?" I flipped the poster over. On the back of the poster, someone had scribbled in violent letters: DEATH TO THE KING AND QUEEN. WE WILL NOT BOW TO THE SOUTHERN CONTINENT. 
      I gingerly handed the poster back to Phina.
      "I'm worried the king is going to do something to the representatives," Phina said as she tucked the poster back into her cloak. "Whether it's bribery or full-out manipulation, I don't know what he's going to do, but I'm sure it can't be good."
      Corinna shook her head tiredly. "Once we get Chloe out of the castle, we can ask her if she knows anything."
      Phina nodded. Then she leaned in closer and lowered her voice. "What's Storm doing outside? He's just been standing there, staring up at the sky."
      "I think he's missing home," I said.
      Phina offered us a sad smile before she turned to leave. "I can take him back to the other house. We'll be back tomorrow. And by then, everything should be ready."
       
~
       
      I sat on the floor next to the bed in the small bedroom. The sun was shining outside and the curtains glowed with golden light. Corinna was lying on the bed, staring blankly up at the ceiling. We were going to break into the castle tomorrow night.
      "I never thought I'd go to the castle before," Corinna said after a long silence. "I never wanted to go there."
      "I know. I feel the same way."
      Corinna rolled onto her stomach before propping herself up on her elbows. She absently ran her fingers through my hair and hummed quietly as she skillfully separated it into sections to braid.
      "What are you humming?" I asked softly, making sure not to move my head. "I think I've heard you hum this tune before."
      I could hear the faint smile in Corinna's voice. "It's the lullaby my mother would sing to my siblings and me. It's a song from the southern continent. Would you like to hear it?"
      "I'd love to."
      As Corinna quietly sang, I listened intently to the melody and the language of the southern continent.
      "That was beautiful," I said, awed. "Now I'm curious to know what the lyrics mean."
      Corinna continued braiding my hair. "It's a poem, actually. Even though I don't understand much of the lyrics myself, my mother told me that it's the story of the sun and the moon. One day, the moon and sun fell in love. Even though they were so deeply in love, the only time the two of them could be together was during the brief transitions between dawn and dusk. But they didn't let that stop them from loving each other. It was enough to glimpse each other from the opposite ends of the sky."
      I clasped my hands together on my skirts as I brought my knees to my chest. "There's something both beautiful and sad about that."
      "Isn't there?" Corinna said wistfully. "At least this one has a happy ending."
      "At least this one has a happy ending," I echoed. But as the words left my mouth, I realized that happy wasn't quite the word I was looking for. Bittersweet was a lot more fitting.

Chapter Twenty-One
       
I took a deep breath as I walked with the line of servants filing into the castle. All of their heads were bowed as they walked toward the back entrance. With all of their eyes on the ground, it wasn't very likely that they would even notice the newcomer in their midst.
      For the past few weeks, I had carefully studied the layout of the castle and the countless other maps of the grounds that the information dealer had given us. He had even given us insight into the servants' daily routines along with the positions of the knights. And thanks to his help, I didn't flinch when we entered the dark tunnels snaking through the castle. Here in the castle, the servants were everywhere; they did all of the cooking, cleaning, and maintenance. But it was a strict rule that they were never to be seen, hence the hidden passageways.
      I was dressed in the uniform of a maid, with a dagger strapped on each of my legs beneath my skirts. I just hoped I wouldn't actually have to use them. Getting into the castle was the easy part-and maybe a little too easy at that. All I had done was put on the maid uniform and walk straight through the servants' entrance. The knights standing guard at the doors hadn't even looked at me twice.
      I followed a group of uniformed young women through the dark passage and through the door to the supplies room. Each of them picked up a bucket and mop before continuing down the hall. I grabbed my own before trailing after them.
      We walked down a flight of steps to a dimly lit room. A small well sat in the middle of the stone floor, and each woman took a turn filling her bucket. As I walked over to fill my own bucket, one of the maids took it from me and shuffled over to the well to fill it. She returned a few seconds later.
      "You're new here," the young woman said quietly as she handed me my bucket. Her eyes were tired and her skin was sallow. She couldn't have been any older than me.
      I nodded.
      "Whatever you do"-the young woman lowered her voice, and I leaned in closer to pick up her words-"stay away from the king."
      "The king?" I asked with as much innocence as I could muster.
      "There's something wrong with his mind," the maid whispered. "I'll let you know that we're not allowed into the dungeons either. Make sure you don't ever end up down there."
      "Noted," I whispered back. "Thank you for your advice."
      The maid nodded once before shuffling off, leaving me alone in the dim room. The smell of mildew was starting to get to my head. With my bucket in one hand and mop in the other, I turned back to the passageway. It was time to do some cleaning.
      I ambled through the dark passageways, grimacing as the bones of a small animal crunched beneath my feet. It was dark and cold save for the occasional torch, and the dwindling flames were the only source of heat.
      After taking a deep breath to center myself, I followed my mental map of the passages to the door leading to the third floor. I gently pushed the door open and squinted against the sudden rush of light. When my eyes finally adjusted to the brightness, I slipped out into the corridor beyond. As I made my way toward the far end of the castle, I realized the entire place was deprived of life. Everything was silent, and my footsteps seemed to echo for miles.
      A shiver ran down my spine as I continued down the hall, scrubbing the large stained-glass windows as I went. I could have sworn I felt eyes pressing down on the back of my head. But each time I snuck a glance over my shoulder, there was never anyone there.
      After what could have been minutes or hours, I finally reached the end of the long hall and pushed open the door to the spiraling staircase beyond. The window was right in front of me, and I set my bucket down on the steps. This was the window Talon and Lynden would enter through at midnight.
      After scrubbing the window down with my rag, I carefully unlatched it and pushed it open to dry. As I scanned the window frame for anything suspicious, my eyes quickly fell on the tiny mirror-like panels lying on the windowsill.
      I stared at them for a moment before I tentatively stuck my hand over the row of panels. Nothing happened. Frowning to myself, I tapped the panels with a finger. Still nothing.
      But as I touched it, the panel shifted. There was something beneath them.
      After setting my mop and rag down as well, I gently shifted one of the panels over. A tiny candle sat beneath the panel, and the little flame danced in the wind from the open window. The candle was too deep inside the wall for me to blow out even if I had wanted to.
      I moved the next panel over to find another candle nestled inside the wall underneath it. Did the panels somehow amplify the light from the flames? It didn't seem to affect me in any way, but I wondered if it was enough to stop a vampire from leaping through the window. Vampires are vulnerable to both light and fire, after all.
      I carefully replaced the panels before picking up my cleaning supplies. I would douse the flames when I came back later. If I put them out now, someone might get suspicious if they were to check on it.
      I climbed the spiraling stairs to the fourth floor before getting to work on the long corridor beyond, all the while trying to ignore the prickling feeling that someone was watching my every movement.
       
~
       
      When night fell, I returned to the dark passageway to put away my bucket and mop. But instead of following the rest of the maids to the servants' quarters, I lingered behind before silently slipping back into the dark passageways. Once the clock tower chimed eleven, I would make my move.
      I took a seat on the cold stones that made up the floor of the passageway, glancing around every few seconds as if someone would emerge from the dark at any moment. The near pitch-black passageways were dreary, with a constant silence pressing down from all sides. Someone had definitely been watching me.
      My fingers closed instinctively around the hilt of one of my daggers. Something was wrong, but it was far too late to go back now. Once Talon and Lynden arrive, I reassured myself, the two of them will be able to fight their way out if needed.
      Whoever had been watching me must have not followed me into the servants' passageways because the pickling under my skin slowly subsided. Either they didn't know how to navigate the tunnels, or they deemed me not a threat after all.
      At long last, the distant clock tower struck eleven, and its loud echo of chimes nearly made me jump out of my skin. I slowly rose from the ground-my heart pounding a little too quickly for my liking-and made my way back to the well. I carefully took a bucket, filled it halfway with water, and started off down the passageway. This time when I emerged on the third floor, everything was dark. The moonlight filtered in through the windows, tinting the light in shades of red, orange, and purple as it passed through the stained glass.
      I held my breath as I tiptoed all the way to the door at the end of the corridor. When I reached it, I pushed it open as quietly as I could. Since the knights switched their posts before twelve, there wasn't going to be anyone on this floor of the castle until a little after midnight-which would give us just enough time to grab Chloe-Jane and escape.
      Someone had closed the window I opened earlier in the day, and I suddenly felt very glad I hadn't put out the candles yet.
      I unlatched the window for a second time and quietly pushed it open. The night sky outside was full of stars, and the moon was hidden behind a layer of clouds. A soft breeze rushed in to rustle my hair as I swiftly removed the rest of the panels from the window seal. The candles were still flickering inside the wall, and I made quick work of dumping the water from my bucket onto them.
      Fortunately I didn't have to wait long for midnight. The moment the first chime sounded, there was a rush of wind as a dark-haired figure gracefully leaped through the open window. She landed on her feet before brushing her inky hair over a shoulder. She turned to smile at me. "I hope you weren't waiting too long."
      "Talon!" I whispered excitedly.
      There was a second rush of wind as Lynden joined us in the stairwell. Both of them were dressed entirely in black to blend in with the night, and Talon had swapped her usual dress for a pair of trousers.
      Lynden went directly to the panels I had moved to the corner of the window. "What are these?"
      I frowned slightly. "I'm not sure. But they probably have something to do with keeping vampires from just jumping into the castle any time they please. We can worry about it later though-we shouldn't linger here."
      Talon nodded. "Let's go."
      I shut the window before I hurried to follow Talon and Lynden up the stairs. We had to go all the way to the top story to get to Chloe-Jane's room and then back down to the ninth story to make our exit from the balconies.
      "I think someone might be onto us," I said under my breath as we jogged up the spiraling staircase. "I felt someone watching me earlier. I could feel their eyes on me for hours."
      Talon's eyes narrowed. "We better hurry."
      The three of us quickened our pace, and when we reached the top story, I followed Chloe-Jane's directions on how to get to her room. As she had said, it was indeed the highest point in the entire castle. In a matter of minutes, we were standing in front of the door to her chambers. I exchanged a glance with Talon before pressing my ear to the door. There was silence. I reached for the knob, and the door swung open without a sound.
      The room was quite large, and all the furniture was polished to a gleam. Even though lavish rugs, curtains, and blankets were abundant, it felt eerily like a prison.
      Chloe-Jane stood with her back to us, staring out the large window arching the stone wall. She was dressed in a cream-colored nightgown, and her thick hair was loose and unbound. The way the moonlight flooded in through the glass gave her an ethereal appearance as she glowed with a faint silver light.
      "Chloe-Jane," I whispered as I tiptoed into the dark room.
      Chloe-Jane remained standing by the window as if she hadn't heard me.
      "Chloe," I tried again, louder this time. "Chloe-Jane?" When she still didn't respond, I reached out and cautiously tapped her on the shoulder.
      Chloe-Jane screamed, and I clapped a hand over my sister's mouth in a panic.
      "Chloe-Jane!" I hissed as she thrashed and clawed at my hand. Her nails drew blood. "It's me! Corinna!"
      "Corinna?" Chloe-Jane stilled as she turned to look up at me. Then she grabbed my arm. Her face was pale and her eyes were wide and wild as they scanned my face. "Who are those two?" Her nails dug into my skin as she nodded toward Talon and Lynden.
      "They're friends," I quickly reassured her. "We're here to get you out."
      "Friends?" Chloe-Jane eyed them cautiously as she squinted through the dark. "Wait! I recognize the girl with the black hair! She was dancing with the king at the ball while you spoke with me . . ."
      I gently took Chloe-Jane's hand with my scratched one. "Quickly now-we don't have much time."
      Chloe-Jane nodded and let me lead her out the door. "Where are we going?" Chloe-Jane asked as we jogged down corridor after corridor.
      "We're going to the ninth-floor balconies."
      "The ninth-floor balconies?" Chloe-Jane repeated blankly. "Are we going to climb?"
      I exchanged a glance with Talon. "You'll find out when we get there." We had agreed it was better not to let Chloe-Jane know that they were vampires until we had made it out safely. I knew Chloe-Jane well enough to know that my sister would not take the information well. And the last thing we wanted right now was to send her into another panic.
      But just as we reached the ninth floor, Lynden threw out an arm, stopping us in our tracks. He narrowed his eyes; his expression was dead serious. "Something's not right."
      Talon's head snapped up. "Vampires. There are vampires here."
      I felt my heart sink. "Vampires?"
      "Vampires?" Chloe-Jane echoed in shock. I blinked as I turned to look at her. It was clear this was the first time she had heard of there being vampires in the castle . . . So then what triggered that reaction earlier?
      "Hurry!" Talon broke into a run. I quickly followed her lead, and my heart pounded away in my chest. Queen Karmen couldn't actually be here, could she?
      Talon threw open the doors to the balcony before skidding to a stop. I felt my heart sink as I staggered to a stop next to her.
      There standing on the balcony railing was a dark-haired male. His fangs glinted as he smiled down at us, and his blood-red irises glowed. "So the king was right after all," the vampire said in feigned amusement. "People actually did break into the castle to try to take the queen away. He never expected them to be vampires and a slave girl, though."
      "Are you going to move?" Lynden glared coldly at the male. "Or are we going to have to make you move?"
      The dark-haired vampire hopped down onto the balcony to lean casually against the railings. "Oh, I'm not going anywhere. I'm supposed to delay you long enough for the king to arrive."
      Talon's daggers were in her hands in an instant as she sprung forward. But before she could reach the male, there was a blur of gold as a figure descended from somewhere above. Metal clashed against metal, and I took in the new figure in horror.
      A blonde-haired female had locked blades with Talon. There was a cat-like smirk on her pale face. "You're outnumbered," she purred.
      "Outnumbered?" Talon angled her head to the side, and her eyes glowed crimson. "Even if that's the case, who says I can't end you right here and now?"
      "Oh?" The female laughed. Her long blonde hair took on a silver sheen in the pearly light. "I'd like to see you try!"
