      One moment the two of them leaped apart; the next, they sprung back at each other again with their blades flashing. They moved too fast for me to keep up, and the two of them were nothing more than a blur of metallic silver, inky black, and blonde against the night.
      After pushing Chloe-Jane behind me, I raised my dagger with shaky hands. My heart was beating so fast now I was surprised I was still conscious. I felt dizzy. Why were there vampires here in the castle? Why were there vampires working for the king?
      "Vampires?" Chloe-Jane was grabbing my arm so tightly now I was afraid my circulation would be cut off. "Corinna, you're working with vampires? But-but that makes you a sinner!"
      "Does that even matter right now?" My voice was unusually high, if not shrill. "We're in big trouble and this is what you're worrying about?"
      "Let's back up," Lynden said under his breath as he motioned for Chloe-Jane and me to follow. "While Talon's got these two distracted, we'll try to find the next balcony."
      I nodded quickly, but just as I took a step back, I felt myself walk into something solid. I froze, then slowly turned around to look into the red eyes of a new vampire.
      The female vampire currently fighting Talon on the balcony had told us that we were outnumbered-but by how much?
      I pushed Chloe-Jane behind me again. My blade arm shook violently. I couldn't let my sister go again. Not this time.
      "What do we have here?" The new vampire sneered down at me. His hair was so light it almost appeared white. "A little girl with a little knife?"
      Lynden drew his sword and pointed it at the vampire. "Stand down."
      "Well, well, well," the vampire purred. "If it isn't Lynden. Looks like you're still Karmen's dog after all."
      "I don't work for the queen anymore," Lynden said coldly. "Now move out of our way."
      "Move?" The vampire arched a brow. "I think not."
      Lynden leaped forward in a flash of metal, and the sound of clashing blades resonated through the corridor.
      "This way," I whispered as I tugged Chloe-Jane down the hall. If only we could get to the next balcony over, maybe-just maybe-
      "I don't think so," a male voice laughed. The dark-haired vampire from the balcony dropped down in front of me. "The king wants to see all three of you thieves."
      "How did the king know that we'd break in?" I demanded with a lot more confidence than I felt.
      "It was actually one of the former guards," the vampire said as if he couldn't care less. "He ran all the way from that shithole of a port town to request an audience with the king. He met with me and said that he had important information. He claimed that a band of knights led by Storm the Dragonhearted wanted to break into the castle. I paid him graciously for such information, of course." The vampire smirked at my thunderstruck expression. "He was right about the castle going to be broken into, but he failed to tell us that it was going to be vampires and a slave girl."
      I narrowed my eyes. "You were watching me earlier."
      "I was." The vampire continued to watch me. "What kind of maid carries around knives with her?"
      I unfastened my second dagger from my holster. "I'm no maid. Now let us pass or else I'll have to fight you."
      The dark-haired vampire howled with laughter. "Fight me? The little girl thinks she can fight me?"
      I sprinted forward with my blades at the ready. The vampire easily sidestepped me, but at the last moment, I swiveled and slashed out with all of my strength. Cloth split as I tore through the vampire's sleeve. I nearly nicked the flesh beneath before the vampire twirled away.
      "What-?" The dark-haired vampire blinked in shock. "The little girl knows how to fight?"
      I remained silent as I eyed the vampire's every movement.
      The vampire drew the sword at his side. "Alright then-let's see how good you really are!"
      He leaped at me so fast that I barely had time to block before his sword made contact with my daggers. The force from his blow was so strong my very arms felt the shock wave roll through them. I gritted my teeth. My arms were screaming and my legs were shaking as I braced them the best I could on the ground. Metal splintered as my first blade broke.
      Suddenly, there was a blur of inky black as Talon dropped down beside me. "Take Chloe-Jane to the secret passageways!" Talon called as she twirled her daggers. "I'll hold them off!"
      I bit my lip as I nodded. The blonde-haired vampire appeared a moment later and I was instantly moving.
      "Hurry." I pulled Chloe-Jane along. My body was powered by the adrenaline flowing through my veins. I had faith that Talon could hold the two of them off.
      Just before we reached the end of the corridor, Chloe-Jane slowed to a stop.
      "Chloe?" I panted. But before I could ask any further questions, Chloe-Jane lunged at me and wrestled my dagger from my hand. "Hey!" I fought with her for a hold over the blade. "Stop that!"
      Maybe it was because Chloe-Jane was too quick or because I was hesitant to be forceful with her that she successfully pried the dagger from my grasp.
      "What are you doing?" I hissed as she danced out of my reach, clutching my dagger tightly in her hands.
      My feet seemed to move on their own as Chloe-Jane lifted the blade to her neck.
      I tackled her in one swift motion and the two of us tumbled to the ground.
      Chloe-Jane let out a yelp as I yanked the dagger from her hands and tossed it away. The blade hit the ground with a clank as it skidded out of reach down the polished tiles. "He's going to kill me! He's going to kill me!" Chloe-Jane cried.
      "Snap out of it!" I shook her shoulders in a panic as she thrashed around in an attempt to crawl toward the discarded dagger. "What do you think you're doing?"
      Another voice spoke up. "I think the real question is what do you think you're doing?"
      My head snapped up to find King Volin standing in the middle of the corridor. Two more vampires stood behind him.
      At the sound of his voice, Chloe-Jane began to flail around in fright.
      The king walked over to where my dagger had skidded to a stop and bent down to pick it up. He eyed the blade before carefully pocketing it. King Volin stared down at Chloe-Jane, and his deep-green eyes were unreadable. "Take them to the dungeons. This one is coming with me."
      "She's not going anywhere," I said angrily. I jumped to my feet in an attempt to shield my sister with my body. But before I could even blink, there was a blur of motion as one of the king's vampires leaped behind me. I barely had time to register what was happening before something heavy collided with my head and everything went black.
       
~
       
      When I came to, I found myself lying on a cold stone floor. I slowly opened my eyes, and my head throbbed painfully as I hauled myself into a sitting position. Looking around the dimly lit space, it didn't take me long to realize I was in a prison cell. The bars slowly came into focus as I squinted through the dark.
      After crawling over to the bars, I tried my best to see out into the rest of the dungeon. I was in a circular room; the cells surrounded an open space in the middle. And from what I could tell, I was the only person here.
      The faint sound of water dripping in the distance told me that I was somewhere deep underground. I shivered as I retreated further into my cell. Other than a pounding headache, I seemed to be fine.
      "Corinna?" a familiar voice asked softly as it echoed through the stone room.
      "Talon!" I jumped to my feet and swayed from a sudden rush of dizziness. I fought through it and hurried over to grasp the bars of my cell. In the center of the large room, Talon was chained to a rectangular pillar. At first glance, I had mistaken her for a statue because of her stillness. "What happened?" I asked as I pressed myself as close to the bars as I could.
      "There were too many vampires, and I was taken by surprise." Talon shook her head in defeat. "I'm sorry Corinna, I never would have thought King Volin would have vampires working with him."
      I exhaled heavily. "This isn't your fault. I couldn't have predicted this either."
      "Here's the weird thing." I could hear the frown in Talon's voice. "These are some of the vampires who oppose Karmen."
      "Oppose Karmen?" I slumped to the floor; my headache was getting the better of me. "I guess we can eliminate the possibility that she's in the castle, then."
      "I'm thinking the vampire I saw in the alley that day was one of the ones working for the king," Talon said grimly. "Karmen wouldn't sneak around the city in a cloak like that. Since no one knows what she looks like, she could just waltz past us, and we still wouldn't have known it was her."
      "Where's Lynden?" I strained my eyes to see if the other vampire was somewhere in the room with us. "Where's Chloe-Jane?"
      Talon's chains clinked as she slumped. "Lynden was separated from me and dragged into a different room. I'm worried about what's going to happen to him. I don't know what's going to happen to us either, and I really don't want to find out."
      I swallowed hard. "How long have I been knocked out?"
      "Just about an hour or so." Talon's voice was tired. Suddenly she stiffened. "Someone's coming."
      Dread began to seep into the very fabric of my being as I backed away from the bars. I wondered if I should have taken the information dealer's advice of slitting my own throat before getting thrown into the dungeons. The sounds of muffled crying grew louder and louder, followed by the sound of footsteps. I staggered back up to the bars. "Chloe-Jane?"
      "That's right." King Volin appeared in the doorway with his hand closed tightly around Chloe-Jane's arm. "This is Chloe-Jane." The sound of iron chains rattling filled the air, and then a number of glowing lamps descended from the high ceiling. I blinked as the sudden light stung savagely at my eyes.
      "How do you know Chloe-Jane?" King Volin stopped outside my cell, and suddenly I was very glad there was a wall of bars between us. Chloe-Jane was still dressed in her nightgown, and her face was almost completely drained of blood. Her wild eyes locked on mine and her bloodless lips mouthed my name.
      I glared at the king. "She's my sister."
      "She's your sister," he repeated slowly. "Now that you tell me, I do see a slight resemblance. But I must say that Chloe-Jane here is prettier than you are. Much more obedient too. How is it that one sister is the perfect wife and the other a thief?"
      "So I'm a thief for wanting to get my sister back?" I demanded, suddenly very brave with the wall of bars between us. For my sister, I would be brave.
      "Watch your tone, girl." King Volin's hand tightened on Chloe-Jane's arm, and I froze. "Now, I'm going to ask you a series of questions, and you're going to answer me."
      "And what if I don't want to answer?"
      The king's eyes flashed as he smirked. "For every question you refuse to answer, dear Chloe-Jane here will lose a finger." In one swift movement, a wicked-looking dagger was in his hand. Its blade pointed at Chloe-Jane. "We'll start now. Question one, what's your name?"
      "Falon," I said with as much confidence as I could muster. My eyes were glued to Chloe-Jane.
      "Liar." The king was smiling a smile that didn't quite reach his eyes. "I don't like being lied to." He forcefully grabbed Chloe-Jane's hand and swung his glinting blade into the air. Chloe-Jane screamed.
      "Stop!" I threw myself against the bars of my cell. "Your Majesty, it's Corinna! My name's Corinna!"
      To my surprise, the king burst into laughter as he shoved Chloe-Jane away. My sister staggered over the stone floor before falling over. She whimpered quietly as she clutched her hands to her chest.
      "That was quite a reaction," King Volin snorted. "It was a joke! You really thought I would cut off her fingers? Don't tell me you can't take a joke. I just thought I'd try to lighten the mood."
      "Jokes are supposed to be funny," I said faintly. My heart pounded so fast it was difficult to breathe. "That was not funny."
      The king just waved me off as he continued to laugh. "Tell me"-King Volin's expression suddenly changed as he pulled Chloe-Jane back up from the ground-"how did a useless slave wench like yourself end up working with vampires?" His green eyes were crazed, and his smile was wild as he dragged the point of his blade along Chloe-Jane's upper arm, drawing blood.
      "I thought you said you weren't going to hurt her!" I cried out, having to raise my voice to be heard over Chloe-Jane's screams.
      "I said I wouldn't cut her fingers off, silly girl." The king laughed again as if this really was nothing more than a game to him. "I never said anything about cutting her-"
      "Stop it!" Talon yelled. "Corinna and I met at the farms. I helped her escape, and we've been working together ever since."
      "Silence, vampire!" King Volin snapped. His expression turned dangerous as he pressed his blade deeper into Chloe-Jane's arm. "I don't remember asking you to speak."
      Talon fell silent as Chloe-Jane screamed again. All three of us were helpless in this situation.
      "It hurts!" Chloe-Jane cried. She was hyperventilating now, and tears streamed down her cheeks as she writhed to no avail.
      "Silence!" the king roared. "I don't care!"
      "It's true." I tried and failed to keep the tremor out of my voice. "We met a number of months ago and have been traveling together ever since."
      The king smirked, and the insanity behind his eyes was becoming more prominent with each passing second. "Not so brave are we now? That's right, you're going to tell me everything I want to know. Now."

Chapter Twenty-Two
       
I could practically smell Corinna's fear; it mingled with Chloe-Jane's pure terror as it shoved its way up my nose. As the king stood with his back to me, I tried as quietly as I could to tug at my chains. But despite my immortal strength, they wouldn't budge.
      King Volin turned to look over his shoulder at me, and I froze. "I never expected you to be a vampire. What a shame. You really got my attention there at the ball too."
      I hissed as my lips curled back from my fangs.
      The king just laughed. As King Volin's attention was on me, Chloe-Jane suddenly twisted out of his grasp and made a grab for his dagger. But before her small hands could even touch the blade, King Volin kicked Chloe-Jane solidly in the stomach. Chloe-Jane hit the floor with a thud before curling into a ball. She clapped her hands over her ears as if to block everything out. "How many times have I told you?" King Volin was still smiling. "You aren't allowed to die yet. If you die now, what am I supposed to do next week when the representatives from the southern continent arrive?"
      "What are you going to do to her?" Corinna demanded shrilly.
      "Silence, slave girl!" The king whirled around. His smile was suddenly replaced by a very ugly look. "Has anyone ever taught you to hold your tongue? You ask too many questions. You will speak only when you're spoken to." The look in his eyes was chilling. "You're lucky I'm in a good mood tonight," he said quietly, dangerously. "Otherwise, I would cut that tongue of yours out myself." Then he was smiling again. "But why would I bother myself with a slave girl tonight while I have vampires here to play with?"
      Corinna's eyes met mine from across the room; they were wide with terror as King Volin walked over to me without a second glance at Chloe-Jane, who was still trembling on the stone floor.
      "I was always curious just how fast vampires can regenerate," King Volin mused as he stopped in front of me, dagger in hand. "As long as I don't take off your head, you won't die. So what happens if I drain all of your blood? Will you become a weak vampire? A creature on par with a human?"
      There was a flash of metal as the king slit my wrists. Even though I couldn't feel the pain, I could feel the blood inside of me ever so slowly begin to drip out, and it took my strength with it. But within seconds, my skin had already begun to knit itself back together; my wounds were healing themselves.
      "Interesting," King Volin said to himself as he looked on. I braced myself as the king's dagger flew through the air and my skin was split open yet again.
      "Stop it!" Corinna yelled from her cell, unable to remain silent any longer. "Why are you doing this?"
      "Why am I doing this?" King Volin paused as he hovered his blade over my right arm. A smirk spread across his face. "I'm curious. And it's fun." There was a flash of metal and the sound of tearing flesh as his blade came down and severed my hand from my body.
      I hissed. It would take me at least a day or two for my hand to grow back, but in the meantime, I would lose blood. A lot of it. And that wasn't something I could regenerate on my own.
      "I've got to do your other hand now, don't I?" King Volin ran a finger over the flat side of his dagger and looked at the blood that came off of it in vague amusement. "The best way to subdue a beast is to cut off its claws." The king swung his wicked blade through the air. It gleamed in the flickering light as my left hand hit the blood-spattered stones at my feet.
      The coppery scent of my blood was thick in the air as I stared at King Volin. "You're a monster."
      "Me?" The king blinked before bursting out in laughter. He wiped away the blood that had splattered on his face. "That's very funny coming from the vampire."
      "Once I get these chains off," I whispered, "I will tear you to pieces."
      King Volin ignored my threat as he turned and walked back over to Chloe-Jane "Now that we've become acquainted, I want you to tell me where Karmen is."
      "Karmen?" Corinna inhaled sharply. "How do you know about Karmen?"
      "How do you know about the queen of the vampires?" The king looked crazed, with traces of blood smeared over his features. He walked over to Corinna's cell and unlocked the door. I watched in horror as the king grabbed her by the arm and forced her out. His dagger was pressed against her throat. "If you don't tell me where Karmen is"-the king turned to look at me-"the slave girl dies."
      "Leave Corinna out of this," I said quickly, my panic rising.
      "Oh?" The king raised a brow. "I'm curious now, vampire. What does a single human mean to you? Are you going to tell me where the queen is, vampire? Or do you still need more of an incentive?"
      Corinna's frightened eyes met mine.
      King Volin turned impatient. In one swift swipe of his dagger, he slashed open the skin on Corinna's face and a long gash appeared over her cheek. "Remembered yet?"
      Corinna inhaled sharply as the scent of her blood filled the large stone room.
      "Karmen's in the capital city," I said desperately.
      "At least she was," Corinna cut in.
      "Was?" King Volin's eyes gleamed. "What do you mean she was?"
      "Karmen is dead," Corinna choked out. "She killed the queen."
      The king looked at me in disbelief; the insanity on his face was briefly replaced with shock. "You killed Karmen?"
      "That's right." I schooled my face into an easy smile as I tried to hide my own surprise. "We killed her right before the ball."
      King Volin shook his head in astonishment. He threw Corinna back into her cell, then marched to Chloe-Jane, who was still curled on the floor, and forcefully pulled the poor girl to her feet. The king dragged Chloe-Jane out of the room. The door slammed shut behind them, and the lights retracted back into the ceiling a moment later.
      I stared at Corinna through the dark. Her eyes were just as wide as mine were as she met my gaze.
      "I can't believe he actually fell for that," Corinna whispered, still shaken.
      I shook my head, stunned. "Me neither."
      Corinna dropped to her knees and leaned her head against the bars of her cell. "It made the king leave for the time being. Are-are you alright?"
      I offered Corinna a weak smile. "I'm fine. I can't feel the pain, remember? I'm really sorry you had to see that, though. It probably looked a lot worse than it actually was. What about you?"
      Corinna let out a breath as her gaze dropped to the hands lying by me on the blood-coated stones. "I'm fine. A little cut won't phase me." She drew her knees to her chest. "I just don't want to see you get hurt."
      I sighed. "It's better me than you. If I lose a limb, at least I can grow it back."
      "I know you can't feel the pain, but I know for a fact that if we ever get out of here, this will haunt me for a very long time."
      I slumped; the tight shackles around my elbows prevented me from moving. "I'm so sorry."
      "Don't be sorry," Corinna said sadly. "We were sold out by that sketchy information dealer. If I ever find that man, he's going to regret ever going to the castle."
      "What do you think happened to Phina and Storm?" I asked. The steady dripping of my blood sent my skin crawling. "Do you think they're still waiting below the balcony for us? Or did they realize that something happened and hid?"
      Corinna stared up at the ceiling of her cell. "I just hope they don't try and break in to save us. They don't know there are vampires in the castle. And Lynden . . . he's all alone right now. For all we know he could be even worse off than we are."
      "Phina and Storm are smart." I wasn't sure who I was trying to convince more, Corinna or myself. "The two of them will probably figure it out pretty quickly. Lynden, on the other hand . . . we can only hope that he's doing better than we are." There was a long pause. "I want to know how King Volin got five vampires to work for him. I know for a fact that those five vampires working for King Volin oppose Karmen."
      "What do you think he wants from Karmen?" Corinna asked. Her voice was tired.
      I let out another sigh. "I have no clue. But Karmen is dead. Well, according to us at least."
      "I don't know how long we'll be able to keep the story up. If the king questions Lynden and gets different answers, I can't see things ending well. Also, did you notice that Chloe-Jane was so intent on killing herself?"
      "Killing herself?" This was new to me.
      "While you and Lynden were fighting those other vampires," Corinna explained quietly, "I took Chloe-Jane to run down the hall. But then Chloe suddenly grabbed my dagger and tried to slit her throat."
      I inhaled sharply. "You think the king did something to her?"
      Corinna looked at her hands. "I don't know. She claimed that the king was going to kill her. When the king was holding me earlier, I noticed that his hands were covered in scratches. Chloe had tried to fight him at some point. I don't think we're going to get answers from the king himself, though, and I'm pretty sure Chloe-Jane won't be coming down here again if she can help it." Corinna fell silent, and for a long time the only sound was Corinna's quiet breathing and the steady dripping of my blood as it pooled around my feet.
      "If we do end up dying here," Corinna said after a while, "I'll admit, I think I'll be a little disappointed. But now that I'm here, as a whole, I don't mind. I might not have been able to free Chloe-Jane, but I want to believe that Phina and Storm will finish the job for me. Ever since I left the farm, I knew death was a possibility. Who knows how long I would have lived on the farm. I don't regret leaving. I don't regret meeting you, Talon. I never have. If there is one thing I regret, it's not being able to have spent more time with you."
      I smiled weakly. "I wish I could have spent more time with you as well. I've never felt this alive in years. Ever since I lost my family and then the sisters, you're the first person in a long time to truly accept me as who I am. I-I just feel so happy whenever we spend time together. I've treasured every moment of it."
      Corinna returned my smile as she let out a small laugh. "Isn't living wonderful?"
      "It is." I held her gaze. "It's a shame that now that I've found a reason to live, death is right around the corner."
      "I guess that can't be helped. At least we'll be able to face it together."
      "There's something I haven't told you yet," I said softly. "About my late family."
      "What is it?"
      "My father," I started, "he was a king. My mother was a queen. And I was the princess of our small kingdom in the east."
      "That's who you reminded me of!" Corinna's eyes widened as she jumped to her feet. "That book my mother snuck back to our house all of those years ago-I remember seeing the picture of a princess there. It was you!"
      My own eyes grew large. "That must have been where the king recognized me from too. I completely forgot that a portrait of me was put in a book."
      "It was Princess . . . Princess . . ." Corinna's brow furrowed. "I can't seem to recall your name."
      "Well, that makes two of us."
      "So the man who killed your parents . . . he wanted to become king?"
      I nodded. "Before I became a vampire, I was actually engaged to my cousin. My parents never pushed the idea of marriage, though. They just wanted me to be happy. But my cousin wanted to rule the kingdom-well, my aunt was the one who wanted to rule the kingdom. But when she realized I wasn't going to marry her son even with the arrangement in place, she grew angry and sent my cousin to attack the castle. But after everyone in my castle was dead, the people of the kingdom were outraged and took the castle back. After that, with no leader, our small kingdom was easily conquered by the west."
      "Your cousin got what he deserved," Corinna said in a mixture of shock and disgust.
      "He did. I'm just slightly disappointed that I couldn't end him myself."
      "And your aunt?"
      "When she heard her precious son had been killed, she committed suicide."
      Corinna fell silent for a long moment. Then her eyes widened. "Have you told anyone else that you're a princess? Wait-you're a queen now, aren't you?"
      "Since both my father and mother passed away, I'm technically the queen now."
      "That means there are three queens in the capital city then." Corinna stared at me in realization. "You, Chloe-Jane, and Karmen."
      I frowned slightly. "If I really am one of the four queens from the legend, that means I don't have much time left to live. All the queens are said to die before the end of the ninth century."
      "That means Chloe-Jane is going to die too?" Corinna's head snapped up. "Or wait-she could just live out her regular mortal lifespan within that time."
      I let out a heavy sigh. "Other than you, Karmen is the only other person who knows that I'm a queen. I was worried Karmen would show up at our door one day, but she never did. It's common knowledge that Karmen killed the first progenitor and the other vampires he turned." I closed my eyes for a brief moment as I remembered how the queen's glowing red eyes shone from the depths of her hooded cloak. "Countless humans have died at her hands as well. At first I wanted to find and put an end to Karmen, like Lynden and Phina, but then I heard about the legend of the four queens from Andreus. The legend of the four queens says that four queens will rise up and change the world for the better. Isn't changing the world for the better one final piece of good we can try to do with our cursed lives?"
      Corinna took a seat on the floor of her cell. "Changing the world certainly isn't going to be easy. Do you really think people can change?"
      "Yes," I said quietly. "I think they can. I believe they can."
      "But what if they don't want to change?" Corinna asked with equal quiet.
      I smiled sadly. "Then all we can do is continue to encourage them to see the world from a new perspective. Encourage them to set aside their hatreds and start again."
      Corinna gave me a small smile. "We've got to get you out of here then. You've got a world to change."
       
~
       
      I wasn't sure how much time had passed since King Volin had come to visit us in the dungeons. It had to have been at least two days, though, as both my hands had grown back. The fact that no one had come down to bring Corinna any food was becoming more and more worrying by the hour.
      Suddenly, the door to our block of the dungeon was thrown open, and I slowly turned my head to watch King Volin step into the room. Chloe-Jane was with him again, and her eyes were downcast and ringed with dark circles. She refused to look at me or Corinna. The king motioned for her to stand by the doors and Chloe-Jane nodded. Her hands were clasped together on top of her skirts so tightly that her knuckles had turned white. It seemed as if the king brought Chloe-Jane everywhere with him.
      The king's eyes flashed as he strode over to me. "We meet again, vampire."
      "What do you want?" I demanded, but my voice was lacking strength. I had lost too much blood already.
      King Volin smiled. It was a terrible smile. "I spent the last three days questioning that other vampire. Oh, don't worry. He's still alive. Barely. But he didn't seem to know anything about Karmen's death."
      "Obviously." I forced a laugh. "Why would I tell him? Even though he claims not to work for the queen anymore, he's still loyal. He wouldn't have wanted his former master dead."
      "That useless vampire refused to tell me anything," King Volin hissed in annoyance. "Even when I set him on fire he still refused to talk!"
      "And why do you think we'd tell you anything?" I angled my head to the side as I tried my best not to let my horror show on my face. "A mortal like yourself should be more afraid of what we'll do to you once we escape."
      The king just laughed. "Who said anything about escaping? You can't escape. Here's the deal, vampire. I want you to turn me into a vampire."
      "What? You're insane!"
      "I'm not insane," King Volin hissed. His head snapped up and his eyes whirled madly. He sure looked insane, and he was even more insane not to see it. "I'm brilliant!" The king waved his hands in the air in a series of wild gestures. "I'm the king! In fact, I'm the youngest king there's ever been on the throne! I killed my own father for this position. I wanted to become king, and king I became."
      "Becoming a vampire isn't just a decision you can make," I said quietly. "This curse isn't meant to be shared."
      "Curse?" The king scoffed. "This isn't a curse. Who wouldn't want to live forever? Who wouldn't want strength and power beyond their wildest imagination?"
      I narrowed my eyes. "You don't deserve this kind of power."
      I flinched as King Volin drew his dagger. The wicked blade was still stained with blood-whose blood it was, was another question entirely. "I'm the king. If I tell you to do something, you will obey my orders." His smile was back, and the crazed look in his eyes returned along with it. "Karmen was supposed to turn me. But now that a certain someone killed her, I can't become a vampire that way now, can I? I don't just want to be any vampire, you see, I need the blood of the strongest one to truly become superior. And now with you being the one to best Queen Karmen, you will be the one to turn me into a vampire."
      "I don't think I will."
      "That's not your choice to make." King Volin pressed his dagger against my neck and a moment later, the smell of my own blood shoved its way up my nose. I thrashed as the king pressed his mouth against my wounded neck and dug his teeth into my skin. "I'm going to be the first king to live forever!" King Volin laughed as he drew back. My blood dribbled from his mouth. "I'm going to-" But whatever he was about to say got cut off abruptly as he collapsed to the ground, clawing at his skin as if it were on fire. "What have you done to me?"
      I stared down at the king, shaken. "Were you really so eager to become a vampire that you forgot to research how actually turning into one worked?"
      "What do you mean?" The king hissed as he continued to thrash. Panic crossed his face, and his dagger had clattered to the ground. Out of the corner of my gaze, I saw Chloe-Jane crawling toward it.
      "To become a vampire," I said quietly, "your human body has to die. You're dying, Your Majesty."
      King Volin opened his mouth to respond, but he suddenly stilled, and his eyes rolled up into the back of his head as he passed out.
      "Is he dead?" Chloe-Jane whispered. She was inches away from the dagger as she stared at the king's limp body.
      "No," I answered. "But if his will to fight through the pain and continue to live isn't strong enough, he will be."
      Chloe-Jane gingerly reached out and snatched the keyring attached to the king's belt before staggering over to open Corinna's cell. The moment the door opened, Corinna pulled Chloe-Jane into a tight hug. Chloe-Jane just stood there like a statue. "Chloe," she said quietly when she finally drew away.
      Chloe-Jane silently passed over the key ring.
      Corinna hurried over to me and knelt down to pick up the king's dagger. "How long is he going to be passed out like this?" she asked quietly as she fumbled with the lock and keys. Her voice was hoarse from lack of water, and the gash in her cheek was beginning to change colors.
      I closed my eyes for a brief moment. My own skin was still crawling from the way the king had dug his teeth into my neck. "It's hard to say. It could be weeks or months."
      My eyes flew open as Corinna wrapped her arms around me, hugging me tightly. Despite my current state, I smiled softly and pressed my forehead against hers.
      "Are you okay?" Corinna whispered.
      I shook my head even as the crawling sensation mercifully subsided at Corinna's touch. "I have very little blood left. My immortal strength is almost completely gone as well."
      Finally, Corinna got the last lock click open, and I nearly collapsed to the floor as the chains clattered around me. My knees hit the hard stones. I hadn't felt this weak in a very long time. Corinna took my hands in her own as she slowly but steadily helped me to my feet.
      From somewhere off to the side of the room, I heard Chloe-Jane suck in a sharp breath.
      "Is everything alright?" Corinna turned to Chloe-Jane in concern only to find her sister staring at the two of us in disbelief.
      "Corinna"-Chloe-Jane took a step backward-"why are you helping that vampire? Humans and vampires are not supposed to work together-they can't work together! Vampires are evil, Corinna. It's a sin to associate yourself with evil."
      "How could anyone be more wicked than King Volin?" Corinna glanced down at where the king was lying in a heap on the stones. After tearing her gaze away from him, Corinna slung one of my arms over her shoulder to help me find my balance. "Talon isn't evil, Chloe."
      "Sinners will go to a very bad place," Chloe-Jane continued as if she hadn't heard her sister. "And I don't want you to go there, Corinna."
      "What should we do about the king?" I asked quietly, changing the topic.
      Corinna frowned. "Should we really just leave him here? If he dies, he won't be a problem anymore, but if he actually completes his transformation, we'll be in big trouble."
      I followed Corinna's gaze to the king's body. "The best thing to do would be to take him with us. That way we can monitor his transformation and then do some questioning of our own when he wakes up. If we can expose him and his plot, we might be able to get his subjects to turn against him."
      "But can we really drag him along with us?" Corinna bit her lip. "Right now you seem even weaker than me."
      I knelt down and cautiously turned over the king's arm. I placed a finger on his wrist to check his pulse. His heart was still beating, but the pulse was getting weaker and weaker by the second. "I think I have enough strength to carry him. I just need a moment to adjust to my new state."
      "We have to find Lynden"-Corinna turned to Chloe-Jane-"do you know where the other vampire that was with us is?" Chloe-Jane hesitated. "Please, Chloe. We're all leaving here together. We're going to get you out of here."
      Chloe-Jane turned to the doorway, conflicted. She clearly didn't want Corinna to leave with me, but her eagerness to get out of the dungeons seemed to take over. "This way."
      I grabbed King Volin by one arm and Corinna quickly grabbed his other. I didn't even want to think about how we planned to get past the guards with the dying king.
      The long hallway outside was lined with doors, and the scent of pain and despair hit me full in the face as we made our way past door after door. Judging by how all of the doors were solid blocks of metal, the cells inside were probably pitch black. I felt my skin crawl. Some of the prisoners here probably hadn't seen the sun-or even light-in years.
      What struck me as strange was how there were no guards at all here in the dungeons. Besides the prisoners locked behind the doors, I couldn't sense anyone else around.
      When we finally came to a stop, Chloe-Jane had arrived in front of a door that looked quite different from the rest. "He's in here," she whispered.
      I exchanged a glance with Corinna before dropping King Volin next to the door. I extended my hand and Corinna handed me the king's dagger. With a flash of metal, I sliced through the lock and quickly pushed the door open.
      I heard Corinna suck in a breath from next to me. A single torch flickered above the door, illuminating the space in a fiery orange light. The entire stone room was covered in soot and burn marks, and the sickening scent of burning flesh hung in the air.
      Lynden was lying on the floor in a pool of drying blood. His long brown hair was burnt, and his skin was practically flaking off. He slowly looked up as we entered the room, his eyes glazed with pain. I winced. Even though vampires can't feel physical pain, direct exposure to fire causes the curse inside us to crawl and scream in an attempt to get away from it. It claws at the very fabric of our being-our soul, blood, and bones-a sort of burning from the inside out.
      "What happened to you?" Corinna asked in horror as I quickly hurried over to slice Lynden's chains from the wall. Chloe-Jane scampered inside as well, not wanting to be left alone in the hall with the king's body.
      "Fire," Lynden said. His voice was as raw as his skin. Even his face was burnt. "The king used fire. And light. How did the two of you manage to escape?"
      "The king used my blood to turn himself into a vampire," I said grimly.
      Lynden's eyes widened. "He did what?"
      "He didn't seem to know about the transitioning period, though," I said quickly. "Once he passed out, we took the opportunity to get out."
      Lynden shakily got to his feet, and ash fell from his blood-stained clothes. "Where is the king right now?"
      "Outside," Corinna said quietly. "We're taking him with us. If he does survive, we can interrogate him later."
      "How are we going to get out?" Lynden pressed a hand against the wall to steady himself. "We might be able to get past the regular guards, but there's no way we'll be able to fight off those other vampires in our current state."
      I handed the dagger back to Corinna as I motioned for us to leave the room. "I don't know yet, but we can't stay here." Suddenly, I froze-aside from the unconscious king, I could sense two other people outside. One human and one vampire. Were the guards here already?
      A knight appeared in the doorway. His helmet reflected the torch light, and a sword gleamed at his side. But just as Corinna raised her blade, the knight pulled off his helmet, and my jaw nearly dropped.
      "I found you!" Storm exclaimed triumphantly. "Phina, look! I found them!"

Chapter Twenty-Three
       
"What are you all doing here?" I said weakly as I lowered my blade. "How did you get here?"
      "We snuck in," Phina said proudly as she appeared in the doorway next to Storm. She pulled off her helmet to let her hair tumble down her back.
      "But what about the vampires?" Talon asked, wide-eyed.
      "Vampires?" Storm furrowed his brow. "They're dead."
      "Dead?" Lynden choked.
      Storm nodded with a shudder as if remembering something unpleasant. "It was strange-they were just lying in the passageways of the castle without their heads. That's not important, though." Storm's eyes widened in horror as they went from the gash on my face to Talon's blood-soaked clothes and finally to Lynden's burnt state. "What in the name of hell happened to all of you?"
      "Lynden!" Phina clapped her hands to her mouth. "Who did this to you?"
      "It was the king," Lynden said grimly as Phina and Storm hurried over to him, completely horrified. "He claimed he wanted information, but I think he just wanted to see how quickly I'd burn."
      Chloe-Jane inhaled sharply from where she was standing by the door. "Are you vampires too?"
      Phina turned to my sister and tried her best to offer a friendly smile. "You must be Chloe-Jane."
      Chloe-Jane just took a step backward. Her eyes traveled rapidly back and forth between the vampires and me.
      Storm finally tore his eyes away from Lynden to look at Chloe-Jane as well. "I'm not a vampire. But I can tell you on their behalf that none of them are going to harm you in any way. We promise."
      Chloe-Jane stared at Storm. "You're a sinner too." Then she extended her hand and pointed wildly at all of us. "All of you are sinners!"
      "Chloe," I tried in a rising panic, "calm down."
      "No," Chloe-Jane said shrilly as she took another step back. "I won't calm down!"
      "Will you please listen?" I pleaded. "We're trying to get you out of here. Just trust us. Trust me."
      Chloe-Jane drew in a deep breath before finally nodding her head. It seemed that despite her fear of the vampires, her dread of staying in the castle outweighed it.
      "We only have two other knight outfits," Storm informed us. "They were a little more difficult to get our hands on than we expected."
      I exchanged a glance with Talon.
      "I think one of them should be given to King Volin," Talon said as she gestured to the door and to where the king's body lay beyond.
      "The king?" Storm said sharply. "But isn't he dead?"
      I blinked. "Dead?"
      "Yeah." Storm frowned in confusion. "Phina and I saw his body outside when we came down here, and when I checked his pulse . . . Well, he's dead, isn't he?"
      Talon shook her head. "Not quite. He's in the process of turning into a vampire."
      "A vampire?" Storm echoed in disbelief.
      "We're taking him back with us," Talon explained. "If he really does complete the transformation, we'll be in trouble if we leave him here in the castle."
      Storm's expression turned serious. "If that's the case, it makes sense to cover his face."
      "Chloe-Jane or Corinna should probably wear the other one," Phina said as she wrung her hands together. "It isn't going to be easy running in a dress."
      I glanced over at my sister. "Chloe can wear it. We wouldn't want people to see her face either-she's the queen after all."
      Talon turned to Phina and Storm. "Do the two of you have an escape plan?"
      The two of them looked at each other before Phina grinned guiltily. "We just snuck in. We haven't really thought about how to get out."
      "Great," Lynden said weakly. "We're too far down to jump from the balconies, and given our current state, I don't know if that's even an option."
      "And how exactly did you get in here?" Talon asked, with a glance in Phina's direction. 
      "We jumped through a window," Phina answered proudly. "Either their anti-vampire defenses are a joke, or Storm acted as a shield against whatever traps there were. Getting out of the dungeons themselves shouldn't be too difficult," she added quickly. "The few guards we passed on the way have already been taken care of."
      Storm ran a hand through his dark hair. "Phina can't carry all of us out of here. We'll either have to make a break for it through the front doors, or we try to get out from the servants' entrance."
      I shook my head. "We can't go out that way. If we run through there, we'll end up putting the servants in danger."
      Storm sighed heavily. "That's what I was afraid of. And in that case, it looks like our only way out is through the front doors. Any of the other exits will result in us getting cornered the moment we get outside."
      "I can draw the guards away," Phina offered. "Once they're after me, the rest of you can make a run for it. Since I'm still at my full strength, I'll be able to jump to safety. Oh, and I can take the king with me."
      "We should go now," Storm said as he turned on his heel. "Even though we managed to sneak in without alerting the guards, it won't take them long to come running when they find the ones we knocked out."
      We made our way out of the dungeons and followed Storm and Phina up staircase after stone staircase. As we climbed, I found myself wondering just how deep underground we were. Of course the king didn't need guards down here; the dungeons were a maze, with different staircases around each corner that seemed to branch off in every direction possible. If it wasn't for Storm and Phina leading the way, we would have gotten lost.
      "I marked the walls," Storm whispered. His armor flickered from the light of the torch he held to illuminate the way. "You're lucky Phina was here to follow your scents." After a long while, we finally reached a door at the end of the stairs, and Storm pushed it open.
      "Right now we're two stories below the front entrance," Phina told us quietly. "This way."
      We followed Phina through the doorway and down the long hallway beyond. At first glance, the hall seemed to be free of guards-until my eyes landed on three of them lying in an unconscious heap on the floor.
      We hurried up a flight of stairs and found ourselves in another hallway. Phina raised a hand to stop us before silently gesturing to the knights standing on the other side of the hall with their backs to us. "I'll go lead the guards away from the entrance," Phina whispered. "Once you get outside, run." Phina took off down the hall a moment later, holding the king tightly under an arm.
      "Hey!" one of the knights yelled as Phina danced past them. "You don't belong in the castle!"
      "Chase her!" another shouted as they all scrambled after the ginger-haired vampire. They disappeared from sight in seconds.
      "Let's go," Storm said quietly. He held his sword at the ready as he led the way, and we followed him up a flight of stairs to find ourselves standing in the entrance hall. My eyes widened as I looked around. The large room didn't have any windows; the stairs were covered in rich carpet, and the walls were adorned with tapestries bearing the royal crest.
      "There's gonna be knights outside," Storm said grimly. "We'll have to fight our way through the gardens."
      I gripped the dagger in my hands tighter. Adrenaline and fear raced through my veins. All five of us broke into a run as we sprinted toward the doors.
      The moment Storm threw them open, the bright sunlight from outside stung my eyes, and I squinted against its brilliance. I heard Talon quietly hiss as the sunlight hit her full in the face, but we kept running. We had to.
      The moment we emerged in the gardens, the sound of shouting filled the air. "Halt!" a voice yelled. "I command you to stop in the name of the Royal Guard!"
      We ignored his cries and sprinted as fast as we could toward the hedge maze. By studying the castle maps, we had all learned that the maze was not only the quickest way to the gates but also our best way of losing the knights.
      I could hear the sound of armored footsteps pounding over the ground behind us; the clanking of armor and the sounds of drawn swords were just as loud. Judging from their footsteps, I could guess there were at least ten of them.
      We crashed into the maze and sprinted in single file down the narrow path. The good thing about the maze was that our pursuers would not be able to charge at us all at once; they'd have to go in single file, and it would be even more difficult for them with the bulk of their armor.
      My heart pounded away in my chest as I dashed down the dirt-covered path with one hand pressed against the tall hedge wall to keep myself from toppling over. All we needed to do was get to the gates and then sprint across the long stretch of open field back to the city itself. Once we were among the buildings, we could lose the knights for good.
      Storm was in the lead, and Chloe-Jane and I brought up the rear. But just as we flew through the exit of the maze, out of the corner of my eye, I saw Chloe-Jane stumble. She fell to the ground with a yelp, and as I spun around to help her, my momentum nearly caused me to topple over as well. "Hurry, Chloe!" I grabbed her hand in an attempt to help her to her feet.
      Just as Chloe-Jane grasped my hand, her eyes widened in horror. My head snapped up as a single knight emerged from the maze, and his sword was raised as he charged toward us.
      "Run, Corinna!" Chloe-Jane pushed me away, terrified. "Run!"
      But I would not run. Not this time.
      Raising my dagger, I met the knight's blade with my own. A split second later, I whirled and slammed the hilt of my dagger into the side of the knight's head with all the strength I could muster. The knight staggered before falling to the ground unconscious.
      I pulled a shocked Chloe-Jane to her feet. "Let's go!"
      "What was that?" she puffed as we sprinted to catch up with the others.
      "Run now," I panted back as I shook my head. "We'll talk later."
      Storm, Talon, and Lynden had already reached the gates and were fighting off the knights standing guard there. Storm's blade flashed in the bright sunlight as he crossed swords with knight after knight. As the knights continued to fall at his hand, I felt relief spread through me. While I regarded Storm as a close friend, it was also true he was the kingdom's famous legend and owned up to his name. Talon and Lynden were doing their best to fend off the charging knights, but they were growing weaker by the second as their skin peeled and flaked from the light.
      I hurried to join Storm, and my blade flew as I danced a dance of steel and blood. I hissed each time one of the knights' swords nicked my skin. I was moving too slowly; I needed to go faster, but my throat was parched from lack of water, and my strength was nearly depleted from lack of food. And yet I needed to keep going.
      I knocked the last knight to the ground and stood there for a moment, swaying on my feet as I stared down at all of the armor-clad figures lying around me.
      Storm slashed through the lock to the side door with his sword. "I've got the gate open-run and don't look back!"
      We sprinted out of the gardens and onto the seemingly infinite stretch of field beyond. I kicked off my shoes to keep from sliding over the grass, and my legs screamed in protest as I ran.
      "Do you think we're going to make it?" I asked. My breath was like a shard of glass in my throat as the wind ripped my voice away.
      "I think we have a very good chance," Talon called back as she ran beside me. "That is unless they-"
      Suddenly, an ear-splitting boom cut through the air, and the ground shook.
      "Unless they have cannons," Talon finished regretfully.
      We all staggered as the ground shook again. Then Chloe-Jane screamed as the field to the left side of us exploded. Grass and dirt flew in every direction.
      "They've got cannons!" Storm yelled as he tossed his sword to the ground in a panic.
      There was another boom as the ground on our right side exploded, closer this time.
      My ears were ringing and my head throbbed as I threw my arms up to shield my face from the flying dirt. I kept running, and my feet continued to bark with pain as the skin on my arms and face were torn open by little rocks. My lungs strained. We were still so far from the safety of the city.
      There was another boom. This time I watched in horror as Talon lost her footing and tumbled to the ground. I pushed Chloe-Jane ahead of me and doubled back for Talon. "Talon!" I pulled Talon to her feet, and we took off again at a sprint. "Are you okay?" Nearly all of her bare skin had flaked away, and her face was raw and red.
      "I'm-" Talon started, but whatever she was about to say was cut off by another cannon blast. And before I could even blink or scream, the ground right behind us exploded, and the force sent us flying.
      My vision blurred as I slammed into the ground with a thud. My ears were ringing so much I couldn't hear. My head was spinning, and my body was screaming. There was so much pain. I tried to rise to my feet, but my vision swam, and agony shot through my right leg.
      "Corinna!" Talon was screaming my name, but her voice sounded so far away. It was as if everything was underwater.
      Talon scooped me up in her arms and leaped into the air just as the ground where I had just been lying exploded. My leg was on fire; every inch of it screamed as if a thousand shards of glass were tearing into it.
      "Corinna!" That was Chloe-Jane's voice.
      "Corinna!" Storm.
      "Corinna!" Lynden.
      My vision was swimming in and out of focus. I could barely think-could barely move as Talon carried me.
      Why did my leg hurt so much? I raised my head in an attempt to look, but Talon stopped me. "Don't look," she whispered. Her eyes were filled with panic.
      I blinked even as a new wave of agony shot through me from my leg. I had never seen Talon like this before. I began to panic as well. Am I dying? Am I going to die here?
      "Hold on, Corinna," Talon was sobbing. "We're almost there."
      Almost there? Where are the buildings? Everything was red. Then everything was tilting forward and the very world was on fire as I collided with the ground. I couldn't tell if I was screaming. It was as if someone had clapped their hands tightly over my ears. When will the pain end?
      Suddenly, I felt something sharp prick my neck. My pain instantly stopped as I lost consciousness and the world around me faded to black.
       
~
       
      When I came to, my entire body ached. My throat still felt raw as I drew in one breath after another, and my head throbbed painfully as I opened my eyes. I was lying on a bed. Curtains hung over the windows, dulling the brilliance of the sunlight outside. I recognized the room as Talon's bedroom back at the forest house. Someone had changed me into a plain nightgown, and as I reached up to touch my face, I found that the gash on my cheek had been patched up. The scratches on my hands had healed as well.
      "Corinna!" Talon's voice said. I turned to find her sitting on the floor next to me. "You're awake!" She was no longer wearing the same blood-soaked clothes from the castle dungeons, and her hair was clean of dirt and blood.
      I clapped a hand to my head to stop my vision from swimming. "How long have I been out this time?" Suddenly everything came rushing back to me. The castle dungeons. Our escape. The cannons.
      I threw my blankets off to look down at my leg-except there was no leg. I nearly stopped breathing as I stared in disbelief at where my right leg was missing below the knee joint.
      Talon's eyes were pained. "I'm so sorry, Corinna. We did everything we could, but most of it was already gone. You're very lucky Clarity prepared a batch of medicine to help with the healing process before she left, otherwise things could have been a lot worse."
      "Are we safe?" I changed the topic, still in a state of shock.
      "We're safe now. We lost the knights and made it back to the house in the forest."
      "What about the others?" I slowly pushed myself into a sitting position, and Talon helped me.
      "They're fine now too." Talon's eyes were still fearful as she held my hands in her own. "Chloe-Jane is in the second bedroom here, and Lynden, Phina, and Storm are back in the other house. Phina successfully brought the king back, and now he's locked in the wine cellar."
      "Good." I let out a breath I hadn't realized I had been holding in. "That's good. We made it out alive. That's all that matters."
      "I'm so sorry, Corinna," Talon said again as her shoulders slumped in defeat. "Your leg-"
      "This isn't your fault." I offered her a weak smile as I squeezed her hands. "If it wasn't for you, I probably would have lost more than just a leg."
      Talon shook her head, and she dropped her gaze, burying her face in her arms. "I-if I didn't have the blood, I wouldn't have had the strength to get us out of there . . . I'm sorry," Talon's voice was muffled as she apologized again. "You were in so much pain that I-that I could only render you unconscious. I didn't want you to continue hurting."
      I smiled faintly as I absently reached up to touch my neck. "I know. And I don't mind." I patted the bed next to me and Talon silently took a seat. "I'm fine, Talon. It seems like my blood saved the both of us. We're both alive still, and that's what matters. But how are you? We were outside in the sun for a long time."
      "I'm fine." Talon offered me a weak smile despite the fact her skin was still flaking.
      "Are you sure?"
      "It doesn't hurt anymore. The light itself doesn't hurt, but it's how it reacts with the curse inside us. The curse recoiling from the light is the painful part."
      "How long does it take to heal?" I asked softly.
      "Maybe about a day if I give it proper treatment."
      "How long has it been since we left the castle?"
      "A week."
      I blinked. "An entire week?"
      Talon nodded tearfully. "I was starting to worry that you wouldn't wake up. Corinna, if you died, I-I-"
      I smiled gently. "I'm awake now."
      Talon let out a broken laugh as she returned the smile. Her eyes filled with relief as she wrapped her arms around me in a hug. When she finally drew away, Talon reached up with a shaky hand to cup the side of my face as if she couldn't believe that the two of us were safe and sound.
      "Talon," I said as I held her gaze, "I love you. That was something I wanted to tell you in the dungeons but never was able to muster the courage to. After nearly dying, I realized that if I don't say it now, I might not get another chance."
      Talon eyes widened as she stilled. Despite her surprise, something hopeful flashed across her face. "You're not afraid of me?" she whispered as she dropped her hand from my face.
      I caught her hand in my own as I smiled. "Of course not."
      "But I'm a monster," Talon's voice broke. "Besides, look at me"-she gestured to the skin flaking off her face-"I'm not beautiful anymore."
      "In my eyes, you're always beautiful," I breathed. "Even right now. I don't care that you're a vampire. Or even a queen. In my eyes, you're just you."
      Talon's eyes were large as if she were fighting an inward battle.
      "I'm not afraid of you," I said softly as I reached up to place my hands on either side of her face.
      "Then you're a fool."
      "They do say that love makes a person a fool."
      Talon gave me a weak smile. "If that's the case, then let's be fools together."
      I leaned forward and gently brushed my lips over hers. Talon leaned into my touch, and her eyes fluttered shut as the two of us savored the brief sweetness.
      "I love you, Corinna," Talon whispered. She pressed her forehead against mine when we drew apart.
      I smiled as I pulled her into a warm embrace. Even though I had just lost one of my legs, everything seemed right. Talon returned the embrace, shaking slightly as she held me tightly.
      "I think it was that night at the ball when it struck me that I wanted to stay with you," Talon admitted as she rested her head on my shoulder. "It was then that I really came to terms with the fact that I didn't want us to go our separate ways after our journey came to an end. But I was afraid to tell you at the time-with you being you and me being a vampire. I was also worried that if I were to stay around you, I'd be putting you in danger if Karmen ever came to look for me."
      "If Karmen really does come to look for you"-I withdrew to hold Talon's gaze-"we can face her together. Besides, if she really is looking for the queens, she'll come here for Chloe-Jane at one point or another."
      "You're right." Talon let out a weak laugh as she reached out to tuck a flyaway curl behind one of my ears. "I'll be putting you in even more danger by leaving."
      The two of us shared a warm smile.
      "Now that I'm awake," I said after a while, "you should worry about your own wounds. What do you need to do to recover?"
      "To recover from burns, a vampire's body needs to shut down and reset," Talon recalled with a slight frown. "It's kind of like going to sleep, in a way. It usually takes about a day or two, and vampires aren't particularly fond of it since they're completely vulnerable throughout that period of time."
      "If you need to rest"-I scooted over to make room for Talon on the bed-"you should rest."
      Talon smiled as she lay down next to me. "Alright."
      I lay back down with my fingers still intertwined through hers. "We got out alive." I squeezed her hands.
      "We got out alive," she echoed as if she still couldn't fully believe it. "Phina escaped the guards without even getting a single scratch! Lynden has fully healed from his own injuries, but he's still a little shaken. All three of them-Lynden, Phina, and Storm-came to visit you while you were unconscious."
      "Did Chloe-Jane ever visit me?" I asked hesitantly.
      "Only once. I had to offer to leave the room before she came in as well. After that first visit, she locked herself in the other bedroom and still refuses to come out. She won't talk to me or Lynden or Phina. She'll talk to Storm, though, even though she makes it clear that she doesn't like him very much-he's gone in a few times to visit her."
      It was my turn to sigh. "Even as her sister, I don't know if she'll listen to anything I say. I don't know what she went through at the castle, and I don't know if she'll ever tell me." I rolled over onto my back to stare up at the ceiling. "I just want to comfort her, but I don't know how I'll be received."
      Talon looked up as well and followed my gaze to the wooden beams. "Lynden and Phina both want to talk to Chloe-Jane, but she won't let them get close enough to try and comfort her."
      "Should we send Chloe-Jane up to Andreus? She can see Mother and Clarity and Cameren there. She'll be safer there than here in the capital city. But . . ."
      "But we don't know how she'll feel about staying with a dragon."
      I nodded my head in defeat.
      I could hear the frown in Talon's voice. "I don't even know if we'll be able to send her out. Apparently the knights are looking for Chloe-Jane and the king. The story got out that the king and queen were abducted by southern continent spies. I don't think they can really link it back to us, but it's probably for the best that we keep a low profile."
      Talon was right; the last thing we wanted was to be stopped on the road. If the knights were looking for people from the southern continent, it was very likely that they would be monitoring all of the roads out of the capital city.
      Talon rested her head on my shoulder. "I don't mind staying here, though. Everything's good now. Chloe-Jane's out of the castle. Maybe we could just stay here forever."
      A wistful smile tugged on my lips. "That would be nice. But there are things we need to do. No matter how much we try to set aside and forget our responsibilities, time will catch up with us eventually. Even if we can't stay here forever, we can definitely stay here right now. You should rest, Talon. You should have healed yourself when we got back to the forest house instead of waiting for me to wake up."
      Talon let out a laugh. "I'll rest."
      "I'll be here when you wake."
      With one final smile, Talon closed her eyes.
      Even though I had slept for days, I was still completely exhausted. Last week's events could have been nothing more than a nightmare, but that wasn't the case; the faint stinging of my cheek and my missing leg told me otherwise. As much as I wanted to dismiss it, the pain had been real.
      All of this was real. Talon's hand in mine was real. This room, this house, this world. All of it. I was living. I propped myself up on my elbow and tenderly brushed Talon's hair away from her face.
      It was true that life had dealt me a great number of hardships, but between the pain and suffering and fear, there was also sweetness. Joy, hope, happiness, and love.
      Life is a journey without a clear end in sight. Sometimes things go to plan and sometimes they don't. If life is a winding river, then I am a boat drifting along the water. Even if I can't control where I end up, how I steer my boat is up to me.
      Life isn't easy. It never has been. But even in the darkest of nights, there are still stars behind the clouds, waiting to light the way.
      Sweetness and bitterness. Hope and despair. Not every second, minute, or even year will be easy. But that is life.

Chapter Twenty-Four
       
"Your Highness," Uncle Altair calls, and his armor clinks as he hurries up the spiraling staircase of the tower after me. "Slow down!"
      I laugh as I race up the steps with my feet bare and long skirts fly behind me. "Hurry! We're going to be late!"
      Uncle Altair lets out an exasperated sigh as he quickens his pace.
      When I finally reach the top of the spiraling staircase, I throw open the doors to the balcony. A strong breeze greets me and whips my unbound hair in every direction. Mother and Father turn to look up at me from where they sit next to a blanket covered in plates of food.
      "Am I late?" I ask breathlessly, tucking loose strands of inky hair behind an ear.
      "Not at all," Father says with a chuckle. "In fact, you're just on time."
      Uncle Altair emerges from the doorway, then sets his sword down as he takes a seat. "I'm sorry we're a little late-the princess insisted on picking flowers for the occasion."
      "Mother, Father, look,"-I drop to my knees as I hold up a little container of flowers-"we can put these in the middle of the blanket as a centerpiece."
      Mother smiles with bright eyes. "They're beautiful."
      I beam as I set the container down. Then I excitedly look around at the treats laid out on the blanket. "Mother, did you make all of these yourself?"
      Mother nods and reaches for a plate. "Have a taste."
      I eagerly take one of the treats and pop it into my mouth. "Delicious!"
      Father turns to Uncle Altair. "Did you tighten security for this evening?" Even though his tone is light, his eyes are serious.
      Uncle Altair inclines his head. "Everything's ready."
      "This evening?" I blink as I turn to look at the two of them. "Why are we tightening security?"
      Mother sighs. "My dear sister-in-law is coming to visit. Don't tell me you've forgotten."
      I reach for another treat. "I knew she was coming to the castle. I just didn't know it was today." Then my hand stills and my fingers hover over the little cakes. "Cousin Evsen is coming too, isn't he."
      Father pinches the bridge of his nose as if to ward off a headache. "Yes, your cousin will be here too."
      "I don't think he'll be very happy to see me." I lift my eyes to look out absently at the grassy fields far below. The vibrant greens are dotted with the occasional pinks and whites and yellows of flowers. "We did call off the engagement, after all." I fall silent as I turn my head to the sky. Clouds streak the brilliant blue canvas above, and I find myself watching them as they float lazily on the breeze.
      "Your Highness?" Uncle Altair taps me lightly on the shoulder. "Are you spacing out? Your mother just asked you a question."
      I blink as I snap back to reality. "I'm sorry! What was the question?"
      "I just asked how you feel about meeting your cousin Evsen for the first time," Mother says lightly.
      I wrinkle my nose. "I don't think I want to meet him. Apparently last year he had an affair with the marquess's daughter. Even though I couldn't care less about what he does, he was still engaged to me at the time. And that doesn't make him very honorable, now does it? Everyone talks about how greedy and possessive he is. I think I'm better off not associating with him."
      "Everyone?" Mother arches a quizzical brow, and her long inky hair flutters lightly in the breeze like fine silk. "And who did you hear all of this from?"
      "Uncle Altair." I pop another cake into my mouth.
      Uncle Altair raises his hands defensively. "The princess needs to keep up with what happens outside the castle somehow."
      "We don't mind," Father says as he shakes his head. "We're just curious how the captain of the knights knows all the gossip in the kingdom."
      My uncle's armor clanks as he crosses his arms. "It's my job, is it not?"
      Father laughs as he claps his brother on the shoulder. "It's your job to know what's going on with the neighboring kingdoms' militaries, not who's been having affairs with who."
      I lean back to look up and watch a flock of birds glide through the air. "Don't worry, Father. Isn't it important for a princess to know what's going on in her kingdom? Well, Uncle Altair and the other knights have done a very good job of informing me."
      "The other knights?" Mother asks as she rearranges her skirts around her legs. "They're in on this too?"
      I take one of Mother's hands in mine. "Please don't be too hard on them-we're just having fun."
      "Do you ever find yourself wanting friends outside the castle?" Father asks jokingly. "I know you consider Altair here to be your best friend, but my brother is about twenty years older than you."
      "I've befriended quite a lot of the knights," I say thoughtfully. "And the maids. There are quite a few of them around my age. This is my home. When I get older, I'll be able to help protect our kingdom too."
      Father places a hand on top of mine. "I know."
      I smile as I take Father's hand and place it on top of Mother's. Then I spring to my feet to look over the balcony railings. The wind rustles through my hair, and I close my eyes to savor the warmth of the sun on my face.
      When I open them, Uncle Altair is standing beside me. He rests his arms on the stone railings as he points down at the courtyard below. "Look."
      A group of young knights are sitting in the grassy courtyard, chatting happily as they eat their lunches. I wave at them, but I'm too far away to be noticed. "It was worth a shot." I rest my chin on my hands, and Uncle Altair lets out a laugh. I turn around to look at my parents and then perk up. "Look!" I say as I tug on my uncle's sleeve.
      Uncle Altair follows my gaze, and we watch as Mother and Father share a smile as they talk quietly among themselves.
      I let out a sigh. "I wonder if I'll ever look at someone the same way Mother looks at Father. I wonder if someone will ever look at me that way."
      Uncle Altair gives me a knowing wink. "Maybe someday you'll meet someone special."
      "Come on, Uncle Altair. And what about you? Have you ever been in love before?"
      "I've told you before," my uncle says as he straightens his cape, "I don't have time for romance. There's nothing I love more than being the captain of the knights. Besides, I've got my older brother, sister-in-law, and dear niece to take care of. I think my heart is full."
      I finally look away from my parents. "I'm not marrying my cousin. I don't mind ruling alone. I love this kingdom just as much as Mother and Father do. Besides, you'll be here to help guide me. Right, Uncle?"
      Uncle Altair ruffles my hair. "You really take after your father, you know. You've got your mother's spirit, though-her spirit of grace and strength and independence. I remember the first time I met your mother was when she was just a knight serving under my father. During the war between the eastern kingdoms and the expanding western empire, your mother and father saved each other countless times. We all fought hard to keep our kingdom and our neighboring ones out of the hands of the cruel western king. Your mother and father both made names for themselves on the battlefield, and with them as the rulers of our kingdom, the west doesn't dare to attack."
      I smile as I return to the picnic blanket, tugging Uncle Altair along by the sleeve. I then take a seat next to Mother. "Are you worried my aunt is going to try something?" I ask quietly. "Is that why you're increasing security?"
      Mother frowns slightly, and the long sleeves of her gown flutter as the wind whispers past. "My sister-in-law hasn't been here in years. I know her better than anyone. After all, she was the one who was the most vocal about my status and how I couldn't possibly marry into the royal family. Now she likes to tell anyone who will listen how I didn't initially want to be queen. I know that if things don't go her way, she'll take her anger out on anything in the same room as her."
      Uncle Altair cuts in. "I think we just shouldn't let our sister into the castle at all. That son of hers is no good either! I heard that when the young woman he had been having an affair with decided to cut all ties with him, he completely wrecked the marquess's flower garden out of spite. Like mother like son, eh?"
      Father lets out a sigh. "We won't know what they want if we don't let them in. They are family after all. All we can do is tighten our security and keep a watchful eye on them."
      Mother nods. "Your father is right."
      Uncle Altair and I both let out dejected sighs.
      "May I be excused?" I stand up and skillfully brush off my skirts. "I'm hoping to catch the knights in the courtyard."
      Mother looks up at me. "Of course. Just remember to get ready in a couple of hours for the meeting."
      "I will!" I turn on my heel to hurry to the door leading back down the spiraling staircase of the tower. When we finally reach the courtyard, I hurry across the stones and grass to where the young knights are still having their lunch.
      "It's the princess!" one of the knights says excitedly. "And look! Sir Altair is here too!"
      All the knights gathered in the courtyard jump to their feet before bowing in our direction.
      "There's no need for that!" I wave my hands quickly as I motion for them to rise.
      One of the younger knights looks at me expectantly. "Your Highness, are you gonna come train with us again?" He couldn't have been more than thirteen years old.
      "You really want me to train with all of you again? I was completely horrible last time, remember?"
      The young knight shakes his head. "You weren't bad at all!"
      "Yeah!" the other knights chime in agreement.
      "Sir Altair"-the young knight turns to my uncle-"could we borrow Her Royal Highness? Please?"
      "Alright." My uncle laughs. "But remember, Your Highness, you should be back in your room in an hour to get ready for the meeting with your aunt and cousin."
      I sigh. "I know."
      The young knight motions for me to follow him. "Come on, Your Highness. It's been a few days since you last visited us."
      I smile as I follow him and the other knights to their large training room. "What do you all want to teach me today?"
      "Let's do bows and arrows today," one of the knights suggests.
      "I think it's better to do swords," another cuts in. "Even we don't know how to use bows properly."
      The knights come to an agreement. "Then swords it is."
      We do the sword training routine for a while, then all of us take a seat on the floor to rest.
      "Your Highness," one of the knights says, and I look over at her. "When we were in town yesterday, guess what we heard?"
      "What did you hear?" My hair sticks to the sides of my face with sweat.
      The knight lowers her voice. "It's about the neighboring kingdom's Duchy of Winfielde."
      I frown. "What happened this time?"
      "Word got out that apparently the son of the duke forced another one of the servants to sleep with him," another knight says. His voice is just as quiet. "The girl was only eleven years old."
      "The girl became pregnant," yet another knight continues sorrowfully. "And not only did she end up having a miscarriage, but she also died shortly after."
      I shake my head sadly. Even in our kingdom, the duke's children have a bad reputation. We all fall silent and bow our heads.
      Soon I say goodbye to the knights and run back through the halls, across the courtyard, then finally up the stairs. My bare feet tap across the polished stones as I come to a stop in front of the doors to my room. I pull them open and step inside.
      After my bath, I change into the dress Mother picked out for me, then take a seat at my vanity. I stare at my reflection for a long moment, and my deep brown eyes stare back at me from behind my wet hair. I reach for a comb. I spend a half hour pinning up my hair and another fifteen minutes decorating it with tiny crystal-like flowers. Finally it's time to meet up with my parents and uncle.
      In the entrance hall, I stand between my mother and father. I exhale through my nose. The sooner we get this over with, the better. We wait and wait and wait, but no one shows up.
      "Are they really coming today?" I ask.
      Uncle Altair is frowning. "They should have been here half an hour ago. Maybe they got delayed."
      As we continue to wait, Father rests his head on Mother's shoulder. "I know that you just wanted the two of us to be a normal couple. No royalty duties or responsibilities. I'm glad that you finally decided to accept my marriage proposal so that we could rebuild this war-torn kingdom together."
      Mother smiles faintly. "Over the years, the quality of life for our people has improved drastically. It shows that when monarchs rule with love instead of greed, the effect it has on their subjects is incredible to behold."
      We stand there in the entrance hall until the sun drops beneath the horizon and paints the sky in pink and yellow and red.
      Finally a knight appears in the doorway. He jogs over to us, bows, then clears his throat. "I just got a letter from your sister," he says. "She's canceling the visit."
      Mother and Father exchange a glance.
      Father sighs. "Did she say whether she was rescheduling for another day?"
      The knight bows his head. "The letter didn't say, Your Majesty."
      "You may be dismissed." Mother says. The knight bows one more time and leaves to return to his post.
