      My uncle stifles a tired yawn. "I'll go tell the guards to go back to their normal positions. Then we can all go to bed earlier."
      Mother and Father nod.
      "Let's go upstairs and have dinner," Mother suggests.
      I absently ran a finger over the smooth metal of the banister as we climbed the grand staircase of the entrance hall. "I don't get it-my aunt and cousin made a big announcement that they were in the city."
      But just as we reach the top of the stairs, we suddenly hear the doors being thrown open as Uncle Altair sprints back into the entrance hall. His armor clanks as he runs, and my heart rate quickens when I spot the look of panic on his face. My stomach clenches as I notice the droplets of blood spattered all over him.
      "What is it?" Father asks quickly as Uncle Altair skids to a stop at the bottom of the stairs.
      "They're inside the castle!" Uncle Altair calls.
      Mother takes a step forward. "Who's inside the castle?"
      "Even with the tightened security, they still managed to get past." Uncle Altair is shaking his head in a state of shock. "They killed the knights guarding the gates!"
      "Who?" Mother asks again; her voice is deadly calm.
      "Your nephew Evsen broke into the castle with an army of knights from our neighboring kingdom." Uncle Altair glances over his shoulder as if they would burst into the entrance hall at any second. "They're making their way to the main castle right now-they've been killing everyone they see." The neighboring kingdom? I feel all the blood drain from my face.
      Father's hand goes to the sword at his side. "We need to stop him-he's killing our people!"
      "If he's really brought an entire army with him"-Mother puts her hand on top of Father's before he can draw his blade-"we can't be hasty. Besides, if we go out and fight, who's going to protect the princess?"
      Suddenly, the sounds of screaming come from the courtyard, and my blood goes cold. I can hear blades clashing behind the entrance hall doors. The sound is growing louder and louder.
      "Oh no." Uncle Altair whirls around, and his own sword is instantly in his hand. "They're here already!"
      Mother pushes me behind her just as the doors to the hall are violently thrown open. My heart is pounding away in my chest as fear latches its claws into the fiber of my being. Armored knights charge into the room and sprint toward us with their swords raised.
      My eyes widen as I see all the fallen and bloody bodies lying in the courtyard outside. No, no, no. This can't be happening.
      "They've surrounded the entire castle!" Uncle Altair raises his voice as he meets the first knight with his sword. The sound of metal against metal reverberates through the room, and I take a step backward. My entire body is shaking.
      Father draws his sword as he joins my uncle in fighting the knights climbing up the steps. "Altair," Father says between swings of his sword, "I want you to get the young knights and try and evacuate as many people from the castle as you can!"
      "What?" Uncle Altair turns to my father as he slashes out at another attacking knight. "I can't leave the three of you here!"
      "Listen to me," Father pants as the two of them are forced to retreat another step. "The young knights are further in the castle. The enemy couldn't have gotten to them yet. If you can't help anyone else escape, the least you could do is take them and leave!"
      "But-" Uncle Altair protests.
      "This is an order from your king," Father says grimly. Then his eyes soften. "Please, Altair. Your brother is asking you to do him a favor."
      "Fine." My uncle reluctantly nods. "I'll do my best." All I can do is watch as Uncle Altair jumps from the stairs, fights his way across the entrance hall, and finally disappears outside into the courtyard beyond.
      Father grabs my hand. "We need to run."
      I let him pull me along as we sprint down the hallway. Night has fully set in by now and the sky outside is dark. I can hear the clanking of armored footsteps as the knights chase us. We are backed into a corner multiple times, and each time Mother and Father work together to fight us out. It doesn't take long for the number of knights on our tail to fall from twenty to zero.
      "If all the entrances and exits are really blocked," Mother says slowly, "we either hide inside the castle or fight our way out."
      Before we can give our options more thought, a door to our left flies open and a large group of knights flood out. However, the knight at the front isn't wearing a helmet as the others are. His inky hair is glowing in the moonlight as he sneers.
      I inhale sharply. "Cousin Evsen!"
      Evsen laughs unpleasantly. "Dear cousin, you really left me no choice." Then he turns to the knights behind him. "What are you waiting for? Kill them all!"
      Mother grabs me by the hand as we push through a door at the end of the hallway. We sprint up the spiraling steps, higher and higher.
      My heart sinks the moment we run through the doorway. This is the way to the balcony. With the knights at the bottom of the stairs, the only way we can go is up.
      Mother and Father whirl on the steps, fighting off the knights together. The two of them are a whirlwind of blades, and the knights fall to the ground one after another. Suddenly, someone grabs my arm, and I cry out in pain and fear.
      "Shut up," Cousin Evsen hisses as he makes to drag me down the stairs. "Stupid princess."
      In my panic, I grab the sword of one of the fallen knights and swing it with all of my strength at my cousin. Cousin Evsen jumps away from me. The moment he lets go of my arm, I drop the sword and run.
      Mother and Father have nearly taken out all of the knights, and they grab me by the hand. But then we hear the sound of bowstrings being drawn back, followed by the whoosh of arrows through the air.
      I barely have time to scream before Mother, Father, and I are all shot in the back.
      Pain explodes through me, but I continue to run. My vision blurs and my blood burns. I look back over my shoulder to see one lone knight running after us, bow in hand. Mother seems to notice the knight as well, and with a flick of her wrist, she throws her dagger at him. The knight collapses to the floor.
      Father pushes open the doors to the balcony, and we stagger out into the night. My hair has come undone somewhere along the way, and it is whipped up by the wind as I drop to my knees. Tears stream down the sides of my face; my hands are covered in blood. This is my blood. The arrow in my stomach hurts when I touch it, and I let out a sob. I slump to the floor. My vision goes in and out of focus as I stare up at the night sky above.
      Mother and Father collapse on either side of me, and each of them take one of my hands in their own. I notice that they have taken even more arrows than I have, and I stifle another sob, which sends a new wave of pain shooting through me.
      Mother squeezes my hand. "I bet by now, your uncle got the young knights out of the castle."
      "I bet Altair and the young knights are far away now," Father says quietly. "I bet they're safe."
      I want to ask, How did this happen? But all I can manage is a choked sob.
      "I'm sorry things had to end this way," Father's voice is strained. "I'm sorry we couldn't have spent more time together. All of us." My heart nearly stops as Father's hand goes limp in my own. I turn to look at him in horror, but I feel Mother place a trembling hand on my shoulder.
      "Mother." Ignoring my pain, I clutch her hand tightly. "I'm scared."
      "Can you see the stars?" she asks. Her voice is strained with tears.
      "I can see the stars," I whisper as a light wind kisses my face.
      Mother draws in a shaky breath. "Don't be afraid. Just look up at the sky. That's all you need to do. Don't look at your father. He's just gone to sleep."
      "I'm scared," I repeat as my tears continue to flow.
      "Look at the stars, Edeline." Mother's voice is fading now. "We love you. Remember that."
      "I love you too." I let out a sob as Mother's hand goes still as well.
      Lying here under the stars with the scent of blood in my nose, the taste of salty tears in my mouth, and the arrow in my back, I feel completely helpless.
      After slowly sitting up, I roll out from between the bodies of my parents. I hiss as the arrow in my stomach shifts, but I grit my teeth and bear the pain.
      I carefully place Mother's hand on top of Father's, gently interlace their fingers together, then collapse back onto the cold stones of the balcony. As I roll over to look up at the stars, I can feel my life force slowly ebb away. I am going to join my parents soon.
      I close my eyes, waiting for the darkness to take me away, waiting for the pain to end.
      I'm not sure how much time passes before my ears pick up the sound of movement. A cloak slithers across the floor.
      I crack open one eye and then the other.
      A pair of glowing red eyes greet me.
      "Hello there," a female voice says from the shadowy depths of the cloak.
      "Hello," I whisper. My own voice is broken.
      "I can give you the strength you need to take your revenge," the voice says softly. "I can give you the power you desire."
      As I fade in and out of consciousness, the cold stones of the castle melt away. And as I leave my dream, I can still hear the voice. There is something familiar about that voice, but I just can't put my finger on it.
       
~
       
      I was wide awake now. I was lying in the dark, and all of my pain had vanished-vanished as if it never even existed in the first place. Look at the stars, Edeline, my Mother's voice echoed in my head. We love you. Remember that.

Chapter Twenty-Five
       
Talon's eyes fluttered open.
      I had been sitting next to her, and I blinked in surprise as she sat upright. She took my hands in her own.
      "My name is Edeline," Talon said breathlessly. "I remember now."
      I met Talon's gaze as I held her hands tightly. "Edeline. Princess Edeline. No-that's Queen Edeline, am I right?"
      "I'm just Edeline." She shook her head as a faint smile tugged on her lips. "Not Princess Edeline or Queen Edeline." Then she paused. "How long have I been out?"
      "About a day and a half," I informed her. "Storm came by earlier to check on Chloe-Jane and dropped a new leg off."
      "A new leg?"
      "It's wooden, of course. Look-" I hopped off the bed to pick up the wooden leg, carefully attached it to my own stump of a leg, and triumphantly stood on two feet. "It's not as great as my real leg was, but it will do."
      Edeline let out a weak laugh. I smiled as I took her by the hand and helped her to her feet, then guided her over to the vanity and gently sat her down on the stool.
      I placed my hands on Edeline's shoulders and looked at her reflection in the glass. "It's amazing-all of your burns are gone just like that."
      Edeline nodded, wide-eyed as she held up a shaky hand to touch the smooth skin of her face. Then she turned to me as she stood back up. "Now that we're both awake, we should head over to Andreus's city house. I think Lynden and Phina will be very happy to see that you're doing okay."
      I took a shaky step back and nearly lost my balance on my new leg. Edeline was there to prevent me from completely toppling over, and her eyes were warm as she helped me recenter myself. "I'll go check on Chloe-Jane." My own smile faltered slightly. "You might want to change before we head out."
      "I'll meet you in the living room."
      I slipped out of the room and quietly closed the door behind me. After taking a deep breath, I gently knocked on the door to the second bedroom.
      "Who is it?" Chloe-Jane's high voice called from the other side of the wood.
      "Corinna," I answered. "May I come in?"
      There was a soft click. "The door's unlocked."
      I pushed open the door. Chloe-Jane sat on the bed with her shoulders back and head held high. In the months that I hadn't seen her, something about Chloe-Jane had changed. She no longer had a constant smile on her face, and her posture had become rigid.
      "Chloe-Jane," I said softly. I closed the door behind me before leaning against it. "How are you feeling?"
      "I'm fine," Chloe-Jane said stiffly.
      I took a step forward to embrace her, but Chloe-Jane took a step back. I let my arms fall back to my side.
      "How's your leg?" Chloe-Jane asked; her eyes went straight to my wooden replacement.
      I offered a small smile. "It's not painful anymore. It will just take some time to get used to."
      My sister turned to stare absently out the window. "I came into your room this morning to check on you."
      "You did?"
      "You and that vampire were both asleep," she said. "The two of you were holding hands. Why were the two of you holding hands?"
      "Who said we couldn't hold hands?"
      "Who is she to you, Corinna?" Chloe-Jane turned back to me. Even though her voice was quiet, it was anything but weak.
      "She's my best friend." I didn't need to think twice about my answer. "She's the person I want to spend the rest of my life with."
      Chloe-Jane shook her head. "You can't."
      "I can't?"
      "She's a vampire, Corinna. A vampire. And not only that"-she stood up-"she's also a girl. Just like you."
      "Chloe, what's so-"
      "It's wrong." Chloe-Jane shook her head again. "Even though I've stopped believing in the Immortal One, I still believe in what He stands for."
      I blinked. "Since when did you stop believing in the Immortal One?"
      "I stopped believing in Him while I was still in the castle." Chloe-Jane turned away from me. "I've always been very faithful to the Immortal One. I trusted that He would always protect me. But when I arrived at the castle, no matter how much I prayed, I still suffered. It felt like I was trapped in there for years, Corinna."
      "I'm so sorry, Chloe-"
      "It was only a matter of time before the king would tear me apart just like the people he had locked up in the dungeons." She kept staring out the window, leaving me to watch the back of her head. "I gave up hope a while ago. I've seen just how unstable this kingdom is. I've seen the corruption. I know all about the conditions of the towns and villages in the outer kingdom. It's horrible, Corinna. It's horrible. And the king himself . . . I had long given up on the hope that anyone would save me. But then you appeared at the ball." She slowly turned around to meet my gaze. "The Immortal One would have never sent vampires."
      I shook my head. No matter how much I argued, Chloe-Jane wouldn't listen. And when her mind was set on something like this, I doubted there was anything I could do to make her change it. Why was I arguing with my sister? We had just gotten her out of the castle. She was safe now. We shouldn't be arguing. "Edeline and I are going to visit Lynden, Phina, and Storm. I assume you wouldn't want to come along and see more vampires."
      Chloe-Jane stared out the window as if she hadn't heard me. "Do you know why it was so easy for us to get out of the castle? We should have died going up against the knights, but all the high ranked knights that usually stand guard were sent to watch the representatives from the southern continent."
      I fell silent. We had gotten lucky, but what mattered was that we got out. "Do you want to go to the city house with Edeline and me?"
      "I'm not going anywhere."
      I sighed. "I'll see you later. If you need anything, I'll be back soon."
      I silently exited the room and found Edeline standing by the door. She had changed into a simple dress and wore the necklace I had made for her, which glittered on her collarbones, partially hidden behind wisps of her long hair. "Ready to go?" She skillfully fastened a cloak around her shoulders before helping me stagger awkwardly across the room. "Avoiding the guards patrolling the town shouldn't be all that difficult. Storm, Lynden, and Phina have been doing it all week after all."
      I nodded as my wooden leg clunked on the floorboards. Edeline pushed open the front door and helped me out onto the porch beyond. I clung to her arm tightly. Even my normal leg felt shakier than usual. But maybe that was because I hadn't used it in an entire week.
      Just as we made our way down the steps and onto the grass beyond, there was a rustling among the trees. I looked up just in time to watch Storm hurry toward us.
      "What is it?" I inquired worriedly as he skidded to a stop.
      "The king finally woke up," Storm wheezed, with his hands on his knees. "He's a vampire alright, but we've got a situation."
      "What kind of situation?" Edeline asked sharply.
      "The king doesn't remember anything," Storm said, still clearly in a state of disbelief. "He doesn't know who he is or even what he's done."
      Edeline frowned. "It's not completely uncommon for people to lose their memories during their transition. It looks like King Volin's resolve wasn't strong enough. It was enough to keep him alive, but not enough to keep his memories intact. His loss of memory is his own fault."
      "Corinna"-Storm looked up at me as if he had just remembered something-"does the leg work?"
      I nodded. "The leg works. It will just take me a little while to get used to. That's all."
      "Perfect. Let's go, then."
      I exchanged a glance with Edeline before the two of us quickly followed him back into the trees.
      "I'm glad to see that you've healed," Storm told Edeline as we walked briskly through the forest. "Lynden was able to heal the day we returned from the castle. We were starting to worry about you, Talon."
      Edeline smiled faintly. "It's Edeline. I've finally remembered my real name."
      "Edeline." Storm looked at us over his shoulder. "I like that. Talon was cool, but I think Edeline suits you better."
      Edeline laughed. "I think so too."
      Storm furrowed his brow. "You seem different than usual." Then he turned to me. "Doesn't she seem different?"
      "I think I've finally come to terms with myself." Edeline's eyes were bright. "I've come to terms with the fact that I want to live."
      "Good." Storm's smile was genuine. "My uncle always told me that it's never too late to start living again."
      "I hope I get the chance to see Andreus again," Edeline said wistfully. "I admire him, really. As a survivor of the mass extermination of the ancient magics, his own life has undoubtedly been filled with hardships. But look at him now. He's living again. And not only is he living, but he's also living for his nephew."
      Storm grinned proudly. "My uncle is amazing. Once all of this stuff about us kidnapping Chloe-Jane and King Volin blows over, let's all go back to visit him."
      Fortunately for us, Storm already knew all the streets to take to avoid the patrolling knights, and when we arrived at the house, the three of us climbed over the fence to the backyard and hurried to the door. Lynden and Phina were standing next to the trap door to the wine cellar when we walked into the living room, and the two of them turned around to face us.
      "Corinna!" Phina's face lit up as she excitedly rocked back and forth on the balls of her feet. "You're awake! How are you? Does your leg still hurt?"
      I smiled. "I'm okay now."
      "That's good to hear," Lynden said as the two of them made their way toward us.
      "I see that you've healed," I observed. All of the burn marks that had covered Lynden's body had vanished. "Are you alright?"
      "For the most part." Then his expression turned serious. "I assume Storm told you about what happened to the king."
      Edeline inclined her head from where she stood next to me. "So he doesn't remember anything? Nothing at all?"
      Lynden frowned in the direction of the trap door. "It's quite pitiful, really. He doesn't even know his own name."
      "Lynden and I were talking to him earlier," Phina said as she wrung her hands together. "We asked him about the vampires in the castle, and he didn't know what we were even talking about! He didn't seem to be lying either."
      I clapped a hand to my face in exasperation. "We risked sneaking him out of the castle for this?"
      "Do you want to go take a look?" Phina asked. "We've got him chained up and everything."
      I exchanged a glance with Edeline.
      Edeline stepped forward. "I'll go talk to him. I'm not sure if there's a way to trigger his memories."
      A frown tugged at Phina's lips. "He'll either slowly regain his memories over time, or he'll just stay like this forever."
      Edeline made her way over to the trapdoor, carefully pulled it open, and climbed down the ladder into the wine cellar below. Phina jumped in after her, and I followed. The room was dark, and it took a moment for my eyes to adjust to the light.
      When my eyes finally adjusted, I saw King Volin chained in the corner of the room by his wrists and ankles. His golden hair was in tangles, and he looked up at us with glowing red eyes.
      "Hello," the king said mildly. "Is it time to feed the horses?"
      Phina folded her arms over her chest in annoyance. "We don't have horses here."
      Edeline took a step forward. "Do you remember me?"
      King Volin frowned faintly as he looked up at Edeline. "I'm sorry . . . I don't think we've met before." Then his eyes widened. "Wait! You're Princess Edeline!"
      Edeline angled her head to the side. "And what makes you think that?"
      "I've seen your portrait in a book I read before!" the king said triumphantly. "You are her!"
      "So he does remember something!" Phina exclaimed with equal triumph. Then she turned to face Edeline. "Talon, you're a princess?"
      Edeline refused to draw her eyes from the king; she watched his face as if it would give something away at any moment. "I'll explain later."
      "Wait," King Volin said again as he furrowed his brow in thought, "that's not right. You can't be Princess Edeline."
      Edeline arched a brow. "Why not?"
      The king frowned. "You're a vampire. And the princess died alongside her family." Then it seemed to finally dawn on him. "That's not right either! The princess didn't die that day! She became a vampire!"
      "Are you familiar with the king of this kingdom?" Edeline directed the conversation away from herself.
      "The king of this kingdom?" King Volin said slowly. He shook his head. "No, I don't know him. Why are you asking me this? She asked me that too." The king gestured at Phina.
      "That's because you are the king," Phina said in exasperation.
      The king laughed good-naturedly. "You must be crazy. I can't be the king."
      Phina turned to Edeline and me. He's crazy, she mouthed.
      "Let's try this again," I said, and everyone turned to look at me. "The king of this kingdom wanted to become a vampire. He wanted to live forever but never truly understood the vampires' curse."
      King Volin was clearly bewildered. "I still don't know of this king." All the insanity we saw in his eyes at the castle was completely gone, and it was replaced by a look of confusion. "Whoever he is, though, he doesn't seem like a very nice guy. Why do you all keep confusing me for this king of yours?"
      "You are the king," Phina said. "How many times do we need to tell you before you believe us?"
      "But I'm not the king. How could I be a king? I don't live in a castle. I live here, don't I?"
      "We live here." Phina gestured to herself, Edeline, and me. "You're our priso-uh, guest."
      "Am I a vampire?" the king asked absently. "I don't think I'm alive."
      "You are a vampire." Edeline stared coldly down at the king. "Does the name 'Chloe-Jane' ring any bells?"
      "Chloe-Jane," King Volin echoed. "I'm sorry, I don't think I know anyone with that name."
      Edeline turned to climb back up the ladder. "I think we're done here."
      "Hey!" the king called after us as we all climbed back into the living room. "May I ask why I'm in chains?"
      "We're worried you're going to escape otherwise," Phina called back in annoyance.
      "Escape? Why would I escape? I think it's great here."
      When we emerged from the cellar, Storm was shaking his head. "Can you believe him?"
      "On a different note," Phina said brightly as she turned to Edeline, "Talon's a princess! Princess Edeline!"
      "You're Princess Edeline?" Lynden turned to Edeline as well, and the surprise was clear on his face. "But wouldn't that make you Queen Edeline?"
      "You're a queen?" Storm looked as if he had been struck by lightning. "I've been so disrespectful this entire time! Am I supposed to call you Your Majesty?"
      Edeline smiled wryly. "There's no need for any of that. I'm not royalty anymore-I'm Edeline. Just Edeline."
      "So then there are three queens in the capital city," Lynden said slowly. "You, Chloe-Jane, and Karmen."
      Edeline suddenly frowned. "Speaking of Karmen, how did she get into the castle? According to Phina and Storm, the other vampires inside the castle had been killed by the time they got there. Karmen's the only one who could have taken them all down that easily. And if Karmen really was inside the castle at the same time as us, wouldn't we have run into her?"
      "Maybe we got really lucky?" Storm suggested.
      Phina let out a sigh. "As much as I want to agree. I don't think that's it. Karmen hasn't been trying to hide the fact that she's killing vampires. So why hasn't she gotten to us yet?"
      "It has to be because Edeline is one of the queens," I said. "But then why was she in the castle? Did she just want to kill the vampires?"
      Edeline sat at the dining room table and rested her chin on the palm of her hand. "We don't exactly know what Karmen is trying to do. But it doesn't seem like she wants to kill the other queens and stop the prophecy from occurring. We've been in the capital city for a while now. Karmen could have easily killed us at any time she wanted. She visited my forest next to the farms months ago and could have killed me then as well."
      "Did we ever figure out why Karmen has been killing vampires?" I asked as I walked over to take a seat next to Edeline.
      Lynden, Storm, and Phina joined us around the table. "I don't think we ever did," Lynden said. "Originally Phina and I wanted to confront her. We wanted to stop her from turning more people into vampires and spreading the curse. But now that I'm thinking about it, Karmen was never creating numerous vampires in the first place."
      Phina shook her head. "Karmen is an interesting character. I don't fully understand her myself."
      Edeline looked up to meet everyone's gaze one by one. "What I do know is that I'm not going to go look for her anymore. I'm just worried she'll come for the three of us eventually."
      "Does that mean the two of you are in danger as well?" Storm looked worriedly at Lynden and Phina. "We should head back to my uncle's place as soon as possible. Karmen shouldn't know that that place exists. But if she does find us, my uncle can protect us from her."
      Lynden shook his head tiredly. "We're stuck here for now. We can't leave the city without alerting the knights stationed around all the roads that lead out. The last thing we want is for the knights to find Andreus."
      "Then what do we do?" Storm asked as he ran an agitated hand through his dark hair.
      "Don't worry." Phina reached over to place a comforting hand on Storm's shoulder. "We should be fine here. We've been in the capital city for almost five months now. Maybe we'll get lucky and Karmen won't show up at all." But even though she was smiling, her eyes were worried.
      During our time in the capital city, Karmen had always been a looming threat-not a threat to me, my family, or even Storm, but rather a threat to Lynden, Phina, and Edeline. I looked back and forth between the three of them. In the months that we had known each other, I felt as if I had grown close enough to the vampires to consider them my family-Storm, too, and even Andreus, for the lengths he went to help and support us. The thought of losing any of them . . .
      I had lost my father early on, and that loss crushed me. I had been fortunate enough to get Chloe-Jane back, but if I lost another person, I wasn't sure if I'd be able to remain strong.
      "It's getting dark outside." The sound of Edeline's voice drew me back to reality. "We should head back to the forest house. Chloe-Jane is still there by herself."
      "How is Chloe-Jane?" Lynden asked suddenly. "Is she doing alright?"
      Storm crossed his arms in irritation. "The last time I visited her she was still spouting the same nonsense about how vampires are evil and that she didn't want anything to do with a sinner like me. I just wanted to try and help her take her mind off what happened in the castle with a game of cards, but she slammed the door in my face."
      "She still refuses to talk to me as well," Phina added sadly.
      I sighed. "She's gone through a lot. I think all we can do is give her time to recover. She might not like any of us, but at least we can treat her better than those at the castle."
      Everyone agreed to that.
       
~
       
      By the time we returned to the forest house, the moon was shining brightly in the night sky above. The stars glittered lazily as they drifted among the sea of inky night, and I took a deep breath of the crisp air. The sweet aroma of flowers found its way to me almost immediately.
      As we walked across the living room, Edeline looked at Chloe-Jane's door. "She's asleep," she whispered. She opened the door to the other bedroom and helped me inside. I took a seat on the bed, unfastened my wooden leg, and carefully placed it under the bed before leaning back against the wall. The light spilling in from the window painted everything in silver.
      "Are you tired?" Edeline asked.
      I shook my head. "I'll stay awake with you."
      I watched Edeline walk over to light the tiny lamp on the dresser. A warm gold glow burst to life amid the cool silver, giving Edeline's silk-like hair a fiery sheen. She sat next to me on the bed a moment later and rested her head on my shoulder. "Would you like to hear about what happened leading up to Karmen turning me into a vampire?"
      I smiled softly. "If you're ready to tell me, I'm here to listen."
      "Thank you." Edeline's voice was a whisper. "Then I'll start at the very beginning."
       
~
       
      The next day, I strapped my wooden leg back on. It was sunset, and we were going to visit Lynden, Phina, and Storm at the city house. And this time, we were bringing the reluctant Chloe-Jane along with us. As much as I wanted to keep my sister in the forest house, Edeline and I had agreed that if she was careful to keep her face hidden, it would do her some good to take a walk, if only to the city house.
      We arrived at the city house just as the sun dipped below the horizon; the sky was still full of fading pinks, purples, and oranges. Fortunately for us, the guards in this section of the city had melted from patrolling on foot all day in the early summer heat. They had all taken shelter in the taverns and brothels, and the streets were clear. We snuck over the fence and through the back door of the house with ease. But just as I carefully pushed the door open, there was the sound of a loud clatter.
      Edeline and I exchanged a glance before we darted inside. My dagger was in my hand in an instant, and my heart sank as I realized the clatter had come from the wine cellar.
      There was a flash of motion as Lynden leaped into the wine cellar. Edeline and I quickly followed, and Phina appeared a split second later.
      The moment I made my way down the ladder to the cellar, the coppery smell of blood hit me full in the face. Storm was standing in the middle of the room, with his hands pressed over his mouth in horror. His sword lay on the floor next to him by an overturned lantern.
      I inhaled sharply. King Volin was still on the cellar floor. His hands and feet were still in chains, but his head . . . I felt my stomach clench unpleasantly. His head was lying next to him in a pool of crimson blood.
      "I didn't do it!" Storm said in a panic as he whirled to face us. "I swear! I just came in here to check on him and his head was already gone-"
      "We know," Lynden cut him off grimly. "This is Karmen's work. I recognize the queen's style."
      "Karmen?" I stared at the king's body in disbelief. "She found us already?"
      Edeline walked over to King Volin and gingerly crouched down to dip a finger in the blood pooling around his severed head. "He was killed less than an hour ago."
      "Let's talk about this upstairs," Lynden said quietly as he glanced in Storm's direction. Storm had gone pale, and Phina was gently trying to avert his gaze from the decapitated corpse. Edeline nodded, and the five of us climbed back up the ladder.
      "Is everyone alright?" Phina asked worriedly.
      "The king was killed right under our noses!" Storm said faintly as he grasped Phina's arm for support.
      I opened my mouth to say something, but I was cut off by a shuffling of movement from the top of the stairs.
      Is the killer still here? My heart nearly skipped a beat as everyone whirled around. But it was just Chloe-Jane. Her brows were knitted together as she looked at Phina in an odd sort of way. "You passed me on the stairs. And when I entered the washroom, there was a half-washed dress in the basin. Why is there blood on the dress and in the water?"
      "What?" Phina stammered. "I-"
      "Look at what you're wearing now," Chloe-Jane continued as her voice grew shrill. "Your new dress is still creased from being folded in a drawer! What have you done?"
      My heart really did skip a beat this time as we all turned to Phina. She just took a step backward. Her eyes were wide as she stared down at her dress.
      "Karmen," Edeline whispered. Her thunderstruck expression was an exact mirror of mine as the realization hit all of us at the same time. "You're Karmen, the queen of the vampires!"

Chapter Twenty-Six
       
I just stared at Phina in disbelief.
      Phina was Karmen. Karmen was Phina.
      I just couldn't seem to wrap my head around it at all. The Karmen I had pictured was calm, cool, and dangerous. As Phina took another trembling step away from us, all I could do was shake my head in shock. The ginger-haired vampire hadn't presented herself as any of those things.
      "Are you really Karmen?" Lynden's eyes flashed with hurt.
      "I-" Phina sputtered. She closed her eyes for a brief moment. "Yes. I am."
      "You were lying to us this entire time?" Lynden asked as his shoulders slumped. "You were lying to me this entire time? Has everything you've done just been an act?"
      "No!" Phina-or rather Karmen-took another step away from us. "I mean yes. I have lied to all of you and I'm sorry. But even though I hid my identity, my friendship with all of you has been genuine. I-"
      Storm's face drained completely of the little color it had left. "You're the vampire queen everyone fears? I don't believe it. But-but-you're Phina. Just Phina."
      "I didn't want to lie to all of you," Phina said tearfully. "I-I . . ."
      Storm took a hesitant step forward, and Phina stiffened.
      "Stay away!" She warned tearfully as she pulled out a hidden dagger from somewhere on her body. Storm froze as he looked from the blade to Phina's panicked face.
      "Phina"-Lynden took a step forward as well-"we're not going to hurt you."
      "You should stay away from me," Phina whispered. Her voice shook just as much as the dagger she was pointing at us.
      Lynden lifted his hands in a gesture of surrender.
      "Phina, please," Corinna tried desperately from my side, "we can talk this out."
      "Phina," I said, still in a state of shock.
      Phina faced me; her eyes were wide and fearful like a hunted deer's. She opened her mouth as if to say something, but then she closed it again. She glanced over her shoulder at the back door instead.
      Knowing what she was about to do a split-second before it happened, I called out to her. "Wait!"
      But my cry was in vain. In a flash of motion, Phina darted from the house and into the night beyond. Her ginger hair was the last thing we saw before she vanished entirely into the darkness.
      We all stood in stunned silence for what could have been seconds or minutes or even hours.
      "I can't believe it." Lynden was the one to break the silence as he dropped to his knees. "Phina and I traveled together for years. How can she be Karmen?"
      "I guess she couldn't have told us even if she wanted to," I said quietly. "Our feelings about the queen weren't exactly neutral."
      "I can't believe it," Storm echoed. "Phina's gone. Just like that. I don't care if she's Karmen, the queen of the vampires. She's our friend."
      Corinna placed a comforting hand on Storm's shoulder even though her own face was still painted with shock.
      "And by how she fled like that," I added, "it didn't look like she wanted to hurt us either." Then I turned to Lynden. "Should we chase her?"
      Lynden stared unseeingly at the wall. "We should let her be. If she wants to come back, she'll return to us on her own. Until then, all we can do is wait for her."
      I took a seat on the floor. The queen of the vampires had been with us this entire time. Today, three of the four queens had been in this very room.
      Corinna took a seat next to me, and her wooden leg clunked softly on the carpet. She looked over at her sister. "Chloe-Jane, how did you know to look at her dress? The blood in the washroom was an obvious giveaway, but I would have never noticed the folds in her dress."
      "Something about her didn't seem right," Chloe-Jane said stiffly. "And less right than just being a vampire, I mean."
      "Why did she kill the king?" Storm joined us on the floor. "Sure, he's useless to us now, but what does she get out of killing him? And if she really wanted to kill him, why didn't she kill him earlier? Why not kill him while she was alone with him in the castle?"
      I shook my head. "She must have wanted to get answers from him as well. I'm willing to bet she didn't kill the king earlier because she wanted to see whether the king's memories would be triggered by seeing me. When they didn't, she must have determined that he really was useless after all and decided to end him."
      Corinna turned to me. "Phina must have already known that you were one of the queens. That's probably why she and Lynden ran into us in the first place."
      "But what did she want with my uncle?" Storm asked in confusion.
      "I'm assuming she probably wanted to ask him about the prophecy," I answered. "But then Andreus must have known that she was Karmen. He knew that I was a queen."
      "He did?" Storm blinked. "Why didn't he tell any of us?"
      "Back at the mountain, Andreus called on me to meet him by myself," I said mildly. I ran my fingers absently over the carpet. "The first thing he said to me when I reached the bottom of the steps was, 'Hello, Your Majesty.' He talked to me about the prophecy. He told me that the moment I stepped into the capital city, all four queens would be there and it was only a matter of time before we all met."
      "He must have had that same talk with Phina," Corinna said thoughtfully. "And since she accepted that she was going to die by the end of the century, I don't think she's as afraid of her death after all. Hold on," Corinna paused as she looked over at Storm, "didn't you and Phina sneak into the castle together? You said all the vampires there were dead when you arrived."
      Storm looked as if he didn't want to believe it. "Phina and I only split up for a few minutes. She came back to me saying that all the vampires in the passageway ahead were dead. I never thought she had done it."
      "Something tells me we don't have to worry about Karmen anymore," Corinna said softly. "I don't think she's going to come after us. Phina could have finished cleaning up the evidence before it was discovered by Chloe-Jane, but she left it and rushed downstairs at the crash to make sure we were okay."
      We all fell silent again.
      This time it was Chloe-Jane who spoke up. "I'm going to go back upstairs." I looked on as she turned and marched up the steps, leaving the four of us sitting on the living room floor.
      "If Chloe-Jane hadn't been here," I said after she vanished into the landing, "we wouldn't have figured out Phina was Karmen."
      Corinna bit her lip. "I can't tell if it's a good thing we've figured this out. Now Phina's gone." There was silence for a long moment.
      "What should we do with the king's body?" Lynden said quietly. His eyes were downcast. "We can't just leave it in the wine cellar."
      "We should burn it," I said with a glance in the direction of the trap door. "We don't want it lying around for someone to find. Even though it was Phina who killed him, all of us now have the crime of regicide on our own heads." Then I met Lynden's gaze. "When we first met, I'll admit I was suspicious of you too. I knew that you were responsible for the deaths of everyone at the Winfielde's estate. But at the time, I didn't remember how awful that family was."
      Lynden blinked, and his eyes flickered up to look at me. "You know about the Winfielde's duchy?"
      "While I was recovering, I remembered a few things. I remembered hearing about a servant girl who was raped by the duke's son."
      "Do you remember hearing if that girl was eleven years old?" Lynden asked tiredly.
      I nodded.
      "That was my little sister." Lynden shook his head, and sadness flashed behind his eyes. "Her death still haunts me to this day. I think it's about time I told you all about my past. The Duchy of Winfielde was a terrible place, and my sister and I worked as indentured servants at the family's estate. Our parents had died when we were very young, and it was up to us to pay off their debt. The duke had many servants at the time-so many that he didn't even know any of our names.
      "The duke also had two children: a boy and a girl. They were twins. And unfortunately the twins happened to take an interest in my sister." Lynden closed his eyes for a brief moment as if to block out the images. "Whenever my sister was asked to accompany them at night, I'd always volunteer myself instead. The punishment for disobedience was getting our toes cut off, and I was willing to do anything to keep my sister away from the two of them.
      "But things got even worse when my sister became pregnant; we were already severely malnourished and she quickly fell ill. She was only eleven. When I went to the duke begging him to help my sister get an abortion, he refused and claimed that neither my sister nor I had the authority to ask for such a thing. And so all I could do was watch as my sister grew sicker and sicker with each passing day.
      "When my sister had a miscarriage, her pain was heartbreaking. Whether it was from physical pain or mental trauma, she died a few hours later. Between the money my sister and I had made and the money my late parents had been able to make, I was actually able to buy my freedom sometime later. So I left and went out into the outside world with nothing but the clothes on my back. Even though I had gotten out, I was lost. I had nowhere to go. I was so broken, both physically and mentally. I couldn't even think straight. For days, all I did was drink.
      "But the alcohol got to my head, and I came up with a foolish plan to storm the duke's estate, seek out all those who had wronged my sister and me, and kill them. I didn't get far before I was captured and thrown in their dungeons. Finally sober, I realized that I had returned to the very place I had spent so long trying to escape. And this time I'd never be able to get out.
      "Just as I was rotting away in my cell, drifting in and out of consciousness, Karmen appeared. I was too delirious at the time to remember what she looked like, but I remember telling her that I wanted revenge. She told me she could give me the power I needed to get my revenge, and I didn't think twice before I accepted her offer. I don't know how long my transition from human to vampire took, but I remember fighting through the pain. When I finally awoke as a vampire, I had been buried in the dirt. I clawed my way out of the ground and returned to kill the duke, the twins, and the rest of that cruel family. After my task had been completed, I left. With their masters dead, the rest of the indentured servants were free to go wherever they pleased."
      "I didn't know that happened to you," Corinna said, completely horrified. "I'm so sorry you went through all of that."
      I nodded, completely at a loss for words.
      "You should have told us this earlier," Storm added in shock. His face was pale. "If we had known, we could have-we could have-"
      "Could have what?" Lynden asked tiredly. "Even though I appreciate the thought, I don't know what any of you could have done."
      Storm fell silent, his brows knitting together.
      "I'm still curious about how you met Phina," I said quietly when I finally found my voice. "Would you be willing to share that with us?"
      Lynden dropped his gaze. "I met Phina even before I had become a vampire. At a tavern she tried to help me, but instead of letting her lift me out of my darkness, I pushed her away. To this day I still regret it. I never would have thought she was Karmen."
      "She had us all fooled." I looked down at my fingers laced tightly together on my lap. "But even during the time she's been with us, she never tried to hurt any of us even once. I'm starting to think that maybe we've misunderstood Karmen."
      "She has been killing vampires though," Corinna pointed out as she frowned slightly. "We still don't know the reason behind it."
      Lynden shook his head. "I just can't seem to imagine how Phina killed the first progenitor. If the story she told me about her past was true, then the jealous man who stole her away on the day of her wedding and killed her lover was the first progenitor. He must have turned her during the time she was in his manor."
      "Wait, hold up." Storm's expression was thunderstruck. "How come I don't know about this?"
      Corinna blinked. "I didn't know about this either. But if that really is the case, I can understand why Phina killed him."
      A silence fell again, and the flickering lamps were the only source of light cutting through the darkness that slowly crept in through the windows.
      "What happens now?" Storm asked after a while. His voice was hesitant.
      Corinna held each of our gazes in turn. "Now that Chloe-Jane is out of the castle, I'd like to start with freeing all of the slaves in the capital city."
      "That's not going to be an easy task," Storm said, "but I'm in. If there's anything you need me to do, I'll try my best to make it happen."
      "What about you?" I turned to Lynden. "Are you going to stay too?"
      Something like determination sparked in Lynden's eyes. "I'm going to stay. Besides, if Phina decides to come back, I want to be here to greet her."
      Corinna smiled. "Once we free the slaves working in the city, we're going to need a safe place to send them and an even safer way to get them there."
      Storm furrowed his brow. "That's going to be a lot of people. Where could they go? I don't think my uncle even has enough space for that many people."
      "We could use the forest next to the farms," I suggested. "The rumor that it's filled with vampires should be enough to keep the overseers and castle knights out until we can find a better space to relocate them."
      "Perfect." A light had returned to Corinna's eyes. "Over the next few months, we can come up with a plan." She climbed to her feet. "But we can do that later. I'm going to make dinner first."
      I sighed softly. "I'll leave you to it, then. I should go clean up the wine cellar." With that, I rose to my feet. I looked down at Lynden for a while. The vampire was still sitting on the floor with a dazed expression. He blinked once but didn't make any motion to rise. "If you want to stay here, I don't mind cleaning up the wine cellar myself."
      "No." Lynden shook his head and finally raised his gaze to look at me. "I'll help you."
      He slowly climbed to his feet, and I walked over to the trap door. The moment I jumped into the cellar, the smell of blood shoved its way up my nose. Lynden landed on the stones next to me. His crimson eyes glowed in the dim light.
      "Lynden," I said quietly as we stood there in the silence. "I want you to know that I'm really sorry that happened to you. No one deserves that."
      Lynden just nodded as he stared down at the king's headless corpse. "It was the kind of experience that no amount of time could heal. It follows me even to this day." Just as I knelt down to remove the chains from the king's lifeless body, Lynden spoke again. "Do you think we're to blame for scaring Phina away?"
      "I don't know." I sighed heavily as my fingers stilled over the metal. "She was probably worried about how we'd react, so instead of facing us, she fled."
      "I hope she comes back." Lynden's voice was tired. "I really hope she comes back. For the longest time, Phina was my only friend. She was my friend when I needed one the most."
      "Hope is a fleeting concept." I dipped a finger in the blood pooling on the floor. The deep red was stark against my pale skin, and a single drop dripped on the stones. "But it's hope that keeps us all moving forward, isn't it?"
      "Of course." Lynden sighed. "Oh, have you heard the way Phina talked about the queen of the vampires? Either Phina was a very, very, good actress, or it was her own self-hatred talking."
      I straightened and took a step away from the king's corpse. "Was it really like that?"
      Lynden nodded. "When we would talk about Karmen, Phina would always express how much she despised the queen. She would condemn the queen's warped idea of reality. It's common knowledge that the queen despises both humans and vampires. I don't blame her, though; it's very easy to hate both of them for their cruelty. But what I've come to realize-what I hope Phina's realized too-is that humans can be kind. That vampires can be good. Even though we possess the bodies of monsters, we don't have to become them."
      "Both humans and vampires can be monsters," I said lightly. "But they're only a true monster once they don't mind being one."
      Lynden looked over at me. "For the longest time, I didn't think humans and vampires could actually work together. And how wrong I was."
      "To me, it never seemed impossible for humans and vampires to work together. Vampires were humans once after all. Unknown to most humans, we're all driven by the same things: power, greed, love, hope. When it comes to morality, we're no different than humans-not better than them and certainly not worse."
      "Being locked up in the castle brought back a lot of unpleasant memories," Lynden said after a long pause. "The last time I had been locked up in a cell like that, my mortal body died."
      "If you ever want to talk," I said softly, "I'm here to listen."
       
~
       
      The moon was high in the sky, and its silvery face was partially blocked by a thick layer of clouds. I lingered outside the front door to the city house for a moment. The scent of smoke still hung in the air around me.
      I had just burned the king's body and scattered his ashes. Even though I should have felt happy that the king was gone, I found that I didn't feel much of anything. When Phina had killed him, King Volin wasn't himself. He couldn't remember any of the atrocities he had committed, and there was something almost unsatisfying about his end.
      I pushed open the door to the house. The living room was dark save for a few dying lamps. Just as I turned to make my way over to the dining room table, I noticed that the back door was partially cracked. I walked over to the door and gently pushed it open.
      Corinna was sitting on the deck outside, dangling her legs. "Edeline." Corinna turned as I stepped outside. Even though her eyes were tired, they still seemed to sparkle as she motioned for me to take a seat next to her.
      A soft smile tugged on my lips as I walked over to join her. "Did Storm already go to bed?"
      Corinna nodded as she turned to look back up at the night sky. "Storm and Chloe-Jane are asleep upstairs. Lynden left the house saying he'd be back in the morning. I think he's trying to look for Phina."
      I sighed as I watched Corinna gaze out over the thousands of little lights twinkling lazily in the sky above. There was curiosity in her eyes, and I angled my head to the side. "What are you thinking?"
      "I'm thinking," Corinna said slowly, "well, I'm wondering if there are other worlds somewhere out there. I'm wondering if somewhere far away there's a better world than ours. A better place. A place where people aren't driven by greed and hate and jealousy."
      "And what do you think?" I asked lightly as Corinna rested her head on my shoulder. "Do you think there's such a world?"
      "I want to believe that there is one." Corinna's voice was no more than a tired whisper. "I want to believe that there's a place out there where people are kind-a place where there is no king, no hierarchy, no slavery, no nonsense about witches, and no death lurking around every corner. A place where everyone has an equal shot at life."
      "That sounds like a good place."
      "It does," Corinna said wistfully. "But even if such a place does exist, it's too bad that the two of us are stuck here."
      I smiled faintly as I watched the clouds drift across the sky. "Maybe if we try hard enough, we can make this world a better place. Then we won't have to figure out how to travel to a different one."
      "You're right." I could hear the traces of a smile in Corinna's voice. "When the sun rises in the morning, we can start coming up with a plan. But for now, can you stay with me here for a little longer?"

Chapter Twenty-Seven
       
I awoke to find myself lying in bed. The blankets had been carefully tucked around my body, and I groggily sat up. I rubbed the sleep from my eyes before looking around the room in a tired daze. I was in the city house, in the same bedroom I had once shared with Clarity.
      The faint sound of the streets outside was the only noise cutting through the otherwise silent morning, and the soft light from the world outside gave the curtains a warm glow. A knock sounded on the door. Edeline? I quickly made my way over to the door. But when I pulled it open, I discovered that the figure standing in the doorway wasn't Edeline. It was Chloe-Jane.
      "That vampire told me you were in here," she said stiffly, refusing to meet my gaze.
      "Would you like to come in?" I asked mildly. Chloe-Jane stepped past me and into the bedroom beyond without a word. I gently shut the door behind her.
      She took a seat on the bed. "I'm not here to talk about vampires." Ever so slowly, she raised her eyes to meet mine. "I'm here to talk about King Volin."
      I inhaled sharply, suddenly very awake. "What is it?"
      Chloe-Jane clasped her hands together in her lap as if she wasn't sure where to begin. Finally she took a shaky breath. "You've seen first-hand the kind of person the king was. Not only was he cruel and relished in the misery and pain of others, but he was also ambitious. His Majesty's grand plan was to conquer the southern continent."
      "Conquer the southern continent?"
      "He had a plan and everything." Chloe-Jane nodded gravely, and her face paled at the thought. "His plan was to actually give the people of the northern continent a proper incentive to go to war against the southern continent and conquer it once and for all. His plan was to kill me and blame it on the representatives from the southern continent. You know what the attitudes of the people here are when it comes to the southern continent-even if they didn't think very highly of the king for choosing me as his wife, their contempt for the southern continent is greater. For the right reason, they'd gladly jump at the chance to take it over.
      "When I figured out what King Volin was planning to do, I got desperate and tried to run away. Unfortunately, the castle is a very heavily guarded place. And as a result, I didn't get very far. After that, King Volin never permitted me to leave his side. He brought me with him everywhere he went. I was in the dungeons too many times, and I don't think I'll ever forget the horrors I witnessed there."
      An unsettling feeling had begun to creep through me. If we hadn't gotten Chloe-Jane out of the castle, there was a chance that my sister would no longer be around.
      "The king was going to kill the representatives from the southern continent too." Chloe-Jane's voice grew quieter and quieter, and I had to lean closer to pick up her words. "It was horrible. And nothing I did made it any better. I prayed and prayed and prayed, but it was all in vain. I always thought the Immortal One protected people who were good-people who were faithful. But I was wrong. All of those poor people locked in the castle dungeons hadn't done anything to deserve that sort of fate."
      Chloe-Jane wrapped her arms around her own trembling shoulders. I reached out a hand and placed it gently on my sister's back. Chloe-Jane flinched at my touch but didn't make any move to shake my hand off. I silently pulled my sister into an embrace, stroking her hair as she rested her chin on my shoulder.
      "What happens now, Corinna?" Chloe-Jane asked tiredly when I finally let her go. Her eyes were unfocused yet alert. "You've saved both the representatives from the southern continent and myself from death. I want to say that you were blessed and guided by the Immortal One, but that isn't the case."
      I sighed. "Lynden wants to talk to you and see if you're okay. Phina did, too-well, before she left, that is. I've been meaning to ask, what do you have against Storm? He's not a vampire."
      "I don't like him very much," Chloe-Jane said shortly. "He has no idea how things are supposed to work-he doesn't have a problem with vampires and humans working together."
      "Chloe-"
      "I know you don't seem to think it's a problem either, but vampires and humans aren't supposed to work together. Vampires are an evil magic that go against everything the Immortal One is and stands for."
      I just shook my head tiredly. "If you don't like the vampires, I don't know how much you're going to like Storm's uncle."
      Chloe-Jane blinked. "Who's Storm's uncle? Or should I say, what's Storm's uncle?"
      "I think you're better off not knowing right now. All you need to know is that his name is Andreus. I'm sure you already know that Mother, Cameren, and Clarity are staying with him."
      Her head snapped up to meet my gaze. "Will we get to see them soon? I miss Mother. I miss Cameren."
      I offered my sister what I hoped was a reassuring smile. "Once the guards move away from the main road, we can send you up to meet them."
      "What about you? Won't you be coming too?"
      My smile faded. "I still have work to do in the capital city. But after that work is finished, we can all leave the capital city behind us."
      "Are we going to leave the vampires behind too?" Chloe-Jane asked hopefully.
      I just turned to the door. "I don't remember you eating dinner yesterday. Let's go get you something to eat. You must be hungry."
      "I can get something on my own." Chloe-Jane followed me out of the bedroom and down to the living room. Edeline was sitting on the couch, and she gave me a bright smile when I walked in. Lynden had returned and was standing next to the back door, seemingly lost in thought as he polished a sword that was already gleaming. Storm was in the living room too, pacing back and forth agitatedly.
      "What's up with him?" I asked quietly as I took a seat next to Edeline. Chloe-Jane continued on her own to the kitchen.
      Edeline sighed softly, and her expression was one of mild amusement as she watched Storm march in circles. "He can't stand staying in the house all day. Except the only people he'll run into if he leaves this place would be the castle knights. It's one thing to move between the two houses, and another just to wander the streets of the town. I don't think the king's decapitation sat well with him either."
      "I can hear you, you know," Storm said irritably. "We've been in this house for over a week already. Phina made things interesting while she was still here with all of us, but she's gone now. I want to go help look for her."
      Edeline opened her mouth to reply, but suddenly a knock sounded on the front door. Edeline and I were both on our feet in an instant, daggers in hand.
      Storm had frozen midstride, and his eyes were glued to the door as if he'd be able to see through it if he tried hard enough. "Phina?" the dark-haired boy asked hopefully.
      Lynden shook his head. His expression was serious. "Those are humans outside."
      "Have the knights found us already?" Chloe-Jane asked shakily as she stuck her head out of the kitchen.
      The knocking sounded again, and we all flinched.
      "Who's going to open it?" Storm hissed fearfully. His hand was on the hilt of his sword.
      "You're going to open it." Edeline crouched down to duck behind the couch and motioned for me to do the same. "You can tell them to go away, and the rest of us will hide."
      "What?" Storm said in a panic. "If they really are castle knights, do you really think I can bluff my way out of this?" Storm continued to look at the door apprehensively. "Can't we just pretend that no one's home?" The knocking sounded for the third time, and Storm jumped.
      Open it, Edeline mouthed.
      "If it comes down to a fight," Lynden said as he joined Chloe-Jane in the kitchen, "at least you'll have us as backup."
      "Fine." Storm marched over to the door and pulled it open.
      Two figures stood in the doorway. The first was a knight dressed head to toe in armor, while the second was a slightly shorter figure in a black cloak.
      "Hello," Storm said stiffly. "Do the two of you need something?"
      "Storm," the cloaked figure said in a sharp voice I would have recognized anywhere. "It's been a while."
      Edeline and I both looked at each other with wide eyes before we slowly rose to our feet to watch the cloaked figure lower her hood.
      "Clarity!" I stared at my sister in shock. Clarity was the last person I would have expected to show up at the house. She had cut her hair; her curls brushed her shoulders as they glowed golden in the sunlight. But her hair seemed to be the only different thing about her. The same steel-like aura was still present as her eyes surveyed the interior of the house.
      Storm beckoned Clarity and the knight inside. "Come in-quickly now."
      "What are you doing here?" I pocketed my dagger as I rushed over to Clarity. "I'm so happy to see you, but-"
      Clarity's face softened ever so slightly. "I was worried about you and the others. When I heard that the queen had been taken from the castle, I knew I needed to come back." She trailed off as she glanced around the room. "Where's Phina?"
      I exhaled through my nose as my gaze went to the armored knight at Clarity's side. "Long story short, she left. We'll give you more details later."
      "Who might this be?" Edeline asked as she looked at the knight.
      The knight slowly raised his gloved hands to his helmet and lifted the metal covering off his face.
      Storm's face split into a grin. "Cameren!"
      "Cameren!" Chloe-Jane cried as she sprinted out of the kitchen. "Clarity!"
      "Cameren," I echoed, shaking my head as if my eyes were playing tricks on me. My brother's posture had completely changed to the point where I hadn't recognize him.
      "Chloe-Jane, Corinna, Storm." Cameren smiled as he knelt down to let Chloe-Jane throw her arms around him. "It's been a while."
      "How-?" I blinked back the stinging tears in my eyes. Cameren was right here in front of me. Healed. Completely healed.
      "I begged Clarity to let me come with her," he explained. "Mother wanted to come too, but Clarity and I managed to talk her out of it because of the danger."
      Clarity turned to look down at Chloe-Jane, and her eyes softened. "Chloe, I'm so happy you're safe. All of us were so worried."
      When Chloe-Jane finally released Cameren, my brother noticed the wooden leg peeking out from under my skirts. "Corinna, what happened to you?"
      I sighed. "Getting Chloe-Jane out of the castle was no easy task. I'd consider myself lucky, though. If Edeline hadn't been there, I would have lost my life instead of just a leg."
      Clarity arched a brow. "Edeline?"
      Edeline smiled softly. "My real name is Edeline. I've decided to go by it now."
      "I've been trying to fill Mother and Cameren in the best I could," Clarity informed me, "but I think you're going to have to continue from where I left off."
      I looked up at my brother. "It's a little bit of a long story."
      Cameren laughed. "That's alright. If you don't mind telling it, I'm more than happy to listen. But right now, I seem to be more out of the loop than anyone here. What happened to Phina? What happened to the king? He was said to have gone missing too."
      "The king's dead," Lynden said shortly.
      Cameren blinked in disbelief. "King Volin is dead?"
      "It wasn't our plan to kill him," Edeline clarified. "Phina just got to him first."
      Cameren shook his head in bewilderment as Clarity stepped forward, looking at us for an explanation. "I don't understand. Why would Phina kill the king?"
      "It turns out Phina is actually Karmen, the queen of the vampires," Storm said.
      "I'm sure you all know that if you get caught and this information gets out, things will not end well," my brother warned. "You know that you can't just waltz into the castle, abduct the queen of the kingdom, and kill the king."
      "We know," I said with another sigh. "All of us are in a lot of trouble, and the last thing I wanted was to drag you and Clarity into it." I walked over to take a seat at the dining room table. Cameren, Clarity, and Chloe-Jane followed close behind. "Oh"-I suddenly remembered one of my many questions-"was it really okay for the two of you to wander around the capital city? You know as well as I do that people connected to the southern continent aren't exactly very popular, to put it lightly. And there are knights out searching for us."
      "As long as I'm wearing the armor, no one bothers me or Clarity," Cameren reassured me. "Andreus made sure we came in costume."
      We spent the rest of the day bringing my brother up to speed on everything that had happened over the past few months during our stay in the capital city. We told him about the representatives King Volin had invited over from the southern continent and how they were here in the capital city now. But even as we talked, I couldn't bring myself to worry about them at the moment-my brother had just shown up without a single injury on his body, and I would spend the rest of the night with a smile on my face.

Chapter Twenty-Eight
       
After dinner, Corinna and I said our farewells before making our way back to the house in the forest. I wasn't sure how late it was when we left, but the moon was high in the sky and the stars flickered softly against the midnight backdrop.
      Corinna was quiet as we walked. She looked troubled; she was undoubtedly excited about the return of her brother and sister, but she was also worried about Chloe-Jane.
      "What are you thinking?" I asked quietly.
      Corinna hummed softly. "Having my brother show up healed-completely healed-I'm thinking this has to be a dream."
      I smiled. "It's not a dream. I saw it too. This is real. All of it."
      We reached the house, and instead of going inside, Corinna took a seat on the front steps to look up at the glittering lights in the sky.
      "Are you sure you don't want to go to sleep?" I asked as I took a seat beside her. "Now that your brother and sister are here, I don't think you'll be able to stay up all night and sleep during the day anymore."
      Corinna let out a sigh. "I know. I'm hoping that with the two of them here, Chloe-Jane will feel more at ease."
      "Come on," I said softly. "You should go to sleep if you want to have enough energy to face everyone tomorrow."
      "You're right." She let me help her to her feet. "You're always right, you know that?"
      "I don't know about that. If I had always made the right decisions, I wonder whether I'd be where I am today. But since all of those choices ended up leading me to you, I don't regret any of them."
      "What would you have done if you had met me back at the time when you were Princess Edeline?"
      "If I had met you when I was still Princess Edeline," I started slowly. "If I had met you back at the time when I lived in my family's castle, I think we still would have been great friends. The only difference would be that the two of us would be safe and happy. And maybe we'd occasionally talk about vampires, but only about how we pitied them for not being able to set foot under the sun."
      Corinna went to her bedroom first to change into her nightgown while I carefully folded our cloaks into neat squares and set them on top of the living room couch. I joined Corinna in the back room a few minutes later to find her sitting at the vanity, holding a hairbrush. A little lantern sat on the table, painting her skin and hair in glowing orange.
      "Mind if I help you?"
      "Not at all." Corinna smiled and let me take the brush from her hands. "Are you sure, though? A queen like yourself doesn't need to do these kinds of trivial tasks."
      "You know I'm only a queen in name." Noticing my fang marks on her skin, I paused as I brushed Corinna's hair over her shoulder.
      She turned to face the mirror, smiling faintly. "It's been a number of days now, and these haven't seemed to fade."
      I covered my face with my hands. "I'm sorry, Corinna. I-I forgot to tell you that the mark of a vampire won't ever go away."
      Corinna giggled at my reaction. When I still wouldn't lift my hands from my face, she stood from her seat and wrapped her arms around me in a warm hug. "I don't mind at all, you know. I know it was the only way to put a stop to my pain and the only way for you to replenish enough blood to get us out of there."
      I finally let my hands drop from my face and rested my head on Corinna's shoulder. "If I had met you when I was still Princess Edeline, we wouldn't have ever been thrown into King Volin's dungeons."
      Corinna held me tightly. "No matter how terrible it was, it's in the past now. King Volin is dead and won't ever touch you again."
      "You think that's the only reason why I have a grudge against him? If we had stayed there any longer, you would have starved to death. We got lucky this time." Then I sighed, slumping my shoulders in defeat. "Even with me being a vampire, I was still completely useless. When Karmen turned me, the main reason I agreed was to gain the strength and power I needed to protect the people I love-to make sure the people who had hurt them wouldn't walk away without any consequences. But before I could get my revenge on the people who had killed my parents, they had already been brought to justice by others. This time, too-Phina killed the king before we could even decide what we wanted to do with him."
      "We're out now, though." Corinna squeezed my hands as she pressed her forehead against mine. "We're safe. We're alive."
      I helped her over to the bed before making my way over to the little lantern and extinguishing the dancing flame inside. I walked over to the door next and paused there to look back at Corinna. "I'll be in the living room if you need anything."
      "Wait." Corinna looked at me through the dark. "Do you think you could stay here with me? I know vampires don't need to sleep, but I want to spend more time with you."
      I smiled softly. "Okay. I'll stay with you." I made my way back over to Corinna and shook back my inky hair before lying down next to her.
      "Thank you," Corinna whispered as she offered me half of the woolen blanket. "Goodnight, Edeline."
      "Goodnight, Corinna."
      The two of us lay there in silence before Corinna's breathing slowed and she drifted off into a deep sleep. The steady beating of her heart and the warmth radiating off her were comforting in a way.
      I found myself smiling softly as I stared up at the ceiling. The moonlight spilled in through the window, cutting through the faint traces of dust, whose lazy spirals moved in slow motion through space. But no matter how slowly the particles danced, they were still moving. Time was still moving. The sun would rise shortly and bathe the northern continent in the light of a new day.
      But right now it was still night. Right now I would enjoy the brief peace and tranquility because I knew that moments like this were short. Fleeting. Precious. Just like life itself.
       
~
       
      "Good morning." I smiled as Corinna slowly opened her eyes. Her lashes fluttered as her eyes adjusted to the light glowing through the curtains.
      Corinna groggily sat up. "Good morning." She slid out of the bed and got to work fastening her wooden leg. I took a seat behind her and skillfully braided back her hair. "So what happens now?" she asked absently as she held her hands on her leg. "King Volin is dead, Phina has disappeared, my siblings returned, and the royal guards are searching for us. So much has happened in the past few weeks-the past few days, even-and I can't seem to wrap my head around any of it. But I stick by what I said before; I want to free all of the slaves. With that said, though, the more I think about it, the more impossible it seems."
      "Since Chloe-Jane is the queen of the kingdom," I said slowly, "if she ordered for all of the slaves to be freed, wouldn't everyone have to listen now that she's the one in charge?"
      "That's right." Corinna's eyes widened as she nodded along. Then she frowned. "But do you really think the people will listen to Chloe-Jane? Do you think the overseers will listen?"
      "It's worth giving it a shot, though, isn't it? If worse comes to worst, we can always go with Plan B."
      "Plan B?" Corinna raised her brows. "Please don't tell me that's where you go in and kill all of the slave owners in the kingdom."
      "Alright." I smiled wryly. "I won't tell you then. But on a more serious note, I'd prefer to settle things in a way that doesn't involve any more death as well."
      "We should ask the others. Maybe they've thought of something."
      I wrapped my arms around her. "Everything will work out in the end. You'll see."
      When Corinna and I reached the house in the city, we were greeted by the sound of raised voices.
      "Just take the dagger," Storm was saying angrily.
      "No," Chloe-Jane replied shrilly.
      "How else are you going to protect yourself if you won't let me teach you?" Storm asked in exasperation.
      "I don't want it." Chloe-Jane's eyes went from Storm to the blade in his hands and back again. "I won't take it. It's not my place to take it."
      "Are you serious?" Storm looked as if he wanted to pull out his own hair. "I'm trying to help you, Chloe-Jane!"
      "I don't want your help," Chloe-Jane snapped. "And when were we ever on a first-name basis?"
      "Chloe-Jane." Cameren appeared in the doorway to the kitchen. His brows were knitted together, and he bore a slight frown on his face. "All of them really are just trying to help you, you know. If your sister hadn't learned how to defend herself-well, you have her to thank for getting you out of the castle."
      "What's going on down there?" Clarity's cool voice called from the top of the staircase, and everyone turned to look at her. "I was trying to sleep. Oh"-Clarity's sharp eyes landed on Corinna and me-"the two of you are here."
      Storm and Chloe-Jane looked over at us as well as if they both just noticed we were in the room. "I'm going upstairs," Chloe-Jane announced. Her voice was higher than usual as she quickly snatched the dagger from Storm before hurrying up the stairs. She ignored Clarity on the landing, and when she vanished from sight, Corinna and I made our way over to Storm.
      "Where did Lynden go anyway?" Storm complained, and it was only then that I realized he was limping. "He's the one who asked me to give the dagger to Chloe-Jane, and she 'accidentally' dropped it on my foot before you got here."
      "You could have asked me to help give the dagger to Chloe," Corinna said. "She's been through a lot already during the past few months. Constantly getting into arguments with her won't help anyone."
      "I know, I know." Storm ran an agitated hand through his dark hair. "I just want to go help look for Phina."
      I shook my head heavily. "Unless she wants to be found, no matter how long you look, you won't find her."
      "I know that Phina's the queen of the vampires," Storm said defeatedly. "And while I've heard the stories of all the terrible things Karmen has done, I can't help feeling sorry for her. It sounds like we were her only friends. If we hadn't reacted the way we did when we found out she was Karmen, do you think she would have stayed?"
      Corinna took a seat on the floor across from the couch, and I joined her. "Would it have changed anything?"
      Storm absently passed his sheathed sword from hand to hand. "I think Lynden sent her into a panic when he accused her of lying to everyone. I don't blame him, though-we were all in shock. It would make sense for us to be wary of her, knowing all the things Queen Karmen has done, but she's never tried to hurt any of us. Everything she's done has been to help."
      Corinna looked up at the ceiling as if it would somehow reveal all the answers. "I wonder whether she's still in the capital city."
      Just as the words left her mouth, there was the sound of the back door opening and closing. Lynden entered the room, and his face was masked in the shadows of his hood. I turned to look over at him. "Seems like you've found something."
      Lynden nodded. "It's about Phina." He briskly walked over to the other side of the room to hang his cloak next to the front door. "She's not in the capital city. Word has spread that the bodies of dead vampires have been turning up around some of the smaller towns and villages."
      I blinked. "Dead vampires?"
      "All of them have been decapitated in the same way too."
      "What is she trying to do?" Corinna mused. "She can't have this many enemies, can she?"
