      "I don't think this is just about her getting rid of those who oppose her," Lynden said with a frown. "From the descriptions of some of the vampires that were found dead, there were quite a few in favor of Queen Karmen as well as a number of neutral ones."
      "Could she be trying to kill all the vampires?" Storm piped up.
      I furrowed my brow. "But if that's the case, why hasn't she gone after Lynden and me?"
      "I guess we'll just have to ask her when she comes back," Storm said determinedly. "And if she really does want to kill all the vampires, she'll be back eventually."
      Corinna leveled Storm a look. "Phina's already made it clear she isn't going to hurt Edeline or Lynden. But changing the topic, Edeline and I have started coming up with a plan."
      "A plan?" Storm said excitedly, his eyes lighting up. "What's the plan?"
      "We'll start freeing slaves at a few select shops at first," Corinna explained. "When the knights are alerted to these occurrences, it's very likely that they'll stop guarding the roads out of the city and go investigate. After that, we can safely leave the capital city and make our way down to the farms." Then, as if she just remembered, she breathlessly added, "Oh, and Chloe-Jane should return to the castle."
      I blinked. I hadn't heard that last part until just now. I opened my mouth to speak, but Storm beat me to it. "You want Chloe-Jane to go back to the castle? But-but didn't we just get her out of there?"
      "Listen," Corinna said tiredly. "Right now there's no one on the throne. If Chloe doesn't return soon, she'll be replaced despite the fact that she is the queen. We also have to address the representatives who came all the way from the southern continent to meet with the king. We don't know how quickly they'll return to their own country, and Chloe-Jane needs to meet them in the king's place. This is a rare opportunity for the two continents to make peace."
      The pieces clicked in my head. "Chloe-Jane will continue to spread the word that the king wanted to cooperate with the southern continent before he was abducted by vampires. And with the help of those southern continent representatives, Chloe-Jane can stop the feud between the northern and southern continents."
      "Exactly." Corinna looked at me with gratitude in her eyes. "The only problem is, I doubt Chloe-Jane wants to return to the castle or even meet these representatives. And if she did, would she even know how to negotiate terms?"
      "You can leave convincing Chloe-Jane and the negotiations to me," Cameren said as he stepped out of the kitchen. "She happens to listen to me."
      "Thank you." Corinna said appreciatively. "If Chloe-Jane can secure her place as the ruler of this kingdom, she can start making the changes we need."
      Cameren nodded.
      Corinna exhaled. "In the meantime, we should send a letter to the representatives-find a time and place for Chloe-Jane to meet them."
      "I can get the letter delivered," Lynden said. "With a little poking around, it won't take me long to figure out where the representatives are staying in the capital city."
      "Wonderful." Corinna clasped her hands together. "Once Chloe-Jane does return to the castle, we'll need some way to communicate. Chloe should replace the entire guard force in the castle. The knights were loyal to the king and the king alone."
      "I'll make sure that happens," Cameren said confidently.
      "Once the guards are replaced," Storm added excitedly, "we'll be able to leave the capital city without any problems!"
      "And then once Chloe-Jane has gained the trust of the people," I said, "she'll be able to free all of the slaves with ease."
      "The only question now is whether she's willing to cooperate." Corinna's shoulders slumped. "I would gladly go in her place, and I'm sure Clarity would too, but Chloe-Jane is the queen after all."
      I reached for Corinna's hands and gently wrapped my fingers around hers. "Don't worry-I'm sure Chloe-Jane will do her part. It's in her own interest to help the people of this kingdom."
      Corinna nodded as she gave me a weak smile.
      Lynden walked over to the chest of drawers against the wall of the living room and rummaged around for parchment and ink for us. "I assume we'd want to get this letter out to the representatives as soon as possible. What are you going to write?"
      "We'll say that the queen is safe and requests an audience with the representatives of the southern continent," Corinna said. "Once Chloe-Jane is out of harm's way, that's when we can start to make our own move against the slave owners in the capital city. If we draw attention to the issue at hand and the conditions that are forced upon the slaves, Chloe-Jane might gain the support of those who oppose it."
      "That might just work." Storm nodded slowly as it seemed to dawn on him. "Most of the kingdom is living in poverty. The farther away from the capital you go, the poorer the people get. The capital city gives the illusion of wealth, and everyone who lives in the villages scattered around the rest of the kingdom despises it because of that. There are a lot more people who oppose the way things are right now than there appears at first glance."
      I turned back to Corinna, smiling. "You're brilliant, you know that?"
      "Of course." Corinna laughed as she took my hands. "With you reminding me so many times, how would I not? But it would be wrong for me to take all of the credit. We're in this together. All of us."

Chapter Twenty-Nine
       
Edeline and I sat at the dining room table, quietly working on a letter. Since Edeline had much better penmanship than I did, she had offered to do the writing. I watched the words bloom from Edeline's quill onto the parchment in neat, elegant script.
      "There." She set down her quill before fanning the wet ink with a hand. "What do you think?"
      I beamed. "It's perfect."
      Edeline smiled back with bright eyes. When the ink dried completely, Edeline carefully folded the letter and tucked it into its envelope.
      "Shall I take that to the representatives?" Lynden asked.
      I nodded. "Please do." Edeline handed me the envelope and I passed it to Lynden.
      "It will take me a few days at most to find their location," Lynden said as he pocketed the letter. Then he paused as he turned to look back at me. "What happens if Chloe-Jane doesn't agree?"
      "She'll agree," I said with a lot more confidence than I felt. "I think when she realizes that she has the power to change things for the better, she'll rise to the occasion."
      Lynden looked down at me. "I hope you're right. But if Chloe-Jane doesn't want to meet the representatives-if she doesn't want to go back to the castle-you shouldn't force her either."
      "I know. If she really doesn't want to, Clarity or I will go in her stead. I don't want to think about what would happen if either of us pretended to be Chloe, but as long as we can get the backing of the southern continent, it will have been worth it."
      Lynden just nodded before he disappeared out the front door.
      "You'd really go in Chloe-Jane's place?" Edeline asked quietly.
      I closed my eyes for a brief moment. "The representatives haven't seen her before. Most of the townspeople probably don't know what she looks like either. The only ones who do know at this point are the nobles and the castle knights. If I really do have to pretend to be Chloe, it's going to be very difficult to steer clear of them. Even if I do look a little bit like my sister, it's definitely not enough to fool anyone for long." I shook my head, trying to collect all of the thoughts and worries spinning around inside it.
      Suddenly, I felt a reassuring hand rest on my shoulder, and I turned to find Cameren standing behind me. "Let's go talk to her together."
      I nodded. "Edeline"-I looked back at Edeline as I rose from my seat-"while my brother and I are talking to Chloe-Jane, do you think you could indulge Clarity for a bit? You know how she is-if she finds out Cameren and I are talking to Chloe-Jane, she'll probably want to join in."
      "Of course." Edeline flashed me a reassuring smile. "Don't worry. I'll keep her downstairs."
      "What about me?" Storm called from the couch. "What should I do?"
      "You should keep off your foot and get some rest." Cameren said. "We can play cards when we're done. I'll try to get Chloe-Jane to apologize properly later."
      Storm shook his head dejectedly. "Don't bother. I know for a fact that she'd prefer not to talk to me." Then he looked at Cameren hopefully. "Cards sound fun, though. I'll take you up on your offer."
      Cameren and I followed Edeline up the stairs, and I watched silently as she knocked on Clarity's door. My older sister appeared in the doorway a moment later. Edeline said something to her in a lowered voice, and Clarity frowned. She stepped out of her room, swiftly closed the door behind herself, and followed Edeline back down the hall. As Clarity passed by Cameren and me, she eyed the two of us suspiciously but didn't stop walking.
      When Edeline and Clarity vanished downstairs, my brother motioned for me to stay outside as he knocked lightly on Chloe-Jane's door.
      Chloe-Jane's high voice came from the other side of the wood. "Who is it?"
      "It's Cameren, Chloe," Cameren said gently.
      "Brother!" Chloe-Jane's tone of voice changed, and we heard the sound of hurried footsteps. The door was thrown open, and Chloe-Jane beamed up at Cameren.
      I stood a short distance down the hall, far enough not to be seen but close enough to hear the conversation.
      "Chloe-Jane." Cameren bent down so he could be at eye level with her. "How are you feeling today?"
      "I'm feeling better. That boy with the black hair annoys me, though." Then Chloe-Jane paused. "Did Corinna ask you to talk to me?"
      "Your sister needs your help."
      "I'm the least helpful out of everyone here." Chloe-Jane's words came quickly. "I know she wants to go and free the slaves from the capital city. Does she really want me to help fight? I-I don't know how to fight. Aren't the vampires and that other boy enough?"
      "Chloe," Cameren said softly. "Listen to my words-the representatives from the southern continent are still in the capital city. As the queen of the kingdom, Corinna thinks you should meet them."
      "Meet them?" Chloe-Jane echoed in confusion.
      "Your sister wants you to meet them and negotiate ending the war between the northern and southern continents once and for all."
      Chloe-Jane's eyes were wide. "But the king wasn't going to end the war. He was going to use that conference as a way to ensure that there could never be peace!"
      "I know." Cameren took Chloe-Jane's hands in his own. "But now that the king is dead, you can be the one to determine how the conference plays out. Chloe, by doing this, you could strengthen the kingdom's ties to the southern continent. You'd never have to tell them about what the king was planning to do. Before we knew what his true intentions were, he had put on the act that he was trying to push our kingdom forward. To progress. I think Corinna and the others were fortunate enough to stop King Volin before he could destroy the fragile balance between the continents for good."
      "I think I understand now," Chloe-Jane said slowly. "Let's say I do meet them. Then what happens?"
      "Your sister wants you to return to the castle and take up the position as queen."
      "She wants me to be the queen?"
      "You are the queen, are you not?" Cameren's tone was calm if not a little tired.
      "You're right!" Chloe-Jane said suddenly. "I am the queen! I-I have the power."
      "Do you think you'll go meet the representatives? If you don't want to, Corinna is willing to go in your stead."
      Chloe-Jane dropped her gaze to her hands. "That I can do." Then she blinked. "Wait, she'll go in my place? But she's not the real queen. Wouldn't that put her in danger?"
      Cameren smiled wryly. "So you do care about your sister after all."
      "Of course I care about my sister. I've been trying to help her this entire time, and she doesn't listen to anything I say!"
      "Alright, alright." Cameren chuckled. "Does this mean you're willing to go back to the castle? We can give you some time to think about it."
      "I-" Chloe-Jane started. "I don't know. I just felt so helpless there. No matter how much I prayed, things kept getting worse. It felt like I was trapped there for years. During the days before Corinna and the others got me out, I just wanted everything to end. The king made it very clear that he was going to kill me as part of his grand scheme.
      "You were right. You, Corinna, Clarity, and Mother-all of you were right. I prayed for all of those poor people locked up in the castle dungeons, but nothing changed. I've done a lot of thinking recently, and I've come to the conclusion that the Immortal One has failed me. It's been said that the Immortal One is the most powerful being in the entire universe. If He's really that powerful, why would He let us suffer? Even though I don't believe in Him anymore, I do believe that everyone should be able to live a peaceful and joyful life."
      "The Immortal One might not be real"-I stepped into view of the doorway, and Chloe-Jane looked up at me with wide eyes-"but we are. The people are real. I know it's difficult, but you should try to put your faith in them-to put your faith in us. Right now, you hold the most power out of anyone in this kingdom. You're the queen. Our queen."
      Chloe-Jane let out a breath. "I know all too well about the state of the outer kingdom. As queen, I'd have the power to actually help out. I could make this kingdom a better place. Despite what has happened, I-I think I would like to try after all. I'll go talk to the representatives. I want to return to the castle and be the queen you think I can be, but I don't know if I'll be able to stay in that place forever."
      "You wouldn't have to stay there for the rest of your life," I said softly. "Just until the kingdom gets back on its feet. We could figure something out. The choice will be yours."
      Chloe-Jane nodded.
      "Thank you, Chloe," I said as I offered my sister a smile.
      Chloe-Jane dropped her gaze. "I'll do my best."
      This was a start. "Cameren will go with you to the conference. All you have to do is agree to stop the war and tell the southern continent representatives that the kingdom would like to work with them."
      Chloe-Jane nodded slowly. "I can do that. That's all?"
      "That's all. I'll work out the details with Cameren later tonight. That way, the two of you can be on your way to meet them as soon as Lynden finds their location and gets a response."
      Chloe-Jane just nodded before backing into her room and quietly shutting the door.
      As we made our way down the stairs, I turned to my brother. "So Chloe-Jane does listen to you after all."
      Cameren just gave me a knowing smile.
       
~
       
      As Lynden had predicted, it didn't take him long at all to find where the southern continent representatives were staying. He was back the following day with their response to our letter. "The representatives have agreed to meet Chloe-Jane," he informed us. All of us were crowded around the dining room table, every inch of which was covered by maps and other miscellaneous diagrams. Well, all of us except for Chloe-Jane; my younger sister was still in her room.
      "That's great," Storm said enthusiastically. "When's the conference going to be? Where's it going to be?"
      "Three days from now," Lynden answered. "That's much sooner than I had anticipated-which is fine, but that means that Chloe-Jane and Cameren would have to leave tonight to reach the rendezvous location on time. I can mark it for you on a map."
      Storm furrowed his brow. "Is it just gonna be the two of them? It's dangerous outside, especially with the late king's guards searching for Chloe-Jane."
      Lynden looked at each of us gathered around the table in turn. "Even though I have faith in Cameren's ability to wield a sword-he trained with the army, after all-I'll follow them from afar. I know that Chloe-Jane would rather not travel in the company of vampires, so I'll make sure to keep out of sight."
      "Are you sure you want to act as the bodyguard, Lynden?" Edeline asked. "You've done quite a lot for us already. If you'd rather stay here at the house, I could follow Chloe-Jane to the conference instead."
      "This is the least I can do. Really."
      "Just because Phina turned out to be the queen of the vampires," I said softly, "you don't have to feel inclined to try and make it up to us."
      Lynden sighed, and his eyes were downcast again. "I know. This isn't entirely about Phina. I don't mind helping out. It's the right thing to do."
      A silence fell at the table, and after a while Cameren said, "I'll tell Chloe-Jane to get ready for our departure. I imagine she'll have some goodbyes to say."
       
~
       
      The next couple of days seemed to drag and fly by at the same time. Lynden, Chloe-Jane, and Cameren were gone from the house, and everything felt quieter than usual. Even Edeline had gone to prepare.
      I spent the majority of the days finalizing our plan with Clarity and Storm, who turned out to be very helpful contributors. Night finally arrived, and Storm bid Clarity and me goodnight. And in minutes, it was just Clarity and I sitting at the table in the dying candlelight.
      "Hey," I said softly.
      "Hey." Clarity turned to look at me. Even though we were both sitting at the same height, she still managed to look down her nose at me. But there didn't seem to be anything cold about the gesture anymore.
      "It's been a while since the two of us have been together like this."
      "I guess you're right," Clarity said shortly as she turned back to the various maps and the shelled nuts we were using as markers.
      "You came back because you said you were worried about me and the others."
      "I did."
      "I didn't realize you were so concerned about Storm and the vampires."
      "We've gone through a lot together," Clarity said simply. "Why shouldn't I care for them too?"
      I smiled faintly.
      There was a long silence before Clarity finally asked, "Do you really think Chloe-Jane can be the queen of this kingdom?"
      "She is the queen of this kingdom."
      Clarity just sighed tiredly. "You know what I mean, Corinna."
      I leaned back in my seat, stiff from sitting for the entire day. "I think she's capable. When it comes to the people of this kingdom, she has a good sense of right and wrong."
      "And you agree with her sense of right and wrong even after what she's said to you?"
      "What else could I have done? Right now, it's important that the people are given a ruler. Someone who can support them and lift them up. Someone who will help this kingdom thrive."
      "You really have a lot of confidence in Chloe, don't you."
      "I do. And I think you should too. She's grown up. I don't think we give her enough credit."
       
~
       
      To my pleasant surprise, Edeline returned the following morning, and Lynden two days after that. According to the latter, the conference went successfully, and Chloe-Jane had charmed the southern continent representatives. She had then gone back to the castle with Cameren and the representatives after claiming that Cameren had rescued her from her captors. She also claimed that the king was still alive and being held hostage somewhere in the capital city. Believing that King Volin was still alive, the people at the castle wouldn't lay a finger on Chloe-Jane in fear of what the king would do to them when he returned.
      Now it was early morning, and the sun was still hidden behind the dark horizon. I had gotten to work strapping an assortment of knives and daggers to my legs under my skirts. We would spend the daylight hours traveling to our chosen location and the night hours to get their inhabitants safely out of the capital city.
      "Are you ready?" Edeline asked from the other side of the room. She had just finished braiding back her inky hair and was now weighing different daggers in her palms. "We didn't exactly choose the easiest place to start."
      I let out a shaky laugh. "As long as we can get everyone out safely, that's what matters."
      "With Lynden and I there, the guards won't stand a chance. All you need to focus on is gaining the slaves' trust and helping them feel as at ease as possible."
      "I know. I'll do my best."
      Edeline walked over to me and pulled me into a reassuring hug. "After breaking into the castle, I think this should be simple."
      I just laughed as I returned the embrace. "Let's never break into a castle again, though, okay?"
      It was Edeline's turn to laugh. "If it means you won't have another near-death experience again, I'll be more than happy to avoid castles for the rest of my life."
       
~
       
      Edeline, Storm, Lynden, and I spent the last few daylight hours meandering through the town at the edge of the capital city as if we were mere tourists enjoying the sights. Back in the castle, Chloe-Jane had ordered that the knights be retracted from the streets, and we were now free to go wherever we pleased. Even though it was summer, the sky was overcast, and a heavy layer of clouds blocked the sun completely.
      Clarity was staying behind at the house. Just in case something happened to us, she'd be able to report back to Cameren and Chloe-Jane later. When the sun finally dropped from the sky, the four of us quickly made our way to our first target: the slave market.
      Even though there were a number of guards standing around the slave market, Edeline and Lynden, mere blurs against the night sky, knocked them out before they could even make a sound. With a swish of her dagger, Edeline severed the lock on the front door and pushed it open.
      I held my breath as we crept into the building beyond. My heart beat rapidly in my chest. Even though there weren't any new slaves being imported from the southern continent, there were quite a lot of slaves from the farms being reassigned to the city.
      I grimaced as we made our way through the empty entrance hall and into the large chamber beyond. A makeshift wooden stage sat in the middle of the room, and the windows along the walls were masked with metal bars.
      "There." Lynden pointed to a closed door on the opposite side of the room. "That's where the slaves are being kept."
      I looked over at Storm. "You know what to do."
      Storm nodded once, then turned on his heel and hurried out of the building.
      When he had disappeared from sight, Edeline, Lynden, and I made our way over to the doorway, and this time I used my own dagger to slice through the chain on the door. I pushed it open with one hand, then fumbled with the miniature lantern I had brought along. The seemingly endless stairway beyond the door was pitch black.
      After lighting the flame in my lantern, I took my first step onto the stone steps. The staircase didn't go quite as far down as I had initially thought and instead led to a large room beneath the main building.
      My heart pounded away in my chest as I slowly raised my lantern and let its fiery light illuminate the entirety of the room. At least fifty people sat against the stone walls, and their wide eyes reflected the light from my lantern. Besides the people inhabiting it, the stone room was completely empty. My heart clenched painfully.
      "Come with me," I called out. My voice echoed in the room, unshaken. "My friends and I are here to get all of you out of here."
      The slaves silently looked at each other before turning back to me and slowly climbing to their feet.
      I blinked. "You're all really going to follow me, just like that?"
      A woman only a few years older than me spoke up. Her voice was hoarse. "Why not? If it means that I can leave this awful place, I'll take my chances."
      The others nodded along in agreement.
      "Follow me," I said. "One of my other friends is outside right now distracting any knights and passersby. Once we're out, we'll travel through the forests until we get to the campsite. We've got food and water along the way. Right now, all you need to do is keep as quiet as possible."
      After the slaves nodded again, I turned and made my way back up the staircase to the main building. Edeline walked next to me while Lynden waited for the last of the slaves to make their way out to bring up the rear.
      When I arrived in the entrance hall, I carefully extinguished my lamp before pushing open the doors and beckoning everyone outside. I quickened my pace to a brisk walk.
      The commotion from some distance away disturbed the otherwise silent night. It looked like Storm had successfully drawn everyone's attention.
      We split into groups to better avoid any potential eyes, and I led my own group through the maze of alleyways I memorized like the back of my hand. When we regrouped at the main road, there were no people in sight, and we made quick work of hurrying out of the capital city. The lights of the buildings slowly faded the farther we got, and it was late enough that there was no one on the roads. We navigated into one of the smaller forests lining the main road about an hour later and continued our journey under the cover of the trees. When the sun began to rise in the morning, we deemed that we were far enough from the capital city to rest and give food and water to our party.
      It was about a week's journey or so on foot to the forest next to the farms, and even though I hadn't walked such a great distance on my wooden leg before, I was determined to make it. If all had gone according to plan, Storm should be back at the house and told Clarity that we escaped.
      As I stared up at the starless sky through the leaves and branches of the trees, I wondered if we'd really be able to pull this off-if we'd really be able to change this kingdom for the better. And as I looked around at the people sitting around, chatting in lowered voices, some even with hopeful expressions on their faces, I found myself thinking that maybe we really could.

Chapter Thirty
       
"Corinna," I whispered. "It's time to wake up."
      Corinna's eyelashes fluttered as her eyes blinked open.
      We had just finished leading the freed slaves to the forest next to the farms and were now on our way back to the capital city. We had spent a few days in the forest, making sure everyone had food and water and a place to sleep. Lynden had also stayed behind to keep an eye on the people for another day or so before rejoining us. Of the people we had just helped escape, a large number of them had eagerly stepped up to take responsibility for the campsite and ensure that everyone was taken care of.
      We decided that even though we were traveling through the forest, it would still be quicker and safer to make our journey under the cover of night. The nights were no longer cold, and I shook my head in amazement at how long ago winter felt.
      "Ready to go back?" Corinna looked over at me.
      I smiled. "Ready."
      When we reached the main road to the capital city, the two of us were able to waltz in without any problems. Due to Chloe-Jane's new orders, there was no one standing at the entrance.
      We had been gone from the capital city for over two weeks, but it almost felt as if time hadn't passed at all. Everything in the city had stayed the same in our absence-the buildings, the lights, the people, the sense of misery and despair beneath a facade of color and wealth. Even with Chloe-Jane now on the throne, we needed to be patient.
      The two of us silently continued on our way until we reached the house and hopped the fence into the backyard. I only had to knock once on the back door before it flew open.
      Storm stood in the doorway, outlined by the warm glow of the lights in the room beyond. "How did it go?" the dark-haired boy asked as he shut the door behind us. "Clarity and I kept worrying that all of you would encounter something unpleasant along the way, but the two of you seem unharmed." Then his eyes fell on all the daggers I had strapped to my arms and legs.
      "You can never be too prepared," I said stiffly.
      Storm folded his arms over his chest. "With that many knives, you'd probably scare Phina away even if she did want to go and talk to you."
      "Even with this many knives," I said lightly, "Phina would probably be able to kill me with her bare hands if she so desired."
      Storm sighed. "I don't doubt that. All I'm saying is that we should give her a chance."
      Corinna put a hand on Storm's shoulder. "We'll wait for her together. And when she returns, we can welcome her back with open arms."
      Storm's smile was genuine, and his eyes were bright.
       
~
       
      I sat cross-legged on the roof of the house, gazing up at the stars dancing in the sky. Despite the fact that I couldn't feel the bite of the cold, I pulled my cloak tighter around myself as the wind swept up my inky hair. It was my turn to keep watch.
      I frowned softly as the winds subsided and the night stilled. There was something that kept nagging at me. If I really was one of the queens from Andreus's prophecy, then I was to die before the end of the century. Being an immortal, the only cause of my death would be if I was killed. If I die, what will happen to Corinna? I thought. Will I die trying to protect her? Well, if that is how it will go down, I have no complaints.
      Chloe-Jane was one of the queens too. And Phina. Chloe-Jane would live out her normal human lifespan before the end of the century, but how would Phina, the queen of the vampires, die?
      The more I thought about it, the less sense it made. And aren't there supposed to be four queens in the prophecy? Why hasn't the fourth queen made an appearance yet? I'd have to ask Andreus the next time I saw him. Even during our first meeting with Andreus, I had gotten the impression that the dragon knew a lot more than he was letting on. Of course he wouldn't have told us that Phina was Karmen, for all of our sakes. But now that we knew, I wondered if he would be willing to tell us more.
      I stared up at the moon. This was the same continent as before. But it had gone through many changes throughout my long lifetime. Sometimes the changes were for the better, while others had made it a much darker place. If we hadn't stopped King Volin when we did, I was sure that the king would have sent the entire continent into another spiral of war and misery.
      I absently reached up to tuck a strand of my hair behind a delicately pointed ear. If I am destined to die, would I be dragging Corinna down with me? I couldn't say at this point. The only thing I was certain of was the growing possibility of our story ending in tragedy. And I hated it.
       
~
       
      Corinna and I lay on the floor of the forest house, hand in hand as we stared up at the ceiling. The light from the falling sun outside painted the curtains in a rose-colored glow and illuminated the lazy spirals of dust in the air.
      "Edeline," Corinna said after a while.
      I turned my head to look at her. "What is it?"
      Corinna rolled over onto her elbows to look at me. "Maybe this is a little sudden, but I want to spend the rest of my life with you-however long that is."
      "I feel the same way." Even though I was overjoyed by Corinna's words, I also felt a pang of sadness at the same time. Corinna knew that I might not have much time left-that she herself might not have much time either. "I have an idea," I said as I quickly sat up.
      "What's the idea?" Corinna tilted her head to the side curiously.
      "What if we get married? What if we have a wedding?"
      Corinna's eyes lit up. "A wedding? The two of us?"
      I nodded.
      "What normally happens when people get married?" Corinna sat up eagerly. "If there's a wedding, I know there's normally a big crowd of people there."
      "And fancy outfits," I added.
      "And fancy outfits," she agreed. "It's just the two of us here, though-we don't need a big crowd of people."
      "You're right. We probably don't need fancy outfits either."
      "You won't wear that ball gown again?"
      "I see how it is-you just wanted to see that dress again!"
      Corinna was laughing now. "Come on, Edeline. You know there's more to it than that!" The two of us collapsed onto the floor in a heap of giggles.
      "Jokes aside, we could definitely bring out the dress," I said as I looked over at her with a smile. "Are you sure you don't want to wear it this time?"
      "How could I wear it?" Corinna propped herself back up on an elbow. "You look beautiful in it."
      "What will you wear, then?"
      "Doesn't Her Majesty have an entire collection of dresses in her closet?"
      I blinked. "You're right-I do. Come on, let's go find you something just as beautiful." I jumped to my feet, helped Corinna stand up, and then the two of us made our way over to my bedroom, hand in hand. I pushed open the closet door and stepped aside to let Corinna take a look at the numerous dresses inside.
      Corinna pulled out the midnight ball gown, and the tiny silver stars shimmered just as brightly as ever over their sea of tulle fabric. "This one's for you."
      As I set the dress aside, I looked over to watch Corinna take a golden evening gown from the closet. "You would look beautiful in that one," I said softly.
      Corinna smiled radiantly as she held the dress to her body. "Would you mind helping me? This will be the second gown I've ever worn."
      Before long, the last of the sunlight had faded and was replaced by a cloudless and star-flecked night. I had just finished lacing up the back of Corinna's dress, and now I met her gaze in the mirror.
      Corinna's eyes were sparkling as she looked on in awe at the way the golden fabric flowed around her.
      "I like helping you try on beautiful dresses," I said with a smile. "Wouldn't it be wonderful if this could be us every day?"
      "You should put on your own gown," Corinna encouraged giddily.
      Just as I made to turn away from the mirror, I paused as I noticed my own reflection. It was the same face I had worn and looked at for years, but something seemed different this time.
      There was light in my eyes. A smile on my face.
      I looked alive.
      
~

      Once I changed into my own gown, the two of us found ourselves in front of the mirror again.
      "What do we think?" Corinna asked as we stared at our reflections.
      The corners of my lips tugged upward in a smile. "I think it's perfect."
      Corinna finally tore her gaze from the mirror. "How about I go set up some candles outside? We'll have our own little ceremony with just the two of us." Corinna took me by the hands, and the two of us made our way out of the room.
      It didn't take us long to set up a small table and candles outside. Now standing next to each other under the open sky, we looked at each other. "Now what happens?" Corinna asked.
      "Now what happens?" I repeated. "I think people normally say vows."
      Corinna nodded along. "Okay. I'll admit that I don't have anything prepared. I'll be improvising. But that's the fun of it, right?" She took my hands in her own. "Edeline, ever since I met you, you've always been there for me. You're my closest friend. I want to continue spending time with you. When I'm with you, I feel like I can be myself. You always push me to be the best version of myself, and I'm grateful for that. Whatever hardships we might meet in the future, I promise that we'll face them together."
      I just stood there smiling with a giddy sort of happiness as I tried my best to gather my thoughts. "Corinna, you're the first person in years to accept me as I am-a monster with a human heart. You're brilliant and beautiful and kind-I couldn't ask for a better friend. I've treasured all the time we've spent together. I'm so happy to have lived this long, and I would do it all again if it meant that this day could happen. In this dark world of night, you've shown me that there's still light. You are my light, Corinna."
      Corinna's radiant smile was the most beautiful thing in the world, and she pressed her forehead against mine. "I love you," she breathed.
      "I love you." I smiled, closing my eyes for a brief moment as if I could stay in the moment forever.
      Corinna pulled me into a hug. "Thank you, Edeline."
      After what could have been minutes or hours, I finally brought myself to draw away. "I know we've got no music, but may I have this dance?"
      "Dance?" Corinna's eyes lit up. "I'd love to dance!"
      I laughed as Corinna and I began to dance to a silent rhythm. Our bare feet flew over the grass and our dresses swished around our legs. I felt lighter than I had ever felt before. We spun in circles until we grew too dizzy to stand properly, then collapsed onto the grass in a heap of skirts, giggling as we stared up at the sky.
      "This reminds me of the ball," Corinna remarked when she caught her breath. "The two of us danced together there too."
      "It really does. Except our garden here is a lot less extravagant than the one at the archduke's estate."
      Corinna laughed as she turned her head to look at me. "We don't need extravagant things. All we need is what is here in front of us."
      I met her gaze with a smile. "You're right. I couldn't ask for anything more." Then I looked back up at the stars. "It's a beautiful night."
      "It is," Corinna agreed. "The night sky never fails to remind me that there are still beautiful things in the world. There's a whole world out there, Edeline. Once, I never even thought I'd get the chance to see even this much of it. In only a matter of months, I've been as high as the mountains and even seen the ocean."
      "Someday we'll travel the oceans too," I said determinedly. "We could go anywhere you'd like. We could go everywhere. And when we've seen it all, we'll have a home for us to return to."
      "I'd love that." I could hear the smile in Corinna's voice. "But until then, I'll keep doing my best."
      I let out a soft sigh. "Me too."
      The two of us stayed outside for a while after that, chatting quietly until the candles burned out. Corinna fell asleep, and the moonlight painted her golden dress in a shade of silvery blue.
      I closed my eyes as well, listening to the soft wind rustling through the grass, the bubbling of the nearby creek, the steady rhythm of Corinna's heartbeat. Everything was peaceful.
       
~
       
      The next day, Corinna and I visited Clarity, Storm, and Lynden at the house in the city. The latter had just returned from the forest next to the farms and, to our relief, brought with us the good news that everything was going well.
      "Look, look!" Storm said excitedly as he waved us all over to the dining room table. "I've got a letter from Cameren!"
      "You've got a letter?" Clarity turned to Storm. "Since when did you have a letter?"
      "Since I went out this morning."
      "You've been holding onto that letter all morning?" Lynden arched a brow. "What if it's urgent?"
      "I just thought we should wait for Corinna and Edeline to arrive before we opened it," Storm said uncomfortably, eyeing Corinna's sister as if she would snatch the letter from him at any moment.
      "Well?" Clarity asked coolly. "What are you waiting for? We're all here now."
      "Okay, okay, okay." Storm frowned as he pulled the letter from its envelope. He quickly unfolded the paper and cleared his throat to read aloud: "Dear friends, as you've already heard, the conference with the representatives from the southern continent was a success. Chloe-Jane was brilliant. She played the role of a sad queen worrying about her husband and kingdom very well. The representatives are here in the castle with us, and they are planning to depart back to their own country in three days' time.
      "Corinna was right. Once Chloe-Jane told the castle staff that King Volin was still alive, they were sure to keep their distance from her. Right now, Chloe and I are working on figuring out who at the castle knew about the king's plans for the future and who might have been involved in them. We have already changed the knights and replaced them with people who we can trust. Even if they will need some time to warm up to Chloe herself, they are willing to pledge their allegiance to the kingdom in the name of protecting the people they care about.
      "Chloe-Jane has appointed me as the temporary captain of the knights. While I don't think I'm qualified, we still haven't found anyone suitable yet for the position. Now that the situation at the castle has been stabilized, Chloe-Jane wants to make her first proclamation as queen and set all the slaves working on the farms free.
      "I will continue to update you as our situation changes. Just in case Chloe's proclamation is ignored, you should start thinking of an alternative way to get the slaves to freedom. Do not bother sending a response at this time. It's too risky. Stay safe. Yours, Cameren." Storm gingerly set the letter down on the table. "See? It wasn't all that urgent."
      "Urgent?" Clarity stared at Storm as if he had completely missed the point. "Maybe it wasn't urgent, but did you hear what Cameren wants us to do?" She whirled around to look at Corinna. "If Chloe-Jane's proclamation falls on deaf ears, Cameren wants you to liberate the slaves from the farms yourself!"

Chapter Thirty-One
       
"Do you think we can do it, Corinna?" Clarity looked at me apprehensively. "You really think two humans and two vampires will be able to get the hundreds of slaves out of there?"
      "I think we can," I said determinedly. "And even if it's a very small chance, we've still got to try, don't we? Also, two humans? Are you not counting yourself, Clarity?"
      "What could I even do to help out?" Clarity asked stiffly. "I'll just slow you down."
      "I think freeing the slaves is less about escorting them off of the farms all at once," Edeline started slowly, "and more about taking the overseers away."
      "You mean kill them?" Storm turned to Edeline in alarm. "Can't we just drag them off and lock them up somewhere?"
      "If you don't want to kill them yourself," Lynden said flatly, "that's fine. I'm sure Edeline and I won't have any problem doing so. They've hurt so many people. Death is too light of a penalty for what they've done."
      I turned to look at Edeline. "Would you really kill them?"
      Edeline held my gaze. "It would be your call, Corinna. Yes, I've killed overseers in the past. It's not exactly like they're innocent." I momentarily flashed back to that first night in the forest where the two of us had been chased through the trees. Edeline was right. But if we didn't have to kill them, I'd rather not add to all the death, pain, and blood.
      Storm looked back and forth between us. "But they're still humans, aren't they?"
      "And does that make them any less guilty?" Lynden countered.
      Storm fell silent at that.
      I spoke up in an attempt to reduce the tension. "Even if they aren't innocent, I have to agree with Storm. I don't think we should go out of our way to kill them. But if we're in a situation where we have to fight for our lives . . ."
      Edeline nodded at my unspoken words hanging in the air. "We'll do things your way."
      "Corinna," Storm said suddenly. "You still remember the layout of the farm you were on, right? I don't know if all three farms were designed the same way, but if they were, do you know if there's some kind of building that could fit a lot of people? We could lock all the overseers up and give the slaves a chance to run."
      "There is a place like that," I recalled. "I think this could work."
      Storm clapped his hands together. "Now we have a plan."
      Lynden frowned. "It sounds like you're planning to round up all of those overseers yourself."
      "Of course not!" Storm blinked. "Aren't you all going to help?"
      "I still think it would be better if we just killed all of the overseers," Lynden said darkly. "But we'll do it your way."
       
~
       
      The next few days dragged into weeks. The peak of summer was officially upon us, and the capital city had become considerably warmer. I couldn't say that I missed the snow, but the heat was becoming more and more stifling. We were sitting around the living room with all of the windows open to prevent us from being baked alive, when suddenly there was the sound of knocking at the door.
      Storm's hand went immediately to the sword hanging at his side as he eyed the door suspiciously. "Who's there?"
      "It's me," a familiar voice called. "Cameren."
      Storm quickly pulled the door open. We all looked up in surprise at my brother, dressed in a castle knight's uniform. He pulled off his helmet as he crossed the threshold.
      "Cameren"-I hurried over to him-"aren't you supposed to be in the castle with Chloe-Jane?"
      "Chloe told me to go back and help you," Cameren said as if he still couldn't believe it himself. "I don't know why she was so adamant to get me out of the castle. She seems to have everything under her control now for the most part, but this decision still feels too soon."
      "You couldn't convince her to let you stay?" Clarity asked, clearly just as stunned as the rest of us.
      Cameren shook his head in defeat. "I tried, but she begged me to go back. She said that she was worried about her sisters and wouldn't be able to think properly until she knew that I was there to help keep them safe."
      I blinked. "Chloe-Jane said that?"
      "And you believed her?" Clarity's brows rose even higher. "Even if she is that worried about us, would she really be so worried that she can't do her work?"
      "I know it was an excuse to get me out of the castle," Cameren said with a slight frown. "But the thing I don't quite understand is why she wanted me to leave so badly."
      I looked up at my brother. "She most likely did it to protect you. But protect you from what?"
      Cameren just shook his head tiredly.
      "I'll go outside and see what's happening with the news of Chloe-Jane's proclamation," Storm announced. "I'm the best person to do it anyway."
      "You're the only person," Clarity corrected, but Storm ignored her and left.
      "Either Chloe-Jane got you out of the castle to protect you," I continued after the door swung shut behind Storm, "or she's planning to do something you as her older brother won't approve of."
      "She wouldn't, would she?" Edeline asked hesitantly.
      I just sighed. "I don't know. All she needs to do right now is gain the public's support and set the slaves free. I don't see how we would disapprove of either of those things. But when it comes to the people, I have faith that she'll do the right thing."
      "All we can do now is wait and see what happens," Lynden said grimly.
      Despite practically being cooked alive in the house, I suddenly felt a cold shiver run down my spine. Something felt off. Was it a mistake to trust Chloe-Jane with such an important task? I wondered. After all, she's only fourteen. No, I can't start doubting myself now-can't start doubting my sister now.
      Time seemed almost to stop as we waited around in the living room. I fanned myself with a hand. The sun reached its zenith, and the temperature was at an all-time high. Edeline had found a paper fan upstairs and was doing her best to try and cool me down with it, but we had given it up quickly when I deemed that blowing hot air around the room wasn't any good.
      After what felt like an eternity of waiting, we heard footsteps outside, then the sound of Storm opening and closing the door.
      "How did it go?" I asked.
      Storm brushed his dark hair out of his face. "Surprisingly enough, quite a few people wanted to hear what the new queen had to say. There wasn't as much of an uproar as I first expected either. But maybe that's just because the people who don't care for Chloe-Jane either decided to stay in their homes and out of the sun, or the heat stripped them of their will to make a scene."
      "Either way," Edeline noted, "that's good news for us and Chloe-Jane."
      "I'll go out once it gets dark and see what I can find as well," Lynden said with a slight frown. "Summer is the most inconvenient time for vampires to be in an environment like this."
      
~
       
      The night didn't fall soon enough. We had all moved from the house in the city to the house in the forest once it got dark. We determined that in the heat of the summer, the neighbors weren't very likely to try and break in. At least the forest house had the small stream bubbling through the clearing. I lay in the grass next to Edeline, relishing the coolness of the night breeze. Clarity, Storm, and Cameren were close by, talking in lowered voices.
      We didn't have to wait more than a couple of hours before Lynden returned. I quickly sat up, opening my mouth to speak, but Storm beat me to it. "Well?" he asked expectantly. "How's it looking?"
      "Most of the townsfolk don't seem to care about whether Chloe-Jane is setting the slaves free or not," Lynden informed us as he lowered the hood of his cloak. "It doesn't affect them, so why should they care in the first place? The ones benefiting from the slave labor the most are those who are already very wealthy. And that isn't a whole lot of people. Apparently the overseers are furious, though. I think they've been enjoying their job a little too much," he concluded in disgust. "They're refusing to give it up."
      Edeline sat up and picked bits of grass out of my hair. "It looks like we'll have to go in there and clean things up in the name of the queen. It's a good thing we have a plan just in case something like this happens."
      Lynden scoffed. "We all knew this would happen. The overseers aren't going to give up that easily."
      I stood up and brushed grass from my skirts. "Let's all get a good night's sleep. Tomorrow we'll pack what we need and make our way down to the farms."
       
~
       
      As our good fortune had it, the heatwave had completely passed when I woke up in the morning. Once we had packed everything we needed-most of which was food and weapons-Storm helped us rent horses from the stables, and we were on our way. Clarity had come along with us to the forest because if any of us happened to get injured, she'd be close by to help out with what she had learned from her medical books.
      We arrived at our target a few days later, and soon it was time to act.
      Dressed completely in black so as to blend in with the night, Edeline, Lynden, Storm, Cameren, and I snuck out of the forest with our blades rustling softly at our sides. The sky was cloudy, and the moon was completely hidden-which would work in our favor.
      We zigzagged past the overseers on the night watch and made our way further into the first farm. None of us could say for sure how long it would take to trap all of the overseers in the storage room we had chosen, but if it went quickly, we'd move on to the second farm and take out the overseers there too. If things went slowly, though, we'd have to stick with one farm per night.
      "Alright," I whispered when we stopped outside the residence of the master overseer. "I'm still hoping we'll be able to talk things out." Standing there in the silence of the night, I looked to Storm.
      Storm nodded, then pulled out a torch and quickly lit it. The flame blossomed quickly, and its fiery light cut through the night as it illuminated our faces. "Hey!" Storm yelled, waving his torch above his head. "Open up in the name of the queen!"
      It didn't take long for a ring of overseers to circle around us. All of them had their swords drawn.
      "Where's your head overseer?" Storm demanded as he looked around the circle. "We're here to tell him that he needs to let all of the slaves here go. Or else!"
      The overseers circling us looked at each other before bursting out in a fit of guffaws.
      "Or else what?" one of the overseers laughed unpleasantly. "You'll attack us?"
      "So this is who that good-for-nothing queen sends," a deep voice sounded. We all turned to watch as the front doors of the master's house were pushed open. A man stood in the doorway, but he made no move to walk down the stairs and join us. He was smiling a smile that didn't quite reach his eyes as he stared down at us. "A couple of girls, a pair of teenagers, and a kid. Oh yes, I'm very afraid."
      "I think there must be something wrong with your eyesight," Storm called up the steps. "What you're looking at here are five very capable people. So, are you going to let the slaves go?"
      The head overseer burst into laughter. "Me? Let the slaves go? Ridiculous! Ever since the new king took over, I thought he would make things even better than before! He seemed to have plans for the slaves, but I lost all faith in that boy once he decided to take that slave girl as his bride. And now look what happened! Now they want to set the slaves free!"
      "So?" Storm asked impatiently. "Are you going to do it or not?"
      The head overseer's smile was more of a sneer at this point as he turned to make his way back inside. "Men, capture these idiots for me, will you? We can't have them running around, spewing their nonsense to the slaves."
      As the circle of overseers drew tighter around us, one of them suddenly rushed forward with his arms extended, trying to grab Edeline. In a flash of movement, Edeline sidestepped him, sending him staggering backward into his companions.
      At the commotion, the head overseer whirled around with shock painted over his features. "You-" he sputtered, pointing wildly at Edeline. "You dare fight back? Capture them! Capture all of them now! I want them alive!"
      The overseers rushed in with a loud cry. I tightened my grip on my daggers. They were still in their sheaths as I raised them in front of me. All of us were going to be using sheathed weapons, especially Edeline and Lynden. We just needed to knock the overseers out. If we ended up killing or seriously injuring any of them, it would reflect badly on Chloe-Jane.
      There was a crash of metal against metal as I threw my arms up to meet the first overseer's sword. In a swift movement, I kicked out at him with my wooden leg. As he stumbled backward, I leaped forward to strike him hard over the head with the hilt of my dagger, and he collapsed to the ground, unconscious.
      Storm, Cameren, and I were doing a decent job fending off the overseers as they continued to make desperate grabs for us. Edeline and Lynden, on the other hand, were on a completely different level-the two of them were a whirlwind of darkness and metal as they knocked out overseers left, right, and center.
      Soon there was a pile of overseers lying around our feet. All of them either unconscious or grumbling angrily under their breath as they clutched at their heads.
      "You-" the head overseer stammered as he watched in horror from the top of the stairs. "Just who exactly are you people?"
      In another flash, Edeline had leaped up to land behind the head overseer. "Don't move," Edeline warned him quietly as his hand hovered on the hilt of his sword. "You're about to join your friends in a moment."
      The head overseer stared at Edeline. "You're a witch, aren't you!"
      "Oh?" Edeline smiled wryly. "Incorrect. I'm no witch-I'm a vampire."
      Even in the dark, I could see the color drain from the head overseer's face. Edeline just gave a glinting, fanged smile, then slammed her fist into the man's head.
      "I'll go look for any other overseers hanging around the area," Lynden said before vanishing into the night in a rush of wind.
      I frowned slightly as I glanced around at the bodies lying at our feet. "There's got to be at least forty of them here. The rest of them should be scattered around the farm, and Lynden should easily be able to pick them off one by one. And now . . . well, it looks like we'll have to take all of these bodies into the storage room ourselves."
      I gingerly knelt down and grabbed the arms of one of the unconscious overseers. But with the weight of all his armor, all I could do was slowly drag him across the ground inch by inch. I dropped the man and staggered back, panting-this was not going to work.
      "Here," Edeline said softly as she appeared at my side. She hosted up the overseer's body with ease. "Let me do this."
      Meanwhile I could hear Storm and Cameren try their best to carry one of the bodies between the two of them. "One, two, three, lift!"
      "The storage room is at least a ten-minute walk from here," I remarked as I rolled up my sleeves. "I think I got ahead of myself. I didn't account for how long we'd be dragging bodies around."
      "What are you doing?" a voice asked mildly.
      I turned to find that a group of slaves had appeared, lurking just outside the lights pouring from the windows of the overseers' residences. They were all watching us curiously as they surveyed the scene in front of them.
      "We heard fighting," another slave spoke up quietly. "Is it true that the queen wants to set us free?"
      "It's true," I said. "We're here in the name of the queen to make sure you get the freedom you deserve."
      The slave eyed the unconscious overseers. "Are they dead?"
      I shook my head. "They're just knocked out. We're going to transport them to the storage room and lock them in there until they decide to listen to Her Majesty's orders."
      "That's a lot of bodies for four people to move. Would you care for some help?"
      "Help?" I broke into a smile. "That would be wonderful."
      With their help, it didn't take more than an hour to transport all of the overseers to the storage room. Before we put them inside, we confiscated all of their weapons, armor, and anything else they could potentially use to force their way out.
      "Couldn't we have found a better place to lock them up?" Storm huffed as he helped me toss the last of the bodies into the large building. "They won't suffer a bit here! They've got food too!"
      "What?" I gave him a sideways look. "Did you think we were going to cram them all into a cupboard? We're trying to keep them alive, remember?"
      "Sunrise isn't too far off," Lynden informed us as we all backed out of the storage room. "We'll have to wait until tomorrow night to tackle the next farm."
      I turned to the slaves. "You're free now. The queen has issued a proclamation, and if the overseers say otherwise, they're defying the queen herself. Right now in the forest, there's a number of former slaves like yourself hiding out. They'll happily welcome all of you if you want to join them. You're free now. You can do anything you want-go anywhere you please. I will say, though, that you might want to avoid the capital city, at least for now. The people there tend not to be very welcoming."
      "Thank you." The freed slaves nodded in unison, and I smiled softly as I watched the hope rekindle in their eyes.
       
~
       
      The following night was just about the same as the first. We snuck into the residential area of the farm, and Storm used his torch to draw the attention of the overseers. I could have sworn that the head overseer on this farm was the same as the one from the night before from how he first laughed us off and then panicked when he realized we were serious. We made quick work of knocking out all of the overseers and then spent the rest of the night dragging them to the storage room.
      The next day was upon us in no time, and I clutched my daggers tightly as we snuck into the third and final farm. This was the place I had been born in, suffered in, and finally escaped from. Now I was back to grant those who had suffered beside me a chance at a proper life.
      We had to be especially careful this time; the overseers here probably knew what had happened to their neighboring farms by now and planned accordingly.
      The residential area of the farm was eerily quiet as we crept up to the house of the head overseer. I shivered slightly as I passed one familiar location after another. None of these places incited good memories.
      When we reached the house of the head overseer, Storm lifted his torch again. "Open the door!" Storm said loudly. "It's time for us to beat you up!"
      The five of us continued to wait outside the house. We waited, and waited, and waited, but no one came out. None of the overseers had made an appearance either.
      "Edeline," I said softly. "Do you sense anyone around?"
      Edeline shook her head, frowning. "I can sense people around-hundreds of people. But with so many human presences, I can't distinguish between the slaves and overseers."
      I felt my heart sink. "Hostages," I breathed.
      "What?" Storm whirled to face me.
      "Hostages," I repeated. "The overseers know what we've been doing. They're using the slaves against us."
      "That's right," a sneering voice called from the shadows. I spun around and spotted an overseer standing between the buildings. His sword was pressed against the neck of an elderly man. The elderly man's eyes were wide and frightened, but the overseer had a smile on his face.
      "What's the meaning of this?" Storm demanded angrily, even though panic had flashed across his face.
      The overseer smirked. "So it's true. I heard that a group of strange people working for the queen would show up and try to take away our workers. How could I let that happen? It's a good thing we came up with a plan."
      A line of overseers stepped out of the shadows behind the first, and all of them held either an elder or a child at blade point.
      I just stared at them. The sinking feeling in my chest was so painful that it was difficult to breathe. But before I could think of anything to do, the night suddenly became alive with the sound of footsteps, and the bellowing of voices filled the air as a crowd of armored overseers charged out of the shadows behind us. The hostages had just been a distraction.
      I quickly exchanged a glance with Edeline. Can you get them away from the overseers safely?
      Edeline's nod was the slightest dip of her head before she sprung into the air.
      I whirled around to face the mad rush of overseers, daggers in hand. The overseers were upon us instantly, swinging their swords wildly. As I dodged and ducked, my heart began to race.
      There were so many of them. Metal crashed against metal, and my arms shook as I blocked a swipe at my head from one of the overseer's blades. Storm, Lynden, Cameren, and Edeline had vanished from sight, surrounded by a mass of overseers. As I kicked at another charging overseer, all I could do was hope that they were okay.
      While I was trying my best not to fatally injure any of my attackers, the overseers had the intention to kill. I needed to draw my daggers from their sheaths. But now even if I wanted to, there was no opportunity to do so. My ears were ringing, and my veins were flowing with adrenaline. I was a whirlwind of steel. I was moving fast, but not fast enough.
      I didn't see the blade coming at me before it was too late.
      Just as the sword scraped my neck, a slender hand closed around my arm and pulled me into the sky. "Thank you," I managed to gasp out, "Ede-" But I broke off as I looked at my savior.
      My eyes widened as her ginger hair blazed like fire in the flickering light of the surrounding torches. My savior wasn't Edeline. It was Phina.

Chapter Thirty-Two
       
I stared in horror at the scene playing out in front of me. Corinna was surrounded by a throng of overseers, and her movements were becoming slower and slower each time one of the overseers managed to nick her with his blade.
      I was too far away, fighting off my own hoard of overseers. I had managed to force them to release their hostages, but as they ran at me all at once, I knew with rising panic that I wouldn't be able to reach Corinna in time.
      Just as I opened my mouth with the words watch out on the tip of my tongue, a rush of flame flashed through the air and swept Corinna away. I blinked in shock as I watched the ginger-haired figure land outside the ring of fighting and set Corinna carefully on the ground.
      Phina had returned.
      I was sure that Corinna's expression was an exact mirror of my own as she stared at Phina. The ginger-haired vampire's face was impassive, and her eyes were blank as she turned back to the overseers. Everyone seemed to stop what they were doing as Phina sprung into the fray. She whirled among the overseers and tore into them with her bare hands.
      "Monster!" the overseers shrieked when they realized what was happening to their companions. "It's a monster! Run!" The overseers standing around me shoved their hostages to the ground, dropped their swords in their panic, and scrambled away as fast as they could.
      But Phina was too fast, and before the overseers could even make it past the buildings, they fell over one by one before they even had time to scream.
      Storm, Lynden, and Cameren had frozen, with their mouths open in shock. Snapping out of my own frozen state, I hurried over to Corinna. "Are you okay?"
      Corinna nodded in a daze as she clung to my arm. "I'm fine." She absently reached up to touch her neck where the overseer's sword had scraped her throat. Even though it was bleeding, it wasn't anything serious. "Phina . . . Phina saved me."
      I turned back to watch the ginger-haired vampire flash through the fleeing overseers, spraying blood in her wake. "Phina!"
      "Phina!" Lynden's alarmed voice cut through the night. "Stop! You're scaring them."
      Phina halted, and her blood-red irises glowed through the darkness as she slowly turned to look at us over her shoulder. She was holding an overseer by the neck, who was whimpering feebly in her iron grasp. "Who?" she asked. Her voice was quiet.
      "Them." Lynden gestured to the slaves, who were staring at Phina in horror. Some of them had their hands pressed over their mouths as they backed away from her. "Us," Lynden added quietly. "You're scaring us."
      Storm had dropped to his knees, and his face was pale as he stared out over the sea of dead overseers, all of whom were splattered with and lying in pools of their own blood. Cameren knelt down to put a reassuring hand on the dark-haired boy's shoulder.
      Corinna had gone pallid as well. I took her hand and twined my fingers through hers before looking over at Phina. "We said we weren't going to kill them. Now how do we explain this?"
      "You didn't kill them," Phina said shortly. She tossed aside the overseer she was holding, and the overseer crawled away from the ginger-haired vampire, gasping for air. "I'm the one who killed them."
      "Phina." Storm looked up at Phina as if he still couldn't believe who was standing in front of us. "You're back."
      "I've been with you these last couple of weeks," Phina said softly. "No matter where I went, I'd always come back to you in the end. I planned to protect all of you from afar, but that changed when I had to make an appearance tonight."
      Storm continued to stare at Phina. "If you've been watching us, didn't you know that we would have welcomed you back with open arms?"
      "I did." Phina's hair was caked with blood as it waved in the cool night breeze. "I knew all of you would let me back in. But it was me who wasn't ready to face you. I know. What a pathetic queen of the vampires I am. Just pretend you never saw me here-"
      "Wait!" Storm jumped to his feet. "Don't leave!"
      Cameren's hand tightened on Storm's shoulder, but Storm shook him off as he sprinted toward Phina.
      "What are you doing?" Phina took a panicked step back before throwing out a hand in a gesture signaling him to halt. Her eyes widened as she saw her hand and the blood that dripped off of it.
      Storm reached Phina in seconds and threw his arms around her in a hug. Storm held Phina tightly. "Please come back with us. We miss you. None of us care if you're the queen of the vampires. You're our friend."
      Phina had frozen; her eyes were large as she looked out at us from over Storm's shoulder. Her hands moved ever so slightly as she made to return the embrace, but she stopped when she seemed to remember that they were caked in blood. She let them fall limply to her sides instead. Phina smiled weakly. "Okay."
      Storm finally drew away with an elated smile on his face. "The sun will rise soon. We should finish up here quickly."
      I looked back at the bodies of the overseers as we made our way toward the forest. "I assume you don't just want to leave them here," I said to Corinna.
      She nodded. "Tomorrow night I'll do my best to move them and bury them properly."
      I gave her hand a squeeze. "I'll help you."
      Corinna turned to address the slaves hiding in the shadows. "All of you are free now. Things weren't supposed to go this way, but now that they did, you have no more masters. We've got an entire camp set up in the forest, and all of you are welcome to stay there until you decide you want to find another safe place to go." Corinna exchanged a glance with me. "I'll show you the way."
      After I watched Corinna walk over to the group and lead them in the direction of the forest, I made my way over to Phina and Storm. Lynden and Cameren had come over as well, and the former walked over to stand next to Phina.
      "Come on," Lynden said quietly. "We should get you cleaned up."
      "Oh." Phina looked down at her bloody clothes and splattered skin. "Right."
       
~
       
      Corinna, Cameren, and Storm slept for the entire day. It seemed like their exhaustion had finally caught up to them.
      Lynden and I helped out around the campsite wherever we could while Phina, on the other hand, isolated herself somewhere far from the others. After the events of the previous night, she had determined that it would probably be best for her to stay out of sight.
      Clarity seemed to be the least fazed out of all of us upon hearing the news of Phina's return. She just shrugged and said something along the lines of "since she wanted to come back, I guess she's back."
      When night fell, Corinna found me, and we made our way back onto the farm to clean up the bodies.
      "I didn't mean for any of them to die," Corinna said quietly as she dragged one of the bodies over to the grave we had dug. "I'm not sure how I'm supposed to feel. Should I be glad that the overseers got what was coming to them? Or sad that we've just contributed to all the pain and death in this world?"
      "Which one do you feel?" I asked as I laid another body in the grave.
      "Both," Corinna answered softly.
      "It isn't wrong to feel the way you do," a voice said. There was a flash of orange flame against the night as Phina appeared. "It's what it means to feel human. They wouldn't think twice about killing you. And yet you still mourn for them."
      Corinna sighed as she turned to meet Phina's gaze. "No one should hold that much hatred in their heart. All I can do is be the better person. Once we stoop to their level, we're no better than they are."
      Phina's voice was soft as she bent down to help carry another body into the grave. "You're a good person, Corinna."
      I looked over at Phina. "Do you regret killing them?"
      "No." Phina let out a humorless laugh. "Unlike the two of you, I'm not a good person. I'll admit it. Once, I fought on a bloodstained battlefield and lost everything there. Now that I finally have people I care about again-people I want to protect-I will do whatever it takes to make sure that no harm ever comes to them."
      "I think you are a good person, Phina-" Corinna started, but Phina cut her off.
      "Could we just leave it here for tonight, please?"
      "Alright. If you don't want to talk, we won't pressure you."
      "Thank you," Phina said quietly. "I know I owe you all an explanation, and I'll try my best to deliver one eventually. I just . . . can't. At least not right now."
      "You don't need to tell us anything if you don't want to," I said as I wiped the dirt from my hands onto my trousers. "We're just really glad you're back."
      "On the way back to the house in the capital city . . ." Phina dropped her gaze. "On the way back to the house, you should all keep an eye on me. If you don't, I think I might run away."
      Corinna dragged another body over. "Okay, we'll keep an eye on you. But if you really want to leave, we won't stop you either."
      Phina nodded, and the three of us transported the rest of the bodies in silence.
       
~
       
      A few weeks later, we all returned to the city house.
      Even though we all tried our best to act as if nothing had changed, Phina was distant and quiet. The moment we returned to the house, Phina went straight to the cellar and had yet to come out. We left the ginger-haired vampire there in the hopes that she'd come out when she was ready to talk to us, but when she didn't emerge from the cellar after a week, we all started to worry.
      "I think we should go check on her," Storm said uneasily as we all sat around the dining room table. "I get the feeling that she's just punishing herself by staying down there."
      "Maybe she just wants some time alone," Clarity said shortly.
      "Edeline," Storm said quietly. "You should go talk to her."
      I blinked. "Me?"
      Corinna put a hand on my arm. "Let's all go talk to her. Come on." Corinna led me to the trap door. Once everyone gathered around it, she crouched down to gently knock on the wood. "Phina, we're coming in."
      Even though I could see inside with my enhanced vision, it was clear that the cellar was pitch black to the human eye; Corinna, Clarity, and Storm strained to see anything as they climbed down the ladder. Cameren had decided to stay in the dining room so we could talk things out between ourselves.
      Phina was lying in the corner of the room. Her ginger hair spilled over the stones, but something about its usual flame was missing.
      "Phina," Lynden said. His tone was uncharacteristically gentle.
      Phina's voice was no louder than a whisper. "Don't come over here. I don't want to hurt any of you."
      "You won't hurt us," Storm said confidently, still trying to pinpoint Phina's exact location in the cellar.
      "Are you sure about that?" Phina slowly raised herself up into a sitting position. Her eyes were lifeless. "Have you forgotten who you're looking at? This is Karmen, the queen of the vampires."
      "But what about Phina?" Corinna asked.
      "There is no Phina." Phina stared blankly at the ground in front of her. "Phina is just a fragment of my imagination. She's the person I wished I could have been. Phina and Karmen-both of them are me . . . but at the same time, neither of them is who I truly am. I've lived for so many years that I no longer know who I am. I've long forgotten my name and everything I had once been."
      I took a step forward. "Phina-"
      "Don't come over here!" Phina repeated. A hint of panic crept into her voice as she backed up against the wall. "You should stay away from me. All of you. It's-it's for your own good."
      Clarity looked down at Phina. "There's one thing I don't understand. You've been killing vampires. Why?"
      "Vampires started out as a curse," Phina whispered. "The first progenitor started out as a human. He was vain, self-absorbed, and clever. A little bit too clever. He began experimenting with ancient, forgotten magic. He figured out a way to live forever, to survive off the blood of others while hiding in the shadows of the night. In his desperate craze to live forever-to stay eternally young and youthful-the first progenitor didn't hesitate to curse himself. He cursed his very blood. It didn't take him long to figure out that whoever drank his blood would be possessed with the same curse. At the time, what the first progenitor wanted was a group of beautiful girls to accompany him. And I was unfortunate enough to be one of those girls he had his sights set on.
      "The night I killed the first progenitor was the night I truly opened my eyes to the world around me. What a wretched world we live in. Vampires and humans are one of the same kinds of cruel monsters-the only kind of creatures that hurts their own kin. The vampires needed to die first. Then the humans. I thought they both needed to die. Just a couple of weeks ago, I tracked down the last of the vampires and killed them." Phina slowly raised her gaze to Lynden and me. "We're the only ones left."
      "You-you," Storm started, his face pale. "You wanted to wipe out the entire human population?"
      Phina drew her knees to her chest. "I once had that thought. And I'm not proud of it. But I realized what it meant to hope for a better world, and how even though the steps one has to take to get there seem small, each one slowly makes it a better place, if only a little bit.
      "At first, when I heard about the prophecy of the four queens, I thought it was foolish. Four queens would rise up to make the world a better place? Even though I couldn't bring myself to fully believe in the prophecy, it gave me a spark of hope. Maybe there really was a way the world could change for the better. I knew that Queen Edeline was hiding out in the forest, and when you began making your way toward the capital city, I decided to follow you. Maybe there really were four queens after all.
      "When I found out that Chloe-Jane had become the queen of the kingdom, I knew for sure that the prophecy really was true after all and that my death would come about soon. I didn't care about dying-why would I want to continue living in this world? But I realized that if I wanted to change things, I'd have to do it fast."
      "Have you really done all of the things that people have said you've done?" Storm asked wearily. "People have made you out to be either completely insane or a selfish and power-hungry monster."
      "Who said I wasn't either of those things?" Phina let out a humorless laugh, and her shoulders shook a little too violently. "They call me a scheming, wicked old hag. A little girl unfit for being queen. They call me emotional. They say that I'm apathetic. They call me a coward who continues to run from death. Whatever I do, they'll take it and twist it! But it's true!" She was really laughing now, and it was a broken sound. "All of it!" Phina buried her head in her arms. "For a while there I just thought that I could try and fix this world before I died-that I could rid it of humans once and for all."
      "What about all of those innocent people?" Storm asked. "Were you going to kill them too?"
