      Phina absently tugged on a strand of her hair before dropping her hands to wring them in her lap. "I thought that the innocents would be lucky to die before they could see how dark and ugly the world truly was. But my way of thinking was wrong. People don't deserve to die. They deserve a chance at life."
      "What about us?" Lynden inclined his head in my direction. "What about me? Were you going to kill us too?"
      "No," Phina whispered as she lifted her head. "I'm ashamed to admit that the thought crossed my mind, but all of you are my friends. I won't hurt you. You know what? Kill me now. I've done all I could. This world doesn't need any more vampires, especially not someone like me. All the ways I managed to kill aren't anything to be proud of."
      "Phina," Corinna said softly, "when will you understand that we don't want to kill you? We just want to be here to support you. To help you."
      Phina slowly raised her head further, and her blood-red irises glowed from behind her limp hair. "You really will just let me back like that even after knowing what I've done?"
      Corinna extended a hand to the ginger-haired vampire. "Let's go upstairs. The wine cellar is a little dreary, don't you think?"
      She stared at Corinna's hand before slowly reaching out. She let Corinna help her to her feet, and Corinna smiled as she led her toward the ladder. Phina quietly hissed at the faint light streaming down from the living room, but Corinna gave her hand a reassuring squeeze.
      I took Phina's other hand in my own. Her pale fingers were stiff and lifeless. "Together," I said quietly. "We're all in this together."
      "Edeline." Phina's eyes were sad as she turned to look at me. "I'm the one who did this to you. You don't hate me for it?"
      I let out a sigh. "I used to. I was always just so confused about what made the queen of the vampires choose to save me. But after I met Corinna, I found that I didn't care anymore. If anything, I should be thanking you for giving me the opportunity for the two of us to meet."
      "What about you, Lynden?" Phina's voice dropped to a whisper. "Do you hate me? If you do, I wouldn't blame you in the slightest. From the time the two of us began traveling together, the thought of killing you eventually was always at the back of my mind. But I didn't want to. Just thinking about it would make me miserable. I'm so sorry, I-"
      "If that's really what you wanted to do," Lynden said as he held Phina's gaze, "I wouldn't have minded. After all, you were the one who gave me this second chance at life. If you wanted to take it back, I would let you. If anything, I could have helped you, Phina. At the time, with my own resentment for the world, I wouldn't have given it a second thought."
      Phina rapidly shook her head. "I couldn't let you do that. You were better than that. I'm sorry, Lynden. I'm sorry for everything."
      "This entire time you were with us"-Clarity gestured to everyone in the cellar-"was everything you said and did just an act? Or were these your true feelings and emotions?"
      Phina averted her gaze. "I've told you before. My friendship was genuine. It is genuine. I had so much fun with everyone, and that made me happy. That made me really happy."
      Corinna and I wrapped our arms around Phina at the same time to pull her into a tight hug.
      "You're our friend," Corinna said determinedly. "We're not changing our minds either."
      Phina let out a weak laugh. "If only I deserved you all."
      I smiled softly. "I think you do. No one deserves to navigate through life alone. And right now, you've got us."
      "Thank you," Phina said again, this time with a little more confidence. "Thank you for restoring my faith that people can be kind. All of you."
       
~
       
      The next couple of days were considerably light and cheery. Even though the summer weather was stifling to the point where we all had to stay inside, none of it seemed to matter. Phina was back-granted, she was a little quieter than before, but that was fine. As long as she was smiling and having fun, I couldn't have asked for anything more.
      It was sunset, and Storm, Phina, and Cameren were sitting outside on the back porch, laughing at a joke Corinna's brother had made.
      Corinna walked up behind me as she observed the three outside. "It's nice to see everyone smiling again."
      "It is, isn't it?" I smiled as Corinna rested her head on my shoulder.
      "We're almost there, Edeline. Once Chloe-Jane has successfully gained the support of the public, then we'll have all the time in the world to travel someplace far away."
      "Speaking of your sister, I think it's starting to get a little concerning how we've lost all contact with her."
      A frown tugged at the corners of Corinna's lips. "As the head of the knights, Cameren has gone to the castle to check on her a couple of times, but Chloe sent him away each time. Clarity sent her a number of letters, too, to ask how she was doing, but Chloe hasn't replied to any of them either. Something tells me that even though she hasn't replied, she's read all of them. You know what? I'm going to write her a letter." Corinna walked over to the dining room table and pulled up a sheet of parchment and a quill. "She must know that everything went well with liberating the slaves from the farms. What's her next move going to be? As her sister, I hope she'd tell me."
      I took a seat next to Corinna, watching her carefully write each letter. The ink soaked into the parchment in neat lines. "Lynden and Storm are heading out to the marketplace tomorrow. You could ask them to try and deliver it to the castle for you."
      "Wonderful." Corinna kept her eyes glued to the page as she concentrated on the lines. "I'll do that."
      When Corinna finished the letter, the two of us made our way outside to join Storm, Phina, and Cameren. Lynden had also gone outside at some point and was sitting a little distance away from the other three. Clarity was nowhere in sight, but I could sense her presence upstairs in her room. Knowing her, she was probably silently worrying about Chloe-Jane as well.
      "Look!" Phina said excitedly as she waved Corinna and me over. "We can see the stars tonight!"
      I looked up and watched the tiny lights peeking out from behind the clouds.
      "It's been a while since I've seen the stars," Phina said as she hopped to her feet and clasped her hands behind her back. "Sometimes I'll be so focused on what's in front of me that I forget to appreciate the small things in life. Look-is that a shooting star?"
      "Where, where?" Storm jumped up eagerly and pulled Cameren along with him.
      Cameren laughed. "The stars look much brighter when we all look at them together."
      Corinna smiled. "They really do."
       
~
       
      All of us stayed at the house in the city for the night, and the following morning, Lynden and Storm took off for the marketplace. Cameren had gone out as well, and it was only Corinna, Phina, Clarity, and me in the house.
      We were sitting on the living room couch, playing a game of cards when suddenly Phina and I froze. The two of us looked at each other. People. There were people outside-a lot of them.
      "What is it?" Corinna asked, her smile fading as she took note of our worried expressions.
      Phina slowly set her cards down. "There's a lot of people coming this way. Should we go out and check what's happening?"
      "I'll go." Corinna tightened her grip on the dagger at her side as she rose to her feet. "If it's the neighbors and they've found out that Clarity is still here, we might have a problem."
      "I should check instead." I rose to my feet as well. "If it really is the neighbors, they won't take your presence well either."
      "You can't go outside," Corinna said worriedly. "It's the middle of the day. A hot summer day, at that."
      Phina looked back and forth between us. "Maybe we should just stay inside-maybe they aren't even coming to our house." But just as the words left her mouth, there was a knock on the door.
      "Open the door," a familiar voice called.
      Corinna's eyes widened in surprise. Chloe-Jane? she mouthed.
      "Did she decide to come back?" Phina blinked. "But then who did she bring with her? Does she really need that many guards to protect her from the townspeople?"
      "I'll get the door." Corinna made to walk over, but I caught her hand.
      "Something's wrong," I whispered.
      Corinna froze as she seemed to notice what I had. The sound of footsteps had surrounded our house.
      Clarity swiftly made her way to answer the door, but Corinna called out in panic. "Clarity! Wait!"
      Clarity blinked in surprise, and her hand stilled on the doorknob as she turned back to us. She opened her mouth, but just before the words could escape her lips, there was an explosion of wood as the door was blasted apart.

Chapter Thirty-Three
       
I instinctively threw out my arms to shield my face from the splinters of wood flying in every direction. Everything happened so fast, and it took me a moment to realize that Phina had leaped to the other side of the room. She had pushed Clarity out of the way a split second before the explosion and was now shielding her with her body.
      I slowly lowered my arms and blinked at the sudden light flooding into the house from the street outside. Chloe-Jane stood in the doorway. She wore an elegant dress, and her hair was pulled back from her face.
      "That's her." Chloe-Jane pointed at Phina, who was lying on the ground next to Clarity, with bits of dust and wood caught in her ginger hair. "That's Queen Karmen."
      "Chloe," I said as confusion and panic filled my voice, "what are you doing?"
      Chloe-Jane turned to look at me as a number of knights charged into the house through the broken doorway. "I need to do this for the kingdom, Corinna."
      The knights yanked the curtains from the windows. The living room was flooded with light, and Phina hissed as her skin immediately started to flake. After pushing Clarity away from her, Phina staggered to her feet, temporarily blinded by the intensity of the light.
      "There's another one!" one of the knights yelled as his gaze fell on Edeline. "Capture her!"
      "Wait!" I stepped in front of Edeline and held her hands tightly behind me. "Stop! What's going on?"
      The knights had surrounded us in an instant and roughly dragged me away from Edeline. I slammed the sheath of my dagger into a knight's stomach. He staggered backward, winded from the blow, but two others lunged forward to take his place. They made a grab for me, and I ducked under their outstretched arms.
      "Corinna!" Edeline cried out as she stepped forward with her blade in hand. But suddenly, there was a clatter as the dagger fell from her hands and hit the floor. I whirled around, and my eyes widened to find that a number of the knights had pulled out torches. They were now brandishing the flames at Edeline. Edeline instinctively threw her hands up. Her skin began to flake as she backed away from the flames only to be caught by the knights behind her.
      "Edeline!" I lunged forward as the knights snapped chains onto Edeline's wrists. But before I could reach her, two sets of hands pulled me back. Just as I raised my dagger, I felt the cool metal of a blade press against my throat. I froze.
      "Drop your weapon," the knight commanded. "We have explosives. Fighting is futile."
      I slowly raised my hands in surrender and let my dagger drop onto the floor.
      "Everyone freeze," Chloe-Jane called out.
      "Did you know these two were vampires?" the knight holding me demanded. My eyes were glued to his blade, and my heart pounded away in my chest.
      "Yes," I choked out.
      "No," Chloe-Jane interrupted. "They did not know that they were sheltering vampires. Queen Karmen is dangerous. How many people has she tricked and deceived in the past? Getting a couple of humans to believe her lies would be easy. Besides, she killed the king with her own two hands."
      "Chloe-Jane!" Clarity had shakily risen to her feet, and now her eyes blazed. "What do you think you're doing?"
      Chloe-Jane turned to face her. "If I'm not mistaken, aren't there supposed to be more of you here?"
      "No," Clarity said shortly. "We're the only ones here."
      Chloe-Jane just frowned before turning back to address Phina and Edeline. "Vampires, the two of you are coming back to the castle with me. Your crimes can only be compensated with your life."
      "Chloe, you're going to kill them?" My voice broke as I looked at my sister in betrayal. "Edeline didn't-"
      "Silence," Chloe-Jane said. "You can't escape, vampires. We've got the entire house surrounded by knights with torches. And if either of you even thinks of fighting your way out, we'll hurt the girl first."
      I was so shocked I had almost forgotten about the knight behind me with his sword against my neck.
      "Stop it!" Edeline called in a panic. "We'll go with you! Just leave them alone! Please!"
      Chloe-Jane turned on her heel. "The execution of Queen Karmen and the other vampire will be held in public in two weeks' time. I hope all of you will be there to witness it."
      "Chloe!" Clarity had thrown herself at my sister's feet. "Let them go, I'm begging you!"
      Chloe-Jane stared down at Clarity for a long moment before ignoring her words and continuing out the door.
      I was stunned into silence as the knights forcefully dragged Edeline and Phina outside. Before I knew what was happening, I was released, and the knight who held me turned to follow the others out the door. My head spun as I dropped to my knees. Chloe-Jane . . . Why? The pain deep inside of me was unbearable-it was like my very heart was fracturing, and if I didn't do anything quickly to stop it, it would shatter. I still wasn't sure which was tearing at me more: the fact that Edeline and Phina were going to be publicly executed or that Chloe-Jane was the one who ordered it.
      "Are you alright?" Clarity was at my side in an instant.
      I lifted a shaky hand to my neck, and my own blood warmed my fingers. "We've got to go after them-"
      "We can't!" Clarity grabbed my arm as I tried to rise to my feet. "Did you see how many knights there were? We should wait for Cameren and the others to return first."
      "Cameren and the others," I said suddenly. "We need to get out of here! Chloe-Jane knows of Lynden's existence. If she has knights stay here and watch the house, they'll try to capture him as well!"
      "We can't go to the house in the forest," Clarity interjected quickly. "Chloe-Jane's been there before."
      "Where can we go?" I grasped my sister's hands in my own. Hopelessness was beginning to sink in. "Edeline and Phina have been taken to the castle! They're-they're going to kill them, Clarity!" Clarity gently patted my hands, and suddenly I realized that my nails were digging into her skin. I hastily released her and stared unseeingly at the shattered doorway.
      "I never thought Chloe-Jane would resort to something like this." Clarity's expression darkened. "Even though the death of the queen of the vampires is something that would very likely unite the people of the kingdom, it just seems unfair. And why does she have to rope in Edeline too? Did Andreus predict that all of this was going to happen?"
      "Andreus!" I jumped to my feet. "Andreus! Clarity, you're brilliant! If there's anyone who can help us right now, it's Andreus!"
      "Wait!" Clarity grabbed my hand before I could hurry out the door. "Cameren's still out there. So are Storm and Lynden. How do we tell them to stay away from the house? How do we tell them that we've gone to see Andreus?"
      "I'll leave a note at the stable since the two of them will be stopping there first. We've got to hurry, though-we've got a long journey ahead of us. We need to be fast if we want to make it to Andreus's place and back before the execution."
      Wasting no time, Clarity threw everything we needed into a single bag while I swiftly dropped off the note and rented us a horse. After regrouping at the house, we were ready to set off.
      I grasped the reins tightly in my hands as Clarity hopped up onto the horse behind me. "Hold on!" With a flick of my wrists, I spurred our horse into motion, and we were off.
      The wind rushed through my hair, and the sun beat down on my face from high above. Edeline was being taken to the castle right now. Two weeks. I had two weeks to get her out of there.
      I wouldn't give up.
      Clasping my necklace in one hand and the reins in the other, I goaded our horse into a faster gallop.
       
~
       
      "Corinna, we've got to stop for the night."
      My eyes were glued to the road in front of us. "We can't stop now."
      Day had slowly melted into night, and the stars glittered in the summer sky above us. We had long left the capital city. Grassy fields rolled out in all directions, and the houses and buildings of the passing villages were mere specs against the horizon. But even at this rate, we had days to go before we arrived at our destination.
      "Corinna!" Clarity said again, raising her voice over the rushing of the wind. "We need to stop! What's going to happen if we wear our horse out? If we lose the horse, there's no way we'll make it in either direction in time!"
      She was right.
      Clenching the reins in my hands, I brought our horse to a stop. "We'll walk, then."
      Clarity let out a tired sigh. "It doesn't seem like the knights followed us out of the capital city. We should be okay keeping to the main road for now."
      "I'm sorry." My voice dropped to a whisper as I slid off the horse and gently patted its neck. "I don't think I'm thinking straight right now."
      The horse stared at me with its big eyes.
      I began my walk along the dirt path. "Come on, we've still got a long way to go."
      We walked in silence while dancing fireflies illuminated the silver-stained fields.
      I finally spoke up. "Is Edeline really going to die?" My mind was a mess of scattered thoughts. "Is Phina really going to die? The prophecy said that the four queens were destined to die before the end of the century. Will their deaths really bring peace and unity to the kingdom? It's not fair-even if Edeline helped break the king out of the castle, she wasn't the one who killed him! What about the fourth queen? Why hasn't she shown up yet? Isn't there something she can do?"
      "The fourth queen?" Clarity let out a rare laugh. "That's you, isn't it?"
      I was completely caught off guard. "Me?"
      "Am I wrong?" Clarity asked lightly.
      My eyes widened. "It must be because of that wedding. Oh, that's right! Edeline and I were so caught up in all the planning that it completely slipped our minds to tell anyone. It wasn't very formal either."
      "Even if it wasn't formal, it seems like since you married a queen, you have become the fourth queen, Corinna."
      I shook my head in disbelief. "The four queens were together all of this time? Did Andreus know this the entire time? Is that why he told everyone about the prophecy?"
      Clarity stared up at the sky. "You'll have to ask him when we see him."
      "I knew Edeline and I didn't have much time to begin with-the two of us being the way we are-but I was hopeful. I was hopeful that we could make it work. I wanted to make it work."
      "You've always been the lucky one, Corinna." Clarity turned to look at me. "I think you still can. When I was back at Andreus's place, Mother, Cameren, and I found some interesting things."
      "What do you mean?"
      "I wouldn't want to get your hopes up on the pretense of something that might be completely useless. I'll tell you when we get there."
      I knew better than to get my hopes up, but if Clarity thought that there might be a way, at least it gave me something to cling to.
      Suddenly, the sound of hooves pounding the ground echoed through the otherwise silent night.
      "Quick!" I grabbed Clarity by the arm. "We need to find somewhere to hide!"
      Clarity squinted into the darkness. "Relax, I doubt whoever's coming is after us."
      I slowly let go of Clarity's arm. I really wasn't in my right mind.
      As the hoofbeats grew closer, I could count two horses. And over the clopping, someone was yelling something.
      "Hey!" a familiar voice was shouting. "Corinna! Clarity!"
      "Storm?" I spun around to watch the dark-haired boy hop off the horse he was sharing with Cameren. He ran over to us, waving his hands wildly in the air. Lynden was atop a second horse close behind.
      "We caught up with you!" Storm said proudly as he skidded to a stop in front of us. "We got your note!" Then his expression turned serious. "What happened? Where are Phina and Edeline? Why was the city house missing a door?"
      "It was Chloe-Jane," Clarity said grimly. "She came to the house with a bunch of knights. They all had torches that they used to threaten Phina and Edeline. Long story short, they've been taken to the castle and will be executed in public in two weeks' time."
      Storm's jaw dropped. "What?"
      "I know," I said quickly. "We thought they'd go after Lynden next, but it seems like the three of you were careful enough to get out of the capital city safely."
      Cameren's eyes were troubled. "When we saw the knights, we knew something had happened. We were careful to sneak past them."
      I pinched the bridge of my nose in an attempt to ward off the headache slowly gnawing at my brain. "There's no way we're breaking into the castle again. I didn't know who to turn to, and then Clarity mentioned Andreus."
      "My uncle is the best," Storm said confidently, despite his worried expression. "He must have a way to save them. I know he will. Oh, there's a small village about a couple of miles down the road from here. We can rest there for the night, and you can fill us in on the way."
      I nodded, and we all continued on our way. As much as I wanted to run as fast as I could toward the mountains, tiredness was beginning to cloud my mind. Rest was important.
       
~
       
      The next day, we set off from the village before sunrise, and our horses kicked up puffs of dirt in their wake. My eyes stung as the winds tore into them, but I refused to slow. More and more time was slipping away from us. The sky gradually lightened as it melted from inky midnight to a clear and brilliant blue.
      Another day passed. We reached the base of the mountain the following evening, then started the tedious trek up its rocky path. Everything seemed different this time as I looked out at the fields and buildings, which grew smaller and smaller as we ascended. Our last trip up the mountain had been at winter's peak, and at that time, the world was covered in snow and the skies were masked in gray clouds. Now everything was green, and colorful flowers dotted color to the extensive landscape.
      As our horses walked in single file along some of the narrower parts of the trail, I found myself gazing out at the capital city in the distance. The castle was outlined against the horizon, with its turrets and towers shooting up from the ground. Edeline and Phina were somewhere in the castle. Chloe-Jane was somewhere there too.
      I wasn't sure when exactly I had fallen asleep or how much time had passed, but I awoke to Clarity's voice. "Corinna, we've arrived."
      My eyes snapped open, and I nearly tumbled off our horse. I dazedly took in the house on the peak of the mountain. It had taken us five long days, but we made it.
      I nearly laughed with joy as my stiff legs hit the ground.
      "Come on"-Storm grabbed me by the hand-"let's go see my uncle!"
      The two of us sprinted into the house, leaving Clarity, Cameren, and Lynden to take care of the horses.
      We ran through the house and down the staircase. I staggered multiple times as my wooden leg impaired my movements. The large cavern beyond was illuminated by hundreds of glowing lanterns, exactly how I remembered it.
      "Hello, Corinna, Storm," Andreus said mildly as he looked down at us with his large golden eyes.
      "Uncle!" Storm called excitedly. He skidded across the stones before throwing himself at Andreus with open arms.
      "Storm." Andreus's chuckle rumbled through the chamber. "You have gotten thinner."
      Storm looked up at his uncle. "Phina and Edeline are in trouble-please, Uncle, we need to help them!"
      Andreus blinked. "Aren't the two of them still in the capital city? Why did you come all the way to me?"
      I dropped to my knees. "I don't know what to do. Chloe-Jane's got them locked up who knows where in the castle. They're going to be publicly executed in eight days."
      "If you think that I can break them out of the castle," Andreus started slowly, "I think you are mistaken."
      "Are you saying that you can't help them?" Lynden questioned in disbelief as he appeared at the bottom of the stairs with Clarity and Cameren.
      "No, no." Andreus shook his head. "I never said that I could not help them, dear boy. I just said that I cannot break them out of the castle."
      My head snapped up hopefully. "So you can help them?"
      "What is it that you would like me to do?"
      "I-" I started, but I realized that I was at a loss for words. What had I thought Andreus could do? "I don't know."
      Clarity took a step forward. "What about that book Cameren and I found while we were looking through your collection of items?"
      "Book?" Andreus blinked. "Which book? I have many books."
      "Wait here," Clarity called to me over her shoulder before sprinting off. "I'll be right back!"
      All I could do was nod my head.
      "I'm going to go check on Mother," Cameren spoke up. "I think she'll be overjoyed to see that all of you are back." He turned and left a moment later, leaving Storm, Lynden, and I alone with the dragon.
      "There's one thing I'm curious about," I said. "Did you know from the start that I was going to be the fourth queen?"
      "Did I know you were going to be the fourth queen?" Andreus repeated my question thoughtfully. "No, I did not. I knew that there was a possibility that you could become the fourth queen. But it might not have been you."
      Before I could open my mouth to ask a follow-up question, Storm interrupted. "You're a queen? Is it because you married Edeline without telling the rest of us?"
      I dipped my head in a nod. "Yes. It slipped our minds. There were more important things to think about at the time, and we didn't want to distract anyone."
      Clarity reappeared a moment later, clutching a thick book tightly in her arms. "I found it!"
      "Oh," Andreus said lightly as Clarity set it down in front of the dragon. "So this was the book you were talking about."
      "This-" Storm's eyes grew large as he hopped over to the book. "Uncle, how did you get your hands on this?"
      "What is it?" I asked quickly.
      "It's a book about the magic of the ancients-it's a book of forgotten magic."
      I stared at the book. My mind was completely empty. It certainly didn't look very special; its cover was battered from age, and its pages were yellow and curling. "I don't get it-how will a book of old magic help us stop Chloe-Jane from executing Edeline and Phina? I don't know a lot about how magic works, but I really doubt we can just magic them to safety."
      "Think about it." Clarity pointed at the book for emphasis. "When Phina was talking about how the first progenitor cursed himself with a long-forgotten magic in his craze to stay young and live forever, I suddenly remembered that Andreus himself had a book of ancient magic. If the first progenitor used magic to curse himself, can't we use magic to reverse it? While Phina did kill the king, Edeline doesn't have that same crime on her head. If we can just turn them back into humans, maybe it could buy them both some more time for us to try to reason with Chloe."
      My eyes widened. "You're right! But how would we do it?"
      "I might know of a way." Andreus gingerly extended a long claw and flipped open the cover of the old book. "Whether it will work, though, is a different question entirely."
      "Please"-I bowed my head to the dragon-"if you have any way to save them, I'm willing to do everything I can."
      Andreus loomed over us as he flipped through the pages and squinted down at the words. "First of all, we will need a vampire to actually turn back into a human."
      Storm, Clarity, and I all turned to Lynden.
      "Would you be willing to test it out?" I asked breathlessly. "Would you be willing to turn back into a human?"
      Lynden nodded. "It's not like I have anything to lose. If it doesn't work and I end up dying, at least I can accompany Phina."
      "You won't die," Storm said confidently. "My uncle is the best. He won't let you die."
      Andreus let out a sigh that seemed to echo through the stone chamber. "Alas, I won't be the one performing the magic. Only humans can reverse the curse, as it was created by a human in the first place."
      "What?" Storm looked at the dragon, taken aback.
      I rose to my feet without hesitation. "I'll do it."
      "Me too." Clarity walked over to stand next to me.
      "And me," Storm added. "Actually, what exactly is it that we're doing?"
      "All you need to do"-Andreus tapped at the ancient book with a claw-"is just repeat after me to say some words from the language of the ancients. I will provide the magic energy needed, and you will shape it."
      "Just like that?" I blinked. "It's that simple?"
      "Not exactly." Andreus gave us a regretful smile. "Using this kind of magic can take years off of your life."
      "What?" Lynden's head snapped up. "If that's the case, don't do it."
      I shook my head. "If there's a chance that we can turn you and the others back into humans, I'm willing to take it." Then I turned to Lynden. "Do you want to be human again?"
      Lynden was silent for a moment before he said quietly, "I'd rather die a human than a vampire."
      I turned back to Andreus. "That settles it, then. What do I have to do?"
      Clarity took one of my hands in her own. "We'll do it together."
      "Me too." Storm hurried over to join the two of us in front of the book. "If the magic really has to take years off our lives, this way we can distribute those years between us."
      Andreus sighed. "As much as I want to talk you out of doing this, it seems like all of you have got your minds set on it. Storm is right, with all of you performing the magic together, it will only take about a year from each of you instead of three from Corinna."
      Edeline was going to be okay. In exchange for her life, this was a small price. A generous deal.
      "When do we want to start?" Andreus asked lightly.
      "Now," I answered.

Chapter Thirty-Four
       
"I'm so sorry, Edeline," Phina said tearfully. "This is all my fault."
      "What are you apologizing for?" I asked softly. "No one could have predicted that Chloe-Jane would barge in with the knights the way she did."
      Phina buried her face in her hands, and her hair hid her eyes behind a curtain of flame. "If I had just stayed away, you wouldn't have been brought here with me."
      I sighed. "Don't worry about it. I was one of the people who convinced you to come back."
      "No." Phina shook her head. "This really is my fault. I sent Chloe-Jane an anonymous letter. I was the one who gave her the idea to unite the kingdom over my death. By eradicating the monster who killed their king, the people would rally behind Chloe-Jane, and she'd finally have enough of their respect to rule the kingdom and change it for the better. I was going to let myself get captured by her too. On my own. But when you and the others asked me to come back . . . I was selfish and went back with you."
      I sat with my back pressed against the stone wall of the cell. "At least Lynden was lucky enough not to get captured alongside the two of us."
      The room itself was fairly large, with a row of bars cutting through the middle of the space, separating us on either side. The back wall had a barred window, high enough on the wall that I could see the moon hanging in the summer sky. At night our cell was illuminated by the moon, but in the day the sunlight poured through the bars. If I sat directly beneath the window, I could avoid the light. But right now, in the middle of the night, I could sit against the wall opposite the window and watch the stars.
      "Did you want to come back with us?" I turned to look at Phina through the bars.
      Phina hugged her knees to her chest. "I did. When you all asked me to come back, there was nothing more I wanted in the world than to do just that. All I wanted to do was return-to be Phina again. But it seems like in the end, I can't escape my fate. I can't escape from myself. Queen Karmen was a creation of my own. It's about time the queen died. But you, Edeline . . . I didn't mean to drag you into any of this. I didn't mean to drag any of you into this."
      "Can I ask you something?" I asked quietly.
      Phina raised her head and looked at me with wide eyes. "Of course."
      I leaned my head against the wall, and my inky hair spilled over the floor around me. "Why did you turn me into a vampire?"
      "Your mother was actually one of the queens I had my eye on for some time." Phina's eyes met mine. "The reason I found you so easily was because I was already watching the castle. Your mother was a brilliant woman, Edeline. I really thought she was going to be one of the four. But then . . ." she trailed off, closing her eyes as if the memories were coming back to her all at once. "I turned you because what happened that night was horrible. By the time I arrived at the castle, it was too late, and all I could do was offer you a chance to avenge your parents. It didn't occur to me until you disappeared that you were a queen as well."
      "What about Lynden?" I asked mildly.
      "I think I saw myself in you," Phina said softly. "Lynden too. I wanted to give the two of you a second chance at living-a chance at taking your revenge. Believe it or not, the two of you were the only people I ever turned into vampires."
      "You aren't the only vampire the first progenitor turned, is that right? It's said that you killed the others."
      "It's true-I did kill them. But it was out of pity. All of us were traumatized by what we were forced to go through. I remember it, Edeline. I remember all of it. How could I ever forget? You see, the first progenitor wanted us to become vampires so we could accompany him for eternity. He tricked the girls at the manor into drinking his blood. A number of the girls died from the agony of the transformation. Their bodies couldn't take it-their minds couldn't take it. The blood killed them. You know as well as I do that a vampire's blood will cause tremendous suffering during the transformation. If one doesn't have the will to fight the pain, death is certain."
      "So you fought through the transformation to kill him?"
      Phina turned to look out at the night sky. "You could say that. He took me away to his manor on the day I was supposed to get married. He murdered the young man I was going to wed. At first, I wanted to die and join my lover in death. But the first progenitor wouldn't let me. He threatened me with the lives of my family. Being the first progenitor, he wasn't just someone I could easily kill. I don't think he even thought that any of us were even capable of killing him. But he underestimated us. He underestimated me.
      "After his death, we were finally free. All of the remaining girls went their separate ways. It didn't take them long to start going crazy, though, as they slowly began to realize what the curse of their immortality truly meant. Some of them came to me, begging for death. But after they all died, I was now the most powerful vampire alive. With that power, I decided I would use it to ensure that the vampires now roaming the northern continent would never do the same thing the first progenitor did.
      "It was many years later when I heard about the prophecy of the four queens for the first time. It sounded too good to be true, but I started to look for these four queens anyway. Now that all four queens have finally appeared, everything is finally coming to a close. I just didn't think things would end this way. I'm sorry, Edeline."
      I blinked. "All four queens? Besides Chloe-Jane, you, and me, who else have we met?"
      Phina's smile was soft. "It's Corinna, isn't it?"
      I stared at her as it suddenly dawned on me.
      Phina's eyes were wistful as she clasped her hands together behind her back. "You and Corinna are very lucky to have each other. Sometimes I wish someone would look at me again the same way you look at Corinna. That I could look at someone that way again. It's been so many years now."
      "What about Lynden?"
      "What about him?" Phina's eyes grew sad. "He was my friend for so many years, and yet I continued hiding my identity from him. With my lack of honesty, I'll be lucky if he ever finds it in his heart to trust me again. He loved me once, you know. I don't know about now. All I did was lie to him. But now I can't even see him one last time to say goodbye."
      The two of us fell silent.
      "So what happens now?" Phina's voice was no more than a whisper. "I'm willing to stay here and accept my fate, but for you to die alongside me . . . it isn't fair."
      "I'm just worried about Corinna." I reached up to touch my necklace and feel the smooth crystals between my fingers. "Knowing her, she's probably got some plan to sneak in and break the two of us out of here. But going anywhere near the castle is dangerous. This time, she's up against her own sister. And her sister knows her a lot better than the previous king. I-I want to see her again. I knew the two of us wouldn't have much time together from the start, but I still chose to stay. We both did. I don't blame Chloe-Jane, though. After all, she just wants to help this kingdom and its people."
      A voice sounded from behind the closed door of the cell. "I hear that you're talking about me."
      I glanced up as Chloe-Jane stepped inside. I had sensed her coming and was sure that Phina had as well.
      I sighed. "Hello, Chloe-Jane. What are you doing visiting us at this time of night?"
      "Where are your guards?" Phina asked, scanning the hallway behind the young queen.
      "They're outside," Chloe-Jane said stiffly. Her skirts swished around her legs as she took another step forward.
      "Are you sure you really want to get this close?" I questioned. "Neither Phina nor I am chained up. You aren't worried that we'll attack you?"
      "You've left the door open too," Phina pointed out. "You don't think we'll try and escape?"
      "You won't try to escape." Chloe-Jane looked back and forth between Phina and me. "If you wanted to escape, you would have done so already. I don't want you to die," Chloe-Jane said quietly as her gaze lingered on me. "If you die, Corinna will be sad. But I need to do this for her. She can't be with a vampire."
      "She can't?" I rested my chin on my hand as I looked up at Chloe-Jane. "Isn't she already?"
      "Vampires and humans can't be together forever." Chloe-Jane's voice was sad. "When the vampire outlives the human, what happens then? Humans can't stay young and youthful forever like the vampires. I know my sister wants to stay with you. And as her sister, I can't let her become a vampire."
      I blinked. "Who said she was going to become a vampire?"
      "Isn't that the only way the two of you can stay together?" Chloe-Jane asked hopelessly.
      I shook my head, and the faintest trace of a smile tugged on my lips. "I was ready to die alongside her when the time came."
      "I need to rid the world of vampires." Chloe-Jane stared at Phina and me as if she were fighting some kind of internal battle. "Everyone in the kingdom now knows that King Volin was killed by Karmen, the queen of the vampires. They've come to believe that the king was trying to change this kingdom for the better. They're angry at Queen Karmen and want to see her dead. The only way I can get the people to truly respect me is if I hold a public execution for the queen."
      Phina rose to her feet, walked to the bars of her cell, and wrapped her slender fingers around them. "If my death is what this kingdom needs to unify its people under you, I'm willing to die. I don't care about my death. Who will be there to mourn me? But please, Chloe, I'm begging you. Spare Edeline for Corinna's sake."
      Chloe-Jane shook her head vigorously. "I-I don't have a choice! You two are the only known vampires left. I have to show the people that I'm taking this chance to purge the world of evil once and for all. This kingdom doesn't need vampires; its people need safety, and this is how I can begin giving it to them. Once the kingdom is united behind me, I can start fixing the mess that all the previous kings have left it in."
      "Chloe-Jane," I said quietly, looking up at her in a disheartened sort of way. "Why? Why does it have to be this way?"
      "Why?" Chloe-Jane's expression was torn. "Why did my sister have to fall in love with you?"
      "What happens after I'm gone? Will you make sure your sister lives her life to the fullest? Will you make sure she continues to live?"
      Chloe-Jane dipped her head. "I will do my best."
      We all fell silent.
      "That's all," Chloe-Jane finally said. "I'll take my leave. The two of you will be burned in front of the castle for all to see on our set date."
      "Corinna always believed that you would be a good queen," I said softly. "And I do too. I think you will be a wonderful queen. I have a feeling that the people of this kingdom will rally around you with the proper incentive. I just wish things didn't have to be this way."
      Chloe-Jane's voice was quiet as she turned and made her way out of the cell. "Me too."
       
~
       
      I wasn't sure how much time had passed before we heard the metallic scraping sound of a knight unlocking the door to our cell. Even with a clear day and night cycle, everything had started to blur together.
      "You're supposed to change into these," he said quickly as he tossed a bundle of white cloth at my feet. "Both of you."
      "What's this?" I asked as I picked at the fabric. But the knight had scurried away, and the cell door slammed shut. I sighed before I carefully unfolded the bundle of fabric to find two plain dresses. "It looks like we're supposed to wear these on the day we're to be executed." I passed one of the dresses to Phina through the bars.
      Phina just took the garment silently and absently ran her fingers over the fabric. "I'm worried," the ginger-haired vampire whispered. "I'm worried about Corinna and Lynden and Clarity and Storm and the others. I don't want them to try and do anything crazy in an attempt to rescue us. I'm half expecting them to show up at our cell any moment."
      I made quick work of changing into the white dress. "It's better if they don't show up. The last thing I want is for any of them to witness us getting burned at the stake. It would be too painful for them to watch." The feeling in my chest was a painful emptiness. There were still so many places I wanted to visit with Corinna. We still had yet to journey to the southern continent to see the land where her parents had been born. We still had yet to journey to the far east, to the eastern kingdoms and where my home had once been.
      Phina hugged the white dress to her chest. "You're right. It is better this way. At least the last time we were all together-Lynden, Storm, Corinna, and the others-we were happy."
      I brushed back my length of inky black hair-a stark contrast to the white dress. "Happiness is fleeting. Sometimes I find myself wishing it could last forever, but nothing's forever in this world."
      Phina gazed up at the night sky outside the barred window. "It's sad, isn't it? Life feels so short once you're at the end of it."
      "Life is short. And that's what makes it precious. We've just been lucky enough-or cursed enough-to have lived multiple lifetimes."
      Phina looked at her hands. "It's just a shame that when you finally meet the person you wanted to spend it with, everything has to come to an end."
      I smiled softly. "Even if my time with Corinna was short, it's better than not having met her at all."
      "If you knew things were going to end this way, would you do it again?"
      "Yes." I didn't even have to think about my answer. "Yes, I would."

Chapter Thirty-Five
       
Clarity, Storm, and I sat on the stone floor of the chamber in a circle. The three of us tightly grasped each other's hands. As we recited after Andreus, I began to feel my skin prickle as if something other than blood was flowing through my veins.
      My blood was slowly heating, and I gritted my teeth as the stabbing sensation started. Andreus's words came rushing back to me as I felt Clarity's and Storm's grip tighten-they were in just as much pain as I was. Magic may seem like an easy solution-an easy way out, Andreus's words of caution echoed through my memory. But in reality, it is quite the opposite. Magic will continue to take and take and take. It will continue to consume the wielder until there is nothing left. If you are not careful, that might well be your fate.
      But I trusted Andreus. I trusted Clarity and Storm. If only I could get Edeline out of the castle-if only we could spend one more day together-it would be enough. Suddenly, there was a blinding flash of light, and I squeezed my eyes shut.
      My entire body was on fire. The pain was never-ending. Would I be stuck this way for eternity? Forever burning, forever blinded by the light. But just then, I felt Clarity's nails dig into my hand from a different time, a different place. I wasn't alone.
      When the light finally cleared, a tiny orb of light no bigger than my thumbnail sat on top of Andreus's ancient book. Storm, Clarity, and I slowly let go of each other's hands, completely shaken. If this had just been reversing the curse, I wondered what kind of magic the first progenitor had used to curse himself in the first place. How had he not died before becoming an immortal? How many years of his own life had he consumed?
      Cameren had returned to the chamber with Mother at some point, and the two of them had the same wide-eyed expression on their faces. Mother rushed over to my side, dumbstruck as she looked at Clarity and me. I shook my head tiredly. My skin was still prickling.
      We all watched silently as Andreus gingerly tapped the tiny orb with his claw and it split in half. The dragon tapped it again and the pieces split for a second time.
      "Here." Andreus held out his hand and offered one of the four shards to Lynden. "I think you are supposed to ingest it."
      Lynden gingerly took one of the glowing pieces. "Well, I guess I shouldn't waste any time." And with that said, he swallowed the bit of light.
      "Well?" Andreus asked mildly. "How do you feel?"
      "How do I feel?" Lynden blinked as he furrowed his brow. "Fine-" But before he could finish his sentence, he suddenly froze. His eyes rolled in their sockets, and he collapsed to the floor.
      "Lynden!" Clarity, Storm, and I cried in unison as we hurried over to him.
      Lynden had stilled completely except for the wild movement of his eyes behind their closed lids.
      "Was this supposed to happen?" Mother asked faintly. The blood had drained from her face as she looked up at Andreus.
      Andreus curiously looked down at Lynden. "Maybe. I have never turned a vampire into a human before. All I can do is try."
      "He'll wake up, right?" Storm asked in a panic as he stared up at Andreus as well.
      "Whether he wakes up or not is entirely up to him." Andreus lowered his magnificent head, and the gold flecking his green scales glowed in the light from the hundreds of hanging cavern lanterns. "How about all of you take him upstairs? It might be many days until he wakes, and I doubt the lot of you would want to wait here in my little cave."
      "Days?" I blinked hopelessly. "That long?"
      Andreus sighed as he offered me a soft smile. "Magic is an interesting thing. It has a mind of its own, and all we can do is be patient with it."
       
~
       
      Clarity, Storm, and I sat next to each other as we silently watched Lynden's unconscious figure. We had moved the brown-haired vampire to one of the bedrooms in the upper story and had barely left his side since.
      Mother and Cameren came in about every hour or so to check on us. When they would come in, I'd quietly talk with Mother while Cameren would pull Storm off to the side of the room and try his best to lighten the mood with a game of cards. Clarity would remain silent, preferring to gaze absently at the wall than engage with the rest of us. At first Mother and Cameren were completely shocked to hear that Storm, Clarity, and I had used magic. But after I did my best to explain the situation, they calmed down a bit.
      At least a day had passed already, and the stars glittered in the night sky outside the opened window. The warm summer breeze floated through the room, sending dust spiraling through the air.
      "He'll wake up, right?" Storm asked worriedly for probably the hundredth time. "I don't think he's breathing."
      "You're worrying too much," Clarity said. Even though her tone maintained its usual sharpness, there was now a tiredness mixed in with it. "He wasn't breathing to begin with, remember?"
      I stared down at Lynden's unconscious figure. The vampire looked peaceful despite the whirling of his eyes behind their lids. "Was it a mistake to come here?"
      "It's not a mistake to try." Clarity rose from her seat and made her way over to the window. "Even if things don't work out, I think it's better this way."
      I looked at the back of my sister's head. "What do you mean?"
      Clarity continued to stare out at the night sky. "What I mean is that this way, we won't have to witness Edeline and Phina's execution."
      "Stop it." Storm's voice shook. "Edeline and Phina aren't going to die. I believe in my uncle. Lynden will wake up soon. We just have to wait a little longer." At this point, I wasn't sure who he was trying to convince more: himself or us. Either way, I took a deep breath to calm myself-breaking down now wouldn't help anything.
      The three of us stayed awake the entire night, and by noon the next day, I could feel the tiredness beginning to creep up on me. Both Cameren and Mother had tried to convince us to rest, but the three of us were far too anxious to rest even if we wanted to.
      "Hey!" Storm's voice cut through the clouds in my head. "Lynden's eyes stopped moving!"
      The fog instantly cleared from my mind as I focused on Lynden's face. Storm was right; his eyes had finally stopped whirling, and he had gone completely still.
      Clarity quickly took one of Lynden's hands in her own and flipped his palm up so she could check for a pulse. Her eyes widened, and Storm and I looked at her expectantly.
      "Well?" I asked breathlessly.
      "He has a heartbeat." Clarity shook her head in disbelief. "It's very faint, but it's there."
      "It really worked," I breathed.
      Clarity nodded. But then her eyes widened, and her expression turned worried.
      "What is it now?"
      Clarity frowned. "It's fading-we need to wake him up now!"
      All I could do was watch with a sinking feeling as Clarity grabbed Lynden's shoulders in an attempt to shake him awake. Lynden's head just lolled back and forth like that of a ragdoll.
      "Wake up!" Storm shouted desperately.
      "Idiot," Clarity snapped, the blood draining from her face. "If our voices could wake him up, he would have awoken days ago!"
      "I have an idea!" Storm jumped to his feet and sprinted out the door. He returned a moment later with a bucket of water. "Here!" he said, then dumped the water onto Lynden's head.
      Clarity and I looked on, dumbfounded as Lynden coughed and sat bolt upright. "What?" he sputtered. He gasped for air as he brushed his soaking hair out of his eyes. "What was that?"
      The first thing I noticed was that Lynden's iris had changed from blood red to a warm brown. His fangs had vanished as if they had never been there in the first place.
      "It worked!" Storm dropped the empty bucket onto the bedroom floor in relief. "It actually worked! My uncle was right! He always told me the first thing to do if you needed to wake someone up was yell at them, and if that didn't work, then the second thing is to try dumping a bucket of ice water on their head. Well, we don't have ice right now since it's summer, but it seems like regular water works just as well! But if that doesn't work-"
      "And what's the third thing your uncle told you to do?" Lynden coughed again. "Breath fire in their face? Actually, don't tell me. I'd rather not know."
      I stared at Lynden. "How do you feel?"
      "Terrible," Lynden admitted as he shook his head. "The entire process of reverting back to a human was very unpleasant, to say the least. Now it feels like all of my senses have been numbed. I haven't felt this weak in a very long time. But this is what it's like to be human."
      "What did I tell you?" Storm grinned from ear to ear. "My uncle is the best!"
      "Yes, yes." Clarity clapped Storm on the back, but there was relief in her eyes too. "How could we forget? You've told us many times."
      Lynden shivered. "I can feel the cold. Everything feels so cold."
      "Cold?" Storm blinked. "I think we should probably get you a change of clothes."
      Lynden gave Storm an exasperated look but nodded all the same.
      Clarity and I made our way downstairs first to tell the others the good news. We hurried down the stone staircase into the heart of the mountain, and our footsteps echoed as we emerged into Andreus's chamber.
      "It worked!" I panted as I skidded to a stop in front of the dragon. "Did you know we could do it this entire time?"
      Andreus smiled. "I do not know anything for sure. Just because I am both old and a dragon does not by any means mean that I am all-knowing. And alas, as predictable as the results are, at the end of the day, they are still predictions. It was the strong will of the three of you that resulted in your success."
      "Will I be able to turn Edeline and Phina back into humans as well?"
      Andreus tilted his head thoughtfully. "You have just about four days left until their execution, correct? If you leave now, you might be able to make it."
      "Corinna!" Clarity grabbed my arm as I made to dash back up the stairs. "Even if you make it to the capital city in time, how are you going to get inside the castle? Sneaking in through the servant's entrance like you did last time will take too long, and you'll get caught long before you even find where Phina and Edeline are being held!"
      "I'll think of another way, then," I said quickly as I tried to shake off my sister.
      "Oh, wait a moment." Andreus looked at me. His golden eyes were like glass as they reflected the lantern light. "I think you are forgetting something."
      The dragon extended a clawed hand to me, from which hung a little pouch. "Right!" I carefully took the pouch from Andreus and glanced inside at its contents. "I need the remaining shards."
      "Good luck, Corinna." Andreus gave me a soft smile. "I wish you safe travels."
      I clutched the pouch of light close to my chest as I bowed to the dragon. "Thank you. Thank you for everything!"
      And with that, Clarity and I turned and sprinted back up the stone steps. When we emerged through the doorway to the mountain house, I was surprised to find that Lynden was sitting alone at the dining room table. Mother and Cameren were standing off to the side, preparing supplies for our trip back to the capital.
      Lynden was gazing out the open window, staring dazedly at the blue sky outside. I could only imagine what it would be like to finally see the sky for the first time in years.
      "Where's Storm?" Clarity asked as she surveyed the room. Her question was answered a moment later as Storm shot out of the kitchen with a bowl of porridge in his hands. The dark-haired boy placed it in front of Lynden before pulling up a chair beside him.
      "You need energy," Storm told Lynden. "You haven't eaten solid food in decades. No wonder why you're so weak."
      Lynden just sighed as he picked up the wooden spoon and took a bite. A moment later, he clapped a hand over his mouth as if he were about to be sick.
      "What?" Storm sprung to his feet in a panic. "Is it really that bad? I'm sorry! I-"
      "No." Lynden swallowed. "It's because I haven't eaten anything solid in at least a decade that my body isn't used to it."
      "So it's alright, then?" Storm asked timidly.
      To all our surprise, Lynden smiled. "It's the best thing I've ever tasted."
       
~
       
      After we finished packing for the journey, we immediately set off down the mountain. Since we only had three horses, Storm had opted to stay behind to help Mother monitor Lynden's recovery. As much as Lynden wanted to join us on our ride back to the capital city, he was in no such state to do so. Clarity and Cameren accompanied me back to the capital instead.
      With the wind in my hair and the sun in my face, I squinted against the light of the horizon. We were running out of time. I urged my horse to run faster as I gazed out at the land expanding before me. Villages and towns dotted the grassy plains, and the capital city rose up in the distance. It looked so small from up here-the castle, the buildings, the forests, everything. In fact, it was small enough for me to hold in the palms of my hands. But when I reached out to take hold of them, the only thing my fingers grasped was air.
      For the next few days, we kept moving. When we weren't riding our horses, the three of us were walking. Sleep-if any-was brief.
      We were going to make it.
      I wouldn't accept the alternative.
       
~
       
      After what felt like years of flying down the road, we finally reached the entrance of the capital city. The townsfolk we passed on the way to the castle seemed very alarmed by three youths charging down the streets on horseback, but I couldn't bring myself to dwell on it.
      The sky was dark by the time we reached the castle gates and the moon shone brightly in the inky sky.
      I dismounted my horse and nearly stumbled as my stiff legs refused to support my weight. The world swayed, and I blinked rapidly as the castle in front of me drifted in and out of focus. Clarity and Cameren were instantly at my side to steady me.
      The three of us sprinted over to the gates, waving wildly to attract the attention of the guards. The knights on guard spotted us quickly and exchanged a look. "What are you doing at the castle?" one of them inquired. His voice was muffled by his helmet.
      "I'm here to see my sister, Queen Chloe-Jane," I announced. My voice was much stronger than I felt. All I could do now was hope that Chloe-Jane would let me see Edeline.
      "Are you Corinna?" the second knight spoke up. Even though he was wearing a helmet, I could feel his gaze go to my wooden leg.
      "I am."
      "The queen's been expecting you." The knight pushed open the gates. "Please follow us."
      After exchanging a glance with Clarity and Cameren, I took a step through the castle's gates and into the garden beyond.
      Just as my siblings made to follow me inside, the knights stepped forward and blocked them with their swords. "The two of you can wait outside," the first knight said.
      "We're Chloe-Jane's family too!" Clarity said angrily as she eyed the silvery light glinting off the blades.
      "The queen made it very clear that only her sister Corinna is allowed inside," the second knight explained tiredly. "Please don't cause us any trouble and wait outside the gates."
      I sighed, turning back to Clarity and Cameren as the former opened her mouth. "It's okay-I can take it from here."
      Clarity and Cameren looked at each other but conceded.
      "This way." The guards waved me in, and with one final glance over my shoulder, I followed them into the castle.
      Even though I had been in this garden before, things were so eerily different during the night. It was almost peaceful-but maybe that was just because I wasn't being chased this time.
      The guards led me through the front doors and through the silent halls. I followed after them, with my wooden leg clunking quietly over the polished marble floors. I took a deep breath to calm myself. My head felt foggy and my body was lethargic. I hadn't slept properly in days and it was beginning to take a toll on me. But I couldn't stop now. Not when I was so close.
      "Corinna," a voice said. My vision blurred as I squinted through the dimly lit halls.
      My eyes finally focused on my sister. "Chloe-Jane."
      "I'll take you to see them." Chloe-Jane's voice was quiet. "I knew you'd come."
      "Please." My voice broke; my throat was hoarse. "I want to see Edeline."
      Chloe-Jane turned away from me. "I'll take you to her on one condition. You can see her just as long as you don't try and break her out of the cell."
      "I understand." I nodded, and my heart rate steadily increased as my fingers tightened around the small pouch under the fabric of my cloak. "I don't think I'd be able to break them out even if I tried."
      "Follow me." Chloe-Jane started down the hall. "You'll have until sunrise. At sunrise, both of the vampires will be taken to the town square to be burned."
      "Sunrise?" I echoed as my head snapped up to the windows. The sky was already slowly beginning to lighten. "Please, Chloe, could we go faster?"
      Chloe-Jane nodded once, and the two of us took off at a sprint.
      I followed my sister down a flight of stairs and into a section of the castle I had never visited before. It seemed to be another type of cell block, but unlike the one Edeline and I had been locked in, this one was lined with large, barred windows. The sky continued to brighten outside them, and the stars slowly but steadily faded from the inky backdrop.
      "Here." Chloe-Jane stopped in front of a metal door and quickly unlocked it with a silver key. "You'll have to be fast."
      I rushed into the stone room beyond. The room was fairly large, with a barred window that took up most of the upper part of the back wall. Metal bars separated the room in half, and I looked down to find Edeline sitting on the floor. Her head already snapped to me the moment I stumbled into the cell.
      "Corinna!"

Chapter Thirty-Six
       
"Edeline!"
      I sprung to my feet as Corinna called my name. The two of us rushed toward each other and met halfway in a tight embrace. I buried my face in her shoulder, not trusting myself to speak.
      Corinna held me tightly as she twined her fingers through my hair. "I'm here."
      "The knights will be here soon," Chloe-Jane said from the doorway. "You have until then to say your goodbyes." With that said, she quietly closed the cell door, leaving her sister alone inside with Phina and me.
      "Corinna, I-"
      "I don't have much time to explain." Corinna lowered her voice as she glanced over at Phina, who was still sitting on her side of the room, separated from us by a wall of bars. The ginger-haired vampire was watching us with wide eyes, but she slowly rose to her feet and made her way over to the bars to listen to what Corinna had to say. "We went to see Andreus. That's why I took so long."
      Andreus? Phina mouthed.
      "He knows how to turn vampires back into humans. Here-" Corinna hastily pulled out a pouch from under her cloak before shaking off the heavy garment completely. "If you take these, you'll revert back into your human state!" She took out two shards of light from the pouch and pressed one in my hand, then held out the second one to Phina. "If you turn back into humans, maybe we'll be able to convince Chloe-Jane not to take your lives!"
      "Does it really work?" Phina whispered as she stared at the little bit of light in Corinna's outstretched hand. Ever so carefully, she reached through the bars and took the shard from her. She raised it up to the light and examined it as she held it between her thumb and forefinger.
      "It does," Corinna said breathlessly. "Lynden took one, and he successfully transformed back into a human."
      "Does that mean"-I whirled to face Corinna with large eyes-"we could be humans together? Live together as humans until we grow old?"
      "Yes!" Corinna laughed as she grasped my hands in her own. "We could spend the rest of our lives together. We could travel the world and grow old."
      Would the little shard of light in my hand really bring me back to life? It sounded too good to be true.
      "Quick"-Corinna turned back to Phina-"you should take them quickly. Sunrise is almost upon us, and the knights will be here any moment to take you both away!"
      "Wait." Phina held out the shard of light to Corinna. "You should have this back."
      Corinna blinked in confusion. "What do you mean?"
      "I have no reason to turn back into a human." Phina let out a humorless laugh as she turned to look up at the rapidly lightening sky. "I'm about to die anyway. There's a crowd out there waiting for me. I can't just disappoint them like this, can I?"
      "You're really willing to die when you have the means to keep living in your very hands?" I asked softly.
      Phina dropped her gaze. "I've lived for too long already. Besides, without the death of Queen Karmen, the people won't feel satisfied. They'll call Chloe-Jane a liar, and she'll lose all of the trust and respect that she managed to build up. This is the only way the people will unite together under her. They'll have avenged their dead king, and the last of the vampires will be gone from this world for good. It will be easy to say that you were wrongly accused of being a vampire, Edeline. They can brush that part off as a simple mistake, but not for Karmen. I've dreamed of a better world, and with Chloe-Jane in complete power, she can make it happen."
      "Are you sure?" Corinna held back her tears. "Please think about it carefully. You could live out the rest of your years as a human."
      Phina just smiled sadly as she reached back through the bars and pressed her little shard of light into Corinna's hands. "Where's Lynden and Storm? You don't know how happy I am to hear that Lynden has become a human again."
      Corinna stared at the shard Phina had returned to her. "The two of them are still at Andreus's place. After his transformation, Lynden wasn't in any state to make the journey back to the capital city."
      "What about Clarity and the rest of your family?" Phina asked softly. Her dress and hair waved gently in the breeze from the window.
      "Clarity and Cameren came with me to the castle," Corinna said as she held onto Phina's hand through the bars. "The guards wouldn't let them in, though."
      "So they're all safe," Phina said in relief, even though the sadness in her eyes deepened. "That's all I could have ever wished for." Suddenly, she froze. "The knights are coming."
      "Quick!" Corinna turned to me with panic clear on her face. "Take the pill quickly! Here"-she took Phina's shard and a third from her pouch and pressed them into my hands as well. "Lynden's transformation wasn't instantaneous-it took a few days for him to fully turn back into a human. I don't know what will happen after you take it."
      As the sky continued to lighten, I dropped to my knees to hide from the sunlight slowly spilling into the room. Corinna dropped to the ground in front of me as I popped all three of the shards of light into my mouth and swallowed. Nothing happened.
      "Well?" she asked, and the desperation in her voice increased. The sound of armored footsteps grew louder and louder outside as the knights flooded into the cell block outside.
      Instead of answering, I took Corinna's face in my hands and leaned forward to gently brush my lips against hers. It was a thank you. And a goodbye. "I love you," I breathed.
      Even if the shards of light could really turn me back into a human, with its delayed reaction, by the time I fully reverted back into a human, it would be too late. We were both too late. This is where it ends.
      A single tear spilled down the side of Corinna's face as the cell door was thrown open with a bang. I could hear the knights' voices, but they were muffled as if I was somewhere deep underwater.
      Suddenly Corinna stilled, and her eyes fluttered close as she collapsed to the stone floor. She was unconscious.
      "Corinna!" I cried as I knelt beside her, clasping her hand tightly in my own. "Corinna!" But before I could wrap my head around what had just happened, a strange burning sensation flooded through me, and I froze.
      "Edeline!" I could hear Phina calling my name from somewhere far away as the world turned sideways. My head hit the stones with a thud, and everything went black.
       
~
       
      "Edeline."
      I blinked as the world slowly came into focus around me, and the stars glittered above as a soft wind kissed my face. I winced as I sat up, and my head spun as I climbed to my feet.
      It didn't take me long to realize that I was standing on the balcony of the castle I had grown up in. I remembered this night clearly. But when I looked around for my parents' bodies, I only found empty space. There wasn't a single drop of blood to be seen on the stones of the balcony.
      It took me a few moments to realize that I wasn't wearing the dress I had worn that night either. I was still dressed in white-the color of absence and mourning and death.
      What happened? Am I dead?
      "Edeline," the voice said again. I slowly turned around, and my eyes widened as I saw the figure standing in front of the railings.
      "Mother!" I dropped to my knees as my strength failed me. "What are you doing here?"
      Father appeared too, seemingly out of thin air. "We're here for you, Edeline," he said, smiling softly. "Is it time for us to be together again? We've all been waiting for you."
      "You've been waiting for me," I echoed, and my vision blurred with tears. I had been waiting too. I had waited so long for the day I'd finally be reunited with my family.
      "Everyone's here." Mother smiled at me, and the long fabric of her gown fluttered in the breeze. "Your uncle, the young knights, everyone."
      "I-" I looked up at Mother and Father. The light from the moon gave them an ethereal glow.
      A voice sounded from behind me. "Edeline."
      I turned to find Corinna standing there. She was smiling as she extended a hand to me, and her eyes sparkled warmly.
      Corinna, I mouthed.
      Behind her, a hooded figure materialized. I knew this person-knew the blood-red eyes shining from the shadows of her hood. It was Karmen, the queen of the vampires. But just as I tensed, the figure lifted her delicate hands and removed her hood.
      "Phina." I looked up at the ginger-haired vampire. Phina just smiled. But there was something wistful behind her eyes as her own white dress glowed silver.
      "Don't forget about us!" another voice echoed as Storm appeared next to Phina, with Lynden, Clarity, and Cameren in tow. "We're here too!"
      I let out a laugh. It was a sound choked with tears, but I was smiling.
      "Edeline," Corinna said again. Her hand was still outstretched.
      I looked back over my shoulder at my parents, who were smiling softly. "The choice is yours to make." Mother's voice drifted to me on the wind. "We'll continue to wait for you."
      "Thank you," I whispered. I took a deep breath and turned back to my friends. I looked up at all of their smiling faces, and slowly but surely, I reached out a shaky hand. My fingers closed around Corinna's. As she pulled me to my feet, the world turned sideways, and I squeezed my eyes shut as everything vanished in a blinding flash of light.
      My eyes flew open a moment later.
      Breathing. I was breathing.
      I slowly sat up as I surveyed my surroundings. I was lying on a large bed in an unfamiliar room. A large window made up most of the back wall of the room. Sunlight poured in through the glass, and the blue sky outside was streaked with clouds. Judging from the fact that I couldn't see the ground outside from the bed, this room must have been very high up.
      But the day . . . it was day, and I could finally see the sky in all of its brilliance.
      I just stared for a while as my heart beat steadily in my chest. It took me a few minutes to realize that something like a pillow had been pressed over all of my senses. My sense of smell had dulled, and my hearing and eyesight were significantly less sharp. But I found that I didn't care a single bit. I was alive again. I was human.
      Suddenly, there was movement, and I looked down to find Corinna lying on the blankets next to me with her eyes closed.
      "Corinna." I gently shook her shoulders. "Corinna."
      "Edeline!" Corinna's eyes fluttered open as she looked up at me, then she slowly sat up and clutched her head. "What happened?" She looked around the room with the same confusion that I had previously felt. "Where are we?"
      "It worked, Corinna!" My vision blurred with tears of joy as I threw my arms around her. "The magic-it worked!"
      Corinna let out a breath of relief as she hugged me tightly. "I almost can't believe it," she whispered, overwhelmed with emotion. When she finally drew away, she put her hands on my shoulders to look at me properly. "Your eyes are no longer red! They're brown! And your ears-they're human ears now too!" Then she frowned slightly as if she had just remembered something. "The last thing I remember was passing out in the cell. What happened after that?"
      "I'm not sure myself-I passed out shortly after you did. I wonder how long we've been out. And what happened to-"
      "Phina!" Corinna and I said in unison as we stared at each other.
      "I see that the two of you are finally awake." The door to our room swung open as Clarity swept inside. Her white skirts swished around her legs.
      "Clarity!" Corinna jumped to her feet and wobbled on her wooden leg. "How long have we been unconscious? What happened to Phina? Are we in the castle? Where's Chloe-Jane and Cameren?"
      "Which question would you like me to answer first?" Clarity sighed. Her voice lacked the usual sharpness.
      Corinna and I exchanged a glance.
      "Is Phina . . . ?" I trailed off.
      Clarity just shook her head, and I fell silent. "The two of you have been unconscious for about three days," Clarity said shortly. "According to Chloe-Jane, when she entered the cell, the two of you were both lying on the floor. I think she thought the both of you had decided to commit suicide and panicked. Chloe-Jane ran out to the castle gates herself to find Cameren and me. The three of us are in the castle right now, and Cameren is currently comforting Chloe in one of the other rooms. We suspect that Lynden and Storm will show up any day now with Mother as well."
      "You should go talk to Chloe-Jane," I said softly as I looked at Corinna. "I can only imagine how worried she is. I think she'll be overjoyed to see that you're awake."
      Corinna nodded. "Let's go together."
      I made to stand up, but the moment my feet touched the floor, I found that they were unable to support my weight. I fell to my knees. All of my strength had vanished, and it would certainly take some time to get used to.
      "Edeline!" Corinna dropped down instantly to help me to my feet.
      "I really am a regular human now." I laughed as Corinna guided me to the door, then we followed Clarity down the long halls of the castle. "Tell me"-my voice grew serious-"what did it take to create the pill that transformed me back into a human?"
      Corinna exhaled. "Clarity, Storm, and I did it together. Andreus claimed that the cost of the magic was a few years off our lives." I opened my mouth, but Corinna cut me off. "Before you say that I shouldn't have done it, I want you to know that I don't regret it. I know I can't speak for Clarity and Storm, but I don't think they have any regrets either."
      I looked at Clarity in surprise. "You did it too?"
      Corinna's sister just nodded her head without turning around. A moment later, she stopped in front of a door. She pushed it open and stood aside to let us pass.
      Chloe-Jane was sitting in a chair, with her hair undone and her face hidden in her hands. Cameren was kneeling next to her as he gently patted her on the back. Both of them turned as Corinna and I entered the room.
      "Corinna!" Chloe-Jane shrieked. She jumped to her feet and ran at her sister before throwing her arms around her in a tight hug.
      "Chloe-Jane!" Corinna exclaimed in surprise. She wrapped her arms around her sister, returning the embrace.
      "I'm so sorry, Corinna." Chloe-Jane's eyes were red and swollen as she sobbed. "I just wanted to do the right thing," she gushed out. "I didn't think you would-I-"
      "Slow down, slow down." Corinna smiled faintly as she stroked her sister's hair. "I'm alive and well now, aren't I? I thought Clarity and Cameren explained what happened to me."
      Chloe-Jane just squeezed her sister tighter. "They did, but the moment I saw you and Edeline lying there on the floor of the cell side by side . . . I suddenly realized if there really was no magic, you'd be dead. I use to take the Immortal One's words as the only truth, but I don't care about any of that anymore. I stopped caring when I thought that my sister had died because of me. I'm so sorry Corinna. I'm just so happy that you're alive!"
      Corinna smiled. "Well, Edeline is no longer a vampire. Does that mean you'll finally approve of the two of us?"
      "If it means you'll keep on living"-Chloe-Jane nodded her head vigorously-"I will."
      "Thank you, Chloe."
      "Thank you," I echoed quietly as I looked at the young queen. "I mean it."
      Chloe-Jane finally drew away and wiped her eyes with a sleeve. "So what happens now?"
      "A lot of things happen now." Corinna looked around at all of us. "You're the queen of the kingdom, and the former kings left you quite a big mess to clean up."
      Chloe-Jane let out a weak laugh. "You're right. I've got my work cut out for me."
      As the two of them talked, I walked over to the large windows lining the room and pressed a hand to the glass. I glanced out at the front of the castle, and if I looked carefully, I could still see the dark scorch marks on the stones.
