And if I looked even closer, I could have sworn that there was still ash drifting through the air, spiraling lazily on the summer breeze.
      The feeling I got from the ash wasn't one of sadness, though. Instead I felt peace. A sad smile tugged at my lips as I dropped my gaze from the window and made my way back over to Corinna.
      "We should definitely start with helping the newly freed slaves settle down and find places to live," Corinna continued with a knowing smile. "They need jobs with good pay. Oh, speaking of jobs, you've got quite a few jobless overseers to take care of. But don't worry too much-we're all here to help you."
      "We do have a lot of work to do." Chloe-Jane was smiling now too.
      Corinna and I exchanged a glance, and we smiled. The worst was over. Now we had a new challenge ahead of us. But this one we'd all face together. All of us.
      "When do we start?" Chloe-Jane looked around at everyone in the room.
      Corinna's eyes sparkled. "Now."

Epilogue
       
The ocean was a wondrous thing-shimmering water in all directions with nothing but the clear blue sky above us.
      I closed my eyes as I rested my arms against the wooden railing of the ship. I relished the salt-tinged breeze as it kissed my face and sent my hair flying. Two years-or maybe it was three years now-we had been away from our kingdom, and now it was about time to return home.
      "Corinna!" There was laughter in Edeline's voice as she came up beside me and joined me at the railing. Her smile was as radiant as ever, and I quickly found myself smiling as well. "I can see land!"
      "Land? Already?"
      Edeline's inky hair swished around her collarbone, and her necklace glittered in the sunlight as she handed me a spyglass. "Here-if you look that way, you'll see the port town in the distance."
      I held the spyglass up to my eye and followed Edeline's finger. She was right: there were buildings in the distance. Buildings and ships and land.
      "It feels like just yesterday and yet also an entire lifetime ago since we left the capital city." I shook my head in awe as I passed the spyglass back to Edeline. "I'm curious to see how everyone's doing. That's right-Storm's an adult now, isn't he? Chloe-Jane's almost one too!"
      With Chloe-Jane in power, the northern continent's relations and overall views of the southern continent had improved drastically. Mother, Cameren, and Clarity now lived in the castle with Chloe-Jane. Cameren had found someone to take over the position of captain of the guards and was now an ordinary castle knight. Clarity was always at Chloe-Jane's side as the young queen's advisor. When my older sister wasn't advising the young queen, she would spend her time studying medicine. But ever since Phina's passing, something about Clarity had changed: my sister's sharpness had vanished and was replaced with a sad wistfulness.
      "We should be there by nightfall," Edeline said as she wrapped an arm around me. "How do we want to make our entrance this time?"
      I leaned into her embrace. "Since we've got some unfinished business to take care of in the port town, we probably shouldn't do things the flashy way."
      Edeline laughed, and her deep brown eyes sparked. Suddenly, there was a chirping sound, followed by the flapping of wings as a colorful bird dove down from the sky. Edeline held out an arm, and the bird landed on top of it before ruffling its feathered wings.
      Edeline extended her arm to me. I carefully slipped off the note tied to the bird's foot, then read the letter. "Everything's ready. All we need to do is show up."
      We needed to make one stop before the castle. But we'd see everyone very soon.
       
~
       
      The sky was flecked with stars by the time we pulled up at the docks. Edeline and I hopped off of our ship, and our daggers jingled softly beneath our coats. The two of us set off through the port town. And to my surprise, it was not nearly as unpleasant as it was the last time we had visited. Even though the buildings were still relatively rundown, all of the filth that I remembered had vanished.
      Finally, Edeline and I came upon a tavern in the middle of the town, and we exchanged a glance before pushing the door open. This was the place.
      The tavern was almost completely empty save for a man with wild brown hair in the corner of the room. He was sitting across a table from a teenage girl. I locked eyes with the elderly bartender across the room and silently motioned for him to leave. The bartender didn't need to question me before he scurried from the tavern.
      "Is this him?" I called across the room.
      The medicine girl turned to look at me as she slowly nodded her head. "It's been a few months, but I finally found him as you instructed."
      "Found me?" the man demanded as he narrowed his deep blue eyes suspiciously. "What's going on?"
      "You are a wanted man," Edeline said silkily. "You're coming with us."
      "I'm not going anywhere!" The man sprung to his feet and squinted at the two of us through the dim light. As he seemed to get a better look at Edeline and me, his face paled. "Pirates!"
      I almost laughed at that. "Pirates?"
      "You-you-" The man slowly took a step backward as his eyes fell on my wooden leg. "You're Corinna!"
      "I wouldn't call myself a pirate." I kept my voice cool. "But I am Corinna."
      "Then you-" The man turned to Edeline, pointing a shaking finger at her. "You're Edeline! So what do I owe the honor of meeting the two most feared and respected pirates of the seas?"
      Edeline rolled her eyes. "We're not pirates. We're the ones who defend the seas from pirates."
      "You've met us before." I smiled at the man, and he flinched backward. "And at that time, you hoped that we would die after you sold us out. If we were dead, we wouldn't be able to come and find you like we are now."
      "I met you?" The man was in a full-out panic now. "I don't remember ever meeting either of you pirates!"
      Edeline casually weighed one of her daggers in a hand. "It was some years back. The two of us came to you with our friend Storm the Dragonhearted, asking you for information."
      "You were the knights that good-for-nothing boy brought with him?" The information dealer's eyes widened in remembrance. "Spare me!" he shrieked and dropped to the floor as I pulled out one of my daggers. "I wouldn't have offended the two of you if I knew who you were back then! I didn't-"
      "You didn't what?" Edeline knelt down in front of the cowering man. The information dealer lifted his chin slightly to look up at her, and when he saw the glinting dagger in her hand, he rapidly bowed his head to the floor. "You're to blame for the captain's wooden leg. If you hadn't tipped off the king, we wouldn't have had to flee for our lives the way we did."
      "It's your fault for breaking into the castle in the first place!"
      "Oh?" Edeline's eyes flashed. "So this is our fault now?"
      "No!" the man said quickly, and his voice was high from fright. "It's all my fault! My fault!"
      "What happened to you?" Edeline scoffed as she stood back up. "The last time we saw you, you were quite intimidating. Now, you either come with us yourself, or we do this the hard way."
      "I'll follow you," the man said as he shakily rose to his feet. "I'll follow you."
      But just as he staggered over to me, there was a flash of metal as he drew his sword and lunged toward me with an angry cry.
      I dodged the swinging sword with ease before kicking the man's sword hand with my wooden leg. The blade clattered to the floor, and the man hissed, clutching his hand in pain.
      I kicked his sword aside. "I'll ask you again. Shall we do this the easy way, or the hard way? You've done a lot of illegal things. The queen has put out a warrant for your arrest, and we're just here to claim the reward money."
      The information dealer just glared as Edeline tied his hands behind his back with a length of rope. "You're lucky your queen is kind," she remarked as she dragged the man toward the door. "Be happy that all you're getting is a long sentence in the dungeons."
      When the man was fully apprehended, the medicine girl walked over to me. "It's been a while, Captain," she said.
      I smiled down at her. "How's everything in the capital city?"
      "I've been having the time of my life." She brushed invisible specks of dirt from her skirts. "Luring him here was too easy."
      "Thank you for doing this," I said gratefully. "How can I ever repay you?"
      "You've repaid me enough already, sister. This is the least I can do." Then the medicine girl paused as if she had just remembered something. "Is it true that you're going to stay here in the capital city for a while? You're not going to go back to sea?"
      I clasped my hands behind my back and watched the lanterns lining the tavern walls flicker softly. "Edeline and I will be back on the sea eventually. The world is waiting for us. But it's been a while since I've seen my friends and family back home."
      "Oh," the medicine girl said, then rummaged through the pockets of her skirts. She produced an envelope and held it out to me. "I'm supposed to deliver this to you."
      "What's this?" I asked, carefully taking the envelope from her and turning it over in my hand.
      "Once you've finished everything you need to do in the capital city, you should read the letter inside. Safe travels, Captain." The medicine girl saluted me. "I'll come visit you when I'm in town."
      I smiled as I pocketed the envelope. "I'll be waiting for you."
       
~
       
      When we arrived at the castle gates early the next morning, the knights standing guard dipped their heads in our direction. We heard footfalls over the grass as Mother came into view.
      "Mother!" I cried excitedly as I hurried to her with outstretched arms.
      "Corinna!" Mother laughed as she scooped me up in her arms the same way she had done when I was younger. "My little girl has returned! No"-Mother corrected herself as she looked me up and down-"you're not a little girl anymore. You've grown into quite the young woman. Even though we've been oceans apart for the past couple of years, all of us here in the capital city have heard the stories of the wanderers that patrol the seas, keeping them free of illegal activity and crime."
      "Do you know if Lynden and Storm are in town?" Edeline asked after she handed off the sulking information dealer to the knights.
      "When they heard that the two of you would be returning to the capital city, they made sure to show up and stick around until you did," Mother said with a warm smile. "They're talking with Cameren in the castle right now."
      I grinned. "What are we waiting for? Lead the way."
      Mother laughed as she led us through the gates and onto the castle grounds beyond.
      We arrived at the throne room, and the moment we entered, we were greeted with the sound of cheering.
      "Corinna! Edeline!" Storm was the first to reach us, and his eyes were bright as he grinned. "Or wait, should I be calling you 'Capitan Corinna' now?"
      I laughed. "Calling me Corinna is fine. You've gotten taller since the last time I've seen you."
      "Corinna, Edeline." Clarity made her way over to us with the faintest trace of a smile on her face. "It's been a while." Then she turned to Edeline. "I see you've cut your hair too. It suits you."
      "You're back!" Chloe-Jane hurried over to join us, with Cameren and Lynden following close behind. My younger sister threw herself at me first and hugged me tightly. Then to my surprise, she hugged Edeline next. "Did you find him?"
      "The information dealer has been apprehended." Edeline nodded as Chloe-Jane finally released her. "The knights are taking him to the dungeons as we speak."
      "Good," Lynden said. "It's about time that crook was captured."
      Storm nodded in agreement. "I would have gone looking for him myself, but my uncle wanted me to run some errands."
      "How is Andreus?" I asked.
      "Andreus is doing fine," Lynden answered. "Storm and I recently started helping him sort through his centuries-old collections. He claims he wants to make room for new stuff, but I think he just enjoys the company."
      I smiled at that. "That's good to hear-I'll have to pay Andreus a visit soon."
      "Tell me about your adventures traveling the oceans!" Chloe-Jane tugged on my sleeve. "I want to hear all about it!"
      "I can tell this is going to be a good story," Cameren added with a smile. "Don't leave anything out."
      I laughed. "I'll do my best. Where should I start? Well, I guess the beginning would be a good place. If I get any of the details wrong, I'm sure Edeline can correct me."
       
~
       
      After spending a week at the castle, Edeline and I bid our farewells to everyone before setting off on horseback toward the eastern part of the city. We still had one place to visit before we began our journey up the mountain to meet up with Storm, Lynden, and Andreus.
      "It almost feels strange," I said aloud as we made our way through the streets and around the buildings of the city. "I can actually travel around the capital city in the day without people staring or giving me weird looks."
      Edeline looked around at the city. The sky above was painted in the pinks and oranges and golds of the sunset. "It just comes to show how effective Chloe-Jane has been on the throne." Then her voice softened. "I think this is the world Phina would have liked to see."
      I nodded silently.
      "There's the city house." Edeline pointed to our right. "We're almost there. We're almost home." The two of us checked our horses in at the stable and continued the rest of our way on foot.
      It was night by the time we reached the forest, and the trees were exactly as I remembered them. Before long, we emerged into the clearing. I felt Edeline's fingers twine through mine, and I gave her hand a squeeze. "We're home."
      Inside the house, Edeline and I sat together in the living room, bathed in the warm glow of the lamp in front of us. The two of us had changed into simple dresses and were getting ready to go to bed after our long day.
      Edeline rose to her feet and made to turn off the lamp, but then she paused. "Do you still have that letter?" she asked as she looked at me expectantly.
      I blinked. "Letter?" After all the excitement at the castle, I had completely forgotten about the letter the medicine girl gave me. I quickly stood up and hurried over to my coat hanging by the door. I rummaged around in the pockets until my hands closed on the envelope.
      When I returned to my seat next to Edeline, I gingerly unfolded the letter. Then resting my head on Edeline's shoulder, I held the letter out for her to see. "What does it say? I think I'm too tired to keep my eyes open for much longer."
      Edeline's eyes widened in surprise as she read the letter. She clasped my hands in her own, and I stared at her in bewilderment as I waited for her to share the news. "Corinna!" she said excitedly. "It's your father! He's been searching for you!"
